    搜神记序
    晋散骑常侍新蔡干宝令升撰
    　　虽考先志于载籍，收遗逸于当时，盖非一耳一目之所亲闻睹也，又安敢谓无失实者哉。卫朔失国，二传互其所闻，吕望事周，子长存其两说。若此比类，往往有焉。从此观之，闻见之难，由来尚矣。夫书赴告之定辞，据国史之方册，犹尚若此；况仰述千载之前，记殊俗之表，缀片言于残阙，访行事于故老，将使事不二迹，言无异途，然后为信者，固亦前史之所病；然而国家不废注记之官，学士不绝诵览之业，岂不以其所失者小，所存者大乎。今之所集，设有承于前载者，则非余之罪也。若使采访近世之事，苟有虚错，愿与先贤前儒，分其讥谤。及其著述，亦足以发明神道之不诬也。群言百家，不可胜览；耳目所受，不可胜载。亦粗取足以演八略之旨，成其微说而已。幸将来好事之士，录其根体，有以游心，寓目，而无尤焉。

    Preface to Records of Searching for Spirits
    By Gan Bao, of Xincang, serving as a Scattered Rider Attendant of the Jin dynasty

    Although I have investigated ancient records and texts, and gathered forgotten or overlooked material from contemporary sources, such things are not something that can be directly heard or seen by one's own ears and eyes. How, then, could I claim that there are no inaccuracies? Wei Shuo's exile was recorded differently in the Zuo Zhuan and the Gongyang Zhuan, and Jiang Ziya's service to the Zhou dynasty was recounted in two ways in Records of the Grand Historian. Such cases are not uncommon. From this, it is clear that the difficulty of obtaining accurate information has been so since ancient times. Even official documents and their fixed language, based on the official histories and records, can still be subject to such issues; how much more so when one looks back to events a thousand years prior, records of unusual customs, pieces together fragments from incomplete sources, and inquires about past events from the elderly? To ensure that events have no double tracks and that words have no divergent paths, so that they may be considered trustworthy, this has indeed been a flaw in earlier histories. However, the state does not abolish the position of those who record and annotate, and scholars do not cease their studies and readings. Is this not because the losses are minor while the gains are great? If what I have compiled here builds upon earlier records, then it is not my fault. If I were to investigate recent events and there were any inaccuracies, I would willingly share the blame with earlier scholars and Confucian scholars. In my writings, I also aim to demonstrate that the ways of the gods are not false. The various schools of thought and writings are too numerous to fully review, and what can be heard and seen cannot be fully recorded. I have roughly selected what is sufficient to illustrate the principles of the Eight Categories, and to complete my modest account. I hope that future scholars who take an interest will record its essence, find it pleasing to the mind, and view it without criticism.

    3

    搜神记卷一
    　　神农以赭鞭鞭百草，尽知其平毒寒温之性，臭味所主，以播百谷，故天下号神农也。
    　　赤松子者，神农时雨师也，服冰玉散，以教神农，能入火不烧。至昆仑山，常入西王母石室中，随风雨上下。炎帝少女追之，亦得仙，俱去。至高辛时，复为雨师，游人间。今之雨师本是焉。
    　　赤将子轝者，黄帝时人也。不食五谷，而啖百草华。至尧时，为木工。能随风雨上下。时于市门中卖缴，故亦谓之缴父。
    　　宁封子，黄帝时人也。世传为黄帝陶正，有异人过之，为其掌火。能出五色烟。久则以教封子，封子积火自烧，而随烟气上下。视其灰烬，犹有其骨。时人共葬之宁北山中。故谓之宁封子。
    　　偓佺者，槐山采药父也。好食松实。形体生毛，长七寸。两目更方。能飞行逐走马。以松子遗尧，尧不暇服。松者，简松也。时受服者，皆三百岁。

    Explanation

    3

    The Search for the Supernatural: Volume One

    Shen Nong struck various plants with a red stick, fully understanding their properties of toxicity, coldness, warmth, and their scents and flavors, and cultivated and spread various grains. Therefore, he was known throughout the world as Shen Nong.

    Chi Songzi was the rain god during Shen Nong's time. He consumed the Ice Jade Powder, which granted him the ability to enter fire without being burned. He traveled to Mount Kunlun, often entering the stone chamber of the Queen Mother of the West, moving with the wind and rain, up and down. The young daughter of Emperor Yan pursued him, and she too attained immortality, leaving together. By the time of Emperor Ku, he returned as the rain god, wandering among humans. Today's rain gods are descendants of him.

    Chi Jiangzi Yu was a man from the time of the Yellow Emperor. He did not eat grains but instead consumed the flowers of various herbs. By the time of Emperor Yao, he became a carpenter. He could move with the wind and rain, up and down. He sometimes sold his nets at the city gate, hence he was also called Net Father.

    Ning Fengzi was also from the time of the Yellow Emperor. He was traditionally known as the chief potter of the Yellow Emperor. A strange man passed by and asked him to manage the fire. He could produce five-colored smoke. After a while, he taught Ning Fengzi, who accumulated fire and burned himself, rising with the smoke. When his ashes were examined, his bones were still visible. People buried him in the north of Ning Mountain. Therefore, he was known as Ning Fengzi.

    Wei Quan was a father who gathered herbs on Mount Hui. He enjoyed eating pine seeds. His body was covered in hair, seven inches long. His eyes were square-shaped. He could fly and chase horses. He gave pine seeds to Emperor Yao, but Yao did not have time to consume them. The pine seeds were from a simple pine tree. Those who consumed them lived for three hundred years.

    4

    彭祖者，殷时大夫也。姓钱，名铿。帝颛顼之孙，陆终氏之中子。历夏而至商末，号七百岁。常食桂芝。历阳有彭祖仙室。前世云：祷请风雨，莫不辄应。常有两虎在祠左右。今日祠之讫地，则有两虎迹。
    　　师门者，啸父弟子也。能使火。食桃葩。为孔甲龙师。孔甲不能修其心意，杀而埋之外野。一旦，风雨迎之。山木皆燔。孔甲祠而祷之，未还而死。
    　　前周葛由，蜀羌人也。周成王时，好刻木作羊卖之。一旦，乘木羊入蜀中，蜀中王侯贵人追之，上绥山绥山多桃，在峨眉山西南，高无极也。随之者不复还，皆得仙道。故里谚曰：“得绥山一桃，虽不能仙，亦足以豪。”山下立祠数十处。
    　　崔文子者，泰山人也。学仙于王子乔。子乔化为白蜺，而持药与文子。文子惊怪，引戈击蜺，中之，因堕其药。俯而视之，王子乔之尸也。置之室中，覆以敝筐。须臾，化为大鸟。开而视之，翻然飞去。

    Explanation

    4

    Translation:

    Peng Zu was a high-ranking official during the Shang dynasty. His surname was Qian, and his given name was Keng. He was a descendant of the Yellow Emperor, the second son of Lu Zhong. He lived through the Xia dynasty and into the late Shang dynasty, and was said to have lived for 700 years. He often consumed lingzhi mushrooms. In Luyang, there is a temple dedicated to Peng Zu, and it is said that prayers for rain and wind were always answered. There were often two tigers near his shrine, and after visiting the shrine, one could see the tracks of these two tigers.

    Shou Fu's disciple could control fire. He ate peach blossoms and served as a dragon teacher for King Kongjia. King Kongjia could not maintain his mind and killed him, burying him outside the city. One day, a storm welcomed him. The trees in the mountains caught fire. King Kongjia offered sacrifices and prayed, but he did not return and died.

    Gao You, from the Western Zhou period, was a person from the Shu region. During the reign of King Cheng of Zhou, he enjoyed carving wooden sheep and selling them. One day, he rode a wooden sheep into the Shu region. The kings, princes, and nobles of Shu followed him to Suishan, a mountain in the southwest, which is very high and has many peaches. Those who followed him did not return, and they all attained immortality. The locals have a saying: "If you get a peach from Suishan, even if you do not become immortal, you can still be proud."

    Cui Wenzi was from Mount Tai. He studied immortality under Prince Qiao. Prince Qiao transformed into a white rainbow and gave him medicine. Cui Wenzi was surprised and struck the rainbow with a spear, hitting it and causing the medicine to fall. He looked down and saw Prince Qiao's body. He placed it in a room and covered it with a worn basket. Soon, it transformed into a large bird and flew away.

    5

    冠先，宋人也。钓鱼为业。居睢水旁，百余年，得鱼，或放，或卖，或自食之。常冠带，好种荔，食其葩实焉。宋景公问其道，不告，即杀之。后数十年，踞宋城门上，鼓琴，数十日乃去。宋人家家奉祠之。
    　　琴高，赵人也。能鼓琴。为宋康王舍人。行涓彭之术，浮游冀州、涿郡间二百余年。后辞入涿水中，取龙子，与诸弟子期之。曰：“明日皆洁斋候。”于水旁设祠屋。果乘赤鲤鱼出，来坐祠中。且有万人观之。留一月，乃复入水去。
    　　陶安公者，六安铸冶师也。数行火。火一朝散上，紫色冲天。公伏冶下求哀。须臾。朱雀止冶上，曰：“安公！安公！冶与天通。七月七日，迎汝以赤龙。”至时，安公骑之，从东南去。城邑数万人，豫祖安送之，皆辞诀。

    Explanation

    5

    冠先, a man from the state of Song, made his living by fishing. He lived by the banks of the Su River for over a hundred years, catching fish, which he sometimes released, sometimes sold, and sometimes ate himself. He always wore formal attire and enjoyed planting litchi trees, eating their fruits. When King Jing of Song asked him about his methods, he refused to reveal them and was executed. Several decades later, he sat on the city gate of Song, played the qin, and stayed for several days before departing. Every household in Song worshipped him.

    Qin Gao, a man from the state of Zhao, was skilled in playing the qin. He served as a retainer to King Kang of Song and practiced the techniques of water management and purification. He wandered between Jizhou and Zhuo Commandery for over two hundred years. Later, he entered the Zhuo River, retrieved a dragon's offspring, and made an appointment with his disciples. He said, "Tomorrow, all of you should purify yourselves and wait." They set up a shrine by the water. Indeed, he rode a red carp out of the water and sat in the shrine. There were thousands of people watching. He stayed for a month and then returned to the water.

    Tao An Gong, a metalworker from Liuan, frequently worked with fire. One day, a burst of fire erupted, producing a purple flame that reached the sky. He prostrated himself in the forge and begged for mercy. Shortly after, a red bird landed on the forge and called out, "Tao Gong! Tao Gong! The forge has become connected to heaven. On the seventh day of the seventh month, we will welcome you with a red dragon." On that day, Tao Gong rode the red dragon and left towards the southeast. Many people from the city came to bid him farewell, all saying their goodbyes.

    6

    有人入焦山七年，老君与之木钻，使穿一盘石，石厚五尺，曰：“此石穿；当得道。”积四十年，石穿，遂得神仙丹诀。
    　　鲁少千者，山阳人也。汉文帝尝微服怀金过之，欲问其道。少千拄金杖，执象牙扇，出应门。
    　　淮南王安，好道术。设厨宰以候宾客。正月上午，有八老公诣门求见。门吏曰王，王使吏自以意难之，曰：“吾王好长生，先生无驻衰之术，未敢以闻。”公知不见，乃更形为八童子，色如桃花。王便见之，盛礼设乐，以享八公。援琴而弦，歌曰：“明明上天，照四海兮。知我好道，公来下兮。公将与余，生羽毛兮。升腾青云，蹈梁甫兮。观见三光，遇北斗兮。驱乘风云，使玉女兮。”今所谓淮南操是也。

    Explanation

    6

    There was once a person who spent seven years in Mount Jiao. Laojun gave him a wooden drill and instructed him to drill through a stone plate, which was five feet thick. He said, "When this stone is drilled through, you will attain enlightenment." After forty years, the stone was drilled through, and he then obtained the elixir of immortality and the secret formula.

    Lu Shaoqian, a person from Shanyang, was visited by Emperor Wen of Han, who once disguised himself and carried gold to inquire about his Daoist practices. Shaoqian held a golden staff and an ivory fan as he answered the door.

    Prince Huai of Anhui, who was fond of Daoist practices, set up a kitchen and staff to welcome guests. On the morning of the first day of the first month, eight old men came to the door to request an audience. The gatekeeper informed the prince, and the prince sent a messenger to reject them, saying, "Our prince desires longevity, but you have no method to halt aging; I dare not inform him." Knowing they would not be seen, the old men transformed into eight young boys, their faces as rosy as peach blossoms. The prince then received them with great ceremony and music, entertaining the eight old men. He took a lute and played it, singing:

    "Bright and clear, the sky shines over the four seas.
    Knowing I love the Dao, you come down from above.
    You will grant me feathers to fly.
    Rising on blue clouds, treading on Liangfu.
    Seeing the three luminaries, meeting the Big Dipper.
    Driving the winds and clouds, commanding the jade maidens."

    This is what is known today as the Huai'an Ode.

    7

    刘根，字君安。京兆长安人也。汉成帝时，入嵩山学道。遇异人授以秘诀，遂得仙。能召鬼。颍川太守史祈以为妖，遣人召根，欲戮之。至府，语曰：“君能使人见鬼，可使形见。不者，加戮。”根曰：“甚易。”借府君前笔砚书符，因以叩几；须臾，忽见五六鬼，缚二囚于祈前。祈熟视，乃父母也。向根叩头曰：“小儿无状，分当万死。”叱祈曰：“汝子孙不能光荣先祖，何得罪神仙，乃累亲如此。”祈哀惊悲泣，顿首请罪。根默然忽去，不知所之。
    　　汉明帝时，尚书郎河东王乔，为邺令。乔有神术，每月朔，尝自县诣台。帝怪其来数，而不见车骑；密令太史候望之。言其临至时，辄有双凫，从东南飞来。因伏伺，见凫，举罗张之，但得一双舄。使尚书识视，四年中所赐尚书官属履也。

    Explanation

    7

    Liu Gen, courtesy name Jun'an, was from Jingzhao Chang'an. During the reign of Emperor Cheng of Han, he entered Mount Song to study the Dao. He met a strange person who taught him secret techniques, and thus became an immortal. He could summon ghosts. The magistrate of Yingchuan, Shi Qi, considered this as witchcraft and sent someone to summon Liu Gen, intending to punish him. When Liu Gen arrived at the magistrate's office, the magistrate said, "You can make people see ghosts; can you make them appear in their true form? If not, you will be punished." Liu Gen replied, "It is very easy." He borrowed the magistrate's brush and inkstone to write a talisman, then tapped the table with it. Soon, he suddenly saw five or six ghosts, who tied two prisoners in front of the magistrate. The magistrate looked closely and recognized them as his parents. They bowed to the ground in front of Liu Gen and said, "Our son has caused trouble; we deserve to die a thousand deaths." Liu Gen scolded the magistrate, "Your descendants cannot honor your ancestors. What crime have you committed against the immortals to cause such trouble for your parents?" The magistrate was filled with grief and fear, wept, and begged for forgiveness. Liu Gen silently vanished, and no one knew where he went.

    During the reign of Emperor Ming of Han, Wang Qiao, a Shangshu Lang from Hedong, served as the magistrate of Ye. Wang Qiao had supernatural powers and often traveled from the county to the capital every first day of the month. The emperor was curious about his frequent visits and noticed that he arrived without any entourage. He secretly ordered the Grand Historian to observe him. The Grand Historian reported that when Wang Qiao was about to arrive, there were always two cranes flying from the southeast. The emperor then hid and waited, saw the cranes, and set up a net to catch them. However, they only caught a pair of shoes. The emperor ordered the Shangshu to identify the shoes, which turned out to be the shoes given to the Shangshu officials over four years.

    8

    蓟子训，不知所从来。东汉时，到洛阳见公卿，数十处，皆持斗酒片脯候之。曰：“远来无所有，示致微意。”坐上数百人，饮啖终日不尽。去后，皆见白云起，从旦至暮。时有百岁公说：小儿时见训卖药会稽市，颜色如此。训不乐住洛，遂遁去。正始中，有人于长安东霸城，见与一老公共摩挲铜人，相谓曰：“适见铸此，已近五百岁矣。”见者呼之曰：“蓟先生小住。”并行应之。视若迟徐，而走马不及。
    　　汉阴生者，长安渭桥下乞小儿也。常于市中丐，市中厌苦，以粪洒之。旋复在市中乞，衣不见污如故。长吏知之，械收系，着桎梏，而续在市乞。又械欲杀之，乃去。洒之者家，屋室自坏，杀十数人。长安中谣言曰：“见乞儿与美酒，以免破屋之咎。”

    Explanation

    8

    Jì Zǐxùn, whose origins are unknown, appeared in the Eastern Han Dynasty and visited Luoyang, where he met with high-ranking officials at several locations. Everywhere he went, people greeted him with a small amount of wine and a bit of dried meat, saying, "We have nothing else to offer, but we hope to convey a small intention." During his visit, hundreds of people gathered to drink and eat with him, and they consumed all day without finishing. After he left, it was said that white clouds rose from dawn until dusk.

    At one time, an elderly man claimed that when he was a child, he had seen Jì Zǐxùn selling medicine in Kuaiji, and he looked just as he did now. Jì Zǐxùn did not enjoy staying in Luoyang and eventually disappeared. During the Zhengshi period, someone in Dongbachi, east of Chang'an, saw him rubbing a bronze figure with an elderly man. They said to each other, "We just saw it being cast, and it is nearly five hundred years old." The onlookers called out to him, "Master Jì, please stay a little longer." Jì Zǐxùn responded politely, and although he seemed to move slowly, even a galloping horse could not catch up to him.

    Hán Yīnshēng, a beggar from the banks of the Wei River in Chang'an, was known for his miraculous abilities. He often begged in the market, and although the people there grew tired of him and sprinkled filth on him, he remained clean as if nothing had happened. The local officials learned of this and tried to capture him, binding him with chains and shackles, but he continued to beg in the market. When they tried to kill him, he vanished. The house of the person who had sprinkled the filth on him collapsed, killing several people. A saying circulated in Chang'an: "Give a beggar a cup of fine wine to avoid the guilt of causing a house to collapse."

    9

    谷城乡平常生，不如何所人也。数死而复生。时人为不然。后大水出，所害非一，而平辄在缺门山上大呼言：平常生在此。云复雨，水五日必止。止，则上山求祠之。但见平衣杖革带。后数十年，复为华阴市门卒。
    　　左慈，字符放，庐江人也。少有神通。尝在曹公座，公笑顾众宾曰：“今日高会，珍羞略备。所少者，吴松江鲈鱼为脍。”放曰：“此易得耳。”因求铜盘贮水，以竹竿饵钓于盘中，须臾，引一鲈鱼出。公大拊掌，会者皆惊。公曰：“一鱼不周坐客，得两为佳。”放乃复饵钓之。须臾，引出，皆三尺余，生鲜可爱。公便自前脍之，周赐座席。公曰：“今既得鲈，恨无蜀中生姜耳。”放曰：“亦可得也。”公恐其近道买，因曰：“吾昔使人至蜀买锦，可敕人告吾使；使增市二端。”人去，须臾还，得生姜。又云：“于锦肆下见公使，已敕增市二端。”后经岁余，公使还，果增二端。问之，云：“昔某月某日，见人于肆下，以公敕敕之。

    Explanation

    9

    Translation:

    Ping Changsheng of Gucheng Town, whose origins are unknown, died and was revived multiple times. People of the time did not believe it. Later, a great flood occurred, causing widespread harm, but Ping was always shouting on the Qiemu Mountain, saying, "Ping Changsheng is here." Clouds and rain appeared, and he predicted that the water would stop in five days. When the water stopped, people went up the mountain to worship him, but they only saw Ping wearing a robe, holding a staff, and wearing a leather belt. After several decades, he became a gatekeeper in Huayin.

    Zuo Ci, whose courtesy name was Yuanfang, was from Lujiang. He had spiritual powers from a young age. Once, while he was at Cao Cao's banquet, Cao smiled and turned to the guests, saying, "Today we have a grand gathering, and most delicacies are prepared. The only thing lacking is the Wusongjiang perch for sashimi." Zuo said, "This is easy to obtain." He then asked for a copper basin to hold water and set up a bamboo pole with bait in the basin. In a short while, he pulled out a perch. Cao clapped his hands in delight, and the guests were all amazed. Cao said, "One fish is not enough for all the guests; two would be better." Zuo then baited the pole again, and in a short while, he pulled out two more, each over three feet long, fresh and appealing. Cao then personally prepared the sashimi, and the guests were served. Cao said, "Now that we have the perch, I regret not having Sichuan ginger." Zuo said, "That can also be obtained." Cao feared that he might buy it nearby, so he said, "I once sent someone to Sichuan to buy silk. You can instruct them to tell my messenger to buy two more bolts." The messenger left and returned shortly with the ginger. He also said, "I saw your messenger at the silk shop, who had already been instructed to buy two more bolts." After more than a year, when Cao's messenger returned, he indeed had two more bolts. When asked about it, the messenger said, "On a certain day last month, I saw someone at the silk shop who gave me your instructions."

    10

    ”后公出近郊，士人从者百数，放乃赉酒一罂，脯一片，手自倾罂，行酒百官，百官莫不醉饱。公怪，使寻其故。行视沽酒家，昨悉亡其酒脯矣。公怒，阴欲杀放。放在公座，将收之，却入壁中，霍然不见。乃募取之。或见于市，欲捕之，而市人皆放同形，莫知谁是。后人遇放于阳城山头，因复逐之。遂走入羊群。公知不可得，乃令就羊中告之，曰：“曹公不复相杀，本试君术耳。今既验，但欲与相见。”忽有一老羝，屈前两膝，人立而言曰：“遽如许。”人即云：“此羊是。”竞往赴之。而群羊数百，皆变为羝，并屈前膝，人立，云：“遽如许。”于是遂莫知所取焉。老子曰：“吾之所以为大患者，以吾有身也；及吾无身，吾有何患哉。”若老子之俦，可谓能无身矣。岂不远哉也。

    Explanation

    10

    After the official went out to the outskirts, hundreds of scholars followed him. Fang then brought a jar of wine and a piece of dried meat, and personally poured the wine for all the officials, who were all drunk and full. The official was surprised and sent someone to find out the reason. He went to the wine shop and found that all the wine and dried meat had disappeared. The official was angry and secretly wanted to kill Fang. Fang was in the official's seat, about to be arrested, but suddenly disappeared into the wall. The official then offered a reward to capture him. Someone saw him in the market, wanting to capture him, but the people in the market all looked like Fang, so no one knew who he was. Later, someone met Fang at the top of Yangcheng Mountain and chased him again. He then entered the sheep flock. The official knew he could not catch him, so he ordered someone to tell him among the sheep: "Cao Cao will not kill you anymore; I just wanted to test your skills. Now that it has been proven, I only want to meet you." Suddenly, an old ram bent its front knees, stood up like a person, and said, "So quickly!" People said, "This is the sheep," and rushed to it. And hundreds of sheep turned into rams, all bending their front knees and standing up like people, saying, "So quickly!" Thus, no one knew what to do. Laozi said, "The great worries I have are because I have a body; if I had no body, what worries would I have?" Those like Laozi can be said to be able to have no body. How far-reaching is this!

    11

    孙策欲渡江袭许，与于吉俱行、时大旱。所在熇厉，策催诸将士，使速引船，或身自早出督切。见将吏多在吉许。策因此激怒，言：“我为不如吉耶？而先趋附之。”便使收吉至，呵问之曰：“天旱不雨，道路艰涩，不时得过。故自早出，而卿不同忧戚，安坐船中，作鬼物态，败吾部伍。今当相除。”令人缚置地上暴之，使请雨若能感天，日中雨者，当原赦；不尔，行诛。俄而云气上蒸，肤寸而合；比至日中，大雨总至，溪涧盈溢。将士喜悦，以为吉必见原，并往庆慰。策遂杀之。将士哀惜，藏其尸。天夜，忽更兴云覆之。明旦往视，不知所在。策既杀吉，每独坐，彷佛见吉在左右。意深恶之，颇有失常。后治疮方差，而引镜自照，见吉在镜中，顾而弗见。如是再三。扑镜大叫，疮皆崩裂，须臾而死。(吉，琅琊人，道士。)

    Explanation

    11

    Sun Ce desired to cross the river and attack Xu, traveling together with Yu Ji. At that time, there was a severe drought everywhere. Sun Ce urged the generals and soldiers to quickly lead the ships, sometimes personally getting up early to oversee and urge them. He saw that many of the generals and officials were in Yu Ji's company. Sun Ce took this opportunity to become angry and said, "Am I not as capable as Yu Ji? And yet you all rush to follow him first." He then ordered Yu Ji to be brought to him and harshly questioned him, saying, "The sky is dry and it does not rain, making the roads difficult to traverse. I have come out early myself, but you do not share in my worries and sorrows. Instead, you sit calmly in the ship, acting like a ghost or supernatural being, disrupting my ranks. Now I will eliminate you." He had Yu Ji bound and placed on the ground to be exposed to the sun, and told him to pray for rain. If he could move heaven and it rained by noon, he would be pardoned; otherwise, he would be executed. Soon after, clouds rose up, merging together inch by inch. By noon, it began to rain heavily, filling the streams and ravines. The soldiers were delighted, believing that Yu Ji would certainly be pardoned, and they all went to congratulate and comfort him. However, Sun Ce proceeded to kill Yu Ji. The soldiers mourned and cherished his body. That night, a cloud suddenly arose and covered it. The next morning, when they went to look, Yu Ji's body was nowhere to be found. After killing Yu Ji, Sun Ce often sat alone and seemed to see Yu Ji by his side. He deeply disliked this and became somewhat unbalanced. Later, when he was treating his wounds and they were healing, he looked into a mirror and saw Yu Ji in it. He turned around but could not see him. This happened three times. Sun Ce struck the mirror and shouted loudly, causing his wounds to burst open, and he died shortly thereafter. (Yu Ji was a Taoist priest from Langya.)

    12

    介琰者，不知何许人也。住建安方山，从其师白羊公杜受玄一无为之道。能变化隐形。尝往来东海，暂过秣陵，与吴主相闻。吴主留琰，乃为琰架宫庙，一日之中，数遣人往问起居。琰或为童子，或为老翁，无所食啖，不受饷遗。吴主欲学其术，琰以吴主多内御，积月不教。吴主怒，敕缚琰，着甲士引弩射之。弩发，而绳缚犹存不知琰之所之。
    　　吴时有徐光者，尝行术于市里：从人乞瓜，其主勿与，便从索瓣，杖地种之；俄而瓜生，蔓延，生花，成实；乃取食之，因赐观者。鬻者反视所出卖，皆亡耗矣。凡言水旱甚验。过大将军孙綝门，褰衣而趋，左右垂践。或问其故。答曰：“流血臭腥不可耐。”綝闻恶而杀之。斩其首，无血。及綝废幼帝，更立景帝，将拜陵，上车，有大风荡綝车，车为之倾。见光在松树上拊手指挥嗤笑之，綝问侍从，皆无见者。俄而景帝诛綝。

    Explanation

    12

    Jie Yan, of unknown origin, resided in Jian'an Fangshan. He followed his teacher, Baiyang Gong Du, to learn the Dao of Xuan Yi Wuwei. He possessed the ability to transform and become invisible. He often traveled to the Eastern Sea and briefly passed through Moling, where he met the ruler of Wu. The Wu ruler kept Jie Yan and built palaces and temples for him, sending people multiple times a day to inquire about his well-being. Jie Yan sometimes appeared as a child and sometimes as an old man, ate nothing, and did not accept any gifts. The Wu ruler wanted to learn his art, but Jie Yan refused to teach for months because the ruler had many concubines. Angered, the Wu ruler ordered Jie Yan to be bound and had armored soldiers draw their bows to shoot him. The bow was drawn, but the ropes remained tied, and no one knew where Jie Yan had gone.

    During the Wu period, there was a man named Xu Guang who often performed magic in the market. He once asked someone for a melon, but the owner refused to give it. Xu Guang then asked for a seed, stuck it in the ground, and planted it. Soon the melon grew, spread, bloomed, and bore fruit. He then took it to eat and gave it to the spectators. The seller looked at what he had sold, and it was all gone. Xu Guang's predictions about drought and flood were very accurate. Passing by the gate of General Sun Chen, he lifted his clothes as he hurried, and his feet were wet from stepping in mud. Someone asked why, and he replied, "The stench of blood is unbearable." Sun Chen heard this and killed him. When his head was cut off, there was no blood. When Sun Chen deposed the young emperor and replaced him with Emperor Jing, and was about to pay homage at the tomb, a strong wind overturned his carriage. He saw Xu Guang on a pine tree, clapping and mocking him. Sun Chen asked his attendants, but none saw anything. Soon after, Emperor Jing had Sun Chen executed.

    13

    葛玄，宅孝先，从左元放受九丹液仙经。与客对食，言及变化之事，客曰：“事毕，先生作一事特戏者。”玄曰：“君得无即欲有所见乎？”乃嗽口中饭，尽变大蜂数百，皆集客身，亦不螫人。久之，玄乃张口，蜂皆飞入，玄嚼食之，是故饭也。又指虾蟆及诸行虫燕雀之属，使舞，应节如人。冬为客设生瓜枣，夏致冰雪。又以数十钱使人散投井中，玄以一器于井上呼之，钱一一飞从井出。为客设酒，无人传杯，杯自至前，如或不尽，杯不去也。尝与吴主坐楼上，见作请雨土人，帝曰：“百姓思雨，宁可得乎？”玄曰：“雨易得耳！”乃书符着社中，顷刻间，天地晦冥，大雨流淹。帝曰：“水中有鱼乎？”玄复书符掷水中，须臾，有大鱼数百头。使人治之。

    Explanation

    13

    Ge Xuan, living in the residence of his father, Xiao Xian, learned the "Nine Elixirs Scripture" from Zuo Yuanfang. While dining with a guest, they spoke of transformational matters. The guest said, "After the meal, the master could perform a special trick." Ge Xuan replied, "Are you not eager to see something?" Then he spat out the food in his mouth, which turned into hundreds of large bees. All the bees gathered on the guest's body but did not sting him. After a while, Ge Xuan opened his mouth, and the bees flew back in. He chewed and ate them, and they were still rice. He also pointed at frogs and various insects like sparrows, making them dance in rhythm like humans. In winter, he provided fresh melons and dates for the guest; in summer, he brought ice and snow. He also threw dozens of coins into the well. Ge Xuan called out to them with a vessel above the well, and the coins flew out one by one. He set up wine for the guest, and no one passed the cup; it came to the guest on its own, and if not finished, it would not leave. Once, while sitting on a balcony with the ruler of Wu, he saw people performing rain rituals. The emperor said, "The people are longing for rain, can it be obtained?" Ge Xuan replied, "Rain is easy to obtain!" He wrote a talisman and placed it in the shrine, and in an instant, the sky darkened and it rained heavily. The emperor asked, "Is there fish in the water?" Ge Xuan wrote another talisman and threw it into the water, and soon, hundreds of large fish appeared. He had them prepared.

    14

    吴猛，濮阳人。仕吴，为西安令，因家分宁。性至孝。遇至人丁义，授以神方；又得秘法神符，道术大行。尝见大风，书符掷屋上，有青乌衔去。风即止。或问其故。曰：“南湖有舟，遇此风，道士求救。”验之果然。西安令于庆死，已三日，猛曰：“数未尽，当诉之于天。”遂卧尸旁，数日，与令俱起。后将弟子回豫章，江水大急，人不得渡；猛乃以手中白羽扇画江水，横流，遂成陆路，徐行而过，过讫，水复。观者骇异。尝守浔阳，参军周家有狂风暴起，猛即书符掷屋上，须臾风静。
    　　园客者，济阴人也。貌美，邑人多欲妻之，客终不娶。尝种五色香草，积数十年，服食其实。忽有五色神蛾，止香草之上，客收而荐之以布，生桑蚕焉。至蚕时，有神女夜至，助客养蚕，亦以香草食蚕。得茧百二十头，大如瓮，每一茧缫六七日乃尽。缫讫，女与客俱仙去，莫知所如。

    Explanation

    14

    Wu Meng, a man from Puyang, served in Wu state and held the position of magistrate in Xianyang, settling in Fenning due to his service. He was extremely filial. He encountered a sage named Ding Yi, who taught him a divine method; he also obtained secret magical talismans, and his Daoist arts became widely popular. Once, he saw a strong wind and wrote a talisman, which he threw onto the roof, and an azure bird carried it away. The wind immediately stopped. Someone asked him why he did this. He replied, "There is a boat on South Lake that encountered this wind, and a Taoist priest sought help." This was verified to be true. When the magistrate Yu Qing died, Wu Meng said, "His time has not yet come to an end; I shall appeal to heaven for him." He then lay down beside the corpse, and after several days, both he and the magistrate came back to life. Later, when he took his disciples back to Yuzhang, the river was flowing very rapidly, and people could not cross. Wu Meng then used his white feather fan to draw on the water, turning it into a land path, and they walked across it at a leisurely pace. After they had crossed, the water returned to its original state. The onlookers were amazed. Once, while serving as governor of Xunyang, a fierce storm arose at the home of a military officer named Zhou. Wu Meng immediately wrote a talisman and threw it onto the roof, and the wind calmed down shortly thereafter.

    Yuan Ke, a man from Jiyin, was handsome, and many people in his town wanted to marry him, but he never married. He once cultivated five-colored aromatic herbs for many years and consumed their fruits. Suddenly, a five-colored divine moth appeared on the herbs, and Yuan Ke collected it and placed it on a cloth, which produced silkworms. When it was time for the silkworms to spin cocoons, a divine woman appeared at night to help him raise them, also feeding them with the aromatic herbs. He obtained 120 silkworm cocoons, each as large as a jar, and it took six to seven days to unravel each one completely. After they were all unraveled, the woman and Yuan Ke both ascended to immortality, and their whereabouts are unknown.

    15

    汉，董永，千乘人。少偏孤，与父居肆，力田亩，鹿车载自随。父亡，无以葬，乃自卖为奴，以供丧事。主人知其贤，与钱一万，遣之。永行，三年丧毕，欲还主人，供其奴职。道逢一妇人曰：“愿为子妻。”遂与之俱。主人谓永曰：“以钱与君矣。”永曰：“蒙君之惠，父丧收藏，永虽小人，必欲服勤致力，以报厚德。”主曰：“妇人何能？”永曰：“能织。”主曰：“必尔者，但令君妇为我织缣百疋。”于是永妻为主人家织，十日而毕。女出门，谓永曰：“我，天之织女也。缘君至孝，天帝令我助君偿债耳。”语毕，凌空而去而去，不知所在。
    　　初，钩弋夫人有罪，以谴死，既殡，尸不臭，而香闻十余里。因葬云陵，上哀悼之。又疑其非常人，乃发冢开视，棺空无尸，惟双履存一云。昭帝即位，改葬之，棺空无尸，独丝履存焉。

    Explanation

    15

    In the Han dynasty, there was a man named Dong Yong from the region of Qi. When he was young, he was orphaned and lived with his father in a workshop, working hard in the fields and traveling in a carriage made of deer skin. After his father's death, he had no means to bury him, so he sold himself into slavery to provide for the funeral. His master, recognizing his virtue, gave him a thousand coins and sent him away. After completing his three-year mourning period, Dong Yong wanted to return to his master to fulfill his duties as a slave. On the way, he met a woman who said, "I wish to be your wife." He agreed, and they went together. The master told Dong Yong, "I have given you money." Dong Yong replied, "I have benefited from your kindness, and my father's funeral has been properly arranged. Although I am a lowly person, I am determined to serve diligently and with effort to repay your great virtue." The master asked, "What can a woman do?" Dong Yong said, "She can weave." The master said, "If that is so, just have your wife weave for me a hundred bolts of silk." Dong Yong's wife then wove for the master's household, completing the task in ten days. The woman then went out and said to Dong Yong, "I am the Weaver Girl from heaven. Because of your great filial piety, the Heavenly Emperor has sent me to help you repay your debt." After saying this, she ascended into the sky and disappeared, and no one knew where she went.

    Initially, the Concubine Gouyi was found guilty and executed by imperial command. After her burial, her body did not decay, and her fragrance could be smelled for more than ten miles. She was buried in Yunling, and the emperor mourned her deeply. Suspecting that she was not an ordinary person, the emperor ordered the tomb to be opened and inspected. The coffin was found to be empty except for a pair of shoes. Later, when Emperor Zhao ascended the throne, he reburied her, and the coffin was again found to be empty, with only a pair of silk shoes remaining.

    16

    汉时有杜兰香者，自称南康人氏。以建业四年春，数诣张传。传年十七，望见其车在门外，婢通言：“阿母所生，遗授配君，可不敬从？”传，先名改硕，硕呼女前，视，可十六七，说事邈然久远。有婢子二人：大者萱支，小者松支。钿车青牛上，饮食皆备。作诗曰：“阿母处灵岳，时游云霄际。众女侍羽仪，不出墉宫外。飘轮送我来，岂复耻尘秽。从我与福俱，嫌我与祸会。”至其年八月旦，复来，作诗曰：“逍遥云汉间，呼吸发九嶷。流汝不稽路，弱水何不之。”出薯●子三枚，大如鸡子，云：“食此，令君不畏风波，辟寒温。”硕食二枚，欲留一，不肯，令硕食尽。言：“本为君作妻，情无旷远，以年命未合，且小乖，大岁东方卯，当还求君。”兰香降时，硕问祷祀何如。香曰：“消魔自可愈疾，淫祀无益。”香以药为消魔。

    Explanation

    16

    A woman named Duran Xiang, claiming to be from Nankang, appeared during the spring of the fourth year of Jianye. She frequently visited Zhang Chuan, who was seventeen years old at the time. Zhang saw her carriage outside his door, and a servant delivered a message: "I was born of my mother and have been entrusted to you as a spouse; should you not respect and follow me?" Zhang, whose name had been changed to Shuo, called the woman forward. She appeared to be sixteen or seventeen, and her story seemed distant and ancient. She had two maidservants: the elder was named Xuanzhi, and the younger was named Songzhi. She arrived in a jeweled carriage drawn by a blue ox, with all necessary provisions for food and drink. She recited a poem: "My mother resides on a sacred mountain, occasionally wandering through the clouds and heavens. Many women attend her in their ceremonial attire, never venturing beyond the walls of her palace. The flying wheel brings me here; why should I be ashamed of earthly impurities? Follow me, and we shall share in fortune; beware, for misfortune may follow if you do not." On the day of the eighth month of that year, she returned and recited another poem: "I wander freely between the Milky Way and the heavens, breathing the air of the Nine Peaks. The stream flows without delay, and the weak waters cannot hinder me." She presented three tuberous roots, each as large as an egg, and said, "Eat these, and you will fear neither the waves nor the cold and heat." Shuo ate two of them, but she insisted he finish the last one. She then said, "I was originally destined to be your wife; our feelings are not distant. However, our fates are not yet aligned, so we must part for now. When the great age of the eastern direction in the year of the wood ox arrives, I will return to seek you." When Lan Xiang arrived, Shuo asked about prayers and rituals. She replied, "Eliminating evil can cure diseases, but excessive or improper worship is of no benefit." She used medicine as a means of eliminating evil.

    17

    魏济北郡从事掾弦超，字义起，以嘉平中夜独宿，梦有神女来从之。自称：“天上玉女，东郡人，姓成公，字知琼，早失父母，天帝哀其孤苦，遣令下嫁从夫。”超当其梦也，精爽感悟，嘉其美异，非常人之容，觉寤钦想，若存若亡，如此三四夕。一旦，显然来游，驾辎軿车，从八婢，服绫罗绮绣之衣，姿颜容体，状若飞仙，自言年七十，视之如十五六女。车上有壶榼，青白琉璃五具。食啖奇异，馔具醴酒，与超共饮食。

    Explanation

    17

    During the JiaPing era, Hui Jibei Commandery's minor official Xian Chao, whose courtesy name was Yiqi, was alone at night when he dreamed of a goddess coming to him. She introduced herself as: "A heavenly jade maiden from Dong Commandery, surnamed Chenggong and given name Zhiqiong, who lost her parents at an early age. The Heavenly Emperor pitied her loneliness and hardship and sent her to marry him." During his dream, Chao was deeply moved by her spirit, admiring her beauty and uniqueness, which were beyond the appearance of an ordinary person. Upon waking, he cherished and longed for her presence, feeling as if she were sometimes there and sometimes not, for several nights. One day, she appeared clearly to visit him, driving a carriage pulled by oxen, accompanied by eight maids, dressed in silk and brocade embroidered clothes. Her appearance and figure were like those of a flying immortal, and she claimed to be seventy years old, yet looked like a girl of fifteen or sixteen. On the carriage, there were five sets of blue and white glassware. They ate strange and exotic foods, delicacies, and sweet wine together.

    18

    谓超曰：“我，天上玉女，见遣下嫁，故来从君，不谓君德。宿时感运，宜为夫妇。不能有益，亦不能为损。然往来常可得驾轻车，乘肥马，饮食常可得远味，异膳，缯素常可得充用不乏。然我神人，不为君生子，亦无妒忌之性，不害君婚姻之义。遂为夫妇。”赠诗一篇，其文曰：“飘浮勃逢敖，曹云石滋芝。一英不须润，至德与时期。神仙岂虚感，应运来相之。纳我荣五族，逆我致祸菑。”此其诗之大较，其文二百余言，不能尽录。兼注易七卷，有卦，有象，以彖为属。

    Explanation

    18

    She said to Chao, "I am a celestial jade maiden, sent down to marry, thus I came to follow you. I do not speak of your virtue. Previously, I felt the movement of fate, and it is fitting that we become husband and wife. I cannot bring you benefit, nor can I cause you harm. However, in terms of travel, you can always drive a light carriage and ride a fat horse; in terms of food, you can always enjoy distant flavors and exotic dishes; in terms of clothing, you can always have silk and fine fabrics without shortage. But as a divine being, I will not bear children for you, nor do I have a jealous nature, and it will not harm your marital duties. Thus, we become husband and wife." She gave him a poem as a gift, the text of which reads: "Drifting and meeting, encountering and wandering, clouds and stones nurture the orchid. One flower does not need moisture, supreme virtue aligns with the time. Gods and immortals are not false, they come to meet you in response to your fate. Accepting me will bring glory to your five clans, rejecting me will bring disaster." This is the general outline of the poem, which is over two hundred words long and cannot be fully recorded. She also annotated the Yijing in seven volumes, with hexagrams, images, and gua titles.

    19

    故其文言既有义理，又可以占吉凶，犹扬子之太玄，薛氏之中经也。超皆能通其旨意，用之占候，作夫妇经。七八年，父母为超娶妇之后，分日而燕，分夕而寝，夜来晨去，倏忽若飞，唯超见之，他人不见。虽居闇室，辄闻人声，常见踪迹，然不睹其形。后人怪问，漏泄其事；玉女遂求去。云：“我，神人也。虽与君交，不愿人知，而君性疏漏，我今本末已露，不复与君通接。积年交结，恩义不轻；一旦分别，岂不怆恨？势不得不尔。

    Explanation

    19

    The classical language is both meaningful and can be used for divination, much like the works of Yang Xiong's Taixuan and Xue's Zhongjing. Chao was able to understand its meaning and used it for divination, creating a book on marital relations. For seven or eight years, after his parents arranged a marriage for him, they shared meals during the day and slept separately at night, with her coming at night and leaving in the morning, swiftly like flying. Only Chao saw her, while others did not. Even in a dark room, he would hear voices, and he often saw traces but never saw her form. Later, people asked about it out of curiosity, and the secret was revealed. The jade maiden then requested to leave, saying, "I am a divine being. Although I have been with you, I do not wish others to know. But your nature is careless, and now everything is known. I will no longer communicate with you. We have been together for many years, and our bond is not light. If we part now, how could we not be sorrowful? The situation leaves me no choice."

    20

    各自努力！”又呼侍御下酒，饮啖，发簏，取织成裙衫两副遗超。又赠诗一首，把臂告辞，涕泣流离，肃然升车，去若飞迅。超忧感积日，殆至委顿。去后五年。超奉郡使至洛，到济北鱼山下，陌上西行，遥望曲道头有一马车，似知琼。驱驰至前，果是也。遂披帷相见，悲喜交切。控左援绥，同乘至洛。遂为室家，克复旧好。至太康中，犹在。但不日日往来，每于三月三日，五月五日，七月七日，九月九日旦，十五日辄下，往来经宿而去。张茂先为之作神女赋。

    Explanation

    20

    "Each one strive hard!" He summoned a court attendant to pour wine, drank and ate, opened the basket, took out two sets of woven skirts and shirts and gave them to Chao. He also gave him a poem, embraced and bid farewell, with tears and sobs flowing uncontrollably, he solemnly mounted the carriage and departed swiftly and quickly. Chao felt grief and emotion for several days, almost to the point of exhaustion. Five years after leaving, Chao served as a messenger from the prefecture and arrived in Luoyang, reaching Fish Mountain in Jibei, traveling west on the road, looking far away and seeing a horse-drawn carriage at the end of a winding road, it seemed to know Qiong. He hurried to the front, and indeed, it was. Then, he lifted the curtain and met, sorrow and joy intermingled intensely. He controlled the left side and pulled the strap, rode together to Luoyang, then became a household or family, overcoming and restoring old friendship. By the middle of the Tai Kang reign, they were still together. But not daily coming and going, every on the third day of the third month, the fifth day of the fifth month, the seventh day of the seventh month, the ninth day of the ninth month in the morning, and the fifteenth day, they would descend, coming and going for a night and then leave. Zhang Maosan wrote the Ode to the Goddess for this.

    21

    搜神记卷二

    　　寿光侯者，汉章帝时人也。能劾百鬼众魅，令自缚见形。其乡人有妇为魅所病，侯为劾之，得大蛇数丈，死于门外，妇因以安。又有大树，树有精，人止其下者死，鸟过之亦坠。侯劾之，树盛夏枯落，有大蛇，长七八丈，悬死树间。章帝闻之，征问。对曰：“有之。”帝曰：“殿下有怪，夜半后，常有数人，绛衣，披发，持火相随。岂能劾之？”侯曰：“此小怪，易消耳。”帝伪使三人为之。侯乃设法，三人登时仆地，无气。帝惊曰：“非魅也，朕相试耳。”即使解之。或云：“汉武帝时，殿下有怪常见，朱衣，披发，相随，持烛而走。帝谓刘凭曰：‘卿可除此否？’凭曰：‘可。’乃以青符掷之，见数鬼倾地。帝惊曰：‘以相试耳。’解之而苏。”

    Explanation

    21

    Records of the Supernatural, Volume Two

    The Marquis of Shouguang, a man of the Han Dynasty during the reign of Emperor Zhang, possessed the ability to expose and confront all ghosts and spirits, forcing them to bind themselves and reveal their forms. In his village, there was a woman who was afflicted by a spirit. The Marquis exposed the spirit, capturing a large snake several zhang in length, which died outside the door, and the woman then recovered. There was also a large tree, which had a spirit. Anyone who stopped under it would die, and birds flying over it would also fall. The Marquis exposed the tree spirit, causing the tree to wither and fall in midsummer. A large snake, seven or eight zhang long, hung dead in the tree. Emperor Zhang of Han heard about these events and summoned the Marquis to inquire. The Marquis replied, "Yes, such things have occurred." The emperor said, "There have been strange occurrences in the palace, especially after midnight, when several people dressed in red, with loose hair, and carrying torches, would appear. Can you expose them?" The Marquis replied, "These are minor spirits, easy to dispel." The emperor pretended to send three people to test the Marquis. The Marquis then devised a method, and the three people fell to the ground immediately, losing consciousness. The emperor was surprised and said, "They are not spirits, I was testing you." He then had them released. Some say that during the reign of Emperor Wu of Han, there were often strange occurrences in the palace, with several people dressed in red, with loose hair, and carrying candles, walking around. The emperor said to Liu Ping, "Can you get rid of them?" Liu Ping replied, "Yes." He then threw an azure talisman at them, and several ghosts fell to the ground. The emperor was surprised and said, "I was testing you." They were released and revived.

    22

    樊英，隐于壶山。尝有暴风从西南起，英谓学者曰：“成都市火甚盛。”因含水嗽之。乃命计其时日，后有从蜀来者，云：“是日大火，有云从东起，须臾大雨火遂灭。”
    　　闽中有徐登者，女子化为丈夫，与东阳赵昺，并善方术。时遭兵乱，相遇于溪，各矜其所能。登先禁溪水为不流，昺次禁杨柳为生稊。二人相视而笑。登年长，昺师事之。后登身故，昺东入长安，百姓未知，昺乃升茅屋，据鼎而爨。主人惊怪，昺笑而不应，屋亦不损。
    　　赵昺尝临水求渡，船人不许。昺乃张帷盖，坐其中，长啸呼风，乱流而济。于是百姓敬服，从者如归。长安令恶其惑众，收杀之。民为立祠于永康，至今蚊蚋不能入。

    Explanation

    22

    Fan Ying lived in seclusion on Mount Hu. Once, a strong wind suddenly arose from the southwest. Fan Ying told his disciples, "There is a great fire in Chengdu." He then held water in his mouth and spat it out. He ordered them to calculate the time, and later, someone came from Shu who reported, "On that day, there was a huge fire. A cloud rose from the east, and shortly after, it rained heavily, extinguishing the fire."

    In Fujian, there was a woman named Xu Deng who transformed into a man. She met Dongyang Zhao Bing, who was also skilled in magic. During a time of war and chaos, they met by a stream and each boasted about their abilities. Xu Deng first stopped the stream from flowing, and Zhao Bing then made the willows sprout. The two looked at each other and laughed. Xu Deng was older, and Zhao Bing regarded him as a teacher. After Xu Deng's death, Zhao Bing traveled east to Chang'an. The common people did not know about this, and Zhao Bing entered a thatched house, sitting on a tripod to cook. The owner was surprised and amazed, but Zhao Bing smiled and did not respond. The house was not damaged.

    Once, Zhao Bing approached the water to ask for a crossing, but the boatman refused. Zhao Bing then spread a canopy, sat inside, emitted a long sigh to call the wind, and crossed the turbulent stream. The common people respected and admired him, and those who followed him felt like they were returning home. The magistrate of Chang'an disliked that he misled the people and arrested and killed him. The people built a shrine in Yongkang in his memory, and even now, mosquitoes cannot enter.

    23

    徐登、赵昺，贵尚清俭，祀神以东流水，削桑皮以为脯。
    　　陈节访诸神，东海君以织成青襦一领遗之。
    　　宣城边洪，为广阳领校，母丧归家。韩友往投之，时日已暮，出告从者：“速装束，吾当夜去。”从者曰：“今日已暝，数十里草行，何急复去？”友曰：“此间血覆地，宁可复住。”苦留之，不得。其夜，洪欻发狂，绞杀两子，幷杀妇。又斫父婢二人，皆被创，因走亡，数日，乃于宅前林中得之，已自经死。
    　　鞠道龙，善为幻术。尝云：“东海人黄公，善为幻，制蛇，御虎。常佩赤金刀。及衰老，饮酒过度。秦末，有白虎见于东海，诏遣黄公以赤刀往厌之；术既不行，遂为虎所杀。”
    　　谢纠，尝食客，以朱书符投井中，有一双鲤鱼跳出，即命作脍。一坐皆得遍。

    Explanation

    23

    Xu Deng and Zhao Bing esteemed simplicity and frugality. They offered the gods water from the east-flowing river and prepared a type of dried meat by peeling the bark off mulberry trees.

    Chen Jie visited various deities, and the God of the Eastern Sea gave him a blue robe made of woven material.

    Bian Hong from Xuanzhou served as an official in Guangyang. After his mother's death, he returned home. Han You went to visit him, but it was already night. Upon exiting, he told his followers, "Quickly prepare yourselves, I will leave tonight." The followers said, "It is already night, and we have to travel through grasslands over dozens of miles. Why are you in such a hurry to leave?" Han You replied, "Blood covers the ground here. How can I stay?" Despite their efforts to persuade him, he would not stay. That night, Bian Hong suddenly went mad, strangled his two sons, and killed his wife. He also killed two of his father's maids, all of whom were wounded. He then fled away. After several days, he was found in the forest in front of his house, having already hanged himself.

    Ju Daolong was skilled in magical arts. He once said, "A man from the East Sea named Huang Gong was skilled in magic, controlling snakes and taming tigers. He always carried a red gold knife. When he grew old, he drank excessively. At the end of the Qin dynasty, a white tiger appeared in the East Sea. The emperor sent Huang Gong with the red gold knife to subdue it. His magic did not work, and he was killed by the tiger."

    Xie Jiu once had guests. He threw a red ink talisman into a well, and two carp leaped out. He immediately ordered them to be prepared as sashimi. Everyone at the gathering got a taste.

    24

    晋永嘉中，有天竺胡人，来渡江南。其人有数术：能断舌复续，吐火。所在人士聚观。将断时，先以舌吐示宾客，然后刀截，血流覆地，乃取置器中，传以示人，视之舌头，半舌犹在，既而还取含续之。坐有顷，坐人见舌则如故，不知其实断否。其续断，取绢布，与人合执一头，对翦中断之；已而取两断合视，绢布还连续，无异故体。时人多疑以为幻，阴乃试之，真断绢也。其吐火，先有药在器中，取火一片，与黍(食唐)合之，再三吹呼，已而张口，火满口中，因就爇取以炊，则火也。又取书纸及绳缕之属，投火中，众共视之，见其烧爇了尽；乃拨灰中，举而出之，故向物也。
    　　扶南王范寻养虎于山，有犯罪者，投与虎，不噬，乃宥之。故山名大虫，亦名大灵。又养鳄鱼十头，若犯罪者，投与鳄鱼，不噬，乃赦之，无罪者皆不噬。故有鳄鱼池。又尝煮水令沸，以金指环投汤中，然后以手探汤：其直者，手不烂，有罪者，入汤即焦。

    Explanation

    24

    During the Yongjia period of the Jin Dynasty, a person from Tianzhu (ancient India) arrived in the south of the Yangtze River. This person possessed various esoteric skills: he could cut off his tongue and reattach it, and he could breathe fire. People gathered to watch wherever he went. When he was about to cut off his tongue, he first showed his tongue to the audience, then cut it with a knife, causing blood to flow onto the ground. He then took the severed tongue, placed it in a container, and passed it around for the audience to see. The audience saw that half of the tongue was still intact, and then he reattached it by holding it in his mouth. After a short while, the audience saw that his tongue appeared whole again, and they could not tell if it had actually been cut. For the silk trick, he took a piece of silk and asked someone to hold one end while he held the other. He then cut the silk in half, and when he brought the two halves together, the silk was seamlessly reconnected, just as it had been before. Many people doubted that this was an illusion, so they secretly tested it and found that the silk was indeed cut. For the fire-breathing trick, he first placed some medicine in a container, took a piece of fire, mixed it with rice, and blew on it several times. He then opened his mouth, and fire filled his mouth. He used this fire to cook, and it was indeed fire. He also took paper and threads and threw them into the fire. The audience watched as they burned completely, but when he picked them up from the ashes, they were the same as before.

    The king of Funan, Fan Xin, kept tigers in the mountains. If someone committed a crime, they were thrown to the tiger. If the tiger did not attack, the person was pardoned. Therefore, the mountain was called "Dachong" (meaning "tiger") and also "Daling" (meaning "great spirit"). He also kept ten crocodiles. If someone committed a crime, they were thrown to the crocodiles. If the crocodile did not attack, the person was pardoned. If the person was innocent, the crocodile would not attack either. Therefore, there was a crocodile pool. He also once boiled water and placed a golden ring in the boiling water, then dipped his hand into the water. If the person was innocent, his hand would not be burned, but if the person was guilty, his hand would burn immediately.

    25

    戚夫人侍儿贾佩兰，后出为扶风人段儒妻，说：“在宫内时，尝以弦管歌舞相欢娱，竞为妖服以趋良时。十月十五日，共入灵女庙，以豚黍乐神，吹笛，击筑，歌上灵之曲。既而相与连臂踏地为节，歌赤凤皇来，乃巫俗也。至七月七日，临百子池，作于阗乐，乐毕，以五色缕相羁，谓之‘相连绶。’八月四日，出雕房北户，竹下围棋。胜者，终年有福；负者，终年疾病。取丝缕，就北辰星求长命，乃免。九月，佩茱萸，食蓬饵，饮菊花酒，令人长命。菊花舒时，幷采茎叶，杂黍米饟之，至来年九月九日始熟，就饮焉，故谓之‘菊花酒。’正月上辰，出池边盥濯，食蓬饵，以祓妖邪。三月上已，张乐于流水。如此终岁焉。”

    Explanation

    25

    Jia Peilan, the servant girl of Empress Qi, later married Duan Ru of Fufeng and recounted: "When I was in the palace, we often enjoyed music and dance together, competing in wearing exotic costumes to celebrate good times. On the 15th day of the 10th month, we would enter the Temple of the Divine Lady, offering pork and rice to the gods, playing the flute, striking the zither, and singing the songs of the Divine Lady. Then, we would link arms and step on the ground in rhythm, singing the song of the Crimson Phoenix coming, which is a witch's custom. By the 7th day of the 7th month, we would approach the Hundred Sons Pool, performing the music of Yutian. After the music ended, we would tie together with colored threads, calling it 'connected ribbons.' On the 4th day of the 8th month, we would go out through the northern door of the carved house and play Go under the bamboo. The winner would have good fortune all year, while the loser would suffer illness all year. We would take threads and pray to the North Star for a long life, thus avoiding misfortune. In September, we would wear wormwood, eat qiong cakes, and drink chrysanthemum wine, which is said to grant longevity. When chrysanthemums bloom, we would collect their stems and leaves, mixing them with millet and rice. By the next year's 9th day of the 9th month, it would be ready to drink, hence it is called 'chrysanthemum wine.' On the first day of the first month, we would wash at the edge of the pond, eat qiong cakes, and purify away evil spirits. On the 3rd day of the 3rd month, we would set up music by the flowing water. Thus, throughout the year, we engaged in these customs."

    26

    汉武帝时，幸李夫人，夫人卒后，帝思念不已。方士齐人李少翁，言能致其神。乃夜施帷帐，明灯烛，而令帝居他帐遥望之。见美女居帐中，如李夫人之状，还幄坐而步，又不得就视。帝愈益悲感，为作诗曰：“是耶？非耶？立而望之，偏婀娜，何冉冉其来迟！”令乐府诸音家弦歌之。
    　　汉北海营陵有道人，能令人与已死人相见。其同郡人妇死已数年，闻而往见之，曰：“愿令我一见亡妇，死不恨矣。”道人曰：“卿可往见之。若闻鼓声，即出，勿留。”乃语其相见之术。俄而得见之；于是与妇言语，悲喜恩情如生。良久，闻鼓声，恨恨不能得住，当出户时，忽掩其衣裾户间，掣绝而去。至后岁余，此人身亡。家葬之，开冢，见妇棺盖下有衣裾。

    Explanation

    26

    During the reign of Emperor Wu of Han, he favored Lady Li, and after her death, he continued to miss her deeply. A Daoist from the state of Qi named Li Shaoweng claimed he could summon her spirit. At night, he set up curtains and lit candles, and had the emperor observe from a distance. The emperor saw a beautiful woman in the tent, resembling Lady Li, who moved around but could not be fully seen. The emperor became even more sorrowful and wrote a poem: "Is it you? Is it not you? Standing and looking at her, graceful and beautiful, why so slowly does she come?" He ordered the Music Bureau to have musicians sing and play it.

    In the city of Yingling in Beihai, there was a Daoist who could make living people see those who had died. A man from the same region whose wife had died several years ago heard about the Daoist and went to see him. He said, "I wish to see my deceased wife once more, so that I may die without regret." The Daoist replied, "You may go and see her. If you hear the sound of drums, leave immediately, do not linger." He then taught the man how to meet his wife. Soon after, the man saw her; they spoke, and their emotions were as strong as if she were alive. After a long time, he heard the sound of drums, regretfully unable to stay. As he was about to leave, she suddenly caught the hem of her clothes in the door, pulling them apart and departing. A year later, the man died. His family buried him, and when they opened his tomb, they found the hem of his wife's clothes under the coffin lid.

    27

    吴孙休有疾，求觋视者，得一人，欲试之。乃杀鹅而埋于苑中，架小屋，施床几，以妇人屐履服物着其上。使觋视之，告曰：“若能说此冢中鬼妇人形状者，当加厚赏，而即信矣。”竟日无言。帝推问之急，乃曰：“实不见有鬼，但见一白头鹅立墓上，所以不即白之。疑是鬼神变化作此相，当候其真形而定。不复移易，不知何故，敢以实上。”
    　　吴孙峻杀朱主，埋于石子冈。归命即位，将欲改葬之，冢墓相亚，不可识别。而宫人颇识主亡时所着衣服，乃使两巫各住一处，以伺其灵，使察鉴之，不得相近。久时，二人俱白见一女人，年可三十余，上着青锦束头，紫白袷裳，丹绨丝履，从石子冈上半冈，而以手抑膝长太息，小住须臾，更进一冢上，便止，徘徊良久，奄然不见。二人之言，不谋而合。于是开冢，衣服如之。

    Explanation

    27

    During the reign of Wu's Sun Shao, he fell ill and sought a shaman to examine him. He found one and decided to test his abilities. The emperor then had a goose killed and buried in the garden, built a small house, and placed a bed and table inside, dressing a woman's shoes, clothes, and accessories on it. He instructed the shaman to examine it and said, "If you can describe the appearance of the ghostly woman in the tomb, you will receive a generous reward, and I will believe you." The shaman remained silent all day. The emperor pressed him urgently, and he finally said, "I did not see any ghost, but I saw only an old white goose standing on the tomb. That's why I didn't immediately report it. I suspected that it was a transformation of a ghost or deity and waited to see its true form before making a decision. It did not change, and I don't know why, but I dare to report the truth."

    Wu's Sun Jun killed Zhu Zhu and buried her at Shi Zi Gang. After surrendering and ascending the throne, Sun Hao intended to reinter her. The tombs were so close together that they were indistinguishable. But the palace women recognized the clothes Zhu Zhu wore when she died. So he sent two shamans to different places to wait for her spirit, instructing them to observe and discern her spirit without getting too close. After a while, both shamans reported seeing a woman. She was about thirty years old, wearing a green silk cap, purple and white striped skirt, and red silk shoes. She walked halfway up Shi Zi Gang, leaning on her knees and sighing deeply. She paused briefly, then walked to another tomb and stopped. She lingered for a long time, then suddenly disappeared. The shamans' reports matched perfectly. They opened the tomb, and the clothes were as described.

    28

    夏侯弘自云见鬼，与其言语。镇西谢尚所乘马忽死，忧恼甚至。谢曰：“卿若能令此马生者，卿真为见鬼也。”弘去良久，还曰：“庙神乐君马，故取之。今当活。”尚对死马坐，须臾，马忽自门外走还，至马尸间，便灭，应时能动，起行。谢曰：“我无嗣，是我一身之罚。”弘经时无所告。曰：“顷所见，小鬼耳，必不能辨此源由。”后忽逢一鬼，乘新车，从十许人，着青丝布袍。弘前提牛鼻，车中人谓弘曰：“何以见阻？”弘曰：“欲有所问。镇西将军谢尚无儿。此君风流令望，不可使之绝祀。

    Explanation

    28

    Xiahou Hong claimed that he saw ghosts and spoke with them. General Xie Shang of the Western Region's horse suddenly died, causing him great distress. Xie said, "If you can bring this horse back to life, then you truly are able to see ghosts." Xiahou Hong left and returned after a long while, saying, "The temple god took pleasure in your horse, so he took it. It will be revived now." Xie sat opposite the dead horse, and soon, the horse suddenly ran back from the door, passed by the horse's corpse, and disappeared. Immediately, it began to move and stood up, walking. Xie said, "I have no heir, which is a punishment for me alone." Xiahou Hong remained silent for a time. He said, "What I have seen recently are just small ghosts; they certainly cannot explain the source of this." Later, he unexpectedly encountered a ghost riding a new carriage, accompanied by about ten people, wearing a blue silk cloth robe. Xiahou Hong held the cow's nose in front, and the person in the carriage asked him, "Why are you blocking me?" Xiahou Hong said, "I want to ask something. General Xie Shang of the Western Region has no son. This gentleman is a man of elegance and prestige, and it would be unfortunate for his lineage to end."

    29

    ”军中人动容曰：“君所道正是仆儿。年少时，与家中婢通誓约不再婚，而违约；今此婢死，在天诉之，是故无儿。”弘具以告。谢曰：“吾少时诚有此事。”弘于江陵，见一大鬼，提矛戟，有随从小鬼数人。弘畏惧，下路避之。大鬼过后，捉得一小鬼，问：“此何物？”曰：“杀人以此矛戟，若中心腹者，无不辄死。”弘曰：“治此病有方否？”鬼曰：“以乌鸡薄之，即差。”弘曰：“今欲何行？”鬼曰：“当至荆、扬二州尔。”时比日行心腹病，无有不死者，弘乃教人杀乌鸡以薄之，十不失八九。今治中恶辄用乌鸡薄之者，弘之由也。

    Explanation

    29

    The soldiers were moved and said, "What you say is exactly my son. When he was young, he made a pact with a maid in the household not to remarry, but broke it; now that this maid has died, she is accusing him in heaven, which is why he has no children." Huang reported all this. The person apologized and said, "I did indeed have this matter when I was young." Huang saw a big ghost holding a spear and halberd, with several small ghosts following him, in Jiangling. Huang was afraid and stepped off the road to avoid him. After the big ghost passed, Huang caught a small ghost and asked, "What is this thing?" The ghost replied, "This spear and halberd are used to kill people. If they hit the internal organs, no one survives." Huang asked, "Is there a cure for this disease?" The ghost said, "Apply a black chicken to it, and it will heal." Huang asked, "Where are you going now?" The ghost said, "He is going to Jingzhou and Yangzhou." At that time, people were dying from internal organ diseases, and no one survived. Huang then taught people to kill black chickens and use them to treat the disease, and out of ten, nine or eight were cured. Now, whenever someone is treated for internal organ diseases using black chickens, it is because of Huang's method.

    30

    搜神记卷三
    　　汉永平中，会稽钟离意，字子阿，为鲁相。到官，出私钱万三千文，付户曹孔诉，修夫子车。身入庙，拭几席剑履。男子张伯除堂下草，土中得玉璧七枚，伯怀其一，以六枚白意。意令主簿安置几前，孔子教授堂下床首有悬瓮，意召孔诉问：“此何瓮也？”对曰：“夫子瓮也。背有丹书，人莫敢发也，”意曰：“夫子，圣人。所以遗瓮，欲以悬示后贤。”因发之。中得素书，文曰：“后世修吾书，董仲舒。护吾车拭吾履，发吾笥，会稽钟离意。璧有七，张伯藏其一。意即召问：“璧有七，何藏一耶？”伯叩头出之。

    Explanation

    30

    Volume 3 of The Records of Searching for the Supernatural

    During the reign of Emperor Ming of Han, Zhongli Yi of Kuaiji, whose courtesy name was Zi'a, served as the magistrate of Lu. Upon assuming office, he used his own money, thirteen thousand coins, and gave it to Kong Su, the house official, to repair the carriage of the Master. He personally entered the temple and wiped the tables, mats, swords, and shoes. A man named Zhang Bo was clearing grass from the hall when he found seven jade discs buried in the soil. Zhang Bo concealed one of them and presented six to Zhongli Yi. Zhongli Yi ordered the chief clerk to place the six discs before the table. In the hall where Confucius once taught, at the head of the bed, there was a hanging jar. Zhongli Yi summoned Kong Su and asked, "What jar is this?" Kong Su replied, "It is the jar of the Master. There is red writing on the back, and no one dares to open it." Zhongli Yi said, "The Master was a sage. He left this jar in order to show future scholars." He then opened it and found inside a plain scroll, which read: "In later generations, those who repair my books are Dong Zhongshu. Those who protect my carriage, clean my shoes, and open my case are Zhongli Yi of Kuaiji. There are seven jade discs; Zhang Bo concealed one." Zhongli Yi immediately summoned Zhang Bo and asked, "There are seven jade discs; why did you conceal one?" Zhang Bo knelt and confessed, producing the jade disc.

    31

    段医，字符章，广汉新都人也。习易经，明风角。有一生来学。积年，自谓略究要术，辞归乡里。医为合膏药，幷以简书封于筒中，告生曰：“有急，发视之。”生到葭萌，与吏争度津。吏挝破从者头。生开筒得书，言：“到葭萌，与吏斗，头破者，以此膏裹之。”生用其言，创者即愈。
    　　右扶风臧仲英，为侍御史。家人作食，设案，有不清尘土投污之。炊临熟，不知釜处。兵弩自行。火从箧簏中起，衣物尽烧，而箧簏故完。妇女婢使，一旦尽失其镜；数日，从堂下掷庭中，有人声言：“还汝镜。”女孙年三四岁，亡之，求，不知处；两三日，乃于圊中粪下啼。若此非一。汝南许季山者，素善卜卦，卜之，曰：“家当有老青狗物、内中侍御者名益喜，与共为之。诚欲绝，杀此狗，遣益喜归乡里。”仲英从之，怪遂绝。后徙为太尉长史，迁鲁相。

    Explanation

    31

    Duan Yi, courtesy name Yuanzhang, was from Guanghan Xindu. He studied the Yijing (Book of Changes) and mastered divination. One day, a student came to learn from him. After many years, the student believed he had roughly mastered the essential techniques and decided to return to his hometown. Duan Yi prepared a medicinal ointment and sealed a note in a tube, telling the student, "In case of an emergency, open it." When the student arrived at Jiamei, he got into a dispute with an official over crossing the ferry. The official struck and broke the head of one of the student's followers. The student opened the tube and found a message that said, "When you reach Jiamei, if you fight with an official and someone's head is broken, use this ointment to wrap the wound." The student followed the instructions, and the injured person was healed immediately.

    Right Fu Feng's Zang Zhongying served as a Supervisory Censor. One day, while his family was preparing food and setting up tables, some unclear dust fell and contaminated the food. As the cooking neared completion, they couldn't find the pot. Suddenly, the weapons and crossbows moved on their own. A fire started from the chests and boxes, burning all the clothes and belongings, yet the chests and boxes remained intact. One day, all the women and maidservants suddenly lost their mirrors; several days later, the mirrors were thrown from the hall to the courtyard, accompanied by a voice saying, "Return your mirrors." A granddaughter, about three or four years old, went missing, and despite searching, no trace was found. After two or three days, she was found crying near the latrine under the excrement. Such strange occurrences were not isolated. Xu Jishan from Runan, who was skilled in divination, was consulted, and he said, "There must be an old green dog spirit and an inner servant named Yi Xi working together to cause these events. If you truly want to stop them, kill the dog and send Yi Xi back to his hometown." Zang Zhongying followed his advice, and the strange occurrences ceased. Later, he was transferred to the position of Chief Clerk of the Grand Commandant and promoted to the governor of the state of Lu.

    32

    太尉乔玄，字公祖，梁国人也。初为司徒长史，五月末，于中门卧，夜半后，见东壁正白，如开门明。呼问左右。左右莫见。因起自往手扪摸之，壁自如故。还床，复见。心大怖恐。其友应劭，适往候之，语次相告。劭曰。“乡人有董彦兴者，即许季山外孙也。其探赜索隐，穷神知化，虽眭孟，京房，无以过也。然天性褊狭，羞于卜，筮者间来候师。”王叔茂谓往迎之。须臾，便与俱来。公祖虚礼盛馔，下席行觞。彦兴自陈：“下土诸生，无他异分。币重言甘，诚有踧踖。颇能别者，愿得从事。”公祖辞让再三，尔乃听之，曰：“府君当有怪，白光如门明者。然不为害也。六月上旬，鸡明时，闻南家哭，即吉。到秋节，迁北行，郡以金为名。位至将军三公。”公祖曰：“怪异如此，救族不暇，何能致望于所不图？此相饶耳。”至六月九日，未明。太尉杨秉暴薨。七月七日，拜钜鹿太守。“钜”边有金。后为“度辽将军，”历登三事。

    Explanation

    32

    太尉乔玄，字公祖，梁国人也。初为司徒长史，五月末，于中门卧，夜半后，见东壁正白，如开门明。呼问左右。左右莫见。因起自往手扪摸之，壁自如故。还床，复见。心大怖恐。其友应劭，适往候之，语次相告。劭曰：“乡人有董彦兴者，即许季山外孙也。其探赜索隐，穷神知化，虽眭孟，京房，无以过也。然天性褊狭，羞于卜，筮者间来候师。”王叔茂谓往迎之。须臾，便与俱来。公祖虚礼盛馔，下席行觞。彦兴自陈：“下土诸生，无他异分。币重言甘，诚有踧踖。颇能别者，愿得从事。”公祖辞让再三，尔乃听之，曰：“府君当有怪，白光如门明者。然不为害也。六月上旬，鸡明时，闻南家哭，即吉。到秋节，迁北行，郡以金为名。位至将军三公。”公祖曰：“怪异如此，救族不暇，何能致望于所不图？此相饶耳。”至六月九日，未明。太尉杨秉暴薨。七月七日，拜钜鹿太守。“钜”边有金。后为“度辽将军，”历登三事。

    33

    管辂，字公明，平原人也。善易卜。安平太守东莱王基，字伯舆，家数有怪，使辂筮之。卦成，辂曰：“君之卦，当有贱妇人，生一男，堕地，便走入灶中死。又，床上当有一大蛇，衔笔，大小共视，须臾便去。又，乌来入室中，与燕共斗，燕死，乌去。有此三卦。”基大惊曰：“精义之致，乃至于此，幸为占其吉凶。”辂曰：“非有他祸，直客(一作官。)舍久远，魑魅罔两，共为怪耳。儿生便走，非能自走，直宋无忌之妖将其入灶也。大蛇衔笔者，直老书佐耳。乌与燕斗者，直老铃下耳。夫神明之正，非妖能害也。万物之变，非道所止也。久远之浮精，必能之定数也。今卦中见象，而不见其凶，故知假托之数，非妖咎之征，自无所忧也。

    Explanation

    33

    Guan Lu, courtesy name Gongming, was a man from the region of Pingyuan. He was skilled in divination using the Yi Jing. Wang Ji, courtesy name Boyu, was the governor of Anping and from Donglai. His household frequently experienced strange occurrences, so he sent Guan Lu to cast the Yi Jing for him. After the hexagram was cast, Guan Lu said, "Your hexagram indicates that there will be a lowly woman who gives birth to a boy. The child will fall to the ground and immediately walk into the stove and die. Additionally, there will be a large snake on the bed, holding a pen, and everyone will watch, and it will leave shortly. Also, a crow will enter the room and fight with a swallow, the swallow will die, and the crow will leave. These are the three signs." Wang Ji was greatly surprised and said, "The profound meaning of your divination reaches such a level. Please interpret whether these signs are auspicious or ominous." Guan Lu replied, "There is no other misfortune. It is only because the guesthouse has been long unused, and the spirits of chimui and wangling have caused these strange occurrences. The child walking is not due to its own ability, but it is the demon of Song Wuji leading it into the stove. The snake holding the pen is actually the ghost of an old clerk. The crow fighting with the swallow is the ghost of an old bell-ringer. The true nature of the spirits cannot be harmed by demons. The changes in all things are not stopped by the way. The floating spirits of long ago will inevitably follow a certain fate. In your hexagram, the signs are visible, but there is no indication of misfortune. Therefore, I know these are false signs and not omens of disaster. There is nothing to worry about."

    34

    昔高宗之鼎，非雉所雊；太戊之阶，非桑所生。然而野鸟一雊，武丁为高宗；桑谷暂生，太戊以兴焉。知三事不为吉祥，愿府君安身养德，从容光大，勿以神奸，污累天真。”后卒无他。迁安南督军后，辂乡里乃太原，问辂：“君往者为王府君论怪云：‘老书佐为蛇，老铃下为乌，’此本皆人。何化之微贱乎？为见于爻象出君意乎？”辂言：“苟非性与天道，何由背爻象而任心胸者乎？夫万物之化，无有常形；人之变异，无有定体。或大为小，或小为大，固无优劣。万物之化，一例之道也。是以夏鲧天子之父，赵王如意，汉高之子，而鲧为黄熊，意为苍狗，斯亦至尊之位，而为黔喙之类也。况蛇者协辰巳之位，乌者栖太阳之精，此乃腾黑之明象，白日之流景。如书佐、铃下，各以微躯，化为蛇乌，不亦过乎。”

    Explanation

    34

    In the past, the cauldron of King Gaozong was not a place for a wild chicken to crow; the steps of King Taiwu were not a place for a mulberry tree to grow. However, when a wild bird crowed once, Wu Ding became a sage king; when mulberry and grain grew temporarily, King Taiwu revived. Knowing that these three events were not auspicious, I wish the governor to maintain his integrity and moral character, act with dignity and grandeur, and not be tainted by supernatural deceptions. Later, nothing else happened. After the governor was relocated to Annan, Lu's hometown was in Taiyuan. Lu asked, "You previously discussed strange occurrences with the governor, saying, 'An old clerk turned into a snake, and an old bell-ringer turned into a crow.' These were originally human beings. Why did they transform into such lowly forms? Were these transformations predicted by the hexagrams or was it your own interpretation?" Lu replied, "Unless one understands the nature and the way of heaven, how can one go against the hexagrams and rely on personal judgment? The transformation of all things does not have a fixed form; human transformations do not have a definite form. Sometimes large things become small, and small things become large; there is no inherent superiority or inferiority. The transformation of all things is a universal principle. Therefore, the father of the Shang Dynasty founder, Gun, the son of the Han Dynasty founder, Liu Ruyi, and the founder of the Han Dynasty, Liu Bang, turned into a yellow bear and a gray dog, respectively. These were once the highest positions but now they are among the lowly. Moreover, snakes are associated with the positions of the earth and fire, and crows are associated with the sun. These are clear symbols of darkness and the flow of the sun. For a clerk and a bell-ringer to transform into a snake and a crow, respectively, is excessive."

    35

    管辂至平原，见颜超貌主夭亡。颜父乃求辂延命。辂曰：“子归，觅清酒鹿脯一斤，卯日，刈麦地南大桑树下，有二人围位，次但酌酒置脯，饮尽更斟，以尽为度。若问汝，汝但拜之，勿言。必合有人救汝。”颜依言而往，果见二人围碁，频置脯，斟酒于前。其人贪戏，但饮酒食脯。不顾数巡，北边坐者忽见颜在，叱曰：“何故在此？”颜惟拜之。南面坐者语曰：“适来饮他酒脯，宁无情乎？”北坐者曰：“文书已定。”南坐者曰：“借文书看之。”见超寿止可十九岁，乃取笔挑上语曰：“救汝至九十年活。”颜拜而回。管语颜曰：“大助子，且喜得增寿。北边坐人是北斗，南边坐人是南斗。南斗注生，北斗主死。凡人受胎，皆从南斗过北斗；所有祈求，皆向北斗。”

    Explanation

    35

    Guan Lu arrived at Pian and saw Yan Chao, whose appearance indicated he would die young. Yan's father then asked Guan Lu to extend his life. Guan Lu said, "Go back and get a pound of clear wine and deer meat. On the day of the rabbit, go to the south side of the wheat field under a large mulberry tree, where two people are playing chess. Then just pour the wine and place the meat in front of them, drink it all and refill, stopping when it is finished. If they ask you, just bow to them and do not speak. There will certainly be someone to save you." Yan followed his instructions and went there, and indeed he saw two people playing chess, frequently placing meat and pouring wine in front of them. The person playing chess was greedy and only drank and ate the meat. After several rounds, the person sitting on the north side suddenly saw Yan there and shouted, "Why are you here?" Yan only bowed to him. The person sitting on the south side said, "Just now, we drank his wine and ate his meat; how could we be无情 (without feeling)?" The person sitting on the north side said, "The documents are already determined." The person sitting on the south side said, "Let me see the documents." They saw that Yan Chao's lifespan was only nineteen years, so they took a pen and wrote, "Save him to live until ninety years old." Yan bowed and returned. Guan Lu told Yan, "Great help, now you will gain additional years of life. The person sitting on the north side is the North Star (Big Dipper), and the person sitting on the south side is the South Star (Southern Dipper). The South Star records births, and the North Star governs deaths. All people are conceived and pass through the South Star and then the North Star; all requests are directed to the North Star."

    36

    信都令家妇女惊恐，更互疾的。使辂筮之。辂曰：“君北堂西头有两死男子：一男持矛，一男持弓箭。头在壁内，脚在壁外。持矛者主刺头，故头重痛不得举也；持弓箭者主射胸腹，故心中悬痛不得饮食也。昼则浮游，夜来病人，故使惊恐也。”于是掘其室中，入地八尺，果得二棺：一棺中有矛；一棺中有角弓及箭，箭久远，木皆消烂，但有铁及角完耳。乃徙骸骨去城二十里埋之，无复疾病。
    　　利漕民郭恩，字义博，兄弟三人，皆得躄疾。使辂筮其所由。辂曰：“卦中有君本墓，墓中有女鬼，非君伯母，当叔母也。昔饥荒之世，当有利其数升米者，排着井中，啧啧有声，推一大石下，破其头，孤魂冤痛，自诉于天耳。”

    Explanation

    36

    The women of the magistrate of Xindu were terrified, suffering alternately from illness. They asked Zuo to divinate the cause. Zuo said, "There are two dead men in the northwest corner of your hall: one man holds a spear, and the other holds a bow and arrow. Their heads are inside the wall, and their feet are outside. The man with the spear is responsible for stabbing the head, hence the severe headache; the man with the bow and arrow is responsible for shooting the chest and abdomen, hence the pain in the heart and inability to eat. They wander during the day and come to haunt the sick at night, causing fear." They then dug into the room, going down eight feet, and indeed found two coffins: one coffin contained a spear; the other contained a horn bow and arrows, which had been there for a long time and were mostly decayed, but the iron and horn were still intact. They moved the bones twenty miles away from the city and buried them, and there was no more illness.

    Guo En, a resident of Licao, whose courtesy name was Yibo, and his three brothers all suffered from a leg disease. They asked Zuo to divinate the cause of the illness. Zuo said, "There is your ancestral tomb in the hexagram, and there is a female ghost in the tomb. It is not your paternal grandmother but your maternal aunt. In times of famine, someone must have taken several handfuls of rice, pushed it into the well, making a sound, and then pushed a large stone down, breaking her head. The lonely spirit is in pain and has appealed to heaven."

    37

    淳于智，字叔平，济北庐人也。性深沈，有思义。少为书生，能易筮，善厌胜之术。高平刘柔，夜卧，鼠啮其左手中指，意甚恶之。以问智。智为筮之，曰：“鼠本欲杀君而不能，当为使其反死。”乃以朱书手腕横文后三寸，为田字，可方一寸二分，使夜露手以卧。有大鼠伏死于前。
    　　上党鲍瑗家多丧病贫苦，淳于智卜之，曰：“君居宅不利，故令君困尔。君舍东北有大桑树。君径至市，入门数十步，当有一人卖新鞭者，便就买还，以悬此树。三年，当暴得财。”瑗承言诣市，果得马鞭悬之。三年，浚井，得钱数十万，铜铁器复二万余，于是业用既展，病者亦无恙。
    　　谯人夏侯藻，母病困，将诣智卜，忽有一狐当门向之嗥叫。藻大愕惧。遂驰诣智。智曰：“其祸甚急。君速归，在狐嗥处，拊心啼哭，令家人惊怪，大小毕出，一人不出，啼哭勿休。然其祸仅可免也。”藻还如其言，母亦扶病而出。家人既集，堂屋五间拉然而崩。

    Explanation

    37

    Chunyu Zhi, courtesy name Shuping, was from Jibei Lu. He was profound and reserved in character, thoughtful and righteous. When young, he was a scholar who could perform divination using the I Ching and was skilled in counter-charms. A man from Gaoqing named Liu Rou, while sleeping at night, was bitten by a mouse on his left middle finger, which he found very unpleasant. He consulted Chunyu Zhi about it. Chunyu Zhi divined and said, "The mouse originally intended to kill you but could not, and will make it die in return." He then instructed Liu to write the character '田' (field) with red ink on his wrist, three inches behind the wrist crease, about one inch and two parts square, and to expose his hand at night while sleeping. A large mouse died at his feet.

    In Shangdang, there was a man named Bao Yuan whose family suffered many deaths, illnesses, and poverty. Chunyu Zhi divined for him and said, "Your dwelling is inauspicious, which is why you are in distress. Your house has a large mulberry tree to the northeast. Go directly to the market, enter and walk dozens of steps, and there will be someone selling new whips. Buy them and return, hanging them on this tree. In three years, you will suddenly gain wealth." Bao Yuan followed the advice and went to the market, indeed finding new whips and hanging them. In three years, when he dug a well, he found tens of thousands of coins and over twenty thousand copper and iron items. His businesses were expanded, and the sick recovered.

    A man from Qiao named Xiahou Zao, whose mother was ill and weak, intended to consult with Chunyu Zhi. Suddenly, a fox appeared at the door, facing him and howling. Xiahou Zao was greatly startled and fearful. He then rushed to consult with Chunyu Zhi. Chunyu Zhi said, "The disaster is very urgent. You must return quickly, where the fox howled. Clutch your chest and cry, making your family surprised and alarmed. Everyone must come out; if one person does not come out, do not stop crying. But the disaster can be avoided." Xiahou Zao returned as instructed, and his mother also came out despite being ill. When the family gathered, the five rooms of the main hall collapsed suddenly.

    38

    护军张劭母病笃。智筮之，使西出市沐猴系母臂。令傍人搥拍，恒使作声，三日放去。劭从之，其猴出门，即为犬所咋死，母病遂差。
    　　郭璞，字景纯，行至庐江，劝太守胡孟康急回南渡。康不从，璞将促装去之，爱其婢，无由得，乃取小豆三斗，绕主人宅散之。主人晨起，见赤衣人数千围其家，就视，则灭。甚恶之，请璞为卦。璞曰：“君家不宜畜此婢，可于东南二十里卖之，慎勿争价，则此妖可除也。”璞阴令人贱买此婢，复为投符于井中，数千赤衣人一一自投于井。主人大悦。璞携婢去，后数旬，而庐江陷。
    　　赵固所乘马忽死，甚悲惜之，以问郭璞。璞曰：“可遣数十人持竹竿，东行三十里，有山林陵树，便搅打之。当有一物出，急宜持归。”于是如言，果得一物，似猿。持归，入门，见死马，跳梁走往死马头，嘘吸其鼻。顷之，马即能起。奋迅嘶鸣，饮食如常。亦不复见向物。固奇之，厚加资给。

    Explanation

    38

    The Commandant Zhang Shao's mother was gravely ill. With wisdom, he divined the situation and instructed someone to go west to the market to buy a monkey and tie it to his mother's arm. He ordered others to beat and make noise, always making it move, and to release it after three days. Zhang Shao followed his instructions. When the monkey went out, it was immediately killed by a dog, and his mother's illness then improved.

    Guo Pu, courtesy name Jingchun, traveled to Lujiang and advised the governor Hu Mengkang to urgently retreat south. Hu did not listen, so Guo prepared to leave quickly. He loved one of the governor's maids but could not obtain her. Therefore, he took three dou of small beans and spread them around the governor's house. The next morning, the governor saw thousands of red-clad figures surrounding his home. Upon looking at them, they disappeared. He greatly disliked this and asked Guo to cast a divination. Guo said, "Your household should not keep this maid. Sell her twenty li to the southeast, and be careful not to haggle over the price. Then this demon can be dispelled." Guo secretly had someone buy the maid at a low price and threw a talisman into the well. Thousands of red-clad figures one by one jumped into the well. The governor was very pleased. Guo took the maid away, and after several weeks, Lujiang fell.

    Zhao Gu's horse suddenly died, and he was very sad and regretful. He asked Guo Pu about it. Guo said, "Send dozens of people with bamboo poles to travel east for thirty li. There will be mountains, forests, and trees. Stir and beat them. An object will appear, and you should quickly bring it back." Following his advice, they indeed found an object that resembled a monkey. They brought it back, entered the house, and saw the dead horse. The monkey jumped and ran to the dead horse's head, blowing and sucking its nose. Soon, the horse could stand up. It struggled and neighed, eating and drinking as usual. The previous object was no longer seen. Zhao Gu found it strange and provided generous support.

    39

    扬州别驾顾球姊，生十年，便病，至年五十余，令郭璞筮，得大过之升。其辞曰：“大过卦者义不嘉。冢墓枯杨无英华。振动游魂见龙车。身被重累婴妖邪。法由斩祀杀灵蛇。非己之咎先人瑕。案卦论之可奈何。”球乃迹访其家事，先世曾伐大树，得大蛇，杀之，女便病。病后，有群鸟数千，回翔屋上，人皆怪之，不知何故，有县农行过舍边，仰视，见龙牵车，五色晃烂，其大非常，有顷遂灭。
    　　义兴方叔保得伤寒，垂死，令璞占之，不吉，令求白牛厌之。求之不得，唯羊子玄有一白牛，不肯借。璞为致之，即日有大白牛从西来，径往临，叔保惊惶、病即愈。

    Explanation

    39

    Yangzhou Deputy Magistrate Guo Qiu's elder sister fell ill shortly after her tenth birthday, and she remained sick for over fifty years. When she reached that age, she had Guo Pu perform a divination, which yielded the hexagram "Great Exceeding" with a changing line to "Ascending." The divination text read: "The Great Exceeding hexagram signifies an unfavorable meaning. The graves and tombstones are like withered poplars without blossoms. The wandering spirits are agitated, and a dragon carriage is seen. The body is burdened with heavy misfortune and entangled with evil spirits. The law is due to the cutting of sacrifices and the killing of a sacred snake. It is not one's own fault but a blemish of the ancestors. According to the hexagram, it can be interpreted as such."

    Guo Qiu then investigated the family's history and discovered that their ancestors had once cut down a large tree and killed a sacred snake, which led to his sister's illness. After her illness began, thousands of birds would circle her house, and people found this strange. One day, a county farmer passing by saw a dragon pulling a carriage, its colors dazzling and its size extraordinary, but it soon disappeared.

    In another instance, Fang Shubao from Yixing contracted a severe fever and was on the verge of death. He asked Guo Pu to divine his fate, and the result was unfavorable. Fang was advised to seek a white ox to ward off evil. However, he could not find one, but only Yang Zixuan had a white ox, who refused to lend it. Guo Pu arranged for the white ox to be brought, and on that very day, a large white ox came from the west and directly came to visit Fang. Fang was startled, and his illness immediately subsided.

    40

    西川费孝先善轨革，世皆知名，有大若人王旻，因货殖至成都，求为卦。孝先曰：“教住莫住，教洗莫洗。一石谷捣得三斗米。遇明即活，遇暗即死。”再三戒之，令诵此言足矣。旻志之。及行，途中遇大雨，憩一屋下，路人盈塞，乃思曰：“教住莫住，得非此耶？”遂冒雨行，未几，屋遂颠覆，独得免焉。旻之妻已私邻比，欲媾终身之好，俟旋归，将致毒谋。旻既至，妻约其私人曰：“今夕新沐者，乃夫也。”将哺，呼旻洗沐，重易巾幯。旻悟曰：“教洗莫洗，得非此耶？”坚不从。妻怒，不省，自沐。夜半反被害。既觉，惊呼邻里共视，皆莫测其由。遂被囚系考讯。狱就，不能自辨。郡守录状，旻泣言死即死矣，但孝先所言，终无验耳。左右以是语上达。郡守命未得行法乎旻。问曰：“汝邻比何人也？”曰：“康七。”遂遣人捕之。“杀汝妻者，必此人也。”已而果然。因谓僚佐曰：“一石谷捣得三斗米，非康七乎。”由是辨雪，诚遇明即活之效。

    Explanation

    40

    In the Western Region of Sichuan, there was a man named Fei Xiaoxian who was renowned for his skills in divination and fortune-telling. A wealthy merchant named Wang Min, who had traveled to Chengdu for trade, sought a reading from Fei. Fei said, "Do not stay where you are told to stay, and do not wash where you are told not to wash. A stone of grain can be ground into three dou of rice. It will thrive in light and perish in darkness." He warned Wang repeatedly, instructing him to memorize these words. Wang took note of them. As he was about to leave, it began to rain heavily, and he took shelter under a roof. The path was crowded with travelers. Reflecting, Wang thought, "Do not stay where you are told to stay, is this not what he meant?" He decided to brave the rain and continue his journey. Soon after, the roof collapsed, but he alone escaped unharmed. Wang's wife had already conspired with a neighbor to forge a lifelong alliance, and upon his return, she planned to poison him.
