When Wang arrived, his wife told her accomplice, "Tonight, the one who has just bathed is my husband." As they prepared to eat, she called Wang to bathe and change his headwear. Wang realized, "Do not wash where you are told not to wash, is this not what he meant?" He firmly refused. His wife became angry and, ignoring his refusal, bathed herself. That night, she was killed. When Wang awoke, he called out to his neighbors, who gathered to see what had happened. None of them could understand why she had been killed. Wang was then arrested and subjected to interrogation. The case was concluded, but he could not defend himself. The local magistrate recorded the case, and Wang wept, saying, "If I am to die, I will die, but Fei's words have ultimately proven to be false." The officials reported this to a higher authority. The magistrate had not yet decided on a punishment for Wang. He asked, "Who is your neighbor?" Wang replied, "Kang Qi." The magistrate then sent someone to arrest Kang Qi. "The killer of your wife must be this person." And indeed, it was. The magistrate then told his subordinates, "A stone of grain can be ground into three dou of rice, is this not Kang Qi?" Thus, the case was clarified, and the truth of the earlier warning about light and darkness was revealed.

    41

    隗照，汝阴鸿寿亭民也。善易，临终，书板授其妻曰：“吾亡后，当大荒。虽尔，而慎莫卖宅也。到后五年春，当有诏使，来顿此亭，姓龚，此人负吾金，即以此板往责之。勿负言也。”亡后，果大困，欲卖宅者数矣，忆夫言，辄止。至期，有龚使者，果止亭中，妻遂赉板责之。使者执板，不知所言，曰：“我平生不负钱，此何缘尔邪？”妻曰：“夫临亡，手书板见命如此，不敢妄也。”使者沈吟良久而悟，乃命取蓍筮之卦成，抵掌叹曰：“妙哉隗生！含明隐迹，而莫之闻。可谓镜穷达而洞吉凶者也。”于是告其妻曰：“吾不负金，贤夫自有金。乃知亡后当暂穷，故藏金以待太平。所以不告儿妇者，恐金尽而困无已也。知吾善易，故书板以寄意耳。金五百斤，盛以青罂，覆以铜柈，埋在堂屋东头，去地一丈，入地九尺。”妻还掘之，果得金，皆如所卜。

    Explanation

    41

    Wei Zhao, a resident of Hongshou Pavilion in Ruyin, was skilled in the Yi Jing (Book of Changes). On his deathbed, he wrote on a wooden tablet and gave it to his wife, saying: "After my death, there will be a great famine. Even then, do not sell the house. In the spring of the fifth year after my death, there will be an imperial envoy who will stay at this pavilion. His surname is Gong, and he owes me money. Use this tablet to demand repayment from him. Do not fail in your promise." After his death, she indeed became very poor and wanted to sell the house many times, but remembering her husband's words, she would stop. On the appointed day, there was indeed an envoy surnamed Gong who stayed at the pavilion. The wife then took the tablet to demand repayment. The envoy held the tablet, not knowing what to say, and said, "I have never owed anyone money. Why would this be so?" The wife replied, "My husband, on his deathbed, wrote these instructions for me by hand and told me not to lie. I dare not deceive you." The envoy pondered for a long time and then realized, ordering to take out the yarrow stalks for divination. The divination was complete, and he clapped his hands and sighed, saying, "How wise was Master Wei! He hid his brilliance and his presence, and no one knew about it. He was like a mirror reflecting both prosperity and adversity, and one who could foresee good and bad omens." He then told his wife, "I do not owe any money. My virtuous husband had hidden gold. It is known that after my death, there will be a temporary period of poverty, so he hid the gold to wait for better times. The reason I did not tell my children and grandchildren was because I feared that if the gold ran out, the poverty would continue indefinitely. Knowing that I was skilled in the Yi Jing, he used this tablet to convey his intentions. There are five hundred pounds of gold, stored in a blue jar, covered with a copper plate, buried in the eastern part of the main hall, one zhang below the ground, and nine chi into the ground." The wife returned and dug it up, and indeed found the gold, just as predicted.

    42

    韩友，字景先，庐江舒人也。善占卜，亦行京房厌胜之术。刘世则女病魅，积年，巫为攻祷，伐空冢故城间，得狸鼍数十，病犹不差。友筮之，命作布囊，俟女发时，张囊着窗牖间。友闭户作气，若有所驱。须臾间，见囊大胀如吹。因决败之。女仍大发。友乃更作皮囊二枚沓张之，施张如前，囊复胀满，因急缚囊口，悬着树，二十许日，渐消。开视，有二斤狐毛。女病遂差。
    　　会稽严卿善卜筮。乡人魏序欲东行，荒年，多抄盗，令卿筮之。卿曰：“君慎不可东行。必遭暴害。而非劫也。”序不信。卿曰：“既必不停，宜有以禳之。可索西郭外独母家白雄狗，系着船前。”求索，止得驳狗，无白者。卿曰：“驳者亦足。然犹恨其色不纯。当余小毒，止及六畜辈耳。无所复忧。”序行半路，狗忽然作声，甚急，有如人打之者。比视，已死，吐黑血斗余。其夕，序墅上白鹅数头，无故自死。序家无恙。

    Explanation

    42

    Han You, courtesy name Jingxian, was from Shu in Lujiang. He was skilled in divination and also practiced the method of suppressing evil spirits as taught by Jing Fang. Liu Shize's daughter was afflicted by a spirit, and for many years, witches performed rituals to exorcise the spirit, searching in the vicinity of abandoned tombs and old cities, and found dozens of weasels and alligators, but her illness still did not improve. Han You consulted the oracle, ordered a cloth bag to be made, and instructed to place it between the window and door when the girl's illness flared up. Han You closed the door and made a sound, as if driving away something. After a short while, he saw the bag swell up like it had been inflated. He then tore it open. The girl's illness flared up again. Han You then made two more leather bags and placed them one on top of the other, arranged as before. The bag swelled up again, so he quickly tied the mouth of the bag and hung it on a tree. After about twenty days, it gradually diminished. When he opened it to see, there were two pounds of fox fur. The girl's illness was then cured.

    Yan Qing from Kuaiji was skilled in divination. A villager named Wei Xu wanted to travel east. It was a year of famine, and there were many bandits. He asked Yan Qing to consult the oracle. Yan Qing said, "You should be very careful not to travel east. You will surely encounter sudden harm, but it will not be a robbery." Wei Xu did not believe him. Yan Qing said, "If you must go, you should have a way to ward off the danger. You can look for a white male dog from the home of a single mother outside the western gate of the city and tie it to the front of your boat." Wei Xu searched but only found a mottled dog, not a white one. Yan Qing said, "Even a mottled one is sufficient. However, I regret that the color is not pure. It will only cause minor harm, affecting only domestic animals. You no longer need to worry." Wei Xu traveled halfway when the dog suddenly made a loud noise, as if it had been struck by someone. By the time he looked, the dog was already dead, having vomited out over a dou of black blood. That night, several white geese on Wei Xu's estate died without reason. Wei Xu's family was safe.

    43

    沛国华佗，字符化，一名敷。琅邪刘勋，为河内太守，有女，年几二十，苦脚左膝有有疮，痒而不痛，疮愈数十日复发，如此七八年。迎佗使视。佗曰：“是易治之。”当得稻糠，黄色犬一头，好马二匹。以绳系犬颈，使走马牵犬，马极，辄易，计马走三十余里，犬不能行，复令步人拖曳，计向五十里，乃以药饮女。女即安卧不知人，因取大刀断犬腹，近后脚之前，以所断之处向疮口，令二三寸，停之须臾，有若蛇者，从疮中出。便以铁椎横贯蛇头，蛇在皮中动摇良久，须臾，不动，乃牵出，长三尺许，纯是蛇，但有眼处而无童子，又逆麟耳。以膏散着疮中，七日愈。
    　　佗尝行道，见一人病咽，嗜食不得下，家人车载，欲往就医。佗闻其呻吟声，驻车往视语之曰：“向来道边，有卖饼家蒜虀大酢，从取三升饮之，病自当去。”即如佗言，立吐蛇一枚。

    Explanation

    43

    Hua Tuo, a renowned physician from Pei, had the courtesy name Yuanhua and was also known as Fu. Liu Xun from Langya served as the governor of Hedong and had a daughter who was nearly twenty years old. She suffered from an itchy but painless ulcer on her left knee, which would heal after several days but recur after about ten days, repeating this cycle for seven or eight years. They invited Hua Tuo to examine her. Hua Tuo said, "This is easily treatable." He required rice husks, a yellow dog, and two good horses. He tied a rope around the dog's neck and had the horses pull the dog, changing the horses when they became exhausted. After the horses had traveled over thirty miles, the dog could no longer walk, so they had people drag it by hand, covering a distance of nearly fifty miles. Then, Hua Tuo gave the woman medicine to drink. She immediately fell into a deep sleep, unaware of her surroundings. Hua Tuo then took a large knife and cut open the dog's belly near the front of its hind legs, positioning the cut over the woman's wound, leaving a gap of two or three inches. After a short while, a snake-like creature emerged from the wound. Hua Tuo struck the snake's head with an iron mallet, causing it to move violently within the skin for a long time. After a moment, it stopped moving, and he pulled it out. The snake was about three feet long, entirely a snake, but it had eyes without pupils and backward-pointing scales. Hua Tuo applied ointment to the wound, and it healed in seven days.

    Once, while traveling, Hua Tuo encountered a man suffering from a throat condition, unable to swallow food. His family carried him in a cart to seek medical help. Hua Tuo heard his groans and stopped to examine him. He told the man, "There is a vendor selling garlic paste and vinegar by the roadside. Take three liters and drink it, and your illness will go away." The man followed Hua Tuo's advice and immediately vomited up a snake.

    44

    搜神记卷四
    　　风伯，雨师，星也。风伯者，箕星也。雨师者，毕星也。郑玄谓：司中、司命，文星第四，第五星也。雨师：一曰屏翳，一曰号屏，一曰玄冥。
    　　蜀郡张宽，字叔文，汉武帝时为侍中。从祀甘泉，至渭桥，有女子浴于渭水，乳长七尺。上怪其异，遣问之。女曰：“帝后第七车者知我。”所来时，宽在第七车。对曰：“天星。主祭祀者，斋戒不洁，则女人见。”
    　　文王以太公望为灌坛令，期年，风不鸣条。文王梦一妇人，甚丽，当道而哭。问其故。曰：“吾泰山之女，嫁为东海妇，欲归，今为灌坛令当道有德，废我行；我行，必有大风疾雨，大风疾雨，是毁其德也。”文王觉，召太公问之。是日果有疾雨暴风，从太公邑外而过。文王乃拜太公为大司马。

    Explanation

    44

    Translation

    The Search for the Supernatural, Volume Four

    The Wind Lord and the Rain Lord are stars. The Wind Lord is the star Jī (箕), and the Rain Lord is the star Bì (畢). Zheng Xuan said that the Lord of the Center and the Lord of Fate are the fourth and fifth stars of the constellation Wén (文). The Rain Lord is also known as Píngyì (屏翳), Hào Píng (號屏), and Xuánmíng (玄冥).

    Zhang Kuān of Shu Commandery, courtesy name Shūwén, served as a Grand Attendant during the reign of Emperor Wu of Han. On a visit to the Temple of Heaven at Gānquán, they reached the Wei Bridge, where a woman was bathing in the Wei River. Her breasts were seven chi long. The emperor found this unusual and sent someone to inquire about her. She said, "The person in the seventh carriage behind the emperor knows me." At that time, Zhang Kuān was in the seventh carriage. He replied, "She is a celestial star. If the person in charge of the sacrifice does not maintain purity and cleanliness, a woman will appear."

    King Wen appointed Tai Gong Wàng as the magistrate of Guantán. After one year, the wind did not rustle the leaves. King Wen dreamed of a beautiful woman who was weeping on the road. He asked her why she was crying. She said, "I am the daughter of Mount Tai, married to a man in the East Sea. I wish to return home, but the magistrate of Guantán, who has great virtue, is blocking my path. If I pass, there will be a great wind and heavy rain, which will damage his virtue." King Wen woke up and summoned Tai Gong Wàng to ask him about it. That day, there was indeed a sudden heavy rain and strong wind, which passed over Tai Gong Wàng's town. King Wen then appointed Tai Gong Wàng as the Grand Marshal.

    45

    胡母班，字季友，泰山人也。曾至泰山之侧，忽于树间，逢一绛衣驺呼班云：“泰山府君召。”班惊楞，逡巡未答。复有一驺出，呼之。遂随行数十步，驺请班暂瞑，少顷，便见宫室，威仪甚严。班乃入阁拜谒，主为设食，语班曰：“欲见君，无他，欲附书与女婿耳。”班问：“女郎何在？”曰：“女为河伯妇。”班曰：“辄当奉书，不知缘何得达？”答曰：“今适河中流，便扣舟呼青衣，当自有取书者。”班乃辞出。昔驺复令闭目，有顷，忽如故道。遂西行，如神言而呼青衣。须臾，果有一女仆出，取书而没。少顷，复出。云：“河伯欲暂见君。”婢亦请瞑目。遂拜谒河伯。河伯乃大设酒食，词旨殷勤。临去，谓班曰：“感君远为致书，无物相奉。”于是命左右：“取吾青丝履来！”以贻班。班出，瞑然忽得还舟。遂于长安经年而还。至泰山侧，不敢潜过，遂扣树自称姓名，从长安还，欲启消息。

    Explanation

    45

    Hu Mu Ban, courtesy name Ji You, was from Tai Shan. Once, while near the side of Mount Tai, he suddenly encountered a red-clothed horseman in the trees who called out to him, saying, "The deity of Mount Tai summons you." Hu Mu Ban was startled and hesitated before responding. Another horseman then emerged and called to him. He followed them for several dozen steps, and the horseman asked him to close his eyes briefly. Soon, he saw a grand palace with strict etiquette. Hu Mu Ban then entered the palace to pay respects, and the deity served him food. The deity said to him, "I wish to see you, not for any other reason, but to send a letter to my son-in-law." Hu Mu Ban asked, "Where is the lady?" The deity replied, "She is the wife of the river god." Hu Mu Ban then traveled westward, as instructed by the deity, and called out for a servant in green clothes. Soon, a female servant appeared, took the letter, and disappeared. Shortly after, she reappeared and said, "The river god wishes to briefly see you." The servant also asked him to close his eyes. Hu Mu Ban then paid respects to the river god, who prepared a grand feast and spoke kindly. Before leaving, the river god said to Hu Mu Ban, "I am grateful for your journey to deliver this letter, and I have no other gift to offer." He then ordered his attendants to bring his green silk shoes, which he gave to Hu Mu Ban. Hu Mu Ban then opened his eyes and suddenly found himself back on the boat. He spent a year in Chang An before returning. Upon reaching the side of Mount Tai, he did not dare to pass by unnoticed, so he knocked on a tree and introduced himself by name, having returned from Chang An, and wished to report his experiences.

    46

    须臾，昔驺出，引班如向法而进。因致书焉。府君请曰：“当别。”再报班，语讫，如厕，忽见其父着械徒，作此辈数百人。班进拜流涕问：“大人何因及此？”父云：“吾死不幸，见遣三年，今已二年矣。困苦不可处。知汝今为明府所识，可为吾陈之。乞免此役。便欲得社公耳。”班乃依教，叩头陈乞。府君曰：“生死异路，不可相近，身无所惜。”班苦请，方许之。于是辞出，还家。岁余，儿子死亡略尽。班惶惧，复诣泰山，扣树求见。昔驺遂迎之而见。班乃自说：“昔辞旷拙，及还家，儿死亡至尽。今恐祸故未已，辄来启白，幸蒙哀救。”府君拊掌大笑曰：“昔语君：死生异路，不可相近故也。”即敕外召班父。须臾至，庭中问之：“昔求还里社，当为门户作福，而孙息死亡至尽，何也？”答云：“久别乡里，自忻得还，又遇酒食充足，实念诸孙，召之。”于是代之。父涕泣而出。班遂还。后有儿皆无恙。

    Explanation

    46

    A short while later, the former attendant appeared, leading 班 according to the proper procedure. He then delivered a letter. The official requested, "We should part." He reported to 班 again, finished speaking, and went to the toilet. Suddenly, he saw his father wearing chains and being a prisoner, along with hundreds of people like him. 班 approached, bowed, and wept, asking, "Why have you come to this situation, father?" His father replied, "Unfortunate, I died and was sent to the underworld for three years. Now it has been two years. The hardships are unbearable. Knowing that you are recognized by the official, you can present my request. I beg to be exempted from this labor. I merely wish to obtain the village god." 班 followed the instruction and bowed deeply to present his request. The official said, "Life and death are different paths and cannot be close. My life is nothing to be spared." 班 earnestly requested, and the official finally agreed. Thereupon, 班 took leave and returned home. After a year, almost all of his children died. Frightened, 班 went to Mount Tai again, tapped on the tree to request an audience. The former attendant welcomed him and let him see the official. 班 then explained, "My former words were inadequate. When I returned home, all my children died. Now fearing that the disaster has not yet ended, I came to inform, humbly requesting pity and rescue." The official clapped his hands and laughed, saying, "I formerly told you: life and death are different paths and cannot be close." He immediately ordered to summon 班's father. 班's father arrived shortly and was asked in the courtyard, "You formerly requested to return to the village god, should have brought blessings to the family, but the grandchildren died all. Why?" He answered, "Having been away from the village for a long time, I was glad to return. Moreover, I encountered ample food and drink, and truly missed my grandchildren, so I summoned them." Thereupon, he was replaced. His father wept and left. 班 then returned home. Afterwards, all his children were safe.

    47

    宋时弘农冯夷，华阴潼乡堤首人也。以八月上庚日渡河，溺死。天帝署为河伯。又五行书曰：“河伯以庚辰日死，不可治船远行，溺没不返。”
    　　吴余杭县南，有上湖，湖中央作塘。有一人乘马看戏，将三四人，至岑村饮酒，小醉，暮还时，炎热，因下马，入水中枕石眠。马断走归，从人悉追马，至暮不返。眠觉，日已向晡，不见人马。见一妇来，年可十六七，云：“女郎再拜，日既向暮，此间大可畏，君作何计？”因问：“女郎何姓？那得忽相闻？”复有一少年，年十三四，甚了了，乘新车，车后二十人至，呼上车，云：“大人暂欲相见。”因回车而去。道中绎络，把火见城郭邑居。既入城，进厅事，上有信幡，题云：“河伯信。

    Explanation

    47

    During the Song Dynasty, Feng Yi of Huayin, a village near the river embankment in the prefecture of Hongnong, drowned on the first day of the lunar month that fell on the "Shàng Gēng" (upper stem) while crossing the river. The Heavenly Emperor appointed him as the River Lord. The Wuxing Shu (Book of the Five Elements) also states: "The River Lord dies on the day of 'Gēngchén,' and one should not repair or travel by boat, as one will drown and not return."

    In the southern part of Yuhang County in Wu, there is a lake called Shanghu. In the center of the lake, there is a pond. One day, a man rode his horse to watch a performance, accompanied by three or four others. They went to Cen Village to drink, became slightly tipsy, and returned in the evening. It was hot, so he dismounted and lay down in the water, resting his head on a stone. His horse ran away on its own, and his companions all went after it, not returning until late in the evening. When he woke up, it was already approaching dusk, and he saw no one or his horse. A young woman, about sixteen or seventeen years old, appeared and said, "Lady respectfully greets you. The day is already late, and this place is very frightening. What are you going to do?" He asked, "What is your name, Lady? How did you suddenly appear before me?" Then a young man, about thirteen or fourteen years old, arrived, very intelligent, riding in a new carriage with twenty people following him. He called out for the man to get on the carriage and said, "The elder wants to see you briefly." They turned the carriage around and left. Along the way, they passed through a lit-up landscape, seeing cities and towns. After entering the city, they went to a hall where there was a banner inscribed with "River Lord's Message."

    48

    ”俄见一人，年三十许，颜色如画，侍卫烦多，相对欣然，敕行酒，笑云：“仆有小女，颇聪明，欲以给君箕帚。”此人知神，不敢拒逆。便敕：备办会就郎中婚。承白：已办。遂以丝布单衣，及纱袷绢裙，纱衫裈履屐，皆精好。又给十小吏，青衣数十人。妇年可十八九，姿容婉媚，便成。三日，经大会客拜阁，四日，云：“礼既有限，发遣去。”妇以金瓯麝香囊与婿别，涕泣而分。又与钱十万，药方三卷，云：“可以施功布德。”复云：“十年当相迎。”此人归家，遂不肯别婚，辞亲出家作道人。所得三卷方：一卷脉经，一卷汤方，一卷丸方。周行救疗，皆致神验。后母老，兄丧，因还婚宦。

    Explanation

    48

    Suddenly, a man appeared, around thirty years old, with an appearance as beautiful as a painting, accompanied by many attendants. Both of them were pleased, and he commanded to serve wine, smiling and saying, "I have a daughter, who is quite intelligent, and I wish to give her to you as a wife." This person knew it was a spirit and dared not refuse. He then commanded: "Prepare everything for the marriage with the official." It was reported: "Everything is ready." So, he gave silk and linen robes, and gauze and silk skirts, gauze shirts, trousers, shoes, and sandals, all finely made. He also gave ten minor officials and dozens of attendants in green robes. The woman, around eighteen or nineteen years old, had a graceful and charming appearance, and they were married immediately. On the third day, a grand assembly of guests greeted the new bride. On the fourth day, he said, "The rites are limited, so send you away." The woman gave her husband a golden jar and a sachet of musk as a farewell gift, and they parted with tears. She also gave him ten thousand coins and three volumes of prescriptions, saying, "You can use these to perform good deeds and spread virtue." She added, "I will come to fetch you in ten years." This person returned home and refused to marry another. He left his family to become a monk. The three volumes of prescriptions included one volume on pulse diagnosis, one volume on decoctions, and one volume on pills. He traveled to heal and treat, and all his remedies were miraculously effective. After his mother grew old and his brother died, he returned to marriage and official duties.

    49

    秦始皇三十六年，使者郑容从关东来，将入函关，西至华阴，望见素车白马，从华山上下。疑其非人，道住止而待之。遂至，问郑容曰：“安之？”答曰：“之咸阳。”车上人曰：“吾华山使也。愿托一牍书，致镐池君所。子之咸阳，道过镐池，见一大梓，有文石，取款梓，当有应者。”即以书与之。容如其言，以石款梓树，果有人来取书。明年，祖龙死。

    Explanation

    49

    In the 36th year of Qin Shi Huang's reign, the envoy Zheng Rong came from the east and was about to enter the Hangu Pass. Traveling west to Huayin, he saw a white carriage and white horse descending from Mount Hua. Suspecting it was not a human, he stopped on the road and waited for it. The figure approached and asked Zheng Rong, "Where are you going?" Zheng Rong replied, "To Xianyang." The figure on the carriage said, "I am the messenger of Mount Hua. I wish to entrust a scroll of writing to the lord of Haochi. When you go to Xianyang, pass by Haochi, see a large paulownia tree with inscribed stones, knock on the tree, and someone will respond." Zheng Rong took the scroll and followed the instructions. When he passed by Haochi and saw the large paulownia tree, he knocked on it with a stone, and indeed, someone came to take the message. The following year, Qin Shi Huang died.

    50

    张璞，字公直，不知何许人也。为吴郡太守，征还，道由庐山，子女观于祠室，婢使指像人以戏曰：“以此配汝。”其夜，璞妻梦庐君致聘曰：“鄙男不肖，感垂采择，用致微意。”妻觉怪之。婢言其情。于是妻惧，催璞速发。中流，舟不为行。阖船震恐。乃皆投物于水，船犹不行。或曰：“投女。”则船为进。皆曰：“神意已可知也。以一女而灭一门，奈何？”璞曰：“吾不忍见之。”乃上飞庐，卧，使妻沈女于水。妻因以璞亡兄孤女代之。置席水中，女坐其上，船乃得去。璞见女之在也，怒曰：“吾何面目于当世也。”乃复投己女。及得渡，遥见二女在下。有吏立于岸侧，曰：“吾庐君主簿也。庐君谢君。知鬼神非匹。又敬君之义，故悉还二女。”后问女。言：“但见好屋，吏卒，不觉在水中也。”

    Explanation

    50

    Zhang Pu, courtesy name Gongzhi, was of unknown origin. He served as the governor of Wu Commandery and was summoned back, traveling via Mount Lu. His children watched in the shrine room, and a maid pointed to a statue and jokingly said, "To match you with this." That night, Zhang Pu's wife dreamed that Lord Lu sent a proposal saying, "My unworthy son is grateful for your choice and sends his humble intentions." The wife woke up feeling strange. The maid explained the situation. The wife became frightened and urged Zhang Pu to leave quickly. In the middle of the river, the boat would not move. The entire ship was shaken with fear. They then all threw objects into the water, but the boat still would not move. Someone said, "Throw a girl." Then the boat moved forward. Everyone said, "The spirit's intention is clear. To sacrifice one girl to destroy an entire family, what shall we do?" Zhang Pu said, "I cannot bear to see it." He then went up to the flying pavilion, lay down, and ordered his wife to drown the girl in the water. The wife then replaced her with the orphaned daughter of Zhang Pu's deceased elder brother. She placed a mat in the water, and the girl sat on it, and the boat then moved forward. When Zhang Pu saw the girl, he became angry and said, "How can I face the world with a face?" He then threw his own daughter. After crossing the river, he saw two girls far below. A clerk stood on the riverbank and said, "I am the main clerk of Lord Lu. Lord Lu thanks you. Knowing that spirits are not suitable matches, and respecting your righteousness, he has returned both girls to you." Later, when asked about it, the girls said, "We only saw good houses and officials, and did not realize we were in the water."

    51

    建康小吏曹着，为庐山使所迎，配以女婉。着形意不安，屡屡求请退。婉潜然垂涕，赋诗序别。幷赠织成裈衫。
    　　宫亭湖孤石庙，尝有估客下都，经其庙下，见二女子，云：“可为买两量丝履，自相厚报。”估客至都，市好丝履，幷箱盛之，自市书刀，亦内箱中。既还，以箱及香置庙中而去，忘取书刀。至河中流，忽有鲤鱼跳入船内，破鱼腹，得书刀焉。

    51

    A minor official from Jiankang named Cao Zhe was welcomed by an envoy from Mount Lu and paired with a woman named Wan. Cao Zhe felt uneasy in body and mind and repeatedly requested to withdraw. Wan secretly shed tears and composed a poem to bid farewell. She also presented a finely woven undergarment and shirt.

    On the shores of Gongting Lake stood a temple dedicated to a solitary stone. Once, a merchant was traveling to the capital and passed by the temple. He saw two women who said, "Can you buy two pairs of silk shoes for us? We will reciprocate with great favor." The merchant reached the capital, bought fine silk shoes, and placed them in a box. He also bought a writing knife and put it in the box. After returning, he placed the box and incense in the temple and left, forgetting to take the writing knife. When he reached the middle of the river, a carp suddenly jumped into his boat. He opened the fish's belly and found the writing knife inside.

    52

    南州人有遣吏献犀簪于孙权者，舟过宫亭庙而乞灵焉。神忽下教曰：“须汝犀簪。”吏惶遽不敢应。俄而犀簪已前列矣。神复下教曰：“俟汝至石头城，返汝簪。”吏不得已，遂行，自分失簪，且得死罪。比达石头，忽有大鲤鱼，长三尺，跃入舟。剖之，得簪。
    　　郭璞过江，宣城太守殷佑，引为参军。时有一物，大如水牛，灰色，卑脚，脚类象，胸前尾上皆白，大力而迟钝，来到城下，众咸怪焉。佑使人伏而取之。令璞作卦，遇遯之蛊，名曰“驴鼠。”卜适了，伏者以戟刺，深尺余。郡纪纲上祠请杀之。巫云：“庙神不悦。此是郱(幷改共)亭驴山君使。至荆山，暂来过我，不须触之。”遂去，不复见。

    Explanation

    52

    A man from Nanzhou sent an official to present a rhinoceros horn hairpin to Sun Quan. As the boat passed by the Palace Pavilion Temple, the official sought divine assistance. Suddenly, the deity issued an order: "I need your rhinoceros horn hairpin." The official, terrified and dared not respond, soon found the hairpin placed in front of him. The deity then said, "Wait until you reach the Stone City, and I will return your hairpin." The official, having no choice, continued on his journey, resigned to losing the hairpin and facing the death penalty. By the time he reached the Stone City, a large carp, three feet long, suddenly jumped into the boat. When he cut it open, he found the hairpin inside.

    Later, Guo Pu crossed the river, and Yin You, the governor of Xuancheng, appointed him as a military advisor. At that time, a creature as large as a water buffalo appeared. It was gray in color, had short legs, feet like an elephant's, and was white on its chest and tail. It was strong but slow, and it came to the city gate, amazing everyone. Yin You ordered someone to ambush and capture it. He instructed Guo Pu to cast a divination, which resulted in the hexagram of Retreat and the hexagram of Influence. The creature was named "Donkey Rat." Just as the divination was completed, the ambushers stabbed it with a spear, more than a foot deep. The county official offered a sacrifice and requested its killing. The shaman said, "The temple deity is displeased. This is the envoy of the Donkey Mountain Lord of Pingting. It came from Jing Mountain, just passing by, so there's no need to harm it." The creature then left and was never seen again.

    53

    庐陵欧明，从贾客，道经彭泽湖，每以舟中所有多少投湖中，云：“以为礼。”积数年后，复过，忽见湖中有大道，上多风尘，有数吏，乘车马来候明，云：“是青洪君使要。”须臾，达见，有府舍，门下吏卒。明甚怖。吏曰：“无可怖！青洪君感君前后有礼，故要君，必有重遗君者。君勿取，独求‘如愿’耳。”明既见青洪君，乃求“如愿。”使逐明去。如愿者，青洪君婢也。明将归，所愿辄得，数年，大富。
    　　益州之西，云南之东，有神祠，克山石为室，下有神，奉祠之，自称黄公。因言：此神，张良所受黄石公之灵也。清净不宰杀。诸祈祷者，持一百钱，一双笔，一丸墨，置石室中，前请乞，先闻石室中有声，须臾，问：“来人何欲？”既言，便具语吉凶，不见其形。至今如此。
    　　永嘉中，有神见兖州，自称樊道基。有妪，号成夫人。夫人好音乐，能弹箜篌，闻人弦歌，辄便起舞。

    Explanation

    53

    Lu Ling Ou Ming, accompanying merchants, passed by Pengze Lake, and often threw items from his boat into the lake, saying, "As a ritual offering." After several years, he passed by again and suddenly saw a wide road in the lake, with much dust on it, and several officials came by carriage and horse to greet him, saying, "This is the envoy of the Lord of Qinghong." Soon, they reached the place, and there was an official residence, with officials and soldiers under the door. Ou Ming was very frightened. The official said, "There is nothing to be afraid of! The Lord of Qinghong is grateful for your previous and current offerings, so he invites you. He will surely give you a valuable gift. Do not take anything else, just seek 'Ruyuan.'" After seeing the Lord of Qinghong, Ou Ming sought "Ruyuan." The official sent Ruyuan to follow Ou Ming back. Ruyuan was a servant of the Lord of Qinghong. Ou Ming took Ruyuan back with him, and all his wishes were fulfilled. Within a few years, he became very wealthy.

    To the west of Yizhou and the east of Yunnan, there is a shrine carved out of the mountain and stone. Below the shrine, there is a deity worshiped there, who calls himself Huang Gong. He says, "This deity is the spirit of Zhang Liang's teacher, the Yellow Stone Elder." He is pure and does not kill animals. Those who pray hold one hundred coins, a pair of brushes, and a ball of ink, and place them in the stone room. They go forward to ask for something, and first hear a voice from the stone room. Soon, they ask, "What does the person desire?" After they speak, they clearly tell about good or bad fortune, but cannot see his form. It is still like this today.

    During the Yongjia period, a spirit appeared in Yanzhou, calling himself Fan Daoji. There was a woman, called Cheng's Lady. She loved music and could play the konghou. When she heard people singing and playing music, she immediately started dancing.

    54

    沛国戴文谋，隐居阳城山中，曾于客堂，食际，忽闻有神呼曰：“我天帝使者，欲下凭君，可乎？”文闻甚惊。又曰：“君疑我也。”文乃跪曰：“居贫，恐不足降下耳。”既而洒扫设位，朝夕进食，甚谨。后于室内窃言之。妇曰：“此恐是妖魅凭依耳。”文曰：“我亦疑之。”及祠飨之时，神乃言曰：“吾相从方欲相利，不意有疑心异议。”文辞谢之际，忽堂上如数十人呼声，出视之，见一大鸟，五色，白鸠数十随之，东北入云而去，遂不见。
    　　麋竺，字子仲，东海朐人也。祖世货殖，家赀巨万。常从洛归，未至家数十里，见路次有一好新妇，从竺求寄载。行可二十余里，新妇谢去，谓竺曰：“我天使也。当往烧东海麋竺家，感君见载，故以相语。”竺因私请之。妇曰：“不可得不烧。如此，君可快去。我当缓行，日中，必火发。”竺乃急行归，达家，便移出财物。日中，而火大发。

    Explanation

    54

    Dai Wenmou, a man from Pei State, lived in seclusion in Yangcheng Mountain. Once, while in his guest hall, during a meal, he suddenly heard a god call out, "I am a messenger of the Heavenly Emperor. I wish to descend and rely on you. Is that acceptable?" Dai Wenmou was greatly surprised. The god said, "You doubt me." Dai Wenmou then knelt and said, "I live in poverty, I fear I am not worthy enough for you to descend." After that, he swept and cleaned, set up a place, and offered food morning and evening, being very careful. Later, in the room, he whispered to his wife, "This might be an evil spirit relying on us." His wife replied, "I also doubt it." When the time for the offering came, the god said, "I am here to help you, I did not expect you to have doubts." While Dai Wenmou was apologizing, suddenly there were shouts like dozens of people in the hall. Looking out, he saw a large bird with five colors, followed by dozens of white pigeons, flying northeast into the clouds and disappearing.

    Mi Zhu, courtesy name Zizhong, was from Qiu, Donghai. His ancestors were engaged in trade, and his family had immense wealth. He often traveled from Luoyang, and before reaching home by dozens of miles, he saw a beautiful young woman on the road who asked him for a ride. After traveling about twenty miles, the woman thanked him and said, "I am a messenger of the Heavenly Emperor. I am going to burn Mi Zhu's house in Donghai. I am grateful for your kindness, so I am telling you this." Mi Zhu then privately asked her, "Can you not burn it? If you can, please tell me." The woman said, "I cannot avoid it. If you want to save your house, you should hurry. I will move slowly, and by noon, the fire will start." Mi Zhu then hurried home, and by the time he arrived, he had moved all his valuables outside. By noon, the fire had started and spread rapidly.

    55

    汉宣帝时，南阳阴子方者，性至孝。积恩，好施。喜祀灶。腊日，晨炊，而灶神形见。子方再拜受庆，家有黄羊，因以祀之。自是已后，暴至巨富。田七百余顷，舆马仆隶，比于邦君。子方尝言：我子孙必将强大，至识三世，而遂繁昌。家凡四侯，牧守数十。故后子孙尝以腊日祀灶，而荐黄羊焉。
    　　吴县张成，夜起，忽见一妇人立于宅南角，举手招成曰：“此是君家之蚕室。我即此地之神。明年正月十五，宜作白粥，泛膏于上。”以后年年大得蚕。今之作膏糜像此。
    　　豫章有戴氏女，久病不差，见一小石形像偶人，女谓曰：“尔有人形，岂神？能差我宿疾者，吾将重汝。”其夜，梦有人告之：“吾将佑汝。”自后疾渐差。遂为立祠山下。戴氏为巫，故名戴侯祠。
    　　汉阳羡长刘(王巳)尝言：“我死当为神。”一夕，饮醉，无病而卒。风雨，失其柩。夜闻荆山有数千人噉声，乡民往视之，则棺已成冢。遂改为君山，因立祠祀之。

    Explanation

    55

    During the reign of Emperor Xuan of Han, there was a man from Nanyang named Yin Zifang, who was extremely filial. He accumulated kindness and loved to give. He enjoyed worshiping the stove god. On the day of the New Year's Eve, while cooking in the morning, the stove god appeared in human form. Yin Zifang bowed twice and received the blessing, and since his family had yellow sheep, he used them to offer sacrifices. After this, he suddenly became immensely wealthy. He owned over seven hundred acres of land, carriages, horses, and servants, comparable to a feudal lord. Yin Zifang once said: "My descendants will surely become powerful, recognized for three generations, and thus flourish." His family had four marquises and governed dozens of regions. Therefore, after that, his descendants would always offer yellow sheep on the day of the New Year's Eve.

    In Wu County, there was a man named Zhang Cheng. One night, he woke up and suddenly saw a woman standing at the south corner of his house, raising her hand to call him. She said: "This is your family's silkworm room. I am the deity of this place. Next year on the fifteenth day of the first lunar month, you should make white porridge and pour oil on top." From then on, he had a great harvest of silkworms every year. Today's practice of making porridge with oil is similar to this.

    In Yuanchang, there was a woman from the Dai family who had been ill for a long time without recovery. She saw a small stone statue resembling a human figure and said to it: "You have a human form, are you a god? If you can cure my chronic illness, I will honor you." That night, she dreamed that someone told her: "I will protect you." After that, her illness gradually improved. Thus, a shrine was built at the foot of the mountain. The Dai family became shamans, and the shrine was named Dai Hou Temple.

    In Yangxi, there was a man named Liu (Wangsi), the magistrate, who once said: "I will become a god after my death." One night, he drank to intoxication and died without illness. In the rain and wind, his coffin was lost. At night, they heard the sounds of thousands of people eating in Jing Mountain. The villagers went to see, and the coffin had already turned into a mound. Thus, it was renamed Jun Mountain, and a shrine was established to worship him.

    56

    搜神记卷五
    　　蒋子文者，广陵人也。嗜酒，好色，挑挞无度。常自谓：“己骨清，死当为神。”汉末，为秣陵尉，逐贼至钟山下，贼击伤额，因解绶缚之，有顷遂死。及吴先主之初，其故吏见文于道，乘白马，执白羽，侍从如平生。见者惊走。文追之，谓曰：“我当为此土地神，以福尔下民。尔可宣告百姓，为我立祠。不尔，将有大咎。”是岁夏，大疫，百姓窃相恐动，颇有窃祠之者矣。文又下巫祝：“吾将大启佑孙氏，宜为我立祠；不尔，将使虫入人耳为灾。”俄而小虫如尘虻，入耳，皆死，医不能治。百姓愈恐。孙主未之信也。又下巫祝：“吾不祀我，将又以大火为灾。”是岁，火灾大发，一日数十处。火及公宫。议者以为鬼有所归，乃不为厉，宜有以抚之。于是使使者封子文为中都侯，次弟子绪为长水校尉，皆加印绶。为立庙堂。转号钟山为蒋山，今建康东北蒋山是也。自是灾厉止息，百姓遂大事之。

    Explanation

    56

    Translation:

    Volume Five of the Search for Spirits

    Jiang Ziwén, a man from Guangling, was a notorious drunkard, a lecher, and a provocateur without bounds. He often said to himself, "My bones are pure; after my death, I shall become a deity." At the end of the Han dynasty, he served as a magistrate in Moling. While pursuing bandits to the foot of Zhong Mountain, the bandits struck him on the forehead, and he tied them up with his sash. Shortly thereafter, he died. During the early reign of the Wu state's founding emperor, his former officials saw him on the road, mounted on a white horse, holding a white feather, and accompanied by attendants as in life. Those who saw him fled in terror. Jiang Ziwén pursued them, saying, "I shall become the land deity of this place, bringing blessings to your people. You should inform the common folk to build an altar for me. If you do not, there will be great calamity." That summer, a major epidemic struck, and the people secretly feared and moved about, with some secretly building altars. Jiang Ziwén then descended through a medium, saying, "I will greatly protect and bless the Sun family; you should build an altar for me. If you do not, I will send small insects into people's ears, causing disaster." Soon, tiny insects like horseflies entered people's ears, killing them, and doctors could not cure them. The people were even more terrified. The Sun ruler did not believe this. Jiang Ziwén then descended again through a medium, saying, "If you do not worship me, I will cause a great fire disaster." That year, fires broke out in many places, reaching the imperial palace. The court believed that if the spirit had a place to rest, it would not cause harm, and they should pacify it. Thus, they sent envoys to confer Jiang Ziwén as the Marquis of Zhongdu and his younger brother Jiang Xù as the Colonel of Changshui, both with seals and ribbons. They built a temple for him. They renamed Zhong Mountain as Jiang Mountain, which is now located northeast of Jiankang. From then on, the disasters ceased, and the people greatly revered him.

    57

    刘赤父者，梦蒋侯召为主簿。期日促，乃往庙陈请：“母老，子弱，情事过切。乞蒙放恕。会稽魏过，多材艺，善事神，请举过自代。”因叩头流血。庙祝曰：“特愿相屈，魏过何人，而有斯举？”赤父固请，终不许，寻而赤父死焉。
    　　咸宁中，太常卿韩伯子某，会稽内史王蕴子某，光禄大夫刘耽子某，同游蒋山庙。庙有数妇人像，甚端正。某等醉，各指像以戏，自相配匹。即以其夕，三人同梦蒋侯遣传教相闻，曰：“家子女并丑陋，而猥垂荣顾。”辄刻某日：“悉相奉迎。”某等以其梦指适异常，试往相问，而果各得此梦，符协如一。于是大惧。备三牲，诣庙谢罪乞哀。又俱梦蒋侯亲来降已曰：“君等既已顾之，实贪，会对克期垂及，岂容方更中悔？”经少时并亡。

    Explanation

    57

    Liu Chifu, a man, dreamed that Jiang Hou summoned him to serve as his secretary. The deadline was pressing, so he went to the temple to make a plea: "My mother is old, my child is young, and the circumstances are too dire. I humbly request your pardon. Wei Guo from Kuaiji is highly talented and skilled in serving the gods; I request that he be nominated to take my place." He knelt and bled. The temple priest said, "I especially wish to trouble you, but who is Wei Guo, and why should he be nominated?" Liu Chifu persisted in his request, but it was finally refused, and soon after, Liu Chifu died.

    During the Xianning era, the Grand Master of Rites, Han Bo, the Governor of Kuaiji, Wang Yun, and the Grand Attendant, Liu Dan, visited the Jiang Hou temple together. The temple had several statues of women, all very beautiful. The officials were drunk and pointed to the statues to playfully match them with each other. That very night, the three of them had the same dream in which Jiang Hou sent a messenger to inform them, saying, "Our daughters are all plain, yet you have honored us with your attention." He set a date, saying, "We will welcome you all." The officials, finding their dreams unusually consistent, decided to visit the temple to inquire, and indeed, they all had the same dream, perfectly matched. They were greatly alarmed. They prepared three sacrificial animals and went to the temple to beg for forgiveness. They also had another dream in which Jiang Hou personally came to them and said, "Since you have already honored us, we are truly greedy, but the appointed date is imminent; how can you now change your mind?" After a short time, all of them died.

    58

    会稽鄮县东野有女子，姓吴，字望子，年十六，姿容可爱。其乡里有解鼓舞神者，要之，便往。缘塘行，半路，忽见一贵人，端正非常。贵人乘船，挺力十余，整顿令人问望子“欲何之？”具以事对。贵人云：“今正欲往彼，便可入船共去。”望子辞不敢。忽然不见。望子既拜神座，见向船中贵人，俨然端坐，即蒋侯像也。问望子“来何迟？”因掷两橘与之。数数形见，遂隆情好。心有所欲，辄空中下之。尝思噉鲤一双，鲜鲤随心而至。望子芳香，流闻数里，颇有神验。一邑共事奉。经三年，望子忽生外意，神便绝往来。

    Explanation

    58

    A Woman Named Wangzi in Kuaiji's Yuyao County

    In the eastern countryside of Yuyao County in Kuaiji Commandery, there lived a girl named Wangzi, whose surname was Wu. She was sixteen years old and possessed a beautiful appearance. Her village had a ritual performer who could invoke deities through drumming and dancing, and he invited her to participate. She agreed and followed him. As they walked along the pond, halfway through their journey, she suddenly saw a nobleman who was exceptionally handsome. The nobleman was riding in a boat, accompanied by more than ten strong men. He had someone ask Wangzi, "Where do you wish to go?" She replied in detail about the situation. The nobleman said, "I am also heading there; you may come aboard and go with me." Wangzi politely declined. Suddenly, the nobleman disappeared. After Wangzi had worshiped at the altar, she saw the nobleman from the boat, sitting upright and composed, which turned out to be the image of Jiang Hou. He asked Wangzi, "Why did you come so late?" and then threw two oranges at her. Over time, the nobleman appeared repeatedly, and their affection deepened. Whenever Wangzi desired something, it would descend from the sky. Once, she thought of eating a pair of fish, and fresh fish appeared as if by her thoughts. Wangzi's fragrance spread for several miles, and there were many miraculous occurrences. The entire county served and worshiped her. After three years, Wangzi suddenly developed external thoughts, and the nobleman ceased to appear.

    59

    陈郡谢玉，为琅邪内史，在京城，所在虎暴，杀人甚众。有一人，以小船载年少妇，以大刀插着船，挟暮来至逻所，将出语云：“此间顷来甚多草秽，君载细小，作此轻行，大为不易。可止逻宿也。”相问讯既毕，逻将适还去。其妇上岸，便为虎将去；其夫拔刀大唤，欲逐之。先奉事蒋侯，乃唤求助。如此当行十里，忽如有一黑衣为之导，其人随之，当复二十里，见大树，既至一穴，虎子闻行声，谓其母至，皆走出，其人即其所杀之。便拔刀隐树侧，住良久，虎方至，便下妇着地，倒牵入穴。其人以刀当腰斫断之。虎既死，其妇故活。向晓，能语。问之，云：“虎初取，便负着背上，临至而后下之。四体无他，止为草木伤耳。”扶归还船，明夜，梦一人语之曰：“蒋侯使助汝，知否？”至家，杀猪祠焉。

    Explanation

    59

    Xie Yu of Chen Commandery, serving as the governor of Langya Commandery, was in the capital city where tigers frequently attacked and killed many people. One day, a man took his young wife on a small boat, with a large knife placed on the boat, and arrived at a patrol post in the evening. The patrol officer spoke to them, saying, "This area has recently become overgrown with weeds. You are traveling in such a small boat, which is quite risky. It would be better to stay here for the night." After their conversation, the patrol officer returned to his duties. The woman stepped onto the shore and was immediately taken by a tiger. Her husband drew his knife, shouted, and tried to chase after the tiger. He had previously been devoted to Lord Jiang, so he called for help. They continued their journey for ten miles when suddenly a mysterious black-clad figure appeared as a guide. The man followed the guide, and they traveled another twenty miles to a large tree and a cave. The tiger cubs, hearing the sound, thought their mother had returned and ran out. The man killed the cubs. He then hid behind the tree with his knife for a long time. When the tiger returned, it dragged the woman to the ground and carried her into the cave. The man cut the tiger in half with his knife. The tiger died, and the woman survived. In the morning, she regained consciousness and could speak. When asked about what happened, she said, "The tiger initially carried me on its back and then dropped me when it reached the cave. I have no other injuries, only those from the grass and trees." They helped her back to the boat. That night, she dreamed of a person who told her, "Lord Jiang has come to help you, did you know?" When they returned home, she sacrificed a pig to Lord Jiang.

    60

    淮南全椒县有丁新妇者，本丹阳丁氏女，年十六，适全椒谢家。其姑严酷，使役有程，不如限者，仍便笞捶不可堪。九月九日，乃自经死。遂有灵向，闻于民间。发言于巫祝曰：“念人家妇女，作息不倦，使避九月九日，勿用作事。”见形，着缥衣，戴青盖，从一婢，至牛渚津，求渡。有两男子，共乘船捕鱼，仍呼求载。两男子笑共调弄之。言：“听我为妇，当相渡也。”丁妪曰：“谓汝是佳人，而无所知。汝是人，当使汝入泥死；是鬼，使汝入水。”便却入草中。须臾，有一老翁，乘船，载苇。

    Explanation

    60

    In the county of Quanjiao in Huainan, there was a young woman named Ding, originally from the Ding family of Danyang. She was sixteen years old when she married into the Xie family of Quanjiao. Her mother-in-law was harsh and cruel, imposing strict time limits on tasks, and those who failed to meet them were beaten mercilessly. On the ninth day of the ninth lunar month, she hanged herself. She then became a spirit and was known among the people. Through a shaman, she spoke and said, "Consider the women of ordinary households, who work tirelessly. Let them avoid the ninth day of the ninth lunar month and refrain from work." She appeared in a light blue robe, wearing a green canopy, accompanied by a maid, and sought to cross the Niu Zhu Ferry. There were two men fishing together, and she called out to them for help. The two men laughed and teased her, saying, "If you become our wife, we will help you cross." The spirit replied, "I thought you were good men, but you know nothing. If you are human, I will make you die in the mud; if you are spirits, I will make you drown." She then retreated into the grass. Soon after, an old man came by boat, carrying reeds.

    61

    妪从索渡。翁曰：“船上无装，岂可露渡？恐不中载耳。”妪言无苦。翁因出苇半许，安处不着船中，徐渡之。至南岸，临去，语翁曰：“吾是鬼神，非人也。自能得过，然宜使民间粗相闻知。翁之厚意，出苇相渡，深有惭感，当有以相谢者。若翁速还去，必有所见，亦当有所得也。”翁曰：“恐燥湿不至，何敢蒙谢。”翁还西岸，见两男子覆水中。进前数里，有鱼千数，跳跃水边，风吹至岸上。翁遂弃苇，载鱼以归。于是丁妪遂还丹阳。江南人皆呼为丁姑。九月九日，不用作事，咸以为息日也。今所在祠之。

    Explanation

    61

    The old woman asked to be ferried across. The old man said, "The boat has no load, how can one cross without being properly loaded? I fear it might not be suitable for carrying." The old woman said it was no trouble. The old man then took out half a bundle of reeds, placed them in the boat, and slowly ferried her across. Upon reaching the south bank, as he was about to leave, he said to the old man, "I am a ghost or spirit, not a human. I can cross by myself, but it is appropriate to make the common people vaguely aware. Your kindness in ferrying me across with the reeds deeply moved me, and I will have something to thank you with. If you quickly return, you will surely see something and gain something." The old man said, "I fear that the dry and wet conditions won't be suitable, so how could I dare to accept your thanks?" The old man returned to the west bank and saw two men lying in the water. He walked several miles ahead and found thousands of fish jumping at the water's edge, blown by the wind onto the shore. The old man then abandoned the reeds, loaded the fish, and returned home. Thus, the old woman returned to Dan Yang. People in southern Jiangnan all called her Ding Gu. On the ninth day of the ninth month, they do not work, considering it a day of rest. Now, she is worshipped everywhere.

    62

    散骑侍郎王佑疾困，与母辞诀，既而闻有通宾者，曰：“某郡，某里，某人，尝为别驾。”佑亦雅闻其姓字，有顷，奄然来至，曰：“与卿士类有自然之分，又州里情，便款然。今年国家有大事，出三将军，分布征发吾等十余人为赵公明府参佐，至此仓卒，见卿有高门大屋，故来投，与卿相得，大不可言。”佑知其鬼神，曰：“不幸疾笃，死在旦夕，遭卿，以性命相托。”答曰：“人生有死，此必然之事。死者不系生时贵贱。吾今见领兵三千，须卿得度簿相付，如此地难得，不宜辞之。”佑曰：“老母年高，兄弟无有，一旦死亡，前无供养。”遂欷歔不能自胜。其人怆然曰：“卿位为常伯，而家无余财，向闻与尊夫人辞诀，言辞哀苦，然则卿国士也，如何可令死。吾当相为。”因起去。明日，更来。其明日，又来。

    Explanation

    62

    Scattered Rider Attendant Wang You was gravely ill, bidding farewell to his mother. Shortly after, he heard of a visitor, who said, "From a certain prefecture, a certain village, a certain person, who once served as a deputy governor." Wang You had also heard of this person's name. Soon, the visitor suddenly arrived and said, "I share a natural bond with you as a member of the scholarly class, and we also have ties from the same province, so we are immediately friendly. This year, the nation has a major event, and three generals have been dispatched to mobilize us ten or more people as assistants to the official of Zhao Gong. We have arrived in haste, and seeing that you have a grand residence, I have come to seek refuge with you. Our bond is profound, beyond words." Wang You recognized the visitor as a spirit and said, "Unfortunate, my illness is severe, and I will die within the day. Meeting you, I entrust my life to you." The visitor replied, "Death is an inevitable part of life, regardless of one's status. I am now leading three thousand troops and need you to hand over the necessary documents. Such a position is hard to come by, and you should not refuse." Wang You said, "My mother is old, and I have no brothers. If I die, there will be no one to care for her." He then wept bitterly, unable to control himself. The visitor, moved, said, "You hold a high position as a constant attendant, yet your family has no surplus wealth. I heard that you bid farewell to your esteemed wife, and your words were filled with sorrow. Indeed, you are a national hero. How can I allow you to die? I will help you." He then stood up and left. The next day, he came again. The day after that, he came once more.

    63

    佑曰：“卿许活吾，当卒恩否？”答曰：“大老子业已许卿，当复相欺耶！”见其从者数百人，皆长二尺许，乌衣军服，赤油为志。佑家击鼓祷祀，诸鬼闻鼓声，皆应节起舞，振袖飒飒有声。佑将为设酒食。辞曰：“不须。”因复起去。谓佑曰：“病在人体中，如火。当以水解之。”因取一杯水，发被灌之。又曰：“为卿留赤笔十余枝，在荐下，可与人使簪之。出入辟恶灾，举事皆无恙。”因道曰：“王甲、李乙，吾皆与之。”遂执佑手与辞。时佑得安眠，夜中忽觉，乃呼左右，令开被，“神以水灌我，将大沾濡。”开被。而信有水在上被之下，下被之上，不浸，如露之在荷。量之，得三升七合。于是疾三分愈二。数日。大除。凡其所道当取者，皆死亡。唯王文英，半年后乃亡。所道与赤笔人，皆经疾病及兵乱，皆亦无恙。初，有妖书云：“上帝以三将军赵公明、钟士季各督数鬼下取人。”莫知所在。佑病差，见此书，与所道赵公明合焉。

    Explanation

    63

    佑曰：“卿许活吾，当卒恩否？”答曰：“大老子业已许卿，当复相欺耶！”见其从者数百人，皆长二尺许，乌衣军服，赤油为志。佑家击鼓祷祀，诸鬼闻鼓声，皆应节起舞，振袖飒飒有声。佑将为设酒食。辞曰：“不须。”因复起去。谓佑曰：“病在人体中，如火。当以水解之。”因取一杯水，发被灌之。又曰：“为卿留赤笔十余枝，在荐下，可与人使簪之。出入辟恶灾，举事皆无恙。”因道曰：“王甲、李乙，吾皆与之。”遂执佑手与辞。时佑得安眠，夜中忽觉，乃呼左右，令开被，“神以水灌我，将大沾濡。”开被。而信有水在上被之下，下被之上，不浸，如露之在荷。量之，得三升七合。于是疾三分愈二。数日。大除。凡其所道当取者，皆死亡。唯王文英，半年后乃亡。所道与赤笔人，皆经疾病及兵乱，皆亦无恙。初，有妖书云：“上帝以三将军赵公明、钟士季各督数鬼下取人。”莫知所在。佑病差，见此书，与所道赵公明合焉。

    佑 said, "You promised to save me, will you fulfill your promise?" The other replied, "I, the elder, have already promised you, how could I deceive you again!" He saw hundreds of followers, all about two feet tall, dressed in black military uniforms with red oil as a mark. At Yu's home, drums were beaten for prayers and offerings, and upon hearing the drum sounds, all the spirits danced in rhythm, their sleeves rustling loudly. Yu intended to prepare wine and food for them. They declined, saying, "It is not necessary." Then they stood up and left. One of them told Yu, "The illness within your body is like fire. It should be extinguished with water." He then took a cup of water and poured it over Yu's head while he was under the covers. Another said, "I have left you more than ten red pens under the mat. You can give them to others to wear. This will protect against evil and misfortune, and ensure safety in all your endeavors." They mentioned, "Wang Jia and Li Yi, I have given them to both of you." They then took Yu's hand and bid farewell. At that time, Yu was able to sleep soundly, and in the middle of the night, he suddenly woke up and called for his attendants, telling them to open the bedding, "A spirit has poured water on me, it will soak me." They opened the bedding, and indeed, there was water between the top and bottom layers, not seeping through, like dew on a lotus leaf. They measured it and found it to be three liters and seven shengs. As a result, his illness improved by two-thirds. After several days, he was completely recovered. All those mentioned as being taken away had died. Only Wang Wenyi died six months later. Those given red pens, having gone through illness and war, remained unharmed. Initially, there was a magical book that said, "The Heavenly Deity has sent three generals, Zhao Gongming and Zhong Shiji, each leading several spirits to take people." Their whereabouts were unknown. After Yu recovered from his illness, he saw this book, and it matched the description of Zhao Gongming.

    64

    汉下邳周式尝至东海，道逢一吏，持一卷书，求寄载。行十余里，谓式曰：“吾暂有所过，留书寄君船中，慎勿发之。”去后，式盗发现书，皆诸死人录，下条有式名。须臾，吏还，式犹视书。吏怒曰：“故以相告，而忽视之？”式叩头流血，良久，吏曰：“感卿远相载，此书不可除卿名。今日已去，还家，三年勿出门，可得度也。勿道见吾书。”式还，不出，已二年余，家皆怪之。邻人卒亡，父怒，使往吊之。式不得已，适出门，便见此吏。吏曰：“吾令汝三年勿出，而今出门，知复奈何？吾求不见，连累为鞭杖，今已见汝，无可奈何。后三日，日中，当相取也。”式还，涕泣具道如此。父故不信。母昼夜与相守。至三日日中时，果见来取，便死。

    Explanation

    64

    Zhou Shi from Xiangpu in the Han dynasty once traveled to the Eastern Sea. On the road, he met a government official who was carrying a scroll and asked Zhou Shi to let him ride. After traveling for more than ten miles, the official said to Zhou Shi, "I will be gone for a short while. Please keep this book in your boat and be careful not to open it." After the official left, Zhou Shi secretly opened the book and found it to be a record of all the dead people. His name was listed below.

    Soon, the official returned, and Zhou Shi was still looking at the book. The official became angry and said, "I specifically warned you not to open it, but you disregarded my warning!" Zhou Shi knelt down and begged for mercy, bleeding from his head. After a long while, the official said, "I am grateful for your kindness in letting me ride. This book cannot remove your name. You have already passed the point of no return. Return home and do not leave your house for three years, and you can be saved. Do not tell anyone about seeing my book."

    Zhou Shi returned home and did not go out. After two years, his family began to wonder why he was staying indoors. One day, a neighbor died suddenly, and Zhou Shi's father became furious and sent him to attend the funeral. Zhou Shi had no choice but to step out the door. As soon as he stepped outside, he saw the official again. The official said, "I told you not to leave your house for three years, but now you have gone out. What can I do? If you had not shown yourself, you would have avoided trouble and punishment. Now that you have been seen, there is nothing I can do. In three days, at noon, I will come to take you."

    Zhou Shi returned home, crying and telling his parents what had happened. His father did not believe him. His mother guarded him day and night. On the third day at noon, the official indeed came to take him, and Zhou Shi died.

    65

    南顿张助，于田中种禾，见李核，欲持去，顾见空桑，中有土，因植种，以余浆溉灌。后人见桑中反复生李，转相告语，有病目痛者，息阴下，言：“李君令我目愈，谢以一豚。”目痛小疾，亦行自愈。众犬吠声，盲者得视，远近翕赫，其下车骑常数千百，酒肉滂沱。间一岁余，张助远出来还，见之，惊云：此有何神，乃我所种耳。”因就斫之。
    　　王莽居摄，刘京上言：“齐郡临淄县亭长辛当，数梦人谓曰：“吾，天使也。摄皇帝，当为真。即不信我，此亭中当有新井出。’亭长起视亭中，因有新井。入地百尺。”

    Explanation

    65

    Zhang Zhu of Nandun was sowing grain in a field when he saw a plum stone and wanted to take it away. Glancing back, he saw an empty mulberry tree with soil in it, so he planted the stone and watered it with leftover water. Later, people saw that the plum tree grew repeatedly in the mulberry tree and spread the news. Someone with an eye ailment rested in the shade and said, "The plum tree has healed my eye. I will thank it with a pig." The eye ailment, though minor, also healed on its own. The news spread like wildfire, and the blind regained their sight. The area became famous, and thousands of carriages and riders arrived, bringing abundant food and drink. After more than a year, Zhang Zhu returned from a journey and saw the tree. He was surprised and said, "What kind of god is this? It is just what I planted." He then cut it down.

    During the regency of Wang Mang, Liu Jing reported to the emperor, "Xindang, the village head of Linzi County in Qi Province, often dreamed of someone saying, 'I am a messenger of heaven. The acting emperor should become the true emperor. If you do not believe me, a new well will appear in this village.' The village head looked and found a new well that went a hundred feet deep."

    66

    搜神记卷六
    　　妖怪者，盖精气之依物者也。气乱于中，物变于外，形神气质，表里之用也。本于五行，通于五事，虽消息升降，化动万端，其于休咎之征，皆可得域而论矣。
    　　夏桀之时厉山亡，秦始皇之时三山亡，周显王三十二年宋大邱社亡，汉昭帝之末，陈留昌邑社亡。京房易传曰：“山默然自移，天下兵乱，社稷亡也。”故会稽山阴琅邪中有怪山，世传本琅邪东武海中山也，时天夜，风雨晦冥，旦而见武山在焉，百姓怪之，因名曰怪山，时东武县山，亦一夕自亡去，识其形者，乃知其移来。今怪山下见有东武里，盖记山所自来，以为名也。又交州脆州山移至青州。凡山徙，皆不极之异也。此二事未详其世。尚书金縢曰：“山徙者，人君不用道，士贤者不兴，或禄去，公室赏罚不由君，私门成群，不救，当为易世变号。

    Explanation

    66

    Translation:

    Records of Searching for the Gods, Volume Six

    Monsters and spirits are manifestations of spiritual energy attached to physical objects. When spiritual energy is in chaos within, physical objects change outwardly; form, spirit, and essence are the inner and outer workings. Their origin lies in the Five Elements, and they connect to the Five Constant Virtues. Though they undergo rise and fall, transformation in myriad forms, all signs of auspiciousness or misfortune can be categorized and discussed.

    During the reign of Jie of Xia, Mount Lishan disappeared; during the reign of Qin Shi Huang, the Three Mountains vanished; in the thirty-second year of King Xian of Zhou, the grand shrine of Song's Daqiuyue disappeared; at the end of Emperor Zhao of Han's reign, the shrine of Changyi, Tengzhou, vanished. The Book of Changes (易传) by Jing Fang states: "When mountains move silently, it is a sign of widespread warfare and the fall of the state." Therefore, in Shanxi, Shanxi, there is a strange mountain known as the "Ghost Mountain," which is said to have originated from Mount Dongwu in Dongwu County, by the sea. One night, it was dark with wind and rain, and the next morning, Mount Dongwu was found there. The people were astonished and named it the "Ghost Mountain." At the same time, the mountain in Dongwu County also disappeared overnight. Those who recognized its shape knew it had moved there. Today, there is a place called Dongwuli at the foot of the Ghost Mountain, which is named after the mountain's origin. Additionally, a mountain from Jiaozhou moved to Qingzhou. All such movements of mountains are extraordinary events that defy explanation. These two events are not detailed in the records of their respective eras. The Book of Documents (尚书) in the chapter Jinteng (金縢) states: "When mountains move, it is a sign that the ruler is not following the Dao, that the wise and virtuous are not rising, that the fiefdoms are losing their wealth, that rewards and punishments are not decided by the ruler, and that private factions are forming. If this is not corrected, it will lead to a change of dynasty and era."

    ”说曰：“善言天者，必质于人；善言人者，必本于天。”故天有四时，日月相推，寒暑迭代，其转运也。和而为雨，怒而为风，散而为露，乱而为雾，凝而为霜雪，立而为蚳●，此天之常数也。人有四肢五脏，一觉一寐，呼吸吐纳，精气往来，流而为荣卫，彰而为气色，发而为声音，此亦人之常数也。若四时失运，寒暑乖违，则五纬盈缩，星辰错行，日月薄蚀，彗孛流飞，此天地之危诊也。寒暑不时，此天地之蒸否也。石立，土踊，此天地之瘤赘也。山崩，地陷，此天地之痈疽也。冲风，暴雨，此天地之奔气也。雨泽不降，川渎涸竭，此天地之焦枯也。
    　　商纣之时，大龟生毛，兔生角，兵甲将兴之象也。
    　　周宣王三十三年，幽王生，是岁，有马化为狐。

    Explanation

    67

    The Art of Understanding Heaven and Humanity

    One said, "Those who speak well about heaven must ground themselves in people; those who speak well about people must base themselves on heaven." Thus, heaven has four seasons, with the sun and moon pushing each other, cold and heat alternating, and their cycles turning. When harmonious, they become rain; when angry, they become wind; when dispersed, they become dew; when chaotic, they become fog; when condensed, they become frost and snow; when standing, they become earth formations. These are the constant rules of heaven. Humans have four limbs and five organs, experiencing one waking and one sleeping, breathing in and out, with vital energy flowing and circulating, manifesting as the circulation of blood and qi, appearing as facial complexion, and expressing as sounds. This is also the constant rule of humans. If the seasons lose their order and cold and heat go awry, then the five planets will fluctuate, stars will move erratically, the sun and moon will experience eclipses, comets will fly, and this is a critical sign of the state of heaven and earth. If cold and heat are not in season, this is a sign of the stagnation of heaven and earth. Rocks standing upright and soil rising indicate tumors on the earth; landslides and sinkholes indicate ulcers on the earth; strong winds and heavy rains indicate the earth's outburst of energy; if rain does not fall and rivers and streams dry up, this is a sign of the earth's desiccation.

    During the reign of King Zhou of Shang, a large turtle grew hair, and a rabbit grew horns, indicating the impending rise of military forces. In the thirty-third year of King Xuan of Zhou's reign, King You of Zhou was born, and in that year, a horse transformed into a fox, indicating a significant and possibly ominous event.

    68

    晋献公二年，周惠王居于郑，郑人入王府，多脱化为蜮，射人。
    　　周隐王二年四月，齐地暴长长丈余，高一尺五寸。京房易妖曰：“地四时暴长占：春、夏多吉，秋、冬多凶。”历阳之郡，一夕沦入地中而为水泽，今麻湖是也。不知何时。运斗枢曰：“邑之沦阴，吞阳，下相屠焉。”
    　　周哀王八年，郑有一妇人，生四十子，其二十人为人，二十人死。其九年，晋有豕生人，吴赤乌七年，有妇人一生三子。
    　　周烈王六年，林碧阳君之御人产二龙。
    　　鲁严公八年，齐襄公田于贝邱，见豕，从者曰：“公子彭生也。”公怒射之，豕人立而唬，公惧坠车，伤足，丧屦。刘向以为近豕祸也。
    　　鲁严公时，有内蛇与外蛇斗郑南门中。内蛇死。刘向以为近蛇孽也。京房易传曰：“立嗣子疑，厥妖蛇居国门斗。”
    　　鲁昭公十九年，龙众于郑时门之外洧渊。刘向以为近龙孽也。京房易传曰：“众心不安，厥妖龙众其邑中也。”

    Explanation

    68

    In the second year of Duke Xian of Jin, King Huai of Zhou resided in Zheng, and the people of Zheng entered the royal treasury, where many items transformed into yu, mythical creatures that shot at people.

    In the second month of the fourth year of King Yin of Zhou, a plant in Qi grew abnormally, over ten feet tall and one foot five inches wide. According to Jing Fang's I Ching commentary, "abnormal growth of the earth is a sign: spring and summer bring good omens, while autumn and winter bring bad omens." In the county of Liyang, one night, a part of the land sank into the ground and became a marsh, now known as Mah Lake. It is unknown when this occurred. Yun Dou Shu said, "The sinking of the city, swallowing the sun, and the destruction of the lower parts."

    In the eighth year of King Ai of Zhou, a woman in Zheng gave birth to forty children, twenty of whom became human, and twenty died. In the ninth year, a pig in Jin gave birth to a human. In the seventh year of the Red Bird period in Wu, a woman gave birth to three children.

    In the sixth year of King Lie of Zhou, the attendant of Lin Biyang Jun gave birth to two dragons.

    In the eighth year of Duke Yan of Lu, Duke Xiang of Qi hunted in Bei Qiu and saw a pig. His attendants said, "It is Prince Pengsheng." The prince angrily shot it, and the pig stood up and roared. The prince was frightened and fell off the carriage, injuring his foot and losing his shoes. Liu Xiang believed this was a sign of pig-related disaster.

    During the reign of Duke Yan of Lu, an inner snake and an outer snake fought in the south gate of Zheng. The inner snake died. Liu Xiang believed this was a sign of snake-related disaster. Jing Fang's I Ching commentary said, "Doubt in the succession of the heir leads to the omen of snakes fighting at the national gate."

    In the nineteenth year of Duke Zhao of Lu, dragons gathered outside the gates of Zheng in Wei Yuan. Liu Xiang believed this was a sign of dragon-related disaster. Jing Fang's I Ching commentary said, "The people's hearts are uneasy, leading to the omen of many dragons in the city."

    69

    鲁定公元年，有九蛇绕柱，占，以为九世庙不祀，乃立炀宫。
    　　秦孝公二十一年，有马生人。昭王二十年，牡马生子而死。刘向以为皆马祸也。京房易传曰：“方伯分威，厥妖牡马生子。上无天子，诸侯相伐，厥妖马生人。”
    　　魏襄王十三年，有女子化为丈夫，与妻生子。京房易传曰：“女子化为丈夫，兹谓阴昌，贱人为王。丈夫化为女子，兹谓阴胜阳，厥咎亡。”一曰：“男化为女宫刑滥，女化为男妇政行也。”
    　　秦孝文王五年，游煦衍，有献五足牛，时秦世大用民力，天下叛之。京房易传曰：“兴繇役，夺民时，厥妖牛生五足。”
    　　秦始皇二十六年，有大人长五丈，足履六尺，皆夷狄服，凡十二人，见于临洮，乃作金人十二以象之。
    　　汉惠帝二年，正月癸酉旦，有两龙现于兰陵廷东里温陵井中，至乙亥夜，去。京房易传曰：“有德遭害，厥妖龙见井中。”又曰：“行刑暴恶，黑龙从井出。”

    Explanation

    69

    During the first year of Duke Ding of Lu's reign, nine snakes were seen coiling around a pillar. Diviners interpreted this as an omen that the ancestral temple would not be worshipped for nine generations, and thus they established a new palace named "炀宫."

    In the twenty-first year of Duke Xiao of Qin's reign, a horse gave birth to a human. In the twentieth year of King Zhao of Qin's reign, a male horse gave birth to a foal and died in the process. Liu Xiang believed that these events were all signs of horse-related disasters. Jing Fang's Yijing commentary states: "When regional leaders divide power, the omen is a male horse giving birth. When there is no central authority and feudal lords wage war against each other, the omen is a horse giving birth to a human."

    In the thirteenth year of Duke Xiang of Wei's reign, a woman transformed into a man and had a child with her wife. Jing Fang's Yijing commentary states: "When a woman transforms into a man, it is a sign of the rise of a lowly person to power. When a man transforms into a woman, it is a sign of the decline of male authority and the rise of female influence." Another interpretation is: "When men transform into women, it indicates excessive castration; when women transform into men, it indicates the implementation of women's governance."

    In the fifth year of King Wen of Qin's reign, during a tour in Xuyang, a five-legged cow was presented as a gift. At that time, the State of Qin was heavily taxing and forcing labor, leading to widespread rebellion. Jing Fang's Yijing commentary states: "When excessive labor and the taking of people's time occur, the omen is a five-legged cow."

    In the twenty-sixth year of Emperor Qin Shi Huang's reign, twelve giants, each five meters tall and wearing barbarian clothing, appeared in Lintao. The emperor then ordered the creation of twelve bronze statues to represent them.

    In the second year of Emperor Hui of Han's reign, on the first day of the first month (癸酉), two dragons appeared in a well in the eastern part of Lanling. They disappeared by the night of the following day (乙亥). Jing Fang's Yijing commentary states: "When a virtuous person suffers, the omen is dragons appearing in a well." It also states: "When excessive and brutal punishment is carried out, the omen is a black dragon emerging from a well."

    70

    汉文帝十二年，吴地有马生角，在耳前，上向，右角长三寸，左角长二寸，皆大二寸。刘向以为马不当生角，犹吴不当举兵向上也，吴将反之变云。京房易传曰：“臣易上，政不顺，厥妖马生角。兹谓贤士不足。”又曰：“天子亲伐，马生角。”
    　　文帝后元五年六月，齐雍城门外有狗生角。京房易传曰：“执政失下，将害之，厥妖狗生角。”
    　　汉景帝元年九月，胶东下密人，年七十余，生角，角有毛。京房易传曰：“冢宰专政，厥妖人生角。”五行志以为人不当生角，犹诸侯不敢举兵以向京师也。其后遂有七国之难。至晋武帝泰始五年，元城人，年七十，生角。殆赵王伦篡乱之应也。
    　　汉景帝三年，邯郸有狗与彘交，是时赵王悖乱，遂与六国反，外结、匈奴以为援。五行志以为：犬，兵革失众之占，豕，北方匈奴之象。逆言失听，交于异类，以生害也。京房易传曰：“夫妇不严，厥妖狗与豕交。兹谓反德，国有兵革。”

    Explanation

    70

    During the twelfth year of Emperor Wen of Han, a horse in the Wu region grew horns in front of its ears, pointing upwards. The right horn was three inches long, the left horn two inches long, and both were two inches wide. Duan Xia believed that a horse should not grow horns, just as Wu should not have raised arms against the central authority. This was seen as an omen of rebellion by Wu. Jing Fang's commentary on the I Ching states: "Officials replace superiors, leading to political disorder. The supernatural phenomenon of a horse growing horns. This indicates a shortage of virtuous officials." It also says: "If the emperor personally leads a campaign, a horse will grow horns."

    In the sixth month of the fifth year of Emperor Wen's posthumous reign, a dog in Qí outside the city gate of Yōng grew horns. Jing Fang's commentary on the I Ching states: "Officials fail to govern properly, leading to harm. The supernatural phenomenon of a dog growing horns."

    In the ninth month of the first year of Emperor Jing's reign, a person over seventy years old in Xia Mi, Jiadong, grew horns, with hair on the horns. Jing Fang's commentary on the I Ching states: "The chief minister exercises excessive power. The supernatural phenomenon of a person growing horns." The Wuxing Zhi (Treatise on the Five Elements) states that a person should not grow horns, just as feudal lords should not raise arms against the capital. Later, there was the rebellion of the Seven States. By the fifth year of the Tai Shi era of Emperor Wu of Jin, a person in Yuan Cheng, seventy years old, grew horns. This was likely a sign of the chaos caused by Zhao Wang Lun.

    In the third year of Emperor Jing's reign, a dog in Handan mated with a pig. At that time, the King of Zhao was behaving in a rebellious manner, joining with six other states in rebellion and forming an alliance with the Xiongnu for support. The Wuxing Zhi states that a dog mating with a pig is a sign of military disorder, with the pig representing the Xiongnu. Ignoring advice and mating with different species leads to harm. Jing Fang's commentary on the I Ching states: "If husband and wife are not strict, the supernatural phenomenon of a dog mating with a pig will occur. This indicates a reversal of virtue, leading to internal strife."

    71

    景帝三年十一月，有白颈乌与黑乌群斗楚国吕县：白颈不胜，堕泗水中死者数千。刘向以为近白黑祥也。时楚王戊暴逆无道，刑辱申公，与吴谋反。乌群斗者，师战之象也。白颈者小，明小者败也。堕于水者，将死水地。王戊不悟，遂举兵应吴，与汉大战，兵败而走，至于丹徒。为越人所斩，堕泗水之效也。京房易传曰：“逆亲亲，厥妖白黑乌斗于国中。”燕王旦之谋反也，又有一乌，一鹊，斗于燕宫中池上，乌堕池死。五行志以为楚、燕皆骨肉，藩臣骄恣，而谋不义，俱有乌鹊斗死之祥。行同而占合，此天人之明表也。燕阴谋未发，独王自杀于宫，故一乌而水色者死；楚炕阳举兵，军师大败于野，故乌众而金色者死：天道精微之效也。京房易传曰：“颛征劫杀，厥妖乌鹊斗。”

    Explanation

    71

    During the eleventh month of the third year of Emperor Jing's reign, there was a fight between white-necked crows and black crows in Lü County of the State of Chu: the white-necked crows were defeated, and thousands of them fell into the Si River and died. Liu Xiang interpreted this as a sign of good or bad fortune. At that time, King Wu of Chu was tyrannical and rebellious, punishing and humiliating Shen Gong, and conspiring with Wu to rebel against the Han dynasty. The fight between the crows was seen as a symbol of military conflict. The smaller white-necked crows represented the weaker side in the conflict. The crows that fell into the water were seen as predicting a watery death. King Wu of Chu did not realize the significance of the omen and subsequently raised an army to join Wu in rebellion. He then fought a great battle with the Han forces, suffered a defeat, and retreated to Dan Tu. He was ultimately killed by the Yue people, fulfilling the prediction of his watery death. Jing Fang's commentary on the Yijing states, "Rebellion against close relatives brings the omen of white and black crows fighting in the capital." During King Dan of Yan's rebellion, there was another incident where a crow and a magpie fought in the pool of the Yan palace, and the crow fell into the pool and died. The Wuxing Zhi interpreted both events as omens of rebellion by close relatives of the emperor, both of whom were proud and rebellious, and both had the omen of crows and magpies fighting and dying. The events were similar in nature and interpretation, clearly showing the interaction between heaven and humanity. The Yan plot was not discovered, and the king committed suicide in the palace, hence the crow that fell into the water died; King Wu of Chu raised his army in the heat of the sun, suffered a major defeat in the field, hence the black crows died: these were the subtle effects of the will of heaven. Jing Fang's commentary on the Yijing states, "Violence and rebellion bring the omen of crows and magpies fighting."

    72

    景帝十六年，梁孝王田北山，有献牛，足上出背上者。刘向以为近牛祸，内则思虑霿乱，外则土功过制，故牛祸作。足而出于背，下奸上之象也。
    　　汉武帝太始四年七月，赵有蛇从郭外入，与邑中蛇斗孝文庙下。邑中蛇死。后二年秋，有卫太子事，自赵人江充起。
    　　汉昭帝元凤元年九月，燕有黄鼠衔其尾舞王宫端门中。王往视之，鼠舞如故。王使吏以酒脯祠鼠，舞不休。一日一夜，死。时燕王旦谋反，将死之象也。京房易传曰：“诛不原情，厥妖鼠舞门。”

    Explanation

    72

    In the sixteenth year of Emperor Jing's reign, Duke Liang of Liang was hunting in the northern mountains when a cow was presented to him, with its hooves protruding from its back. Liu Xiang believed this was a sign of a cow disaster, indicating internal confusion and external excessive earthworks. The hooves protruding from the back symbolize lower elements undermining the upper ones.

    In the fourth month of the seventh year of Emperor Wu's Taishi era, a snake entered from outside the city wall of Zhao and fought with a snake from the city against the temple of Emperor Wen. The city's snake died. Two years later in autumn, there was an incident involving the Crown Prince Wei, initiated by Jiang Chong from Zhao.

    In the ninth month of the first year of Emperor Zhao's Yuanfeng era, a yellow rat appeared in Yan and entered from outside the city wall. It fought with a snake from the city against the temple of Emperor Wen, and the city's snake died. At that time, Prince Yan Dan was plotting rebellion, and this was a sign of impending death. According to the commentary on the I Ching by Jing Fang, "Not considering the circumstances of the crime, the omen is a rat dancing at the gate."

    73

    昭帝元凤三年正月，泰山芜莱山南汹汹有数千人声。民往视之，有大石自立，高丈五尺，大四十八围，入地深八尺，三石为足。石立后，有白乌数千集其旁。宣帝中兴之瑞也。
    　　昭帝时上林苑中，大柳树断仆地，一朝起立，生枝叶，有虫食其叶，成文字，曰：“公孙病已立。”
    　　昭帝时昌邑王贺见大白狗，冠“方山冠”而无尾。至熹平中，省内冠狗带绶以为笑乐，有一狗突出，走入司空府门，或见之者，莫不惊怪。京房易传曰：“君不正，臣欲篡，厥妖狗冠出朝门。”
    　　汉宣帝黄龙元年，未央殿辂軨中雌鸡化为雄，毛衣变化，而不鸣，不将，无距。元帝初元元年，丞相府史家雌鸡伏子，渐化为雄，冠距鸣将。至永光中有献雄鸡生角者。五行志以为王氏之应。京房易传曰：“贤者居明夷之世，知时而伤或众在位，厥妖鸡生角。”又曰：“妇人专政，国不静，牝鸡雄鸣，主不荣。”

    Explanation

    73

    In the first month of the third year of the Yuanshi era during Emperor Zhao's reign, there was a loud noise resembling thousands of people coming from the south of Mount Wulai on Mount Tai. When the locals went to investigate, they found a large stone standing up by itself. The stone was fifteen feet tall, had a circumference of forty-eight feet, was embedded eight feet deep into the ground, and had three stones as its base. After the stone stood up, thousands of white crows gathered around it. This event was considered a sign of the revival under Emperor Xuan.

    During Emperor Zhao's reign, in the Shanglin Park, a large willow tree broke and fell to the ground. One day, it stood up again and grew branches and leaves. Insects ate the leaves, forming the words "Gongsun Bingyi has been established."

    During Emperor Zhao's reign, King Changyi of Changyi saw a large white dog wearing a "Fangshan hat" but without a tail. By the Xiping period, inside the palace, dogs were worn with sashes for amusement. One day, a dog suddenly ran out and entered the door of the Siku official's residence, and those who saw it were all surprised. Jing Fang's Yi transmission states: "If the ruler is not upright, ministers may attempt to usurp power, and the sign of this is a dog wearing a hat appearing at the palace gate."

    In the year Huanglong of Emperor Xuan, a hen in the Luoling area of Weiyang Palace turned into a rooster. The hen turned into a rooster but did not crow, did not lead, and had no spurs. In the year Chuyuan of Emperor Yuan, a hen in the household of a historian in the Chancellor's office gradually turned into a rooster with spurs, crowing, and leading. By the year Yongguang, someone presented a rooster with horns. The Five Elements Records considered these events signs of the Wang family's rise. Jing Fang's Yi transmission states: "If a wise person lives in a dark age and feels sorrow over many people in power, the sign of this is a rooster with horns." It also states: "If women rule, the country will not be peaceful, and if a hen crows like a rooster, the ruler will not be honored."

    74

    宣帝之世，燕、岱之闲，有三男共取一妇，生四子，及至将分妻子而不可均，乃致争讼。廷尉范延寿断之曰：“此非人类，当以禽兽从母不从父也。”请戮三男，以儿还母。宣帝嗟叹曰：“事何必古，若此，则可谓当于理而厌人情也。”延寿盖见人事而知用刑矣，未知论人妖将来之验也。
    　　汉元帝永光二年八月，天雨草，而叶相樛结，大如弹丸。至平帝元始三年正月，天雨草，状如永光时。京房易传曰：“君吝于禄，信衰，贤去，厥妖天雨草。”
    　　元帝建昭五年，兖州刺史浩赏，禁民私所自立社。山阳橐茅乡社有大槐树，吏伐断之，其夜树复立故处。说曰：“凡枯断复起，皆废而复兴之象也。”是世祖之应耳。

    Explanation

    74

    During the reign of Emperor Xuan, in the region between Yan and Dai, there were three men who shared one wife and had four sons. When it came time to divide the family and the children could not be equally distributed, a dispute arose. The Grand Judge Fan Yan寿 adjudicated and said, "This is not human; it should be treated as an animal, following the mother rather than the father." He proposed executing the three men and returning the child to the mother. Emperor Xuan sighed and said, "Why must things be done according to ancient practices? If this is the case, it can be said to be in accordance with reason but unsatisfactory to human emotions." Fan Yan寿 saw the human situation and knew how to apply punishment, but he did not know the future implications of human anomalies.

    In the eighth month of the second year of Emperor Yuan's Yongguang era, it rained grass, and the leaves intertwined, as large as bullets. In the first month of the third year of Emperor Ping's Yuanshi era, it rained grass again, similar to the time of Yongguang. Jing Fang's Yijing commentary says, "The ruler is stingy with rewards, trust is declining, and the virtuous are leaving. The anomaly is the rain of grass."

    In the fifth year of Emperor Yuan's Jianzhao era, the governor of Yan Prefecture, Hao Shang, prohibited the people from privately establishing shrines. In the shrine of Tuomao Village, Shanyang, there was a large locust tree. An official cut it down, but that night it stood up again in its original place. It is said, "Any dead thing that rises again is a sign of abandonment and revival." This is the response of the founding ancestor.

    75

    汉成帝建始四年九月，长安城南，有鼠衔黄稿柏叶，上民冢柏及榆树上为巢，桐柏为多，巢中无子，皆有干鼠矢数升。时议臣以为恐有水灾。鼠盗窃小虫，夜出，昼匿，今正昼去穴而登木，象贱人将居贵显之占。桐柏，卫思后园所在也，其后赵后自微贱登至尊，与卫后同类，赵后终无子，而为害。明年，有鸢焚巢杀子之象云。京房易传曰：“臣私禄罔干，厥妖鼠巢。”
    　　成帝河平元年，长安男子石良、刘音相与同居，有如人状，在其室中，击之，为狗，走出。去后，有数人披甲，持弓弩至良家。良等格击，或死，或伤，皆狗也。自二月至六月，乃止。其于洪范，皆犬祸，言不从之咎也。
    　　成帝河平元年二月庚子，泰山山桑谷，有鸢焚其巢。男子孙通等闻山中群鸟鸢鹊声，往视之，见巢燃，尽堕池中，有三鸢鷇，烧死。树大四围，巢去地五丈五尺。易曰：“鸟焚其巢，旅人先笑后号咷。”后卒成易世之祸云。

    Explanation

    75

    In the fourth year of the Jian Shi era during the reign of Emperor Cheng of Han, in the ninth month, in the southern part of Chang'an, there were mice carrying yellow straw and cypress leaves, building nests on cypress trees and willows above graves, with the most occurrences in Tongbai. The nests were empty and contained several sheng of dried mouse droppings. At the time, the ministers believed this was a sign of an impending flood. Mice, which are small and steal, usually come out at night and hide during the day, but now they were active during the day, leaving their burrows and climbing trees, which was seen as an omen that lowly people would soon occupy high positions. Tongbai was the location of the garden of Empress Wei Si. Later, Empress Zhao rose from a lowly position to become the most honored, similar to Empress Wei Si. Empress Zhao remained childless and caused harm. The following year, there was a sign of an eagle burning its nest and killing its young. According to Jing Fang's Commentary on the Changes, "Officials taking private benefits would lead to the omen of mice building nests."

    In the first year of the He Ping era during the reign of Emperor Cheng of Han, in the second month on the day Gengzi, in the Shan Sang Valley of Mount Tai, there was an eagle burning its nest. Men named Sun Tong and others heard the sounds of birds and eagles in the mountains and went to see. They found the nest burning and falling into a pond, with three eagle chicks dying. The tree was four zhi around, and the nest was five zhang and five chi above the ground. The I Ching says, "When the bird's nest is burned, the traveler first laughs and then weeps." This eventually led to a change in the ruling dynasty.

    In the first year of the He Ping era during the reign of Emperor Cheng of Han, in the second month, in Chang'an, two men named Shi Liang and Liu Yin lived together. There was a figure resembling a human in their room. When they attacked it, it turned into a dog and ran away. After it left, several men in armor with bows and arrows arrived at Shi Liang's house. Shi Liang and others fought them, and some died or were injured, and they were all dogs. This continued from the second to the sixth month before stopping. According to the Great Plan, these were all signs of dog-related disasters, indicating the consequences of not following orders.

    76

    成帝鸿嘉四年秋，雨鱼于信都，长五寸以下。至永始元年春，北海出大鱼，长六丈，高一丈，四枚。哀帝建平三年，东莱平度出大鱼，长八丈，高一丈一尺，七枚。皆死。灵帝熹平二年，东莱海出大鱼二枚，长八九丈，高二丈余。京房易传曰：“海数见巨鱼，邪人进，贤人疏。”
    　　成帝永始元年二月，河南街邮樗树生枝，如人头，眉目须皆具，亡发耳。至哀帝建平三年十月，汝南西平遂阳乡有材仆地生枝，如人形，身青黄色，面白，头有髭发，稍长大，凡长六寸一分。京房易传曰：“王德衰，下人将起，则有木生为人状”。其后有王莽之篡。
    　　成帝绥和二年二月，大厩马生角，在左耳前，围长各二寸。是时王莽为大司马，害上之萌，自此始矣。
    　　成帝绥和二年三月，天水平襄有燕生雀，哺食至大，俱飞去。京房易传曰：“贼臣在国，厥咎燕生雀，诸侯销。”又曰：“生非其类，子不嗣世。”

    Explanation

    76

    In the fourth year of the Hongjia era of Emperor Cheng, during the autumn, fish rained down in Xindu, each measuring no more than five cun in length. By the spring of the first year of the Yongshi era, a great fish emerged from Beihai, measuring six zhang in length and one zhang in height, with four such fish appearing. In the third year of the Jianping era of Emperor Ai, a great fish appeared in Pingdu of Donglai, measuring eight zhang in length and one zhang one chi in height, with seven such fish appearing. All of them died. In the second year of the Xiping era of Emperor Ling, two great fish emerged from the sea of Donglai, each measuring eight to nine zhang in length and more than two zhang in height. The Jing Fang Commentary on the Book of Changes states: "When the sea frequently produces great fish, it signifies that wicked men will rise to power and virtuous men will be sidelined."

    In the second month of the first year of the Yongshi era of Emperor Cheng, a branch grew from a chū tree at the street post of Henan, resembling a human head, with eyebrows, eyes, and beard all clearly formed, though it lacked hair on the ears. By the tenth month of the third year of the Jianping era of Emperor Ai, in Suoyang village of Xiping, Ruanan, a piece of wood fell to the ground and sprouted a branch in the shape of a human figure, with a body of greenish-yellow color, a white face, and a head with beard and hair. It gradually grew larger, eventually reaching a total length of six cun and one fen. The Jing Fang Commentary on the Book of Changes states: "When the virtue of the king declines and the lower people rise, trees will grow in the shape of human beings." After this, Wang Mang usurped the throne.

    In the second month of the second year of the Suhe era of Emperor Cheng, a horn grew on a horse in the imperial stables, located in front of the left ear, with a circumference and length of two cun each. At that time, Wang Mang was serving as Grand Commandant, and the seeds of treachery against the emperor began from this moment.
