    In the third month of the second year of the Suhe era of Emperor Cheng, in Pingxiang of Tianshui, a swallow gave birth to a sparrow, which grew to a large size and then flew away together with its mother. The Jing Fang Commentary on the Book of Changes states: "When a traitorous minister exists within the state, the omen is a swallow giving birth to a sparrow, leading to the downfall of the feudal lords." It also says: "When something is born that does not belong to its kind, its descendants will not inherit the throne."

    77

    汉哀帝建平三年，定襄有牡马生驹三足，随群饮食，五行志以为：马，国之武用。三足，不任用之象也。
    　　哀帝建平三年，零陵有树僵地，围一丈六尺，长十丈七尺，民断其本，长九尺余，皆枯，三月，树卒自立故处。京房易传曰：“弃正，作淫，厥妖本断自属。妃后有颛，木仆，反立，断枯，复生。”
    　　哀帝建平四年四月，山阳方与女子田无啬生子，未生二月前，儿啼腹中，及生，不举，葬之陌上。后三日，有人过，闻儿啼声。母因掘收养之。
    　　哀帝建平四年夏，京师郡国民聚会里巷阡陌，设张博具歌舞，嗣西王母。又传书曰：“母告百姓：佩此书者，不死。不信我言，视门枢下，当有白发。”至秋乃止。
    　　哀帝建平中，豫章有男子化为女子，嫁为人妇，生一子。长安陈凤曰：“阳变为阴，将亡；继嗣，自相生之象”。一曰：“嫁为人妇，生一子者，将复一世，乃绝。”故后哀帝崩，平帝没，而王莽篡焉。

    Explanation

    77

    In the third year of the Jianping era of Emperor Ai of Han, a male horse in Dingxiang gave birth to a three-legged foal, which followed the herd in eating and drinking. The Wuxing Zhi (Book of the Five Elements) interpreted this as a sign: "Horses are the martial tools of the state. Three legs are an omen of uselessness."

    In the third year of the Jianping era, a tree in Lingling fell to the ground, with a circumference of one zhang six chi and a length of ten zhang seven chi. The people cut its base, leaving it nine chi or more, all of which withered. After three months, the tree suddenly stood upright in its original place. The Yi Zhuan (Commentary on the Book of Changes) by Jing Fang said: "Abandoning the proper, indulging in excess, the omen is that the root will be cut and belong to itself. The empress has dominance, the tree falls, stands again, is cut and withered, but regrows."

    In the fourth month of the fourth year of the Jianping era, a woman named Tian Wuse in Fangyu, Shanyang, gave birth to a son. Two months before birth, the child cried in her womb. Upon birth, the child was not raised and buried on the road. Three days later, someone passing by heard the child's cry. The mother then dug up the child and raised him.

    In the summer of the fourth year of the Jianping era, the people of the capital and the counties gathered in the lanes and fields, setting up gambling tools and singing and dancing in honor of the Western Mother. Another book was transmitted saying: "The mother tells the people: 'Those who wear this book will not die. If you do not believe me, look under the door hinge; there will be white hair.'" By autumn, it ceased.

    In the middle of the Jianping era, a man in Yuzhang transformed into a woman, married, and had a son. Chang'an's Chen Feng said: "Yang transforming into yin, foretells death; the heir, a self-generating image." Another interpretation was: "Married as a woman, bearing a son, will repeat once, then cease." Thus, after Emperor Ai died, Emperor Ping died, and Wang Mang usurped the throne.

    78

    汉平帝元始元年二月，朔方广牧女子赵春病死，既棺殓，积七日，出在棺外。自言见夫死父，曰：“年二十七，汝不当死。”太守谭以闻，说曰：“至阴为阳，下人为上。厥妖人死复生。”其后王莽篡位。
    　　汉平帝元始元年六月，长安有女子生儿：两头，两颈面，俱相向；四臂，共胸，俱前向；尻上有目，长二寸所。京房易传曰：“暌孤见豕负涂，厥妖人生两头，下相攘。善妖，亦同人。若六畜，首目在下。”兹谓亡上，政将变更。厥妖之作，以谴失正，各象其类。两颈，下不一也。手多，所任邪也。足少，下不胜任，或不任下也。凡下体生于上，不敬也；上体生于下，媟渎也。生非其类，淫乱也；人生而大，上速成也；生而能言，好虚也。群妖推此类。不改，乃成凶也。

    Explanation

    78

    In the first year of Yuanshi during the reign of Emperor Ping of Han, in the second month, a woman named Zhao Chun from Shuofang Guangmu died of illness. After she was placed in a coffin, seven days later, she appeared outside the coffin. She claimed to have seen her deceased father, who said, "You are twenty-seven years old; you should not have died." The governor Tan reported this to the court, explaining, "Extreme cold becomes warmth, the lowly rise to the high. Such a marvel, a person dying and coming back to life." Later, Wang Mang seized the throne.

    In the first year of Yuanshi during the reign of Emperor Ping of Han, in the sixth month, a woman in Chang'an gave birth to a child with two heads, two necks facing each other, four arms all attached to the chest and facing forward, and eyes on the buttocks, about two inches long. The Commentary on the Yi by Jing Fang states, "The separation of the lonely, seeing pigs carrying mud, such a marvel, a person being born with two heads, the lower taking from each other. Good omens, also like people. If like livestock, with heads and eyes below." This is called losing the superior, the government will undergo changes. Such marvels are created to punish the loss of correctness, each representing its own kind. Two necks, the lower is not unified. Many hands, the one appointed is corrupt. Few feet, the lower cannot bear the burden, or does not bear the lower. All lower parts growing above, it is disrespectful; upper parts growing below, it is disrespectful. Born not of its kind, it is licentious; born large, the upper quickly completes; born able to speak, it is fond of emptiness. All marvels follow this pattern. If not changed, it becomes an omen of disaster.

    79

    汉章帝元和元年，代郡高柳乌生子，三足，大如鸡，色赤，头有角，长寸余。
    　　汉桓帝即位，有大蛇见德阳殿上。洛阳市令淳于翼曰：“蛇有鳞，甲兵之象也；见于省中，将有椒房大臣受甲兵之象也。”乃弃官遁去。到延熹二年，诛大将军梁冀，捕治家属，扬兵京师也。
    　　汉桓帝建和三年秋七月，北地廉雨肉，似羊肋，或大如手。是时梁太后摄政，梁冀专权，擅杀，诛太尉李固、杜乔，天下冤之。其后，梁氏诛灭。
    　　汉桓帝元嘉中，京都妇女作“愁眉”“啼妆”“堕马髻”“折腰步”“龋齿笑。”“愁眉”者，细而曲折。“啼七”者，薄拭目下若啼处。“堕马髻”者，作一边。“折腰步”者，足不在下体。“龋齿笑”者，若齿痛，乐不欣欣。始自大将军梁冀妻孙寿所为，京都翕然，诸夏效之。天戒若曰：“兵马将往收捕：妇女忧愁，踧眉啼哭；吏卒掣顿，折其腰脊，令髻邪倾；虽强语笑，无复气味也。”到延熹二年，冀举宗合诛。

    Explanation

    79

    In the first year of the Yuanhe era of Emperor Zhang of Han, a three-legged bird with a red color and horns, about the size of a chicken, was born in Gao Liu, Dai Commandery.

    After Emperor Huan of Han ascended the throne, a large snake appeared on the De Yang Palace. The magistrate of Luoyang, Chunyu Yi, said, "Snakes have scales, which symbolize military force; their appearance in the imperial palace indicates that a powerful minister will be involved in military matters." He then resigned and fled. By the second year of the Yuanxi era, the Grand General Liang Ji was executed, and his family was arrested and punished, displaying military power in the capital.

    In the seventh month of autumn in the third year of the Jianhe era of Emperor Huan of Han, meat rained down in the north, resembling sheep ribs, some as large as a hand. At that time, Empress Dowager Liang was regent, and Liang Ji held absolute power, committing arbitrary killings. He executed the Grand Commandant Li Gu and Du Qiao, and the whole country mourned them. Afterward, the Liang family was exterminated.

    During the Yuangjia era of Emperor Huan of Han, women in the capital made up their eyebrows in a sorrowful style, wore tearful makeup, styled their hair in a drooping manner, walked with bent waists, and laughed with clenched teeth. "Sorrowful eyebrows" were fine and curved; "tearful makeup" was lightly applied under the eyes; "drooping hair" was styled to one side; "bent waist walk" involved walking with a bent waist; "clenched-toothed laugh" resembled laughing with clenched teeth. These trends started by the wife of Grand General Liang Ji, Sun Shou. The capital followed suit, and all regions emulated this. Heaven seems to say, "Soldiers will go to capture: women will be sad, frown and cry; officials and soldiers will drag and pull, bend their backs, make their hair tilt to one side; even if they force a laugh, there will be no joy left." By the second year of the Yuanxi era, Liang Ji and his entire clan were executed.

    80

    桓帝延熹五年，临沅县有牛生鸡，两头四足。
    　　汉灵帝数游戏于西园中，令后宫采女为客舍主人，身为估服，行至舍，问采女下酒食，因共饮食，以为戏乐。是天子将欲失位，降在皂隶之谣也。其后天下大乱。古志有曰：“赤厄三七。”三七者经二百一十载，当有外戚之篡。丹眉之妖，篡盗短祚，极于三六，当有飞龙之秀，兴复祖宗。又历三七，当复有黄首之妖，天下大乱矣。自高祖建业，至于平帝之末，二百一十年，而王莽篡，盖因母后之亲。十八年而山东贼樊子都等起，实丹其眉，故天下号曰“赤眉。

    Explanation

    80

    In the fifth year of Emperor Huan's reign during the Eastern Han dynasty, a cow in Linyuan County gave birth to a chicken with two heads and four feet.

    Emperor Ling of Han frequently played in the West Garden, ordering the palace ladies to act as innkeepers. He dressed up as a merchant, walking to the inn and asking the ladies to serve wine and food. They enjoyed meals together, considering it a form of entertainment. This was interpreted as a sign of the emperor's impending downfall and demotion to a lowly status. Following this event, widespread chaos ensued.

    Ancient records mention, "There will be a period of calamity lasting three sevens." Three sevens refer to a period of 210 years, during which there will be a usurpation by an external family member. The red-haired or red-mustached figure, associated with rebellion, will have a short-lived usurpation, lasting for three sixes, or 18 years. Then, a remarkable figure, often associated with a hero or savior, will emerge to restore the imperial lineage. After another period of 210 years, there will be another calamity associated with a figure with yellow hair or beard, leading to widespread chaos once again.

    From the founding of the Han dynasty by Emperor Gaozu to the end of Emperor Ping's reign, spanning 210 years, Wang Mang usurped the throne, likely due to the influence of the empress dowager. Eighteen years later, rebels led by Fan Zidu rose in Shandong, with red hair or mustaches, and were known as the "Red Eyebrows."

    81

    ”于是光武以兴祚，其名曰秀。至于灵帝中平元年，而张角起，置三十六方，徒众数十万，皆是黄巾，故天下号曰“黄巾贼，”至今道服，由此而兴。初起于邺，会于真定，诳感百姓曰：“苍天已死，黄天立。岁名甲子年，天下大吉。”起于邺者，天下始业也，会于真定也。小民相向跪拜趋信。荆、扬尤甚。乃弃财产，流沈道路，死者无数。角等初以二月起兵，其冬十二月悉破。自光武中兴至黄巾之起，未盈二百一十年，而天下大乱。汉祚废绝，实应三七之运。
    　　灵帝建宁中，男子之衣好为长服，而下甚短；女子好为长裾，而上甚短。是阳无下而阴无上，天下未欲平也。后遂大乱。

    Explanation

    81

    Emperor Guangwu founded the Eastern Han Dynasty, and his successor was named Liu Xiu. By the first year of Emperor Ling's Zhongping era, Zhang Jiao rose up, establishing 36 regions with a following of hundreds of thousands. All of them wore yellow turbans, and thus they were called "Yellow Turban Rebels." To this day, Taoist clothing has become widespread, originating from this movement. The rebellion began in Ye and gathered in Zhending, where they deceived the people with the slogan: "The sky of the old era has died, and the yellow sky has risen. In the year of Jiazi, the world will be greatly blessed." The rebellion began in Ye, marking the start of the era, and gathered in Zhending. The common people knelt and bowed to one another, believing in the movement. The provinces of Jing and Yang were particularly affected. People abandoned their property, wandering the roads, and countless died. Zhang Jiao and his followers initially rose in February and were completely defeated by December. From the rise of Emperor Guangwu to the outbreak of the Yellow Turban Rebellion, less than 210 years passed, and the world fell into chaos. The Han Dynasty's legacy was extinguished, truly fulfilling the prophecy of the 210-year cycle.

    In the Jianning era of Emperor Ling, men's clothing favored long robes with very short hems, while women's clothing favored long skirts with very short upper sections. This symbolized a lack of balance between the yang and yin, indicating that the world was not yet at peace. Subsequently, great chaos ensued.

    82

    灵帝建宁三年春，河内有妇食夫，河南有夫食妇。夫妇阴阳，二仪有情之深者也。今反相食，阴阳相侵，岂特日月之眚哉。灵帝既没，天下大乱，君有妄诛之暴，臣有劫弒之逆，兵革相残，骨肉为雠，生民之祸极矣。故人妖为之先作。而恨不遭辛有、屠乘之论，以测其情也。
    　　灵帝熹平二年六月，雒阳民讹言：虎贲寺东壁中，有黄人，形容须眉良是。观者数万。省内悉出，道路断绝。到中平元年二月，张角兄弟起兵冀州，自号“黄天”。三十六方，四面出和。将帅星布，吏士外属。因其疲餧牵而胜之。
    　　灵帝熹平三年，右校别作中，有两樗树，皆高四尺所，其一枝宿昔暴长，长一丈余，麤大一围，作胡人状，头目鬓须发俱具。其五年，十月壬午，正殿侧有槐树，皆六七围，自拔，倒竖，根上枝下。又中平中长安城西北六七里，空树中，有人面，生鬓。其于洪范皆为木不曲直。

    Explanation

    82

    Emperor Ling's Jianning third year in spring, in Hebei, there was a woman who ate her husband, and in Henan, there was a man who ate his wife. Husband and wife embody the profound emotional connection of yin and yang, the two fundamental principles. Now they have turned to cannibalism, with yin and yang invading each other—this is not just a minor celestial disturbance. After Emperor Ling's death, the world fell into chaos, with rulers committing unjust killings and officials rebelling. Armies clashed, kin turned against each other, and the suffering of the people reached its peak. Therefore, unnatural phenomena appeared as precursors. I regret not living in the time of scholars like Xin You and Tu Cheng, who could provide deeper insights into these events.

    In the second month of Emperor Ling's Xiping era, rumors spread in Luoyang: In the eastern wall of the Tiger Banner Temple, there was a yellow-skinned person, whose appearance, eyebrows, and beard were remarkably lifelike. Thousands gathered to see it, causing the inner palace to empty and traffic to be cut off. By the first month of the Zhongping era, Zhang Jiao and his brothers rose up in rebellion in Jizhou, calling themselves "Yellow Heaven." The rebellion spread in all directions, with thirty-six factions emerging. Generals were scattered like stars, and officials and soldiers defected. The rebels were ultimately defeated due to their own exhaustion and lack of resources.

    In the third year of Emperor Ling's Xiping era, in a specific area, there were two large elm trees, both about four feet tall. One branch of one of the trees grew rapidly overnight, reaching over ten feet in length, with a circumference of one zhang, taking on the appearance of a foreigner, complete with head, eyes, hair, beard, and mustache. In the fifth year, on the day of Renshu in October, near the main hall, there was a locust tree, six to seven zhang in circumference, which uprooted itself and grew upside down, with roots above and branches below. Additionally, during the Zhongping era, in the northwest of Chang'an, about six to seven li away, a face with hair appeared inside an empty tree. According to the Book of Changes, these phenomena are signs of disorder in the natural world.

    83

    灵帝光和元年，南宫侍中寺雌鸡欲化为雄，一身毛皆似雄，但头冠尚未变。
    　　灵帝光和二年，洛阳上西门外女子生儿：两头，异肩，共胸，俱前。向以为不祥，堕地，弃之。自是之后，朝廷霿乱，政在私门，上下无别，二头之象。后董卓戮太后。被以不孝之名，放废天子，后复害之，汉元以来，祸莫踰此。
    　　光和四年，南宫中黄门寺有一男子，长九尺，服白衣，中黄门解步呵问：“汝何等人？”白衣妄入宫掖，曰：“我梁伯夏。后天使我为天子。”步欲前收之，因忽不见。
    　　光和七年陈留、济阳、长垣、济阴、东郡、冤句、离狐界中路边生草，悉作人状，操持兵弩；牛马龙蛇鸟兽之形，白黑各如其色，羽毛头目足翅皆备，非但彷佛，像之尤纯。旧说曰：“近草妖也。”是岁有黄巾贼起，汉遂微弱。

    Explanation

    83

    During the first year of Emperor Ling's Guanghe era, a hen chicken in the South Palace's Attendant-in-Attendance residence appeared to be transforming into a rooster, with feathers resembling those of a rooster, but its head crest had not yet changed.

    In the second year of Emperor Ling's Guanghe era, a woman in Luoyang gave birth to a child outside the western gate of the city: the child had two heads, different shoulders, a shared chest, and both heads facing forward. People considered it an omen of bad luck and abandoned the child. From then on, the court became disordered, with politics dominated by private interests, no distinction between public and private life, symbolized by the two-headed child. Later, Dong Zhuo killed Empress Dowager He, was accused of filial impiety, deposed the emperor, and later killed him. Since the founding of the Han dynasty, there was no greater calamity than this.

    In the fourth year of Emperor Ling's Guanghe era, a man nine feet tall, dressed in white, appeared at the Yellow Gate Attendant's residence in the South Palace. The Yellow Gate Attendant Xie Bu questioned him, asking, "Who are you?" The man claimed to be Liang Bexia and said that he was appointed by the heavens to be emperor. Xie Bu tried to apprehend him, but the man suddenly disappeared.

    In the seventh year of Emperor Ling's Guanghe era, grass grew along the roadside in the regions of Chenliu, Jiyang, Changyuan, Jiyin, Dongjun, Yuanju, and Lixu. The grass appeared to be human figures holding weapons. It also took the forms of cows, horses, dragons, snakes, birds, and beasts, with distinct colors and features, including feathers, heads, eyes, feet, and wings. These figures were not just vaguely similar to animals but were highly detailed and realistic. According to ancient sayings, this was a sign of grass demons. That same year, the Yellow Turban Rebellion broke out, and the Han dynasty began to weaken.

    84

    灵帝中平元年六月壬申，雒阳男子刘仓，居上西门外，妻生男，两头共身。至建安中，女子生男，亦两头共身。
    　　中平三年八月中，怀陵上有万余雀，先极悲鸣，已因乱斗，相杀，皆断头悬着树枝枳棘。到六年，灵帝崩。夫陵者，高大之象也；雀者，爵也。天戒若曰：“诸怀爵禄而尊厚者，还自相害，至灭亡也。”
    　　汉时，京师宾婚嘉会，皆作“魁櫑，”酒酣之后，续以“挽歌。”“魁櫑，”丧家之乐；“挽歌，”执绋相偶和之者。天戒若曰：“国家当急殄悴，诸贵乐皆死亡也。”自灵帝崩后，京师坏灭，户有兼尸，虫而相食者，“魁櫑”“挽歌”斯之效乎？
    　　灵帝之末，京师谣言曰：“侯非侯，王非王。千乘万骑上北邙。”到中平六年，史侯登蹑至尊，献帝未有爵号，为中常侍段圭等所执，公卿百僚，皆随其后，到河上，乃得还。

    Explanation

    84

    In the first year of the Zhongping era of Emperor Ling, on the day Ren Shen in June, a man named Liu Cang from Luoyang, residing outside the western gate of the upper city, had a wife who gave birth to a son with two heads on one body. By the Jian'an period, another woman gave birth to a son with the same condition.

    In the third year of the Zhongping era, during August, tens of thousands of sparrows were seen at the Mausoleum of Emperor Ling, crying out in extreme sorrow before engaging in chaotic fighting and killing each other, with their heads severed and hanging from thorny branches. By the sixth year, Emperor Ling passed away. The mausoleum symbolizes something grand and elevated; sparrows symbolize titles or ranks. It seems the heavens were warning, saying, "Those who hold titles and wealth and are esteemed will harm each other, leading to their destruction."

    During the Han dynasty, at grand gatherings in the capital for weddings and other celebrations, the music "Kuaili" was played, followed by "Wangge" after the guests were drunk. "Kuaili" is music associated with funerals, and "Wangge" is a song sung by mourners who hold ropes and sing in harmony. It seems the heavens were warning, saying, "The country is about to face great disaster, and all the nobles and their pleasures will perish." After Emperor Ling's death, the capital fell into ruin, with households containing multiple corpses, some being eaten by insects. Could this be the effect of "Kuaili" and "Wangge"?

    Towards the end of Emperor Ling's reign, there were rumors in the capital that said, "A marquis is not a marquis, a king is not a king. Thousands of chariots and tens of thousands of horses ascend Mount Beimang." By the sixth year of the Zhongping era, a marquis ascended to the highest position, while Emperor Xian, who had no title, was seized by eunuchs including Duan Gui, with all the high officials and courtiers following him, and they were allowed to return only when they reached the river.

    85

    汉献帝初平中，长沙有人姓桓氏，死，棺敛月余，其母闻棺中有声，发之，遂生。占曰：“至阴为阳，下人为上。”其后曹公由庶士起。
    　　献帝建安七年，越隽有男子化为女子，时周群上言：哀帝时亦有此变，将有易代之事。至二十五年，献帝封山阳公。
    　　建安初荆州童谣曰：“八九年间始欲衰，至十三年无孑遗。”言自中兴以来，荆州独全；及刘表为牧，民有丰乐；至建安九年，当始衰。始衰者，谓刘表妻死，诸将并零落也。十三年无孑遗者，表当又死，因以丧败也。是时华容有女子，忽啼呼曰：“将有大丧。”言语过差，县以为妖言，系狱，月余，忽于狱中哭曰：“刘荆州今日死。华□□□□□(编者按：原缺。)里即遣马里验视，而刘表果死。县乃出之。续又歌吟曰：“不意李立为贵人。”后无几，曹公平荆州，以涿郡李立，字建贤，为荆州刺史。

    Explanation

    85

    During the early years of Emperor Xian's reign in the Chuping era, a woman surnamed Huang in Changsha died, was buried, and remained in her coffin for over a month. Her mother heard a sound coming from the coffin and opened it, only to find her daughter had come back to life. An interpretation was made: "Extreme yin becomes yang, the lowly become exalted." Later, Cao Cao rose from an ordinary official to become a powerful warlord.

    In the seventh year of Emperor Xian's reign in the Jian'an era, a man in Yuejun transformed into a woman. At that time, Zhou Jun reported: "Such a transformation also occurred during the reign of Emperor Ai, foreshadowing a change of dynasties." By the twenty-fifth year, Emperor Xian was enfeoffed as the King of Shanyang.

    In the early years of the Jian'an era, a children's rhyme in Jingzhou said: "Between the eighth and ninth years, things will begin to decline; by the thirteenth year, there will be no survivors." This referred to the fact that since the revival of the Han dynasty, Jingzhou had remained intact; when Liu Biao became its governor, the people enjoyed prosperity. By the ninth year of Jian'an, things began to decline, which was interpreted as Liu Biao's wife dying and his generals falling. By the thirteenth year, there would be no survivors, as Liu Biao was expected to die, leading to the downfall of Jingzhou. At that time, a woman in Huarong suddenly cried out: "A great death is coming." Her words were considered overly extreme, and the county authorities imprisoned her as a troublemaker. After a month, she suddenly cried out in her prison cell: "Governor Liu of Jingzhou will die today." The county immediately sent someone to verify, and indeed, Liu Biao died that day. The county then released her. She continued to sing: "Who would have thought Li Li would become a noble?" Soon after, Cao Cao conquered Jingzhou and appointed Li Li, a man from Zhuo County with the courtesy name Jianxian, as the governor of Jingzhou.

    86

    建安二十五年正月，魏武在洛阳起建始殿，伐濯龙树而血出。又掘徒梨，根伤，而血出。魏武恶之，遂寝疾，是月崩，是岁，为魏武黄初元年。
    　　魏黄初元年，未央宫中有鹰，生燕巢中，口爪俱赤。至青龙中，明帝为凌霄阁，始构，有鹊巢其上。帝以问高堂隆，对曰：“诗云：‘惟鹊有巢，惟鸠居之。’今兴起宫室，而鹊来巢，此宫室未成，身不得居之象也。”

    Explanation

    86

    In the first month of the 25th year of the Jian'an era, Wei Wu (Cao Cao) was building the Jianshi Hall in Luoyang when he cut down a tree and blood flowed from it. He then dug up another tree, injuring its roots, and blood flowed from them as well. Wei Wu considered these signs unfavorable and soon fell ill; he died that month. This year marked the beginning of the Huangchu era, the reign of Wei Wu (Cao Pi).

    In the first year of the Huangchu era, there was an eagle born in a swallow's nest in the Weiyang Palace, with both its mouth and claws red. During the Qinglong era, Emperor Ming began constructing the Lingxiao Pavilion. Just as the construction started, a magpie nested on top of it. The emperor asked Gao Tanglong about this, who replied: "The Book of Songs says, 'The magpie has a nest, but the jay occupies it.' Now that we are building palaces, and a magpie comes to nest, this is an omen that the palace will not be completed, and the emperor will not be able to live in it."

    87

    魏齐王嘉平初，白马河出妖马，夜过官牧边鸣呼，众马皆应；明日，见其迹，大如斛，行数里，还入河。
    　　魏景初元年，有燕生巨鷇于卫国李盖家，形若鹰，吻似燕。高堂隆曰：“此魏室之大异，宜防鹰扬之臣，于萧墙之内。”其后宣帝起，诛曹爽，遂有魏室。
    　　蜀景耀五年，宫中大树无故自折。谯周深忧之，无所与言，乃书柱曰：“众而大，期之会。具而授，若何复。”言：曹者，大也。众而大，天下其当会也。具而授，如何复有立者乎。蜀既亡，咸以周言为验。
    　　吴孙权太元元年八月朔，大风，江海涌溢，平地水深八尺，拔高陵树二千株，石碑差动，吴城两门飞落。明年权死。
    　　吴孙亮五凤元年六月，交址稗草化为稻。昔三苗将亡，五谷变种。此草妖也。其后亮废。
    　　吴孙亮五凤二年五月，阳羡县离里山大石自立。是时孙皓承废故之家得复其位之应也。

    Explanation

    87

    In the early years of the Jiaqing era of King Qi of Wei, a supernatural horse emerged from the Bai Ma River, passing through the government pastures at night and calling out. The other horses all responded. The next day, its tracks were found, as large as a hu, having traveled several li before returning to the river.

    In the first year of the Jingchu era of Wei, a large nestling was born in the home of Li Gai in the state of Wei. It had the shape of an eagle and the beak of a swallow. Gao Tang Long said, "This is a great anomaly for the Wei dynasty. It is advisable to guard against the 'flying eagle' officials within the inner walls." Later, Emperor Xuan rose to power, executed Cao Shuang, and thus came to control the Wei dynasty.

    In the fifth year of the Jingyao era of Shu, a large tree in the palace courtyard broke off without cause. Qiao Zhou deeply worried about this, but had no one to discuss it with, so he wrote on a pillar, "Many and great, the time of gathering. Complete and bestow, how can there be another?" He said, "Cao means great. Many and great, the world will surely gather. Complete and bestow, how can there be another who can stand?" After Shu fell, everyone considered Qiao Zhou's words to be true.

    In the first month of the Taiyuan era of Sun Quan, a great wind blew, causing rivers and seas to overflow. The water level rose eight chi above the ground, uprooting two thousand trees in Gaoling, slightly moving stone steles, and causing two gates of Wu City to fly off. The following year, Sun Quan died.

    In the first month of the Wufeng era of Sun Liang, wild grass in Jiaozhi transformed into rice. When Sanmiao was about to perish, the five grains changed species. This was a grass anomaly. Later, Sun Liang was deposed.

    In the second month of the Wufeng era of Sun Liang, a large stone in Lili Mountain in Yangxian County stood up on its own. At that time, it was a sign that Sun Hao would succeed the throne after the deposed family.

    88

    吴孙休永安四年，安吴民陈焦死，七日，复生，穿冢出乌程。孙皓承废故之家得位之祥也。
    　　孙休后，衣服之制，上长，下短，又积领五六，而裳居一二。盖上饶奢，下俭逼，上有余，下不足之象也。
    搜神记卷七
    　　初，汉元、成之世，先识之士有言曰：“魏年有和，当有开石于西三千余里，系五马，文曰：‘大讨曹。’”及魏之初兴也，张掖之柳谷，有开石焉：始见于建安，形成于黄初，文备于太和，周围七寻，中高一仞，苍质素章：龙、马、鳞、鹿、凤凰、仙人之象，粲然咸着。此一事者，魏、晋代兴之符也。至晋泰始三年，张掖太守焦胜上言：以留郡本国图，校今石文，文字多少不同，谨具图上。案其文有五马象：其一，有人平上帻，执戟而乘之。其一，有若马形而不成，其字有金，有中，有大司马，有王，有大吉，有正，有开寿。其一，成行，曰：金当取之。

    Explanation

    88

    During the fourth year of the Yong'an era under Emperor Sun Quan's successor, Sun Xiu, a man named Chen Jiao from Wu County died, only to come back to life after seven days, emerging from a grave in Wu County. This event was seen as a sign of good fortune for the fallen families, indicating the rise of Sun Hao. After Sun Xiu's reign, the fashion trend was for longer upper garments and shorter lower garments, with multiple layers on top and fewer on bottom. This reflected the social inequality of the time, with the upper class being more extravagant and the lower class being more frugal, symbolizing an imbalance where the upper class had excess and the lower class had scarcity.

    In Volume 7 of the Search for the Supernatural, it is recorded that during the early Western Han period, wise men predicted: "In the Wei dynasty, there will be an opening of a stone in the west, thousands of miles away, with five horses tied to it, inscribed with 'Greatly Destroy Cao.'" When the Wei dynasty first rose, in Liugou, Zhangye, a stone opened: it was first seen during the Jian'an era, formed during the Huangchu era, and its inscriptions were fully developed during the Taiping era. The stone was seven zhang in circumference, one ren in height, with a dark blue body and white markings: dragons, horses, scales, deer, phoenixes, and immortals were all clearly depicted. This event was seen as a sign of the rise of the Wei and Jin dynasties. By the third year of the Tai Shi era during the Jin dynasty, the governor of Zhangye, Jiao Sheng, reported: comparing the local map with the current stone inscription, the number of characters differed, and he carefully presented the map. The inscription had five horse figures: one had a man wearing a flat hat and holding a spear riding it. Another had a horse-like shape but was incomplete, with inscriptions including "gold," "center," "Grand Marshal," "king," "great good fortune," "correct," and "longevity." Another line of text read: "Gold should be taken."

    89

    晋武帝泰始初，衣服上俭，下丰，着衣者皆厌腰。此君衰弱，臣放纵之象也。至元康末，妇人出两裆，加乎交领之上。此内出外也。为车乘者，苟贵轻细，又数变易其形，皆以白篾为纯。盖古丧车之遗象。晋之祸征也。
    　　胡床，貊盘，翟之器也。羌煮，貊炙，翟之食也。自太始以来，中国尚之。贵人，富室，必畜其器。吉享嘉宾，皆以为先。戎翟侵中国之前兆也。
    　　晋太康四年，会稽郡蟛蚑及蟹，皆化为鼠。其众覆野。大食稻，为灾。始成，有毛肉而无骨，其行不能过田●，数日之后，则皆为牝。
    　　太康五年正月，二龙见武库井中。武库者，帝王威御之器，所宝藏也；屋宇邃密，非龙所处。是后七年，藩王相害；二十八年，果有二胡，僭窃神器，皆字曰龙。

    Explanation

    89

    During the early years of Emperor Wu of Jin's reign in the Tai Shi era, clothing was simple at the top and elaborate at the bottom, with people tucking their garments in at the waist. This fashion trend symbolized a weakening of authority and increasing indulgence among officials. By the end of the Yuan Kang era, women began wearing two pieces of clothing over their collars, reflecting internal social dynamics manifesting externally. Vehicles were valued for being lightweight and delicate, with frequent changes in design, often adorned with white bamboo strips, reminiscent of ancient funeral vehicles. These trends were omens of disaster for the Jin dynasty.

    Foreign furniture and utensils, such as the hu bed and mo tray, and foreign foods like Qiang stew and Mo roast, were favored since the Tai Shi era. Wealthy and influential people would own these foreign items, using them first in important social gatherings, which was a sign of impending invasion by non-Han peoples.

    In the fourth year of the Tai Kang era, in the Huiji region, crabs and frogs turned into mice, causing widespread destruction, particularly by eating rice. These mice had fur and flesh but no bones, could not move beyond a certain point, and after a few days, all became female.

    In the first month of the fifth year of the Tai Kang era, two dragons appeared in the well of the imperial armory. The imperial armory, a place where the emperor's weapons and treasures are stored, is a deep and secure place, not suitable for dragons. Seven years later, there was conflict among the princes; twenty-eight years later, two Xianbei leaders, named Long, usurped power, fulfilling the earlier omen.

    90

    晋武帝太康六年，南阳获两足虎。虎者，阴精而居乎阳，金兽也。南阳，火名也。金精入火，而失其形，王室乱之妖也。其七年十一月景辰，四角兽见于河间。天戒若曰：“角，兵象也。四者，四方之象。当有兵革起于四方”，后河间王遂连四方之兵，作为乱阶。
    　　太康九年，幽州塞北有死牛头语。时帝多疾病，深以后事为念，而付托不以至公，思瞀乱之应也。
    　　太康中，有鲤鱼二枚，现武库屋上。武库，兵府；鱼有鳞甲，亦是兵之类也。鱼既极阴，屋上太阳，鱼现屋上，象至阴以兵革之祸干太阳也。及惠帝初，诛皇后父杨骏，矢交宫阙，废后为庶人，死于幽宫。元康之末，而贾后专制，谤杀太子，寻亦诛废。十年之间，母后之难再兴，是其应也。自是祸乱构矣。京房易妖曰：“鱼去水，飞入道路，兵且作。”

    Explanation

    90

    During the sixth year of the Tai Kang era of Emperor Wu of Jin, a two-legged tiger was captured in Nanyang. The tiger is a yin spirit residing in the yang realm, likened to a golden beast. Nanyang is associated with fire. The metal essence (tiger) entering the fire element leads to a loss of form, which is an omen of disorder in the royal family. In the eleventh month of the seventh year of the Tai Kang era, on the day Jingchen, a four-horned creature appeared in Hejian. Heaven warns: "Horns symbolize weapons. The number four represents the four directions or regions. There will be warfare arising from the four regions." Later, the Prince of Hejian united forces from the four regions, leading to chaos.

    In the ninth year of the Tai Kang era, a dead cow's head spoke in the northern frontier of Youzhou. At that time, the emperor was often ill and deeply concerned about future matters, but did not entrust them with absolute fairness, which is a response to mental confusion or disorder.

    During the middle of the Tai Kang era, two carp fish appeared on the roof of the armory. The armory is a place for military storage. The fish have scales and armor, symbolizing military equipment. The fish are extremely yin, and the roof is associated with the sun or yang. The appearance of the fish on the roof symbolizes the yin (negative) causing military disaster to the yang (positive). During the early years of Emperor Huai of Jin, the father of the Empress Dowager, Yang Jun, was executed. Arrows flew around the imperial palace. The Empress was demoted to a commoner and died in a secluded palace. By the end of the Yuan Kang era, Empress Dowager Jia exercised power, falsely accused and killed the Crown Prince, and was later executed and demoted. Within ten years, the difficulties caused by the Empress Dowager arose again, fulfilling the prophecy. From this point, chaos and disorder began. The divination book "Yi A" by Jing Fang states: "If fish leave water and fly into the roads, warfare will ensue."

    91

    初，作屐者：妇人圆头，男子方头。盖作意欲别男女也。至太康中，妇人皆方头屐，与男无异，此贾后专妒之征也。
    　　晋时，妇人结发者，既成，以缯急束其环，名曰“撷子髻”。始自宫中，天下翕然化之也。其末年，遂有怀、惠之事。
    　　太康中，天下为“晋世宁”之舞。其舞，抑手以执杯盘，而反复之。歌曰：“晋世宁舞，杯盘反复。”至危也。杯盘，酒器也，而名曰“晋世宁”者，言时人苟且饮食之间，而其智不可及远，如器在手也。
    　　太康中，天下以毡为絔头，及络带裤口。于是百姓咸相戏曰：“中国其必为胡所破也。夫毡，胡之所产者也，而天下以为絔头，带身，裤口，胡既三制之矣，能无败乎？”

    Explanation

    91

    Initially, when making shoes, women's shoes had rounded tops and men's shoes had square tops. The intention behind this was to distinguish between men and women. By the time of the Tai Kang period, women's shoes also had square tops, making no difference from men's. This was seen as a sign of the jealousy of Empress Jia Nanfeng.

    In the Jin Dynasty, when women tied their hair, they would tightly bind the ring with a cloth, which was called "Xiezi Jui" (a type of hairstyle). This style first started in the palace and quickly spread throughout the country. By the end of the dynasty, there were incidents involving Emperor Huai and Emperor Huizong.

    During the Tai Kang period, people performed the "Jin Shi Ning" dance. In this dance, the hands were pressed down to hold cups and plates, which were then repeatedly flipped. The song accompanying the dance said, "The Jin Shi Ning dance, cups and plates are repeatedly flipped." This was a sign of danger. Cups and plates are drinking vessels, but naming the dance "Jin Shi Ning" suggests that people were living in a state of complacency, unable to think far ahead, like holding a vessel in their hands.

    During the Tai Kang period, people used felt to make socks and to decorate the waistbands and cuffs of trousers. People joked among themselves, saying, "China will surely be conquered by the barbarians." Felt is produced by the barbarians, and if the Chinese use it for socks, waistbands, and cuffs, the barbarians have three ways to control them, how can they avoid being defeated?

    92

    太康末，京、洛为“折杨柳”之歌。其曲始有兵革苦辛之辞，终以擒获斩截之事。自后扬骏被诛，太后幽死，杨柳之应也。
    　　晋武帝太熙元年，辽东有马生角，在两耳下，长三寸。及帝宴驾，王室毒于兵祸。
    　　晋惠帝元康中，妇人之饰有五佩兵。又以金、银、象、角、玳瑁之属，为斧、钺、戈、戟而载之，以当笄。男女之别，国之大节故服食异等。今妇人而以兵器为饰，盖妖之甚者也。于是遂有贾后之事。
    　　晋元康三年闰二月，殿前六钟皆出涕，五刻乃止。前年，贾后杀杨太后于金墉城，而贾后为恶不悛，故钟出涕，犹伤之也。
    　　惠帝之世，京、洛有人，一身而男女二体，亦能两用人道，而性尤好淫。天下兵乱，由男女气乱，而妖形作也。
    　　惠帝元康中，安丰有女子，曰周世宁，年八岁，渐化为男。至十七八，而气性成。女体化而不尽，男体成而不彻，畜妻而无子。

    Explanation

    92

    At the end of the reign of Emperor Hui of Jin, the capital cities of Luoyang and Chang'an were filled with the song "Breaking the Willow." The lyrics began with descriptions of the hardships and sufferings of war and ended with accounts of capturing and killing enemies. Afterward, Yang Jun was executed, and the empress dowager was imprisoned and died, which was a sign of the song's prophecy.

    In the first year of Emperor Wu of Jin's reign, a horse in Liaodong grew horns on its ears, each horn three inches long. When the emperor passed away, the royal family suffered greatly due to the wars.

    During the reign of Emperor Hui of Jin, women began to wear weapons as decorations. They used gold, silver, ivory, horn, and tortoiseshell to make swords, spears, halberds, and other weapons, wearing them instead of hairpins. The distinction between men and women was considered a fundamental principle of the state, so their clothing and dietary practices were different. Now, women wearing weapons as decorations was a very ominous sign, leading to the events involving Empress Dowager Jia.

    In the third year of the leap month of Emperor Hui of Jin's reign, the six bells in front of the palace wept, and it took five hours for them to stop. The previous year, Empress Dowager Jia had killed the empress dowager Yang in Jin'yang City, and her wickedness did not cease, so the bells wept, still mourning her.

    During the reign of Emperor Hui of Jin, there was a person in Luoyang and Chang'an who had both male and female characteristics and could engage in both male and female activities, but they had a strong inclination towards promiscuity. The widespread military conflicts were due to the disruption in the natural balance between male and female energies, leading to the manifestation of supernatural phenomena.

    In the reign of Emperor Hui of Jin, a woman in Anfeng named Zhou Shining, who was eight years old, gradually transformed into a man. By the time she was seventeen or eighteen, her temperament had fully changed. Her female body did not completely disappear, and her male body was not fully formed, and she had a wife but no children.

    93

    元康五年三月，临淄有大蛇，长十许丈，负二小蛇，入城北门，径从市入汉阳城景王祠中，不见。
    　　元康五年三月，吕县有流血，东西百余步，其后八载，而封云乱徐州，杀伤数万人。
    　　元康七年，霹雳破城南高禖石。高禖，宫中求子祠也。贾后妒忌，将杀怀、愍，故天怒贾后将诛之应也。
    　　元康中，天下始相效为乌杖，以柱掖其后，稍施其镦，住则植之。及怀、愍之世，王室多故，而中都丧败，元帝以藩臣树德东方，维持天下，柱掖之应也。
    　　元康中，贵游子弟，相与为散发，裸身之饮，对弄婢妾。逆之者伤好，非之者负讥。希世之士，耻不与焉。胡狄侵中国之萌也。其后遂有二胡之乱。
    　　惠帝太安元年，丹阳湖熟县夏架湖，有大石浮二百步而登岸，百姓惊叹相告曰：“石来寻。”而石冰入建邺。

    93

    In the third month of the fifth year of the Yuankang era, a large snake appeared in Linzi, measuring about ten zhang in length, carrying two smaller snakes. It entered the city through the northern gate, passing through the market and disappearing into the Jing Wang Temple in Han Yang City.

    In the third month of the fifth year of the Yuankang era, blood flowed in Lu County for over a hundred steps in the east-west direction. Eight years later, Yun Feng rebelled in Xu Zhou, killing and injuring tens of thousands of people.

    In the seventh year of the Yuankang era, a thunderbolt struck and broke a stone at the southern part of the city, associated with the High Rites of Fertility. The High Rites of Fertility is a temple in the palace where people pray for children. Empress Jia was jealous and intended to kill the heirs, Huai and Min. This natural disaster was a sign of heaven's anger at Empress Jia's actions.

    During the Yuankang era, people began to use walking sticks with an umbrella-like top, supporting their backs and gradually adding caps or knobs to the ends. When standing still, they planted the sticks. During the reigns of Huai and Min, the royal family faced many troubles, and the central capital suffered defeat. Emperor Yuan, as a vassal prince, established virtue in the east and maintained the empire, fulfilling the prophecy of the walking stick.

    During the Yuankang era, wealthy and influential young men gathered, their hair loose, drinking naked, and playing with maids and concubines. Those who opposed them would damage their friendships, and those who criticized them would be ridiculed. People of the time were ashamed not to follow this trend, which was a sign of the impending invasion by barbarians from the north. Later, there was the rebellion of the two Hu tribes.

    In the first year of the Taian era, a large stone floated for two hundred steps and came ashore in Lake Shu in Hu County, Dan Yang. The people were amazed and exclaimed, "The stone is coming to seek something." This was followed by the rebellion led by Shi Bing, who entered Jian Ye (modern-day Nanjing).

    94

    太安元年四月，有人自云龙门入殿前，北面再拜，曰：“我当作中书监。”即收斩之。禁庭尊秘之处，今贱人竟入，而门卫不觉者，宫室将虚，下人踰上之妖也。是后帝迁长安，宫阙遂空焉。
    　　太安中江夏功曹张骋所乘牛，忽言曰：“天下方乱，吾甚极为，乘我何之？”骋及从者数人皆惊怖。因绐之曰：“令汝还，勿复言。”乃中道还，至家，未释驾。又言曰：“归何早也？”骋益忧惧，秘而不言。安陆县有善卜者，骋从之卜。卜者曰：“大凶。非一家之祸，天下将有兵起。一郡之内，皆破亡乎！”骋还家，牛又人立而行。百姓聚观。其秋张昌贼起。先略江夏，诳曜百姓，以汉祚复兴，有凤凰之瑞，圣人当世。从军者皆绛抹头，以彰火德之祥，百姓波荡，从乱如归。骋兄弟并为将军都尉。未几而败。于是一郡破残，死伤过半，而骋家族矣。京房易妖曰：“牛能言，如其言占吉凶。”

    Explanation

    94

    In the first month of the Taian era, a man claimed to have entered the palace through the Longmen Gate, bowed twice facing north, and said, "I will become the Minister of the Secretariat." He was immediately apprehended and executed. The highly respected and secret areas of the imperial court, where now a lowly person had managed to enter, and the gatekeepers had not noticed, indicated that the palace would soon become empty, a strange phenomenon where the lower class surpasses the upper class. After this, the emperor moved to Chang'an, and the palace gates became empty.

    During the middle period of the Taian era, Zhang Cheng, the official in charge of Jiangxia, had a cow that suddenly spoke, saying, "The world is about to be in chaos; I am very tired. What are you riding me for?" Zhang Cheng and several of his followers were all terrified. They then deceived the cow, saying, "Let you return, do not speak again." The cow returned halfway, and when they arrived home, it had not yet been dismounted. The cow spoke again, "Why did you return so early?" Zhang Cheng became increasingly fearful and kept the incident secret. In Anlu County, there was a skilled fortune-teller, and Zhang Cheng consulted him. The fortune-teller said, "Great misfortune. It is not just a single family's calamity; there will be war across the land. The entire region will be destroyed!" Zhang Cheng returned home, and the cow stood on its hind legs and walked. The common people gathered to watch. That autumn, Zhang Chang's rebels rose up. They first attacked Jiangxia, deceiving and dazzling the common people with the claim that the Han dynasty's rule would be restored, there was the auspicious sign of the phoenix, and a sage was in the world. Those who joined the army all wore red headwear to signify the good fortune of the fire element. The common people were swayed, and followed the chaos as if returning home. Zhang Cheng's brothers all became generals and magistrates. Soon after, they were defeated. As a result, the entire region was destroyed, and more than half of the people died or were injured, and Zhang Cheng's family was wiped out. According to the I Ching (Book of Changes) by Jing Fang, "A cow can speak; its words can be used to predict good or bad fortune."

    95

    元康、太安之间，江、淮之域，有败屩自聚于道，多者至四五十量。人或散去之，投林草中，明日视之，悉复如故。或云：“见猫衔而聚之。”世之所说：“屩者，人之贱服。而当劳辱下民之象也。败者，疲弊之象也。道者，地里四方所以交通，王命所由往来也。今败屩聚于道者，象下民疲病，将相聚为乱，绝四方而壅王命也。”
    　　晋惠帝永兴元年，成都王之攻长沙也，反军于邺，分外陈兵。是夜，戟锋皆有火光，遥望如悬烛，就视，则亡焉。其后终以败亡。

    Explanation

    95

    Between the years of Yuankang and Tai'an, in the region between the Yangtze and Huai rivers, there were instances of discarded shoes gathering on the roads by themselves, with as many as forty to fifty pairs at a time. People would scatter them into the forest or grass, but the next day, they found them all gathered back together as before. Some said, "A cat was seen carrying and gathering them." The world interpreted this as follows: "Shoes are the lowly clothing of people, symbolizing the labor and humiliation of the lower classes. Discarded shoes represent a state of exhaustion and poverty. Roads are the means by which the four directions are connected, and the routes by which royal commands travel. Now, the discarded shoes gathering on the roads symbolize the exhaustion and illness of the lower classes, who will gather to rebel, cutting off communication and obstructing royal commands."

    In the first year of Yongxing during the reign of Emperor Huai of Jin, Prince Chengdu attacked Changsha. He retreated his army to the city of Ye and deployed his troops outside the city. That night, the tips of the spears emitted fire, appearing from a distance like hanging candles. Upon closer inspection, the fire disappeared. Ultimately, he met defeat and destruction.

    96

    晋怀帝永嘉元年，吴郡吴县万详婢，生一子，鸟头，两足，马蹄，一手，无毛，尾黄色，大如碗。
    　　永嘉五年，枹罕令严根婢，产一龙，一女，一鹅。京房易传曰：“人生他物，非人所见者，皆为天下大兵。”时帝承惠帝之后，四海沸腾，寻而陷于平阳，为逆胡所害。
    　　永嘉五年，吴郡嘉兴张林家，有狗忽作人言曰：“天下人俱饿死”于是果有二胡之乱，天下饥荒焉。
    　　永嘉五年十一月，有蝘鼠出延陵，郭璞筮之，遇临之益，曰：“此郡之东县，当有妖人欲称制者。寻亦自死矣。”
    　　永嘉六年正月，无锡县欻有四枝茱萸树，相樛而生，状若连理。先是，郭璞筮延陵蝘鼠，遇临之益，曰：“后当复有妖树生，若瑞而非，辛螫之木也。傥有此，东西数百里，必有作逆者。”及此生木，其后吴兴徐馥作乱，杀太守袁琇。

    Explanation

    96

    In the first year of the Yongjia era under Emperor Huai of Jin, a servant named Wan Xiang from Wuxian County, Wu Prefecture, gave birth to a child with a bird's head, two legs, horse hooves, one hand, no fur, a yellow tail, and a size comparable to a bowl.

    In the fifth year of the Yongjia era, a servant of Yan Gen, the magistrate of Fuhuan, gave birth to a dragon, a girl, and a goose. Jing Fang's commentary on the I Ching states: "When humans give birth to non-human creatures, it signifies widespread warfare." At the time, Emperor Huai ascended the throne after Emperor Hui, and the empire was in chaos. Soon, he was captured and killed by the Xiongnu in Pingyang.

    In the fifth year of the Yongjia era, a dog in the household of Zhang Lin from Jiaxing, Wu Prefecture, suddenly spoke human words, saying, "All people will starve to death." Indeed, there followed the Xiongnu invasion, leading to widespread famine across the land.

    In the eleventh month of the fifth year of the Yongjia era, a strange mouse appeared in Yanling. Guo Pu divined and encountered the hexagram of Lin with Yi (both danger and gain), and said, "In one of the eastern counties of this prefecture, there will be a malevolent person who seeks to seize power. He will soon die."

    In the first month of the sixth year of the Yongjia era, four branches of the zhu yu tree suddenly grew intertwined in Wuxi County, resembling a lian li tree. Previously, when Guo Pu divined the strange mouse in Yanling, he encountered the hexagram of Lin with Yi, and said, "Later, there will be a strange tree that grows, which will be a sign of rebellion, though it appears auspicious. If this happens, within several hundred miles east and west, there will surely be a rebellion." When this strange tree grew, it was followed by the rebellion of Xu Fu in Wuxing, who killed the governor Yuan Xiu.

    97

    永嘉中寿春城内有豕生人，两头而不活。周馥取而观之。识者云：“豕，北方畜，胡狄象。两头者，无上也。生而死，不遂也。”天戒若曰：“易生专利之谋，将自致倾覆也。”俄为元帝所败。
    　　永嘉中，士大夫竞服生笺单衣。识者怪之，曰：“此古练纕之布，诸侯所以服天子也。今无故服之，殆有应乎！”其后怀、愍晏驾。
    　　昔魏武军中无故作白帢，此缟素凶丧之征也。初，横缝其前以别后，名之曰“颜帢，”传行之。至永嘉之间，稍去其缝，名“无颜帢，”而妇人束发，其缓弥甚，紒之坚不能自立，发被于额，目出而已。无颜者，愧之言也。覆额者，惭之貌也。其缓弥甚者，言天下亡礼与义，放纵情性，及其终极，至于大耻也。其后二年，永嘉之乱，四海分崩，下人悲难，无颜以生焉。

    Explanation

    97

    During the Yongjia period, a pig gave birth to a human with two heads in the city of Shouchun, but the child did not survive. Zhou Fu took it to observe. Those who know say, "The pig is a northern livestock, a symbol of Hu and Di. Two heads mean no ruler. Born and died, not succeeding." Heaven seems to warn, "It is easy to generate profit-seeking schemes, which will lead to self-destruction." Soon, Yuan Di was defeated.

    During the Yongjia period, scholars and officials competed to wear freshly made single-layered clothes. Those who know found this strange and said, "This is the ancient linen cloth used by feudal lords to serve the emperor. Wearing it without reason, probably there is a response!" Afterward, Emperor Huai and Emperor Min abdicated.

    In the past, during Cao Cao's army, they made white hats without reason, which is a sign of mourning and misfortune. Initially, they stitched horizontally at the front to distinguish the back, calling it "Yan's hat," and passed it on. By the time of the Yongjia period, they gradually removed the stitching, naming it "No-Face Hat," and women tied their hair, with the looseness increasing more and more. The hair could not stand up on its own, falling over the forehead, and only the eyes were visible. No-Face means a word of shame. Covering the forehead means a look of shame. Its looseness increased more and more, indicating the loss of ritual and righteousness, letting loose emotions and nature, until its ultimate end, becoming a great shame. Two years later, the Yongjia Rebellion broke out, the world fell apart, people below suffered, and they could not live with shame.

    98

    晋愍帝建兴四年，西都倾覆，元皇帝始为晋王四海宅心。其年十月二十二日，新蔡县吏任乔妻胡氏年二十五，产二女，相向，腹心合，自腰以上，脐以下。各分。此盖天下未一之妖也。时内史吕会上言：“按瑞应图云：‘异根同体，谓之连理。异亩同颍，谓之嘉禾。’草木之属，犹以为瑞；今二人同心，天垂灵象。故易云：‘二人同心，其利断金。’休显见生于陈东之中，盖四海同心之瑞。不胜喜跃。谨画图上。”时有识者哂之。君子曰：“知之难也。以臧文仲之才，独祀爰居焉。布在方册，千载不忘。故士不可以不学。古人有言：木无枝谓之瘣，人不学谓之瞽。当其所蔽，盖阙如也。可不勉乎？”
    　　晋元帝建武元年六月，扬州大旱；十二月，河东地震。去年十二月，斩督运令史淳于伯，血逆深上柱二丈三尺，旋复下深四尺五寸。是时淳于伯冤死，遂频旱三年。刑罚妄加，群阴不附，则阳气胜之。罚，又冤气之应也。

    Explanation

    98

    During the fourth year of the Jianxing era of Emperor Min of Jin, the Western capital fell, and the Prince of Jin, who would become Emperor Yuan, gained the allegiance of all under heaven. On the twenty-second day of the tenth month of that year, the wife of a county official named Ren Qiao from Xincai County, aged twenty-five, gave birth to two girls facing each other, with their upper bodies joined from the waist up but separate below the navel. This was considered an omen of the world not yet unified. At the time, the governor of the region, Lü Hui, submitted a report stating: "According to the Book of Auspicious Signs: 'Different roots but the same body, called intertwined branches. Different fields but the same grain, called auspicious rice.' Even plants are considered auspicious; now two people with one heart, a divine sign from heaven. The Book of Changes says: 'Two people with one heart, their strength can cut through metal.' The auspicious sign appears in the eastern part of Chen, indicating the four seas being united in heart. Overjoyed, I respectfully draw a diagram and present it." At the time, those with knowledge laughed at it. The virtuous say: "It is difficult to know. Even with the talent of Zang Wenzhong, he alone worshipped the sea gull. Recorded in books, never forgotten for a thousand years. Therefore, scholars cannot avoid learning. Ancient people said: A tree without branches is called a cripple, a person without learning is called blind. When one is blinded, it is as if there is a gap. How can one not strive?"

    In the first year of the Jianwu era of Emperor Yuan of Jin, in June, there was a severe drought in Yangzhou; in December, there was an earthquake in Hedong. Last December, the supervisor of transportation, Chunyu Bo, was executed, and his blood rose to a height of twenty-three feet on a pillar, then fell back down four feet and five inches. At that time, Chunyu Bo was wrongfully executed, leading to three consecutive years of drought. When punishments are arbitrarily imposed and the yin forces are not aligned, the yang forces dominate. Punishment is also a response to wrongful death.

    99

    晋元帝建武元年七月，晋陵东门，有牛生犊，一体两头。京房易传曰：“牛生子，二首，一身，天下将分之象也。”
    　　元帝太兴元年四月，西平地震，涌水出。十二月，庐陵、豫章、武昌、西陵地震，涌水出，山崩。此王敦陵上之应也。
    　　太兴元年，三月武昌太守王谅，有牛生子，两头，八足，两尾，共一腹。不能自生，十余人以绳引之。子死，母活。其三年后，苑中有牛生子，一足三尾，生而即死。
    　　太兴二年，丹阳郡吏濮阳演马生驹，两头，自项前别。生而死。此政在私门二头之象也。其后王敦陵上。
    　　太兴初，有女子，其阴在腹，当脐下。自中国来，至江东。其性淫而不产。又有女子，阴在首。居在扬州。亦性好淫。京房易妖曰：“人生子，阴在首，则天下大乱。若在腹，则天下有事。若在背，则天下无后。”

    Explanation

    99

    In the seventh month of the first year of the Jianwu era of Emperor Yuan of Jin, in the eastern gate of Jinling, a cow gave birth to a calf with two heads on one body. Jing Fang's Yijing commentary states: "When a cow gives birth to a calf with two heads and one body, it is an omen of the world being divided."

    In the first year of the Taixing era of Emperor Yuan of Jin, in April, an earthquake struck Xiping, and water gushed out. In December, earthquakes struck Luling, Yuzhang, Wuchang, and Xiling, with water gushing out and mountains collapsing. These events were omens of Wang Dun's rebellion.

    In the first year of the Taixing era, in March, the governor of Wuchang, Wang Liang, had a cow give birth to a calf with two heads, eight legs, and two tails, all in one body. The calf could not be born naturally and was pulled out by ten people using ropes. The calf died, but the mother survived. Three years later, in the imperial gardens, a cow gave birth to a calf with one leg and three tails, which died immediately after birth.

    In the second year of the Taixing era, a horse born to a local official in Danyang, Puyang Yan, had two heads, separated at the neck, and died shortly after birth. These events were signs of political instability and the rise of powerful private individuals, foreshadowing Wang Dun's rebellion.

    At the beginning of the Taixing era, a woman was born with her genitalia in her abdomen, below the navel, who came from the central region to the Jiangnan area and was sexually active but did not bear children. Another woman was born with her genitalia on her head, living in Yangzhou, and was also sexually active. Jing Fang's Yijing commentary states: "When a person is born with genitalia on their head, it is an omen of great chaos. If it is in the abdomen, it is an omen of conflict. If it is on the back, it is an omen of the end of the dynasty."

    100

    太兴中王敦镇武昌，武昌灾，火起，兴众救之，救于此，而发于彼，东西南北数十处俱应，数日不绝，旧说所谓“滥灾妄起，虽兴师不能救之”之谓也。此臣而行君，亢阳失节。是时王敦陵上，有无君之心，故灾也。
    　　太兴中兵士以绛囊缚紒。识者曰：“紒在首，为干，君道也，囊者，为坤，臣道也。今以朱囊缚紒，臣道侵君之象也，为衣者上带短纔至于掖；着帽者，又以带缚项，下逼上，上无地也。为裤者，直幅，无口，无杀，下大之象也。”寻而王敦谋逆，再攻京师。
    　　太兴四年，王敦在武昌，铃下仪仗生花，如莲花，五六日而萎落。说曰：“易说：‘枯杨生花，何可久也。’今狂花生枯木，又在铃阁之间，言威仪之富，荣华之盛，皆如狂花之发，不可久也。”其后王敦终以逆，命加戮其尸。

    Explanation

    100

    During the Taixing period, Wang Dun was stationed in Wuchang. A disaster struck Wuchang, and a fire broke out. People were mobilized to put out the fire, but while they were fighting the fire here, it spread there. Fires broke out in dozens of places across the east, west, south, and north, and continued for several days without ceasing. This is what the ancient saying refers to as "a disaster that arises without reason, which cannot be stopped even by mobilizing troops." This disaster symbolizes a minister acting like a ruler, indicating a loss of proper order. At that time, Wang Dun was disrespectful to the emperor and harbored ambitions to usurp power, hence the disaster.

    During the Taixing period, soldiers wore red bags tied around their hairbands. A knowledgeable person said, "The hairband is at the head, representing the 'Heavenly' principle, which symbolizes the ruler. The bag represents the 'Earthly' principle, which symbolizes the minister. Now, by tying a red bag around the hairband, it symbolizes the minister encroaching on the ruler's authority. Those who wear clothes have their upper belts only reaching the armpit; those who wear hats tie the belt around their necks, with the lower part pressing against the upper part, leaving no room for the upper part. Those who wear trousers have them straight, without a waistband or hem, indicating a symbol of the lower part being too large." Soon after, Wang Dun plotted rebellion and attacked the capital twice.

    In the fourth year of Taixing, while Wang Dun was in Wuchang, flowers grew on the ceremonial staffs in the bell pavilion, resembling lotus flowers. After a few days, the flowers withered and fell. Someone said, "The Yi Jing says, 'A withered elm tree producing flowers, how can it last long?' Now, flowers are growing on a withered tree, and this is happening in the bell pavilion. It symbolizes the temporary nature of wealth and glory, which are like the fleeting bloom of these flowers." Later, Wang Dun was executed for his rebellion, and his body was publicly displayed as a warning.

    101

    旧为羽扇柄者，刻木象其骨形，列羽用十，取全数也。初，王敦南征，始改为长柄，下出，可捉。而减其羽，用八。识者尤之曰：“夫羽扇，翼之名也。创为长柄，将执其柄以制其羽翼也。改十为八，将未备夺已备也。此殆敦之擅权，以制朝廷之柄，又将以无德之材，欲窃非据也。”
    　　晋明帝太宁初，武昌有大蛇，常居故神祠空树中，每出头从人受食。京房易传曰：“蛇见于邑，不出三年，有大兵，国有大忧。”寻有王敦之逆。
    搜神记卷八
    　　虞舜耕于历山，得“玉历”于河际之岩，舜知天命在己，体道不倦。舜，龙颜，大口，手握褒。宋均注曰：“握褒，手中有‘褒’字，喻从劳苦受褒饬致大祚也。”
    　　汤既克夏，大旱七年，洛川竭。汤乃以身祷于桑林，翦其爪、发，自以为牺牲，祈福于上帝。于是大雨即至，洽于四海。

    Explanation

    101

    Final Translation

    The traditional feather fan handle was carved to resemble the shape of a bird's bone, with ten feathers arranged to symbolize completeness. Initially, during Wang Dun's southern campaign, the design was changed to a longer handle, making it easier to hold. However, the number of feathers was reduced to eight. Those who understood criticized this change, saying: "A feather fan is named after a wing. By creating a long handle, one is controlling the wings. By reducing the number of feathers from ten to eight, one is taking something that is incomplete and making it complete. This is likely Wang Dun's attempt to seize power and control the court, and he is using someone without virtue to seize power improperly."

    During the early years of Emperor Ming of Jin's reign, a large snake appeared in Wuchang, living in an old shrine and emerging to eat from people. Jing Fang's commentary on the Yijing (Book of Changes) states: "The appearance of a snake in a town portends war and national disaster within three years." Soon after, Wang Dun rebelled.

    In the Search for the Supernatural, Volume Eight, it is recorded: Shun farmed at Lishan and found the "Jade Calendar" at the edge of a river. Shun understood that he was destined to rule and practiced the Dao diligently. Shun had a dragon-like face, a large mouth, and hands holding the character "褒." Song Jun commented: "Holding the character '褒' means holding the character '褒' in one's hands, symbolizing that through hard work and discipline, one can achieve great fortune."

    After King Tang of Shang defeated the Xia dynasty, a seven-year drought occurred, and the Luo River dried up. Tang offered himself as a sacrifice in the mulberry forest, cutting off his claws and hair, and praying for blessings from the Supreme Deity. Immediately, heavy rain came, spreading across the land.

    102

    吕望钓于渭阳。文王出游猎，占曰：“今曰猎得一狩，非龙，非螭，非熊，非罴。合得帝王师。”果得太公于渭之阳，与语，大悦，同车载而还。
    　　武王伐纣，至河上，雨甚。疾雷，晦冥。扬波于河。众甚惧。武王曰：“余在天下，谁敢干余者？”风波立济。
    　　鲁哀公十四年，孔子夜梦三槐之间，丰、沛之邦，有赤氤气起，乃呼颜回、子夏同往观之。驱车到楚西北范氏街，见刍儿打鳞，伤其左前足，束薪而覆之。孔子曰：“儿来！汝姓为谁？”儿曰：“吾姓为赤松，名时乔，字受纪。”孔子曰：“汝岂有所见乎？”儿曰：“吾所见一禽，如麇，羊头，头上有角，其末有肉。方以是西走。”孔子曰：“天下已有主也。为赤刘。陈、项为辅。五星入井，从岁星。”儿发薪下鳞，示孔子。孔子趋而往，鳞向孔子蒙其耳，吐三卷图，广三寸，长八寸，每卷二十四子。其言赤刘当起日周亡，赤气起，火耀兴，玄丘制命，帝卯金。

    Explanation

    102

    Lü Wang fished on the western bank of the Wei River. King Wen of Zhou went out hunting and divined, saying, "Today, in the hunt, I will catch a beast that is neither a dragon, nor a chimeric creature, nor a bear, nor a wild boar. I will surely find a teacher to a king." Indeed, he found Jiang Ziya on the western bank of the Wei River. They conversed, and King Wen was greatly pleased, so he returned together in the same carriage.

    King Wu of Zhou attacked King Zhou of Shang, reaching the riverbank, where it rained heavily. There was a sudden thunderstorm, and darkness fell. Waves rose in the river, and the people were very frightened. King Wu said, "If I am in the world, who dares to challenge me?" The waves immediately calmed.

    In the fourteenth year of Duke Ai of Lu, Confucius had a dream at night between three locust trees in Feng and Pei. He saw a red mist rise and called Yan Hui and Zi Xia to go and observe it. They drove to the northwest of Chu, to Fan Street, where they saw a child beating a fish, injuring its left front paw, and covering it with firewood. Confucius said, "Child, come here! What is your surname?" The child replied, "My surname is Chi Song, my given name is Shi Qiao, and my courtesy name is Shou Ji." Confucius said, "Have you seen anything?" The child replied, "I saw a creature that looked like a deer, with a sheep's head, horns, and a fleshy tip on the horns. It was running westward." Confucius said, "The world already has a ruler. It will be Chi Liu. Chen and Xiang will be his auxiliaries. Five stars will enter the well, following the age star." The child removed the firewood and showed Confucius a fish. Confucius hurried to it, and the fish covered its ears, spitting out three scrolls of writing, each three inches wide and eight inches long, with twenty-four characters on each scroll. The scrolls said that Chi Liu would rise when the Zhou dynasty fell, with red vapor arising, fire shining, the black hill commanding, and the emperor of the metal element (Jin dynasty) coming to power.

    103

    孔子修春秋，制孝经，既成，斋戒向北辰而拜，告备于天。乃洪郁，起白雾摩地，白虹自上而下，化为黄玉，长三尺，上有刻文。孔子跪受而读之，曰：“宝文出，刘季握。卯，金，刀，在轸北。字禾子，天下服。”
    　　秦穆公时，陈仓人掘地，得物，若羊非羊，若猪非猪。牵以献穆公。道逢二童子，童子曰：“此名为媪。常在地，食死人脑。若欲杀之，以柏插其首。”媪曰：“彼二童子，名为陈宝。得雄者王，得雌者伯。”陈仓人舍媪逐二童子，童子化为雉，飞入平林。陈仓人告穆公，穆公发徒大猎，果得其雌。又化为石。置之汧、渭之间，至文公时，为立祠陈宝。其雄者飞至南阳。今南阳雉县，是其地也。秦欲表其符，故以名县。每陈仓祠时有赤光，长十余丈，从雉县来，入陈仓祠中，有声殷殷如雄雉。其后，光武起于南阳。

    Explanation

    103

    Confucius edited the Spring and Autumn Annals and compiled the Classic of Filial Piety. Upon completion, he fasted and bowed towards the North Star, informing the heavens of his work. A dense fog then rose from the ground, and a white rainbow descended from the sky, transforming into a yellow jade, three chi long, with inscribed text. Confucius knelt to receive and read it, which said: "A treasure text appears, held by Liu Ji. The character '卯' (卯), metal, and knife are in the north of the constellation Zhen. The one with the name 'Huo Zi' will be revered by all under heaven."

    During the reign of Duke Mu of Qin, a man from Chen Cang was digging and found an object that resembled but was not a sheep or a pig. He brought it to Duke Mu of Qin. On the way, he encountered two children who said, "This is called 'Aow,' an earth spirit that resides in the ground and feeds on the brains of the dead. If you wish to kill it, use a pine branch to pierce its head." The earth spirit said, "Those two children are called 'Chenbao.' Whoever captures the male will become king, and whoever captures the female will become a hegemon." The man from Chen Cang abandoned the earth spirit and chased the two children, who transformed into pheasants and flew into the forest. He then reported the incident to Duke Mu of Qin, who organized a large hunting party and indeed captured the female. It then transformed into a stone, which was placed between the Qian and Wei rivers. During the reign of Duke Wen of Qin, a shrine was built for Chenbao. The male flew to Nanyang, where the current Nanyang Chixian county is located. The Qin dynasty wanted to mark this place as a sign of their legitimacy, so they named the county after it. Every time the Chen Cang shrine was worshipped, a red light over ten zhang long appeared, coming from Chixian county and entering the Chen Cang shrine, accompanied by a deep, resonant sound like that of a rooster. Later, Emperor Guangwu of Han rose to power in Nanyang.

    104

    宋大夫邢史子臣明于天道。周敬王之三十七年，景公问曰：“天道其何祥？”对曰：“后五十年五月丁亥，臣将死。死后五年五月丁卯，吴将亡。亡后五年，君将终。终后四百年，邾王天下。”俄而皆如其言所云。邾王天下者，谓魏之兴也。邾，曹姓，魏亦曹姓，皆邾之后。其年数则错。未知刑史失其数耶？将年代久远，注记者传而有谬也？

    Explanation

    104

    The Song official Xing Shi Zichen was knowledgeable about the ways of heaven. In the thirty-seventh year of King Jing of Zhou, King Jing asked, "What signs does the heavens portend?" Xing Shi Zichen replied, "Fifty years from now, on the day Dinghai in May, I will die. Five years after my death, on the day Dingmao in May, the state of Wu will fall. Five years after Wu's fall, you will pass away. Four hundred years after your passing, the state of Zhu will rule the world." Soon, all these predictions came true. The state of Zhu ruling the world refers to the rise of the state of Wei. Both Zhu and Wei belong to the Cao clan, descendants of Zhu. However, the years mentioned are incorrect. Is it because Xing Shi made a mistake in his calculations? Or is it because the passage of time has led to errors in the records?

    105

    吴以草创之国，信不坚固，边屯守将，皆质其妻子，名曰：“保质童子。”少年以类相与娱游者，日有十数。孙休永安三年二月，有一异儿，长四尺余，年可六七岁，衣青衣，忽来从群儿戏。诸儿莫之识也，皆问曰：“尔谁家小儿，今日忽来？”答曰：“见尔群戏乐，故来耳！”详而视之，眼有光芒，爚爚外射。诸儿畏之重问其故。儿乃答曰：“尔恐我乎？我非人也，乃荧惑星也，将有以告尔。三公归于司马。”诸儿大惊，或走告大人，大人驰往观之。儿曰：“舍尔去乎！”耸身而跃，即以化矣。仰而视之，若曳一疋练以登天。大人来者，犹及见焉。飘飘渐高，有顷而没。时吴政峻急，莫敢宣也。后四年而蜀亡，六年而魏废，二十一年而吴平：是归于司马也。
    　　都水马武举戴洋为都水令史，洋请急还乡，将赴洛，梦神人谓之曰：“洛中当败，人尽南渡。年五年，扬州必有天子。”洋信之，遂不去。既而皆如其梦。

    Explanation

    105

    In the early state of Wu, trust was not firm, and the commanders at the frontier garrisons were all made to hold their wives and children as hostages, known as "Guaranteed Children." Young men who associated and played together numbered in the dozens. During the third month of Yong’an Year Three in the reign of Sun Liang, there appeared an extraordinary child, about four feet tall, around six or seven years old, dressed in green clothing, who suddenly came to join the group of children in play. None of the children recognized him, and they all asked, "Who are you, little boy, and why have you come today?" He replied, "I saw that you were all playing and having fun, so I came!" Upon closer inspection, his eyes emitted a radiant light, shining outward. The children, frightened by this, asked him again why he was there. The child then answered, "Are you afraid of me? I am not a human; I am the planet Mars, and I have something to tell you. The Three Excellencies will fall under the control of the Sima family." The children were greatly alarmed, and some ran to tell the adults. The adults hurried to see what was happening. The child said, "Shall I leave you?" He then leaped upward, transforming into nothingness. Looking up, it seemed as if he was dragging a piece of white silk up to heaven. Those who arrived later still saw him, floating higher and higher, until he disappeared after a short while. At that time, the political situation in Wu was severe, and no one dared to speak of what had happened. Four years later, Shu Han fell; six years after that, Cao Wei was overthrown; and twenty-one years later, Eastern Wu was conquered: all of which fulfilled the prophecy of the Sima family's rise to power.

    Ma Wu, the Water Conservancy Commissioner, recommended Dai Yang as the Water Conservancy Inspector. Dai Yang requested urgent leave to return to his hometown, intending to go to Luoyang. On his way, he dreamed of a divine being who told him, "Luoyang will fall, and people will all flee south. In five years, there will be a ruler in Yangzhou." Dai Yang believed this prophecy and did not go to Luoyang. As it turned out, all of his dreams came true.

    106

    搜神记卷九
    　　后汉中兴初，汝南有应枢者，生四子，而尽见神光照社。枢见光，以问卜人。卜人曰：“此天祥也。子孙其兴乎！”乃探得黄金。自是子孙宦学，并有才名。至玚，七世通显。
    　　车骑将军巴郡冯绲，字鸿卿，初为议郎，发绶笥，有二赤蛇，可长二尺，分南北走。大用忧怖。许季山孙宪，字宁方，得其先人秘要，绲请使卜。云：“此吉祥也。君后三岁，当为边将，东北四五里，官以东为名。”后五年，从大将军南征，居无何，拜尚书郎，辽东太守，南征将军。
    　　常山张颢为梁州牧，天新雨后，有鸟如山鹊，飞翔入市，忽然坠地。人争取之，化为圆石。颢椎破之，得一金印，文曰：“忠孝侯印。”颢以上闻，藏之秘府。后议郎汝南樊衡夷上言：“尧舜时旧有此官。今天降印，宜可复置。”颢后官至太尉。

    Explanation

    106

    The Search for the Divine, Volume 9

    At the beginning of the Eastern Han dynasty's revival, there was a man named Ying Shu in Ru'an. He had four sons, and they all witnessed divine light illuminating the altar. Ying Shu saw the light and consulted a diviner. The diviner said, "This is a heavenly omen. Will your descendants prosper?" Upon further investigation, they found gold. From then on, Ying Shu's descendants pursued official careers and acquired great reputations. By the time of Ying Chang, the family had maintained prominence for seven generations.

    General of the Chariots Feng Jun, from Ba Commandery, whose courtesy name was Hongqing, initially served as an Imperial Censor. One day, he opened a chest containing his seals and found two red snakes, each about two feet long, moving north and south. He was greatly alarmed. Xu Ji-shan's descendant Sun Xian, whose courtesy name was Ningfang, possessed secret knowledge passed down from his ancestors. Feng Jun asked him to divinate. Sun Xian said, "This is a good omen. In three years, you will become a frontier general, and your official position will have the character 'east' in its name." Five years later, Feng Jun followed the Grand General on a southern campaign. Soon after, he was appointed as an Imperial Censor, Governor of Liaodong, and General of the Southern Campaign.

    Zhang Hao of Changshan served as the Administrator of Liangzhou. After a fresh rain, a bird resembling a mountain magpie flew into the market and suddenly fell to the ground. People gathered around it, and it transformed into a round stone. Zhang Hao struck the stone with a hammer and found a golden seal inscribed with the words "Seal of the Lord of Loyalty and Filial Piety." Zhang Hao reported this to the emperor, and the seal was kept in the imperial treasury. Later, the Imperial Censor Fan Hengyi of Ru'an suggested, "In the time of Yao and Shun, there was an ancient official position called 'Lord of Loyalty and Filial Piety.' Since this seal has descended from heaven, it is appropriate to reinstate this position." Zhang Hao eventually reached the rank of Grand Commandant.

    107

    京兆长安有张氏，独处一室，有鸠自外入，止于床。张氏祝曰：“鸠来，为我祸也，飞上承尘；为我福也，即入我怀。”鸠飞入怀。以手探之，则不知鸠之所在，而得一金钩。遂宝之。自是子孙渐富，资财万倍。蜀贾至长安，闻之，乃厚赂婢，婢窃钩与贾。张氏既失钩，渐渐衰耗！而蜀贾亦数罹穷厄，不为己利。或告之曰：“天命也。不可力求。”于是赉钩以反张氏，张氏复昌。故关西称张氏传钩云。
    　　汉征和三年三月，天大雨，何比干在家，日中，梦贵客车骑满门。觉，以语妻。语未巳，而门有老妪，可八十余，头白，求寄避雨，雨甚，而衣不沾渍。雨止，送至门，乃谓比干曰：“公有阴德，今天锡君策，以广公之子孙。”因出怀中符策，状如简，长九寸，凡九百九十枚，以授比干，曰：“子孙佩印绶者，当如此算。”

    Explanation

    107

    In Jingzhao (modern-day Xi'an), there was a family named Zhang who lived alone in a room. One day, a magpie flew in from outside and landed on their bed. The Zhang family member wished aloud, "If this magpie brings me misfortune, let it fly up to the ceiling; if it brings me good fortune, let it enter my embrace." The magpie then flew into the person's arms. When they reached out to touch it, they did not find the magpie, but instead found a golden hook. They treasured it greatly. From then on, the Zhang family's descendants gradually became wealthy, and their wealth increased ten thousandfold. A merchant from Sichuan came to Chang'an, heard about the story, and bribed the maid, who stole the hook and gave it to the merchant. The Zhang family, having lost the hook, gradually declined. Meanwhile, the merchant from Sichuan also frequently encountered poverty and misfortune, not benefiting himself. Someone told him, "It is fate. It cannot be forced." Thus, he returned the hook to the Zhang family, and the Zhang family revived. Hence, in the western part of the pass, the Zhang family is known as the 'Hook-Transmitting Zhang Family.'

    In the third month of the third year of Emperor Wu's reign during the Han dynasty, it rained heavily. He Bigan was at home, at noon, when he dreamed of noble visitors filling his courtyard with carriages and horses. Upon waking, he told his wife about the dream. Before he finished speaking, an elderly woman, around eighty years old with white hair, appeared at the door, asking to take shelter from the rain. Despite the heavy rain, her clothes did not get wet. When the rain stopped, he sent her to the door and said to her, "You have done good deeds secretly. Today, heaven has given you a scroll, to expand your descendants." She then took out a scroll from her chest, which was in the form of a bamboo slip, nine inches long, containing a total of nine hundred and ninety items, and gave it to He Bigan, saying, "Those who wear seals and sashes among your descendants should be counted in this way."

    108

    魏舒，字阳元，任城樊人也。少孤，尝诣野王，主人妻夜产，俄而闻车马之声，相问曰：“男也？女也？”曰：“男。”书之。“十五，以兵死。”复问：“寝者为谁？”曰：“魏公舒，”后十五载，诣主人，问所生童何在？曰：“因条桑，为斧伤而死。”舒自知当为公矣。
    　　贾谊为长沙王太傅，四月庚子日，有鹏鸟飞入其舍，止于坐隅，良久，乃去。谊发书占之，曰：“野鸟入室，主人将去。”谊忌之，故作鵩鸟赋，齐死生而等祸福，以致命定志焉。
    　　王莽居摄，东郡太守翟义，知其将篡汉，谋举义兵。兄宣，教授诸生，满堂。群鹅雁数十在中庭，有狗从外入，啮之，皆死。惊救之，皆断头。狗走出门，求，不知处。宣大恶之。数日，莽夷其三族。

    108

    Final Translation

    Hui Shu, courtesy name Yangyuan, was from Fan, Rencheng. He lost his parents at a young age and once visited Yewang. The host's wife gave birth at night, and soon after, they heard the sound of carriages and horses. They asked, "Is it a boy or a girl?" The response was, "A boy." They recorded it. "At fifteen, he will die in battle." They asked again, "Who is the sleeper?" The response was, "Duke Wei Shu." Fifteen years later, he visited the host and asked about the child who had been born. The response was, "He died while pruning mulberry trees, cut by an axe." Hui Shu knew he would become a high-ranking official.

    Jia Yi served as the Grand Tutor to the Prince of Changsha. On the day of Gengzi in the fourth month, a peng bird flew into his room and settled by the side of his seat. After a long while, it left. Jia Yi consulted a book and interpreted it, saying, "A wild bird entering the room means the master will leave." Jia Yi was troubled by this and thus wrote the "Feng Bird Ode," equating life and death and treating misfortune and fortune equally, dedicating his life to set his mind.

    Wang Mang acted as regent, and Zhai Yi, the governor of Dongjun, knew he would usurp the Han dynasty and planned to raise righteous troops. His brother Xuan taught many students, filling the room. There were dozens of geese and cranes in the courtyard. A dog came from outside, bit them all, and they all died. They rushed to save them, but all had their heads cut off. The dog ran out of the door, and they searched for it, but could not find it. Xuan deeply resented this. After several days, Wang Mang destroyed his three clans.

    109

    魏司马太傅懿平公孙渊，斩渊父子。先时，渊家数有怪：一犬着冠帻，绛衣，上屋。欻有一儿，蒸死甑中。襄平北市，生肉，长围各数尺，有头、目、口、喙，无手、足，而动摇。占者曰：“有形不成，有体无声，其国灭亡。”
    　　吴诸葛恪征淮南，归，将朝会之夜，精爽扰动，通夕不寐。严毕趋出，犬衔引其衣。恪曰：“犬不欲我行耶？”出，仍入坐，少顷，复起，犬又衔衣。恪令从者逐之。及入，果被杀。其妻在室，语使婢曰：“尔何故血臭？”婢曰：“不也。”有顷，愈剧。又问婢曰：“汝眼目瞻视，何以不常？”婢蹶然起跃，头至于栋，攘臂切齿而言曰：“诸葛公乃为孙峻所杀。”于是大小知恪死矣。而吏兵寻至。
    　　吴戍将邓喜杀猪祠神，治毕，悬之，忽见一人头，往食肉。喜引弓射中之，咋咋作声，绕屋三日。后人白喜谋叛，合门被诛。

    Explanation

    109

    The Grand Tutor of Wei, Sima Yi, pacified Sun Xun, beheading Sun Xun and his son. Previously, the Sun family had experienced several strange omens: a dog was seen wearing a cap and headgear, dressed in a crimson robe, and climbed onto the roof. Suddenly, a child was found steamed to death in a steaming vessel. In the northern market of Xiangping, a mass of raw flesh, several feet in circumference, appeared, having a head, eyes, a mouth, and a beak, but no hands or feet, and it moved about. A diviner remarked: "It has form but is not complete, has a body but no voice; the kingdom will be destroyed."

    The Wu general Zhuge Ke, after his campaign in the southern part of the Huai River, returned and was about to attend a court session that night. His spiritual state was disturbed, and he could not sleep all night. After dressing, he hurried out, and a dog grabbed and pulled at his robe. Zhuge Ke said, "Does the dog not want me to go?" He went out, then returned to sit, and shortly afterward, rose again, with the dog once more pulling at his robe. Zhuge Ke ordered his attendants to drive the dog away. When he entered the palace, he was indeed killed. His wife, still in the room, asked the servant, "Why do you smell of blood?" The servant replied, "I do not." After a while, the odor became more intense. She asked the servant again, "Why is your gaze so strange?" The servant suddenly jumped up, her head touching the ceiling, and with raised arms and clenched teeth, she said, "General Zhuge was killed by Sun Jun." At this, everyone realized that Zhuge Ke was dead. Soon afterward, officials and soldiers arrived.

    The Wu garrison commander Deng Xi killed a pig to offer to the gods. After the ritual, he hung the pig up, when suddenly a human head appeared and began to eat the meat. Deng Xi drew his bow and shot it, causing it to make a guttural sound and circle the house for three days. Later, someone reported that Deng Xi had plotted rebellion, and the entire family was executed.

    110

    贾充伐吴时，常屯项城，军中忽失充所在。充帐下都督周勤时昼寝，梦见百余人，录充引入一径。勤惊觉，闻失充，乃出寻索。忽睹所梦之道，遂往求之。果见充行至一府舍，侍卫甚盛，府公南面坐，声色甚厉，谓充曰：“将乱吾家事者，必尔与荀勖。既惑吾子，又乱吾孙，间使任恺黜汝而不去，又使庾纯詈汝而不改。今吴寇当平，汝方表斩张华。汝之暗戆，皆此类也。若不悛慎，当旦夕加诛。”充叩头流血。府公曰：“汝所以延日月而名器若此者，是卫府之勋耳。终当使系嗣死于钟虞之间，大子毙于金酒之中，小子困于枯木之下。荀勖亦宜同然。其先德小浓，故在汝后。数世之外，国嗣亦替。”言毕命去。充忽然得还营，颜色憔悴，性理昏错，经日乃复。至后，谧死于钟下，贾后服金酒而死，贾午考竟用大杖终。皆如所言。

    110

    Jia Chong was attacking Wu when he was stationed at Xiangcheng. Suddenly, his troops lost track of where he was. One day, Zhou Qin, the commandant under Jia Chong, was napping during the day and had a dream in which over a hundred people led Jia Chong into a path. Zhou Qin woke up in a panic, heard that Jia Chong was missing, and went out to search for him. Suddenly, he saw the path he had dreamed about and followed it. He found Jia Chong walking to a government office, surrounded by many guards. The official was sitting facing south, looking very stern. He said to Jia Chong, "Those who will disrupt my family affairs are certainly you and Xun Xu. You have misled my son and disrupted my grandson. You secretly made Ren Kai demote you but you did not leave, and made Yu Chun curse you but you did not change. Now that the enemy from Wu will be pacified, you just proposed to execute Zhang Hua. Your stupidity and stubbornness are all like this. If you do not repent and be cautious, you will be punished day and night." Jia Chong knelt down and bled from his forehead. The official said, "You have managed to prolong your life and maintain your position due to your service in the government office. Eventually, your heir will die between Zhong and Yu, the crown prince will die from poisoned wine, and your young son will be trapped under dead wood. Xun Xu should also be the same. His ancestors' virtue is slightly thick, so he is behind you. After several generations, the heir to the throne will also decline." After speaking, the official ordered him to leave. Jia Chong suddenly managed to return to the camp, but his appearance was worn out, and his mental state was confused. It took several days for him to recover. Later, Mi died at the place called Zhong, Jia Hou died from poisoned wine, and Jia Wu died from being beaten with a stick. All these events happened exactly as the official had said.

    庾亮，字文康，鄢陵人，镇荆州，豋厕，忽见厕中一物，如“方相，”两眼尽赤，身有光耀，渐渐从土中出。乃攘臂，以拳击之。应手有声，缩入地。因而寝疾。术士戴洋曰：“昔苏峻事公，于白石祠中祈福，许赛其牛。从来未解。故为此鬼所考，不可救也。”明年，亮果亡。
    　　东阳刘宠字道弘，居于湖熟，每夜，门庭自有血数升，不知所从来。如此三四。后宠为折冲将军，见遣北征，将行，而炊(食卞)尽变为虫。其家人蒸炒，亦变为虫。其火愈猛，其虫愈壮。宠遂北征，军败于坛邱，为徐龛所杀。

    111

    Yu Liang, courtesy name Wenkang, from Yanling, governed Jingzhou. One day, while using the restroom, he suddenly saw something in the toilet that resembled the "Fangxiang," a mythical creature with both eyes completely red and a radiant glow around its body. The creature gradually emerged from the ground. Yu Liang raised his arm and struck it with his fist, and there was a sound upon impact. The creature retracted into the ground, and Yu Liang fell ill as a result. The diviner Dai Yang said, "Formerly, when Su Jun served you, he prayed for blessings at the White Stone Shrine and promised to offer a cow in return. This has never been resolved. Thus, he was being tested by this ghost, and there was no way to save him." The following year, Yu Liang indeed died.

    Dongyang Liu Cong, courtesy name Dao Hong, lived in Lusu. Every night, there was several liters of blood in his courtyard, without knowing its origin. This happened three or four times. Later, Liu Cong was appointed as a Zhifeng General and sent north to campaign. As he was about to leave, his cooked food turned into insects, and even his family's steamed and fried food turned into insects. The more intense the fire, the more robust the insects. Liu Cong then went north to campaign, but his army was defeated at Tanqiu and he was killed by Xu Kan.
