    搜神记卷十
    　　汉和熹邓皇后，尝梦登梯以扪天，体荡荡正清滑，有若钟乳状。乃仰嗡饮之。以讯诸占梦。言：“尧梦攀天而上，汤梦及天砥之，斯皆圣王之前占也。吉不可言。”
    　　孙坚夫人吴氏，孕而梦月入怀。已而生策。及权在孕，又梦日入怀。以告坚曰：“妾昔怀策，梦月入怀；今又梦日，何也：”坚曰：“日月者，阴阳之精，极贵之象，吾子孙其兴乎。”
    　　汉蔡茂字子礼，河内怀人也。初在广汉，梦坐大殿，极上有禾三穗。茂取之，得其中穗，辄复失之。以问主簿郭贺。贺曰：“大殿者，官府之形象也。极而有禾，人臣之上禄也。取中穗，是中台之象也。于字，‘禾’‘失’为‘秩’，虽曰失之，乃所以禄也。兖职中阙，君其补之。”旬月，而茂征焉。

    Explanation

    112

    Search for Gods, Volume Ten

    Empress Deng of the Han Dynasty, during her reign as the Consort of Emperor He, once dreamed of climbing a ladder to touch the sky. Her body felt light, clear, and smooth, as if she were touching stalactites. She then drank something while looking up. She consulted a dream interpreter, who said, "Emperor Yao dreamed of climbing to the heavens, and Emperor Tang dreamed of reaching the sky. These were signs of their future greatness. The good fortune is indescribable."

    Wu, the wife of Sun Jian, dreamed that the moon entered her womb while she was pregnant. Later, she gave birth to Sun Ce. When she was pregnant with Sun Quan, she again dreamed that the sun entered her womb. She told Sun Jian, "When I was pregnant with Ce, I dreamed that the moon entered my womb; now I have dreamed of the sun. What does this mean?" Sun Jian replied, "The sun and moon represent the essence of yin and yang, symbols of the utmost nobility. Our descendants will surely prosper."

    Cai Mao, a scholar and official of the Han Dynasty, whose courtesy name was Zilǐ, was from Huai, He Nei. While serving in Guanghan, he dreamed of sitting on a grand hall, with three ears of grain at the highest point. Cai Mao picked one of the ears, but then lost it. He asked his subordinate Guo He for an interpretation. Guo He said, "The grand hall represents the image of an official residence. At the highest point, there is grain, which symbolizes the highest salary for a minister. Taking the middle ear of grain is a symbol of the middle platform. In the character, '禾' (grain) and '失' (lost) make '秩' (rank). Although it seems lost, it is actually a salary. There is a vacancy in the central position of the state, you should fill it." Within a month, Cai Mao was summoned to serve in a high position.

    113

    周揽啧者，贫而好道，失妇夜耕，困，息卧。梦天公过而哀之，敕外有以给与。司命按录籍，云：“此人相贫，限不过此。惟有张车子，应赐录千万。车子未生，请以借之。”天公曰：“善。”曙觉，言之。于是夫妇戮力，昼夜治生，所为辄得，赀至千万。先时。有张妪者，尝往周家佣赁，野合，有身，月满，当孕，便遣出外，驻车屋下，产得儿。主人往视，哀其孤寒，作粥糜食之。问：“当名汝儿作何？”妪曰：“今在车屋下而生，梦天告之，名为车子。”周乃悟曰：“吾昔梦从天换钱，外白以张车子钱贷我，必是子也。财当归之矣。”自是居日衰减，车子长大，富于周家。
    　　夏阳卢汾，字士济，梦入蚁穴，见堂宇三间，势甚危豁，题其额，曰：审雨堂。
    　　吴选曹令史刘卓，病笃，梦见一人，以白越单衫与之，言曰：“汝着衫，污，火烧，便洁也。”卓觉，果有衫在侧。污，辄火浣之。

    Explanation

    113

    Zhou Lanze, a man who was poor but fond of the Way, lost his wife and worked at night, growing tired and resting to sleep. In his dream, the Heavenly Official passed by and pitied him, ordering someone outside to give him something. The Official of Life and Death checked the records and said, "This person's destiny is poverty, limited to this. Only Zhang Cheli should be given a record of ten thousand. Zhang Cheli has not been born, please lend it to him." The Heavenly Official said, "Good." Upon waking, Zhou shared his dream. From then on, the couple united their efforts and worked all day and night to improve their livelihood, achieving everything they set out to do, accumulating wealth to the tune of ten thousand. Previously, there was an old woman named Zhang who had once gone to Zhou's house as a hired worker. They had a wild union, and when the moon was full, she was pregnant. She was sent outside, where she stopped under the carriage house and gave birth to a son. The master went to see and pitied her loneliness and poverty, making porridge to feed her. He asked, "What should you name your child?" The woman said, "Now that he was born under the carriage house, I dreamed that the Heavenly One told me to name him Zhang Cheli." Zhou then realized, "I once dreamed of exchanging money with heaven, and someone told me to lend me Zhang Cheli's money. It must be this child. Wealth should return to him." From then on, his residence declined, and Zhang Cheli grew up to be wealthier than the Zhou family.

    In the summer of Yang, Lu Fen, styled Shiji, dreamed of entering an ant nest, where he saw a three-room hall with a very precarious structure. He inscribed its name as "Shen Yu Tang."

    Wu Xuan Cao Ling Shi Liu Zhuo, who was seriously ill, dreamed of a person who gave him a white Yue single robe and said, "You wear the robe. If it gets dirty, burn it, and it will be clean." Liu Zhuo woke up, and indeed there was a robe beside him. When it got dirty, he washed it with fire.

    进南书佐刘雅。梦见青刺蜴从屋落其腹内。因苦腹痛病。
    　　后汉张奂为武威太守，其妻梦帝与印绶，登楼而歌。觉，以告奂。奂令占之，曰：“夫人方生男，后临此郡命终此楼。”后生子猛，建安中，果为武威太守杀刺史，邯郸商州兵围急，猛耻见擒，乃登楼自焚而死。
    　　汉灵帝梦见桓帝，怒曰：“宋皇后有何罪过，而听用邪孽，使绝其命。渤海王悝，既已自贬，又受诛毙。今宋氏及悝，自诉于天，上帝震怒，罪在难救。”梦殊明察。帝既觉而恐，寻亦崩。
    　　吴时嘉兴徐伯始病，使道士吕石安神座，石有弟子戴本、王思，三人居住海盐，伯始迎之以助石。昼卧，梦上天北斗门下见外鞍马三匹。云：“明日当以一迎石，一迎本，一迎思。”石梦觉，语本、思云：“如此死期，可急还，与家别。”不卒事而去。伯始怪而留之。曰：“惧不得见家也。”间一日，三人同时死。

    114

    Translation:

    Liu Ya, promoted to the position of Shuzuo in the southern region, had a dream where a green spiny lizard fell into his abdomen, after which he suffered from severe abdominal pain.

    During the Later Han period, Zhang Huan served as the governor of Wuwei. His wife dreamed that the emperor gave her a seal and sash, and she climbed a tower to sing. Upon waking, she told Zhang Huan about the dream. Zhang Huan had it interpreted, and the interpreter said, "Your wife will give birth to a son who will later die in this tower while serving as the governor of Wuwei." Indeed, during the Jian’an period, Zhang Huan’s son, Liu Yong, became the governor of Wuwei and killed the governor (刺史). When the army of Shangdang besieged him, Liu Yong, feeling ashamed of being captured, climbed the tower and committed suicide by fire.

    Emperor Ling of Han dreamed of Emperor Yuan and became angry, saying, "What crimes did Empress Song commit that you allowed wicked forces to execute her? Prince Ku of Bohai, who had already abdicated, was also executed. Now, the spirits of Empress Song and Prince Ku are petitioning heaven, and the gods are furious, making their punishment inevitable." The dream was clear and insightful. After waking, Emperor Ling was terrified and soon died.

    During the Wu period in Jiaxing, Xu Bishi fell ill and invited the Taoist priest Lu Shi to perform a ritual. Lu Shi had disciples named Dai Ben and Wang Si, who lived in Haisan. Xu Bishi invited them to assist Lu Shi. During the day, Xu Bishi had a dream where he saw three saddled horses at the North Star gate. The dream said, "Tomorrow, one horse will be for Lu Shi, one for Dai Ben, and one for Wang Si." Lu Shi woke up and told Dai Ben and Wang Si, "You are facing death. Return home quickly and say goodbye to your families." They left without completing their task. Xu Bishi was surprised and kept them. They said, "We are afraid we won’t see our families again." A day later, all three died simultaneously.

    会稽谢奉与永嘉太守郭伯猷善，谢忽梦郭与人于浙江上争樗蒲钱。因为水神所责，堕水而死。已营理郭凶事。及觉，即往郭许，共围棋，良久，谢云：“卿知吾来意否：”因说所梦。郭闻之，怅然云：“吾作夜亦梦与人争钱，如卿所梦，何期太的的也？”须臾，如厕，便倒，气绝。谢为凶具。
    　　嘉兴徐泰，幼丧父母，叔父隗养之，甚于所生。隗病，泰营侍甚勤。是夜三更中，梦二人乘船持箱，上泰床头，发箱，出簿书示曰：“汝叔应死。”泰即于梦中叩头祈请。良久，二人曰：“汝县有同姓名人否？”泰思得，语二人云：“张隗，不姓徐。”二人云：“亦可强逼。念汝能事叔父，当为汝活之。”遂不复见。泰觉，叔病乃差。

    115

    The Prefect of Kuaiji, Xie Feng, was on good terms with the Governor of Yongjia, Guo Boyou. One night, Xie had a dream in which he saw Guo playing a game of chupu with someone by the Yangtze River, and because they lost the bet, they were punished by a water deity and drowned. Xie then arranged the funeral affairs for Guo. Upon waking, he immediately went to Guo's residence and played chess with him. After a long while, Xie said, "Do you know why I came?" and told Guo about his dream. Guo, upon hearing this, sighed and said, "Last night, I also had a dream where I was arguing over money with someone, just as you described. How could it be so precise?" Shortly after, Guo went to use the restroom and suddenly collapsed, dying on the spot. Xie then prepared for the funeral.

    In Jiaxing, there was a man named Xu Tai who lost his parents at a young age. His uncle, Wei, took care of him more than his own parents. When Wei fell ill, Xu cared for him diligently. One night during the third watch, Xu had a dream in which two men arrived on a boat carrying a chest, which they placed at the foot of his bed. They opened the chest and took out a ledger, showing it to Xu and saying, "Your uncle is destined to die." Xu immediately knelt in the dream and pleaded with them. After a long time, the two men asked, "Is there anyone in your county with the same name as your uncle?" Xu thought for a moment and replied, "There is a man named Zhang Wei, but he does not share the same surname." The two men said, "We can also compel him. Considering your filial piety towards your uncle, we will save him for you." With that, they disappeared. Xu woke up, and his uncle's illness soon improved.

    搜神记卷十一
    　　楚熊渠子夜行见寝石，以为伏虎，弯弓射之。没金，铩羽。下视，知其石也。因复射之，矢摧，无迹。汉世复有李广，为右北平太守，射虎，得石，亦如之。刘向曰：“诚之至也，而金石为之开，况于人乎！夫唱而不和，动而不随，中必有不全者也。夫不降席而匡天下者，求之己也。”
    　　楚王游于苑，白猿在焉；王令善射者射之，矢数发，猿搏矢而笑；乃命由基，由基抚弓，猿即抱木而号。及六国时，更羸谓魏王曰：“臣能为虚发而下鸟。”魏王曰：“然则射可至于此乎？”羸曰：“可。”有顷闻雁从东方来，更羸虚发而鸟下焉。

    Explanation

    116

    The Search for Spirits, Volume XI

    In the state of Chu, there was a man named Xiong Quchi who, while walking at night, saw a sleeping stone and mistook it for a crouching tiger. He drew his bow and shot at it. The arrow penetrated the stone and broke the bowstring. Looking down, he realized it was a stone. He then shot it again, and the arrow shattered, leaving no trace. In the Han dynasty, there was another archer named Li Guang, who served as the governor of Youbeiping. He once shot at a tiger and struck a stone, just as Xiong Quchi had done. Liu Xiang commented, "When sincerity reaches its utmost, even metal and stone will open up; how much more so, then, for people! If one sings and no one responds, or if one moves and no one follows, there must be something incomplete within. One who can govern the world without leaving their seat must seek it within themselves."

    The King of Chu was walking in the garden, and a white monkey was there. The king ordered a skilled archer to shoot at it. The archer shot several arrows, and the monkey caught the arrows and laughed. The king then summoned You Ji, who drew his bow, and the monkey immediately hugged the tree and cried. In the time of the Warring States, Geng Lei told King Wei of Wei, "I can shoot and make the bird fall without actually hitting it." King Wei asked, "Then can archery reach this level?" Geng Lei replied, "Yes." Shortly after, they heard a goose flying from the east, and Geng Lei shot, and the bird fell.

    117

    齐景公渡于江、沅之河，鼋衔左骖，没之。众皆惊惕；古冶子于是拔剑从之，邪行五里，逆行三里，至于砥柱之下，杀之，乃鼋也，左手持鼋头，右手拔左骖，燕跃鹄踊而出，仰天大呼，水为逆流三百步。观者皆以为河伯也。
    　　楚干将莫邪为楚王作剑，三年乃成，王怒，欲杀之。刘有雌雄，其妻重身，当产，夫语妻曰：“吾为王作剑，三年乃成；王怒，往，必杀我。汝若生子，是男，大，告之曰：‘出户，望南山，松生石上，剑在其背。’”于是即将雌剑往见楚王。王大怒，使相之，剑有二一雄，一雌，雌来，雄不来。王怒，即杀之。莫邪子名赤，比后壮，乃问其母曰：“吾父所在？”母曰：“汝父为楚王作剑，三年乃成，王怒，杀之。去时嘱我：‘语汝子：出户，往南山，松生石上，剑在其背。’”于是子出户，南望，不见有山，但睹堂前松柱下石砥之上，即以斧破其背，得剑。日夜思欲报楚王。王梦见一儿，眉间广尺，言欲报雠。

    Explanation

    117

    King Jing of Qi was crossing the Yangtze and Xiang rivers when a giant turtle bit the left horse and drowned it. Everyone was startled; at this point, Gu Yezhi drew his sword and followed the turtle, swerving five li and backtracking three li, until he reached the foot of the Stone Pillar. He killed the turtle, which turned out to be the giant turtle, holding its head in his left hand and pulling the left horse out with his right hand. He leaped like a swallow and jumped like a swan, emerging from the water, and cried out to the sky, causing the water to flow backward three hundred steps. Onlookers all thought it was the River God.

    The legendary swordsmiths Gan Jiang and Mo Ye were making swords for the king of Chu, taking three years to complete them. The king became angry and wanted to kill them. They had a pair of swords, one male and one female. When Mo Ye's wife was pregnant, her husband told her, "I made the sword for the king, and it took three years to complete. The king is angry, and if I go, he will definitely kill me. If you give birth to a son, tell him when he grows up: 'Go out the door, look toward the south mountain, where a pine tree grows on a rock, and the sword is on its back.'" So she took the female sword to see the king. The king became furious and had it examined, and it was found that there were two swords, one male and one female, with the female present and the male absent. The king became even angrier and killed her. Mo Ye's son, named Chi, grew up and asked his mother, "Where is my father?" She replied, "Your father made the sword for the king, and it took three years to complete. The king was angry and killed him. Before he left, he entrusted me with a message: 'Tell your son: Go out the door, go to the south mountain, where a pine tree grows on a rock, and the sword is on its back.'" So the boy went out the door and looked south, but saw no mountain, only a pine tree growing on a stone base at the foot of a pillar in the hall. He immediately broke open the back of the pillar with an axe and found the sword. Day and night, he thought about avenging the king of Chu. The king dreamed of a boy with a broad forehead, saying he wanted to take revenge.

    118

    王即购之千金。儿闻之，亡去，入山，行歌。客有逢者。谓：“子年少。何哭之甚悲耶：”曰：“吾干将莫邪子也。楚王杀吾父，吾欲报之。”客曰：“闻王购子头千金，将子头与剑来，为子报之。”儿曰：“幸甚。”即自刎，两手捧头及剑奉之，立僵。”客曰：“不负子也。”于是尸乃仆。客持头往见楚王，王大喜。客曰：“此乃勇士头也。当于汤镬煮之。”王如其言。煮头三日，三夕，不烂。头踔出汤中，踬目大怒。客曰：“此儿头不烂，愿王自往临视之，是必烂也。”王即临之。客以剑拟王，王头随堕汤中；客亦自拟己头，头复堕汤中。三首俱烂，不可识别。乃分其汤肉葬之。故通名三王墓。今在汝南北宜春县界。

    Explanation

    118

    The king offered a thousand gold coins for the head of the son of Gan Jiang and Mo Ye. The son heard this and fled into the mountains, singing as he walked. A guest met him and said, "You are young. Why are you crying so bitterly?" The son replied, "I am the son of Gan Jiang and Mo Ye. The king of Chu killed my father, and I wish to avenge him." The guest said, "I have heard that the king offered a thousand gold coins for your head. Bring your head and the sword to me, and I will avenge your father for you." The son said, "That would be wonderful." He immediately cut his own throat, held his head and the sword with both hands, and presented them to the guest, then stood rigidly. The guest said, "I will not fail you." Then the body fell down. The guest took the head to see the king, who was very pleased. The guest said, "This is the head of a brave warrior. It should be cooked in a pot of boiling water." The king followed his advice. The head was boiled for three days and three nights but did not rot. The sword leaped out of the boiling water, stumbled with its eyes, and showed great anger. The guest said, "This sword will not rot. I hope you will come and see it yourself, and it will definitely rot." The king immediately came to see it. The guest held the sword to the king's head, and the king's head fell into the boiling water. The guest also held the sword to his own head, and his head also fell into the boiling water. All three heads rotted simultaneously, and they could not be distinguished. They were then buried together. This is why it is commonly known as the Three Kings' Tomb. Now it is located in the territory of Yichun County, Northern Yu Prefecture.

    119

    汉武时，苍梧贾雍为豫章太守，有神术，出界讨贼，为贼所杀，失头，上马回营中，咸走来视雍。雍胸中语曰：“战不利，为贼所伤。诸君视有头佳乎？无头佳乎？”吏涕泣曰：“有头佳。”雍曰：“不然。无头亦佳。”言毕，遂死。
    　　渤海太守史良姊，一女子，许嫁而不果，良怒，杀之，断其头而归，投于灶下。曰“当令火葬。”头语曰：“使君我相从，何图当尔。”后梦见曰：“还君物。”觉而得昔所与香缨金钗之属。
    　　周灵王时，苌弘见杀，蜀人因藏其血，三年，乃化而为碧。
    　　汉武帝东游，未出函谷关，有物当道，身长数丈，其状象牛，青眼而曜睛，四足，入土，动而不徙。百官惊骇。东方朔乃请以酒灌之。灌之数十斛，而物消。帝问其故。答曰：“此名为患忧气之所生也。此必是秦之狱地，不然，则罪人徒作之所聚。夫酒忘忧，故能消之也。”帝曰：“吁！博物之士，至于此乎！”

    Explanation

    119

    During the reign of Emperor Wu, Jia Yong from Cangwu served as the governor of Yuzhang. Possessed of divine powers, he crossed the border to attack rebels and was killed by them, losing his head. He mounted his horse and returned to camp, where all rushed to see him. From his chest, he spoke: "The battle was not favorable, and I was injured by the rebels. Do you think it is better to have a head or not to have one?" The officials wept and said, "It is better to have a head." Jia Yong replied, "Not so. Even without a head, it is still good." After he finished speaking, he died.

    In another incident, Shi Liang, the governor of Bohai, had a sister who was promised in marriage but the engagement did not materialize. Enraged, Liang killed her, cut off her head, and took it home, throwing it into the stove. He said, "I will have it cremated by fire." The head spoke, "Sir, I followed you, but who could have foreseen this?" Later, Liang dreamed that the head said, "Return your belongings to you." Upon waking, he found the perfumed hairpin and golden hairpin that she had given him before.

    During the reign of King Ling of Zhou, Chang Hong was executed, and the people of Shu collected his blood. After three years, it transformed into a blue gemstone.

    Emperor Wu of Han embarked on an eastern tour and had not yet left the Hangu Pass when he encountered a creature blocking the road. It was several zhang long, resembling a cow with blue eyes and shining pupils, with four feet and part of its body buried in the ground, moving but not moving away. The officials were terrified. Dongfang Shuo then requested to pour wine over it. After pouring dozens of dou of wine, the creature disappeared. The emperor asked him why it happened. Dongfang Shuo replied, "This is called a manifestation of sorrow and anger. It must be a place where people were buried in the Qin prison, or a gathering place for criminals and convicts. Wine forgets sorrow, hence it can dispel it." The emperor exclaimed, "Ah! Scholars with vast knowledge can understand such things!"

    120

    后汉，谅辅，字汉儒，广汉新都人，少给佐吏，浆水不交，为从事，大小毕举，郡县敛手。时夏枯旱，太守自曝中庭，而雨不降；辅以五官掾出祷山川，自誓曰：“辅为郡股肱，不能进谏，纳忠，荐贤，退恶，和调百姓；至令天地否隔，万物枯焦，百姓喁喁，无所控诉，咎尽在辅。今郡太守内省责己，自曝中庭，使辅谢罪，为民祈福；精诚恳到，未有感彻，辅今敢自誓：若至日中无雨，请以身塞无状。”乃积薪柴，将自焚焉。至日中时，山气转黑，起雷，雨大作，一郡沾润。世以此称其至诚。
    　　何敞吴郡人，少好道艺，隐居，里以大旱，民物憔悴，太守庆洪遣户曹掾致谒，奉印绶，烦守无锡。敞不受。退，叹而言曰：“郡界有灾，安能得怀道！”因跋涉之县，驻明星屋中，蝗蝝消死，敞即遁去。后举方正博士，皆不就，卒于家。

    Explanation

    120

    During the Eastern Han Dynasty, Liang Fu, also known as Hanru, was a native of Xindu, Guanghan. As a young man, he served as an assistant official, barely making ends meet. He later became an attendant official, handling both major and minor affairs with thoroughness, earning the respect of the local officials. During a severe summer drought, the magistrate exposed himself in the courtyard in self-punishment, but no rain came. Liang Fu, as an assistant clerk, went out to pray at the mountains and rivers, vowing, "I am the pillar of the county. I have failed to offer advice, accept loyalty, recommend the worthy, and remove the wicked, leading to the separation of heaven and earth, the withering of all things, and the suffering of the people, who have nowhere to appeal. The fault lies entirely with me. Now, the magistrate has self-examined and exposed himself in the courtyard, asking me to confess my sins and pray for the people. Despite my sincere and earnest prayers, there has been no response. I dare to swear: if there is no rain by noon, I will sacrifice myself to atone for my sins." He then piled up firewood and prepared to burn himself. By noon, the mountain atmosphere turned dark, thunder rumbled, and heavy rain began to fall, drenching the entire county. The world praised him for his utmost sincerity.

    He was a native of Wu County, fond of the Dao and arts, and lived in seclusion. During a severe drought, the people were suffering, and the magistrate, Qian Hong, sent a household official to present a letter and seals, asking him to take office as the governor of Wuxi. He refused. Later, he sighed and said, "There is a disaster in the region, how can I remain devoted to the Dao?" He then traveled to the county, staying in a star-lit house, where the locusts and grasshoppers died, and he immediately retreated. Later, he was nominated as a scholar of integrity and righteousness but refused all nominations, dying at home.

    121

    后汉，徐栩，字敬卿，吴由拳人，少为狱吏，执法详平。为小黄令时，属县大蝗，野无生草，过小黄界，飞逝，不集。刺史行部责栩不治。栩弃官，蝗应声而至。刺史谢令还寺舍，蝗即飞去。
    　　王业，字子香，汉和帝时为荆州刺史，每出行部，沐浴斋素，以祈于天地，当启佐愚心，无使有枉百姓。在州七年，惠风大行，苛慝不作，山无豺狼。卒于湘江，有二白虎，低头，曳尾，宿卫其侧。及丧去，虎踰州境，忽然不见。民共为立碑，号曰：湘江白虎墓。
    　　吴时，葛祚为衡阳太守，郡境有大槎横水，能为妖怪，百姓为立庙，行旅祷祀，槎乃沈没，不者，槎浮，则船为之破坏。祚将去官，乃大具斧斤，将去民累。明日，当至，其夜闻江中汹汹有人声，往视之，槎乃移去，沿流下数里，驻湾中。自此行者无复沈覆之患。衡阳人为祚立碑，曰“正德祈禳，神木为移。”

    Explanation

    121

    During the Eastern Han Dynasty, Xu Xu, courtesy name Jingqing, was from Youquan in Wu. He began his career as a prison official and administered justice with fairness and thoroughness. When he served as the governor of Xiaohuang, a major locust infestation occurred in the subordinate counties, leaving the fields devoid of living grass. However, when the locusts passed through Xiaohuang, they flew away and did not settle. The governor, on inspection, blamed Xu for failing to manage the situation. Xu resigned his office, and the locusts responded to his resignation by appearing. The governor apologized and invited him back to his official residence, and the locusts immediately flew away.

    Wang Ye, courtesy name Zi Xiang, served as the governor of Jingzhou during the reign of Emperor He of Han. Before each inspection, he took a ritual bath and fasted, praying to heaven and earth to enlighten and assist his foolish heart and prevent the oppression of the people. Under his governance, benevolent policies were widely implemented, harsh and wicked deeds did not occur, and there were no tigers or wolves in the mountains. He died in Xiangjiang, and two white tigers, crouching down and dragging their tails, guarded beside his body. Upon his departure after death, the tigers crossed the borders of the state and suddenly disappeared. The people collectively erected a stele and named it: The Tomb of the White Tigers of Xiangjiang.

    During the Wu period, Ge Zuo served as the governor of Hengyang. There was a large log blocking the river in the jurisdiction, capable of causing mischief. The people built a temple for it, and travelers prayed and made offerings. The log would sink if they did so, but if not, it would float and destroy boats. Ge Zuo was about to leave his office and gathered many axes to remove the burden on the people. That night, he heard loud noises like people in the river. He went to see and found the log had moved away, flowing downstream several miles and stopping in a bay. From then on, travelers no longer suffered from the danger of sinking. The people of Hengyang erected a stele for Ge Zuo, naming it: Righteousness and prayers moved the divine wood.

    122

    曾子从仲尼在楚，而心动，辞归，问母，母曰：“思尔，啮指。”孔子曰：“曾参之孝，精感万里。”
    　　周畅，性仁慈，少至孝，独与母居，每出入，母欲呼之，常自啮其手，畅即觉手痛而至。治中从事未之信。候畅在田，使母啮手，而畅即归。元初二年，为河南尹，时夏大旱，久祷无应；畅收葬洛阳城旁客死骸骨万余，为立义冢，应时澍雨。
    　　王祥，字休征，琅邪人，性至孝，早丧亲，继母朱氏不慈，数谮之，由是失爱于父。每使扫除牛下。父母有疾，衣不解带。母常欲生鱼，时天寒，冰冻，祥解衣将剖冰求之，冰忽自解，双鲤跃出，持之而归。母又思黄雀炙，复有黄雀数十，入其幙，复以供母。乡里惊叹，以为孝感所致。

    Explanation

    122

    Zengzi was following Confucius in the state of Chu when his heart was moved, and he respectfully declined and returned home. He asked his mother, who said, "I miss you, and I bite my finger." Confucius remarked, "Zengzi's filial piety could move over a thousand miles."

    Zhan Chang was a kind and filial man who lived alone with his mother. Whenever she wanted to call him, she would bite her hand, and Zhan Chang would feel pain in his hand and come to her. The governor of Henan did not believe this story. He waited for Zhan Chang to be in the fields and made his mother bite her hand, and Zhan Chang immediately returned. In the second year of the Yuanchu era, Zhan Chang became the governor of Henan. There was a severe drought in summer, and long prayers had no response. Zhan Chang gathered and buried more than ten thousand travelers' remains near the city of Luoyang and established a public cemetery. In response to the time, abundant rain fell.

    Wang Xiang, with the courtesy name Xiuzheng, was from Langya. He had an extremely filial nature and lost his parents at a young age. His stepmother Zhu was not kind and often slandered him, causing him to lose his father's affection. He was often made to clean under the ox. When his parents were ill, he did not take off his clothes or remove his belt. His mother often wanted fresh fish, and it was cold at the time with the ice frozen. Wang Xiang took off his clothes and intended to cut through the ice to find it. The ice suddenly split open by itself, and two carp jumped out. He took them and returned. His mother also thought of roasted quail, and there were again dozens of quail that entered his tent, which he used to provide for his mother. The local people were amazed and exclaimed, believing that his filial piety caused these miracles.

    123

    王延，性至孝；继母卜氏，尝盛冬思生鱼，敕延求而不获，杖之流血；延寻汾叩凌而哭，忽有一鱼，长五尺，跃出冰上，延取以进母。卜氏食之，积日不尽。于是心悟，抚延如己子。
    　　楚僚，早失母，事后母至孝，母患痈肿，形容日悴，僚自徐徐吮之，血出，迨夜即得安寝。乃梦一小儿，语母曰：“若得鲤鱼食之，其病即差，可以延寿。不然，不久死矣。”母觉而告僚，时十二月，冰冻，僚乃仰天叹泣，脱衣上冰，卧之。有一童子，决僚卧处，冰忽自开，一双鲤鱼跃出。僚将归奉其母，病即愈。寿至一百三十三岁。盖至孝感天神，昭应如此。此与王祥，王延事同。

    Explanation

    123

    Wang Yan was known for his utmost filial piety. His stepmother, Bo, once in the severe winter, thought of fresh fish and ordered Wang Yan to find it. He failed to obtain it and was beaten until he bled. Wang Yan then went to the Fen River and knocked on the ice while crying. Suddenly, a fish five feet long leaped out of the ice. Wang Yan caught it and presented it to his mother. Bo ate it, and for several days it did not finish. She then realized the truth and treated Wang Yan as her own son.

    Liao, on the other hand, lost his mother early and showed utmost filial piety to his stepmother. His stepmother suffered from boils, and her appearance became increasingly emaciated. Liao slowly sucked on the boils, and blood came out, and by night she was able to sleep peacefully. One night, she dreamed of a little boy who said to her, "If you can eat a carp, your illness will be cured, and you can live longer. Otherwise, you will die soon." She woke up and told Liao about the dream. It was December, and the ice was frozen. Liao then looked up to the sky, wept, and took off his clothes to lie on the ice. A little boy appeared and broke the ice where Liao lay, and a pair of carps leaped out. Liao took them back to his stepmother, and her illness was cured. She lived to be 133 years old. It is said that his utmost filial piety moved the gods, and thus this miraculous event occurred. This is similar to the stories of Wang Xiang and Wang Yan.

    124

    盛彦，字翁子，广陵人，母王氏，因疾失明，彦躬自侍养。母食，必自哺之。母疾，既久，至于婢使数见捶挞，婢忿恨，闻彦蹔行，取蛴螬炙饴之。母食，以为美，然疑是异物，密藏以示彦。彦见之，抱母恸哭，绝而复苏。母目豁然即开，于此遂愈。
    　　颜含，宇弘都，次嫂樊氏，因疾失明，医人疏方，须蚺蛇胆，而寻求备至，无由得之。含忧叹累时，尝昼独坐，忽有一青衣童子，年可十三四，持一青囊授含，含开视，乃蛇胆也。童子逡巡出户，化成青鸟飞去。得胆，药成，嫂病即愈。

    Explanation

    124

    Sheng Yan, courtesy name Wengzi, was from Guangling. His mother, Wang, had lost her sight due to an illness, and Yan personally took care of her. Whenever his mother ate, he would feed her himself. After his mother's illness persisted for a long time, the servant, resentful of being frequently beaten, took advantage of Yan's brief absence to prepare a roasted beetle larva and serve it to his mother. His mother thought it delicious but suspected it was something unusual, so she secretly kept it to show to Yan. When Yan saw it, he held his mother and cried bitterly, causing her to faint and then revive. His mother's eyes suddenly opened, and she was healed at that moment.

    Yan Han, courtesy name Hongdu, had a sister-in-law named Fan who also lost her sight due to an illness. The doctor prescribed a remedy that required the bile of a king cobra, and they searched thoroughly but could not obtain it. Yan Han worried and sighed for a long time. One day, while sitting alone during the day, he suddenly saw a young boy dressed in green, about thirteen or fourteen years old, holding a green bag and giving it to him. Yan Han opened it and found it contained the snake bile. The boy hesitated and went out the door, transforming into a green bird and flying away. With the bile, the medicine was prepared, and his sister-in-law's illness was cured.

    125

    郭巨，隆虑人也，一云河内温人，兄弟三人，早丧父，礼毕，二弟求分，以钱二千万，二弟各取千万，巨独与母居客舍，夫妇佣赁以给公养。居有顷，妻产男，巨念举儿妨事亲，一也；老人得食，喜分儿孙，减馔，二也；乃于野凿地，欲埋儿，得石盖，下有黄金一釜，中有丹书，曰：“孝子郭巨，黄金一釜，以用赐汝。”于是名振天下。
    　　新兴刘殷，字长盛，七岁丧父，哀毁过礼，服丧三年，未尝见齿。事曾祖母王氏，尝夜梦人谓之曰：“西篱下有粟。”寤而掘之，得粟十五钟，铭曰：“七年粟百石，以赐孝子刘殷。”自是食之七岁，方尽。及王氏卒，夫妇毁瘠，几至灭性。时柩在殡，而西邻失火，风势甚猛，殷夫妇叩殡号哭，火遂灭。后有二白鸠来巢其树庭。

    Explanation

    125

    Guo Ju was from Longlu (modern-day Henan), though some say he was from Henan's Wen County. He had two younger brothers, and after their father died, they completed the funeral rites. The two younger brothers then requested to divide the inheritance, which amounted to two million coins. Each brother took one million coins, leaving Guo Ju to live alone with his mother in a rented house, where he and his wife worked as hired laborers to support their mother. After a short while, Guo Ju's wife gave birth to a son. Guo Ju thought that raising a son would interfere with serving his parents, and the elderly enjoyed sharing food with their grandchildren, reducing their own meals. So, he dug a hole in the wilderness, intending to bury his son. He found a stone lid covering a pot of gold, and inside there was a red scroll that read, "To the filial son Guo Ju, a pot of gold, to be used as a gift to you." His fame spread throughout the world.

    Liu Yin, from Xinxing, whose courtesy name was Changsheng, lost his father at the age of seven. His grief and mourning exceeded the prescribed rituals, and he observed the three-year mourning period without smiling. He cared for his great-grandmother Wang. Once, he dreamed that someone told him, "There is millet under the western fence." He woke up and dug there, finding fifteen shi of millet. The inscription said, "Seven years of millet, to be given to the filial son Liu Yin." He and his family ate from this supply for seven years until it was finished. When Wang passed away, his husband and wife were so grief-stricken that they nearly lost their lives. When the coffin was being mourned, a fire broke out in the west neighbor's house. The wind was very strong. Liu Yin and his wife knelt by the coffin and cried, and the fire was extinguished. Later, two white doves came to nest in the courtyard trees.

    126

    杨公伯，雍雒阳县人也，本以侩卖为业，性笃孝，父母亡，葬无终山，遂家焉。山高八十里，上无水，公汲水作义浆于阪头，行者皆饮之。三年，有一人就饮，以一斗石子与之，使至高平好地有石处种之，云：“玉当生其中，”杨公未娶，又语云：“汝后当得好妇。”语毕，不见。乃种其石，数岁，时时往视，见玉子生石上，人莫知也。有徐氏者，右北平着姓女，甚有行，时人求，多不许；公乃试求徐氏，徐氏笑以为狂，因戏云：“得白璧一双来，当听为婚。”公至所种玉田中，得白璧五双，以聘。徐氏大惊，遂以女妻公。天子闻而异之，拜为大夫。乃于种玉处四角，作大石柱，各一丈，中央一顷地名曰“玉田。”

    Explanation

    126

    Elong, from Yanggong, was a man from Long County who originally made a living as a merchant. By nature, he was filial. After his parents' death, he buried them at Wu Zong Mountain and settled there. The mountain was eighty li high, and there was no water at the top. Elong fetched water and made a charitable drink at the top of the slope, and all passersby drank it. After three years, a man came to drink and gave him a basket of stones, instructing him to plant them in a high, flat place with good soil. He said, "Jade will grow from these stones." Elong had not yet married, and the man also said, "You will eventually get a good wife." After speaking, the man disappeared. Elong planted the stones, and after several years, he often went to check on them and saw jade sprouting from the stones. No one knew about this.

    There was a woman from the Xu family, a prominent family in the right and north of Ping, who was very virtuous. Many people sought her hand in marriage, but she refused them all. Elong then tried to marry her, and she laughed at him, thinking he was crazy. She said, "Bring me a pair of white jade, and I will agree to the marriage." Elong went to the field where he had planted the stones and found five pairs of white jade. He brought them to the Xu family, and she was greatly surprised. She then married him.

    The emperor heard about this and was impressed, and he appointed Elong as a high official. In the place where the jade grew, four large stone pillars were built, each one zhang tall, and the central area of one mu of land was named "Jade Field."

    127

    衡农，字剽卿，东平人也。少孤，事继母至孝。常宿于他舍，值雷风，频梦虎啮其足，农呼妻相出于庭，叩头三下。屋忽然而坏，压死者三十余人，唯农夫妻获免。
    　　罗威，字德仁，八岁丧父，事母性至孝，母年七十，天大寒，常以身自温席而后授其处。
    　　王裒，字伟元，城阳营陵人也。父仪，为文帝所杀。裒庐于墓侧，旦夕常至墓所拜跪，攀柏悲号，涕泣着树，树为之枯。母性畏雷，母没，每雷，辄到墓曰：“裒在此。”

    Explanation

    127

    衡农，字剽卿，是东平人。他自幼失去父亲，对继母极为孝顺。有一次，他在别人家住宿时，遇到雷雨天气，频繁梦见老虎咬他的脚。衡农便叫妻子一起到院子里，向天叩头三次。突然，房屋倒塌，压死了三十多人，唯独衡农夫妇幸免于难。

    罗威，字德仁，八岁时父亲去世，他对母亲非常孝顺。母亲年已七十，每当天气寒冷，罗威都会用自己的身体先温暖床铺，然后再让母亲睡上去。

    王裒，字伟元，是城阳营陵人。他的父亲王仪被文帝所杀。王裒在父亲的墓旁搭建了一间草屋，早晚都会到墓前拜祭，有时还会爬到柏树上痛哭流涕，眼泪滴在树上，以至于树都枯萎了。母亲生前害怕打雷，母亲去世后，每当打雷，王裒就会跑到墓前说：“我在这里。”

    128

    郑弘迁临淮太守，郡民徐宪在丧，致哀，有白鸠巢户侧。弘举为孝廉。朝廷称为“白鸠郎。”
    　　汉时，东海孝妇养姑甚谨，姑曰：“妇养我勤苦，我已老，何惜余年，久累年少。”遂自缢死。其女告官云：“妇杀我母。”官收，系之。拷掠毒治，孝妇不堪苦楚，自诬服之。时于公为狱吏，曰：“此妇养姑十余年，以孝闻彻，必不杀也。”太守不听。于公争不得理，抱其狱词哭于府而去。自后郡中枯旱，三年不雨。后太守至，于公曰：“孝妇不当死，前太守枉杀之，咎当在此。”太守实时身祭孝妇冢，因表其墓，天立雨，岁大熟。长老传云：“孝妇名周青，青将死，车载十丈竹竿，以悬五旛，立誓于众曰：‘青若有罪，愿杀，血当顺下；青若枉死，血当逆流。’既行刑已，其血青黄缘旛竹而上，极标，又缘旛而下云。”

    Explanation

    128

    Zhen Hong was promoted to the position of Governor of Linyi. A local resident named Xu Xian, while in mourning for his parents, expressed his grief so deeply that a white dove nested near his house. Zhen Hong recommended Xu Xian as a孝廉. The court then referred to him as "White Dove Gentleman."

    During the Han Dynasty, there was a filial woman from the Eastern Sea region who took care of her mother-in-law with utmost diligence. Her mother-in-law said to her, "You have been taking care of me with great effort. I am old, and why should I cherish my remaining years and burden you, the young?" She then hanged herself. The woman's daughter reported to the authorities, claiming that her mother had killed her grandmother. The officials arrested the filial woman and subjected her to severe torture. Unable to bear the pain, she falsely confessed to the crime. At that time, Yu Gong was a prison official who said, "This woman has cared for her mother-in-law for over ten years, known for her filial piety, and surely would not kill her." However, the governor did not listen. Yu Gong argued in vain, and with the case documents in hand, he cried before the governor and left. After this, the entire county experienced a severe drought that lasted for three years without rain. When the new governor arrived, Yu Gong said, "This filial woman should not have died; the previous governor wrongfully executed her, and the calamity should be attributed to this." The new governor immediately went to the filial woman's grave to offer sacrifices and erected a monument at her tomb. Immediately, it rained, and the year produced a bountiful harvest. The elders passed down that the filial woman's name was Zhou Qing. Before her execution, she loaded a cart with a ten-zhang bamboo pole and hung five flags, swearing to the crowd, "If I am guilty, I wish to be killed; my blood should flow downward. If I am wrongfully executed, my blood should flow upward." After the execution, her blood flowed upward, turning green and yellow as it climbed the flagpole, reaching the top, and then flowed back down.

    129

    犍为叔先泥和，其女名雄，永建三年，泥和为县功曹，县长赵祉遣泥和拜檄，谒巴郡太守，以十月乘船，于城湍堕水死，尸丧不得。雄哀恸号咷，命不图存，告弟贤及夫人，令勤觅父尸，若求不得，吾欲自沈觅之。时雄年二十七，有子男贡，年五岁，贳，年三岁，乃各作绣香囊一枚，盛以金珠，环，预婴二子，哀号之声，不绝于口，昆族私忧。至十二月十五日，父丧不得，雄乘小船于父堕处，哭泣数声，竟自投水中，旋流没底。见梦告弟云：“至二十一日，与父俱出。”至期，如梦，与父相持幷浮出江。县长表言郡太守，肃登承上尚书，乃遣户曹掾为雄立碑，图象其形，令知至孝。

    Explanation

    129

    During the Yongjian era, in the third year, Shu Xian Ni He of Jianwei was a county official responsible for various administrative duties. The county magistrate, Zhao Zhi, sent him to deliver an official notice to pay respects to the governor of Bashu. In October, while traveling by boat, he fell into the turbulent waters of Chengtuan and drowned, and his body could not be recovered. His daughter, Xiong, who was twenty-seven years old, was overcome with grief and wept loudly, declaring that she had no intention of living. She told her brother Xian and her husband, instructing them to diligently search for her father's body. If they failed to find it, she said, she would drown herself in search of it. At the time, Xiong had two sons: Gòng, who was five years old, and Shì, who was three years old. She made each son a small embroidered bag filled with gold and jewels, and wore them around their necks, continuously crying out in grief. Her family privately worried about her. On the fifteenth day of December, when her father's body still could not be found, Xiong took a small boat to the place where her father had fallen, wept several times, and then jumped into the water, sinking to the bottom. She appeared in a dream to her brother and said, "On the twenty-first day, I will come out with my father." On that day, as predicted in her dream, she emerged from the water with her father, holding him tightly as they floated out of the river. The county magistrate reported this to the governor of the prefecture, who in turn reported to the imperial court. The court then sent an official to erect a stele in honor of Xiong, depicting her image, to show her extreme filial piety.

    130

    河南乐羊子之妻者，不知何氏之女也。躬勤养姑。尝有他舍鸡，谬入园中，姑盗杀而食之。妻对鸡不食而泣。姑怪问其故。妻曰：“自伤居贫，使食有他肉。”姑竟弃之。后盗有欲犯之者，乃先劫其姑，妻闻，操刀而出。盗曰：“释汝刀。从我者，可全；不从我者，则杀汝姑。”妻仰天而叹，刎颈而死。盗亦不杀姑。太守闻之，捕杀盗贼，赐妻缣帛，以礼葬之。
    　　庾衮，字叔褒，咸宁中大疫，二兄俱亡，次兄毗复殆，疠气方盛，父母诸弟皆出次于外，衮独留，不去。诸父兄强之，乃曰：“衮性不畏病。”遂亲自扶持，昼夜不眠。间复抚柩哀临不辍。如此十余旬，疫势既退，家人乃返。毗病得差，衮亦无恙。

    Explanation

    130

    The Wife of Le Yangzi from Henan
    The wife of Le Yangzi from Henan, whose family name is unknown, diligently cared for her mother-in-law. Once, a hen from another house mistakenly entered their garden, and the mother-in-law secretly killed and ate it. The wife, upon seeing this, did not eat the meat and wept. Her mother-in-law was surprised and asked her why she was crying. The wife replied, "I feel ashamed to live in poverty and eat food that is not earned by my own labor." The mother-in-law was so moved that she threw away the meat.

    Later, a thief intended to rob them. Before attacking, he first kidnapped the mother-in-law. The wife, hearing the commotion, took a knife and went out. The thief said, "Put down your knife. If you follow me, you can be spared; if you do not, I will kill your mother-in-law." The wife, looking up to the sky, sighed and then cut her own throat and died. The thief did not kill the mother-in-law. The local official, hearing of this, captured and killed the thief, granted the wife silk and cloth, and buried her with proper rites.

    Gu Yun, also known as Shubiao
    During the Xian period of the Three Kingdoms era, a great epidemic broke out. Two of Gu Yun's brothers died, and his third brother, Bi, was gravely ill. The epidemic was at its peak, and his parents and younger brothers all left the house. Only Gu Yun stayed behind, refusing to leave. His elders and brothers tried to persuade him to go, but he said, "I am not afraid of the disease." He stayed with his brother, Bi, day and night, never sleeping. Occasionally, he would mourn at his brother's coffin without ceasing. This continued for more than three months. Once the epidemic subsided, the family returned. Bi recovered, and Gu Yun remained unharmed.

    131

    宋康王舍人韩凭娶妻何氏，美，康王夺之。凭怨，王囚之，论为城旦。妻密遗凭书，缪其辞曰：“其雨淫淫，河大水深，日出当心。”既而王得其书，以示左右，左右莫解其意。臣苏贺对曰：“其雨淫淫，言愁且思也。河大水深，不得往来也。日出当心，心有死志也。”俄而凭乃自杀。其妻乃阴腐其衣，王与之登台，妻遂自投台，左右揽之，衣不中手而死。遗书于带曰：“王利其生，妾利其死，愿以尸骨赐凭合葬。”王怒，弗听，使里人埋之，冢相望也。王曰：“尔夫妇相爱不已，若能使冢合，则吾弗阻也。”宿昔之间，便有大梓木，生于二冢之端，旬日而大盈抱，屈体相就，根交于下，枝错于上。又有鸳鸯，雌雄各一，恒栖树上，晨夕不去，交颈悲鸣，音声感人。宋人哀之，遂号其木曰“相思树。”“相思”之名，起于此也。南人谓：此禽即韩凭夫妇之精魂。今睢阳有韩凭城，其歌谣至今犹存。

    Explanation

    131

    King Kang of Song had a retainer named Han Peng, who married a woman named He, renowned for her beauty. King Kang coveted her and took her for himself. Han Peng, filled with resentment, was imprisoned by the king and sentenced to penal labor. His wife secretly sent him a letter, obfuscating its meaning with poetic language: “The rain falls heavily, the river is deep and wide, the sun rises in my heart.” Later, the king obtained the letter and showed it to his attendants, none of whom could decipher its meaning. Minister Su He explained, “The rain falling heavily signifies sorrow and longing. The deep and wide river indicates separation. The sun rising in the heart means she has resolved to die.” Soon after, Han Peng committed suicide. His wife then secretly made her clothes rot, and the king took her to the tower. She leaped from the tower, and her attendants tried to catch her, but her clothes did not catch, and she died. She left a message on her belt: “The king benefits from my life, but I benefit from my death. I wish to be buried together with Han Peng.” The king was furious and refused to allow it, ordering her to be buried by the villagers, with their tombs facing each other. The king said, “If your love for each other persists, and you can make the tombs join, then I will not obstruct you.” Within a night or day, a large catalpa tree grew from the ends of the two tombs, growing to a size that could be embraced within ten days. The trees bent towards each other, their roots intertwining below and their branches above. There were also mandarin ducks, one male and one female, always perched on the tree. They did not leave day or night, calling to each other in sorrow, and their sounds moved people. The people of Song mourned their plight and named the tree the “Thinking of Each Other Tree.” The term “Thinking of Each Other” originated from this. Southern people say: these birds are the spirits of Han Peng and his wife. Now in Suizhou, there is a city named after Han Peng, and its songs and ballads still exist today.

    132

    汉末零阳郡太守史满，有女，悦门下书佐；乃密使侍婢取书佐盥手残水饮之，遂有妊。已而生子，至能行，太守令抱儿出，使求其父。儿匍匐直入书佐怀中。书佐推之仆地，化为水。穷问之，具省前事，遂以女妻书佐。
    　　鄱阳西有望夫冈。昔县人陈明与梅氏为婚，未成，而妖魅诈迎妇去。明诣卜者，决云：“行西北五十里求之。”明如言，见一大穴，深邃无底。以绳悬人，遂得其妇。乃令妇先出，而明所将邻人秦文，遂不取明。其妇乃自誓执志登此冈首而望其夫，因以名焉。

    Explanation

    132

    During the end of the Han Dynasty, the governor of Lingyang County, Shi Man, had a daughter who fell in love with a subordinate clerk. She secretly sent a female servant to fetch the leftover water from the clerk's handwashing and drink it, and thus became pregnant. Later, she gave birth to a son. When the child was able to walk, the governor ordered him to be taken out to find his father. The child crawled directly into the clerk's arms. The clerk pushed him down, and he turned into water. When thoroughly questioned, he fully understood the previous events, and so married his daughter to the clerk.

    West of Poyang there is a hill called Wife-Watching Hill. In the past, a man named Chen Ming from the county was betrothed to the family of Mei. But before the marriage was completed, a demon deceitfully took the bride away. Chen Ming went to a fortune-teller, who advised him: "Go fifty miles northwest to find her." Chen Ming followed the advice and saw a large cave, deep and bottomless. He lowered someone with a rope and eventually found his wife. He then ordered his wife to come out first, but the neighbor Qin Wen did not take Chen Ming. His wife then vowed to remain faithful and climbed to the top of this hill to look for her husband, and thus the hill was named after her.

    133

    后汉，南康邓元义，父伯考，为尚书仆射，元义还乡里，妻留事姑，甚谨。姑憎之，幽闭空室，节其饮食，羸露，日困，终无怨言。时伯考怪而问之，元义子朗，时方数岁，言：“母不病，但苦饥耳。”伯考流涕曰：“何意亲姑反为此祸！”遗归家，更嫁，为华仲妻。仲为将作大匠，妻乘朝车出，元义于路旁观之，谓人曰：“此我故妇，非有他过，家夫人遇之实酷，本自相贵。”其子朗，时为郎，母与书，皆不答，与衣裳，辄以烧之。母不以介意。母欲见之，乃至亲家李氏堂上，令人以他词请朗。朗至，见母，再拜涕泣，因起出。母追谓之曰：“我几死。自为汝家所弃，我何罪过，乃如此耶！”因此遂绝。

    Explanation

    133

    During the Eastern Han Dynasty, in Nankang, there was a man named Deng Yuanyi. His father, Deng Bokao, held the position of Secretary of the Imperial Secretariat. After returning to his hometown, Deng Yuanyi's wife remained to serve her mother-in-law with great respect. However, the mother-in-law detested her and confined her in an empty room, restricting her food and causing her to weaken and suffer daily, yet she never complained. At this time, Deng Bokao was surprised and asked about it. Deng Yuanyi's son, Lang, who was only a few years old at the time, said, "Mother is not sick, she just suffers from hunger." Deng Bokao wept and said, "How could treating one's mother-in-law result in such misfortune!" He sent her back home to be remarried, and she became the wife of Hua Zhong. Hua Zhong was the Chief Architect, and when his wife rode out in an official carriage, Deng Yuanyi watched from the side of the road and said to others, "This is my former wife; she had no other fault, but my wife treated her terribly, and we were originally respected by each other." At that time, Deng Lang was a junior official. When his mother wrote to him, he did not reply, and when she gave him clothes, he would burn them. The mother did not take it to heart. She wanted to see him and went to the R family's hall, sending someone to invite Lang with another excuse. When Lang arrived, he bowed twice and wept, then got up and left. The mother followed and said, "I nearly died. I was abandoned by your family, what have I done wrong to be treated like this!" Because of this, they became estranged.

    134

    严遵为扬州刺史，行部，闻道傍女子哭声不哀。问所哭者谁。对云：“夫遭烧死。”遵敕吏舁尸到，与语，讫，语吏云：“死人自道不烧死。”乃摄女，令人守尸，云：“当有枉。”吏曰：“有蝇聚头所。”遵令披视，得铁锥贯顶。考问，以淫杀夫。
    　　汉，范式，字巨卿，山阳金乡人也，一名泛，与汝南张劭为友，劭字符伯。二人并游太学，后告归乡里，式谓元伯曰“后二年，当还。将过拜尊亲，见孺子焉。”乃共克期日。后期方至，元伯具以白母，请设馔以候之。母曰：“二年之别，千里结言，尔何相信之审耶！”曰：“巨卿信士，必不乖违。”母曰：“若然，当为尔酝酒。”至期，果到。升堂，拜饮，尽欢而别。后元伯寝疾，甚笃，同郡到君章殷子征晨夜省视之。元伯临终，叹曰：“恨不见我死友。

    Explanation

    134

    Yan Zun served as the governor of Yangzhou. On one of his inspections, he heard a woman weeping by the roadside, and her voice was not sorrowful. He asked whom she was weeping for. She replied, "My husband died in a fire." Yan Zun ordered the officials to carry the corpse to him. When he spoke to the dead man, the man claimed, "I did not die from fire." Yan Zun then arrested the woman and ordered someone to guard the corpse, saying, "There must be some injustice." An official reported, "There were flies gathering around her head." Yan Zun ordered the corpse to be examined, and they found an iron spike through her head. Upon investigation, it was discovered that she had killed her husband through adultery.

    During the Han dynasty, Fan Shi, courtesy name Jüqing, was from Jinxiang, Shanyang. He was also known by the name Pan and was friends with Zhang Shao from Runan, whose courtesy name was Yuanbo. Both of them studied at the Imperial Academy. Later, they returned to their hometowns. Fan Shi told Yuanbo, "In two years, I will return. I will visit my esteemed relatives and see your young son." They agreed on a specific date. When the agreed date arrived, Yuanbo told his mother in detail, asking her to prepare a meal to welcome him. His mother said, "After two years of separation, you are making a promise from a thousand miles away. How can you be so sure of your trust?" Yuanbo replied, "Jüqing is a trustworthy man; he will surely not go back on his word." His mother said, "If that is so, I will prepare wine for you." When the day arrived, Fan Shi indeed came. They went up to the hall, bowed, drank, and parted in joy.

    Later, Yuanbo fell seriously ill. His fellow townsman Dao Junzhang and Yin Zizheng visited him day and night. As Yuanbo lay dying, he sighed, "I regret not seeing my dear friend die."

    135

    ”子征曰：“吾与君章尽心于子，是非死友，复欲谁求？”元伯曰：“若二子者，吾生友耳。山阳范巨卿，所谓死友也。”寻而卒。式忽梦见元伯，玄冕，垂缨，屣履，而呼曰：“巨卿！吾以某日死，当以尔时葬。永归黄泉。子未忘我，岂能相及！”式恍然觉悟，悲叹泣下。便服朋友之服，投其葬日，驰往赴之。未及到而丧已发引。既至圹，将窆，而柩不肯进。其母抚之曰：“元伯！岂有望耶？”遂停柩移时，乃见素车，白马，号哭而来。其母望之，曰：“是必范巨也。”既至，叩丧，言曰：“行矣元伯！死生异路，永从此辞。”会葬者千人，咸为挥涕。式因执绋而引柩。于是乃前。式遂留止冢次，为修坟树，然后乃去。

    Explanation

    135

    Zǐzhēng said, "I and your brother devoted ourselves to you. These are not true friends, but whom else do we seek?" Yuánbó replied, "If these two are true friends, they are only my living friends. Fan Jüqing of Shanyang, that is what is meant by true friends." Soon after, he died. Zhì suddenly dreamed of Yuánbó, who was wearing a black cap, with hanging tassels, and sandals, and called out, "Jüqing! I will die on a certain day, and will be buried at that time. I will forever return to the Yellow Springs. You have not forgotten me, how could you not come?" Zhì suddenly realized, and wept bitterly. He immediately dressed in mourning clothes, and on the day of the burial, he rushed to attend. Before he arrived, the funeral had already started. After arriving at the grave, when they were about to lower the coffin, the coffin would not move forward. His mother comforted him, saying, "Yuanbo! Is there any hope?" So they stopped the coffin for a while. Then they saw a white carriage, with a white horse, and came crying. His mother looked at them, saying, "It must be Fan Jüqing." When they arrived, they knelt in mourning, saying, "Farewell, Yuanbo! Life and death are different paths, we will never meet again." A thousand people gathered for the funeral, all of them wept. Zhì then took hold of the ropes and led the coffin. So it moved forward. Zhì then stayed at the grave, and repaired the tomb and planted trees, and then left.

    136

    搜神记卷十二
    　　天有五气，万物化成：木清则仁，火清则礼，金清则义，水清则智，土清则思：五气尽纯，圣德备也。木浊则弱，火浊则淫，金浊则暴，水浊则贪，土浊则顽：五气尽浊，民之下也。中土多圣人，和气所交也。绝域多怪物，异气所产也。苟禀此气，必有此形；苟有此形，必生此性。故食谷者智能而文，食草者多力而愚，食桑者有丝而蛾，食肉者勇橄而悍，食土者无心而不息，食气者神明而长寿，不食者不死而神。

    Explanation

    136

    Heaven has five elements, and all things are transformed through them: when wood is pure, it embodies benevolence; when fire is pure, it embodies propriety; when metal is pure, it embodies righteousness; when water is pure, it embodies wisdom; when earth is pure, it embodies thought. When the five elements are entirely pure, the virtues of a sage are complete. When wood is impure, it becomes weak; when fire is impure, it becomes licentious; when metal is impure, it becomes violent; when water is impure, it becomes greedy; when earth is impure, it becomes stubborn. When the five elements are entirely impure, it results in the lowest level of the people. The Central Land produces many sages because of the harmonious interaction of the elements. Remote regions produce many strange creatures because of the unusual elemental influences. If one is endowed with such elements, they will have such a form; if one has such a form, they will have such a nature. Therefore, those who eat grains are intelligent and cultured; those who eat grass are strong but foolish; those who feed on mulberry leaves produce silk and become silkworms; those who eat meat are brave and fierce; those who eat earth have no heart but continue to live; those who live on qi (vital energy) are divine and long-lived; and those who do not eat physical food are immortal and divine.

    137

    大腰无雄，细腰无雌；无雄外接，无雌外育。三化之虫，先孕后交；兼爱之兽，自为牝牡；寄生因夫高木，女萝托乎茯苓，木株于土，萍植于水，鸟排虚而飞，兽跖实而走，虫土闭而蛰，鱼渊潜而处。本乎天者亲上，本乎地者亲下，本乎时者亲旁：各从其类也。千岁之雉，入海为蜃；百年之雀，入海为蛤；千岁龟鼋，能与人语；千岁之狐，起为美女；千岁之蛇，断而复续；百年之鼠，而能相卜：数之至也。春分之日，鹰变为鸠；秋分之日，鸠变为鹰：时之化也。

    Explanation

    137

    A creature with a large body lacks a male counterpart, and one with a slender body lacks a female counterpart; without external fertilization by males, and without external nurturing by females. There are insects that become pregnant before mating, and animals that can change their sex; parasitic organisms depend on tall trees, and climbing plants rely on fungi, while trees grow in the soil, and water plants thrive in water. Birds soar through the air, and beasts walk on solid ground; insects burrow into the earth and hibernate, and fish hide in deep waters. Those rooted in heaven are drawn upward, those rooted in earth are drawn downward, and those rooted in time are drawn to the sides: each follows its own kind. A thousand-year-old pheasant transforms into a sea shell; a hundred-year-old sparrow turns into a clam; a thousand-year-old turtle or softshell turtle can communicate with humans; a thousand-year-old fox transforms into a beautiful woman; a thousand-year-old snake can regenerate after being cut; a hundred-year-old mouse can predict the future: this is the limit of numbers. On the day of the Spring Equinox, eagles transform into doves; on the day of the Autumn Equinox, doves transform into eagles: this is the transformation of time.

    138

    故腐草之为萤也，朽苇之为蛬也，稻之为●也，麦之为蝴蝶也；羽翼生焉，眼目成焉，心智在焉：此自无知化为有知，而气易也。雀之为獐也，蛬之为虾也：不失其血气，而形性变也。若此之类，不可胜论。应变而动，是为顺常；苟错其方，则为妖眚。故下体生于上，上体生于下：气之反者也。人生兽，兽生人：气之乱者也。男化为女，女化为男：气之贸者也。鲁，牛哀，得疾，七日化而为虎，形体变易，爪牙施张。其兄启户而入，搏而食之。

    Explanation

    138

    Therefore, when decaying grass transforms into fireflies, rotten reeds into cicadas, rice into [unknown creature], and wheat into butterflies; wings and feathers grow, eyes and eyes form, and intellect arises: this is the transformation from a state of no consciousness to one of consciousness, with a change in qi. When sparrows transform into deer, and cicadas into shrimp: the vital energy remains the same, but the form and nature change. Such transformations are numerous and cannot be fully discussed. Responding to changes and acting accordingly is in accordance with the natural order; if the order is disrupted, it becomes an omen of misfortune. When the lower body is born from the upper, and the upper body is born from the lower: this is a reversal of the usual order of generation. When humans transform into animals, and animals transform into humans: this is a transformation between genders. When men transform into women, and women transform into men: this is a transformation of gender. In the state of Lu, Niu Ai, suffering from illness, transformed into a tiger after seven days; his form changed, and his claws and teeth emerged. His brother opened the door and entered, and he attacked and ate him.

    139

    方其为人，不知其将为虎也；方有为虎，不知其常为人也。故晋，太康中，陈留阮士瑀，伤于虺，不忍其痛，数嗅其疮，已而双虺成于鼻中。元康中，历阳纪元载客食道龟，已而成瘕，医以药攻之，下龟子数升，大如小钱，头足壳备，文甲皆具，惟中药已死。夫妻非化育之气，鼻非胎孕之所，享道非下物之具：从此观之，万物之生死也，与其变化也，非通神之思，虽求诸已，恶识所自来。然朽草之为萤，由乎腐也；麦之为蝴蝶，由乎湿也。尔则万物之变，皆有由也。农夫止麦之化者，沤之以灰；圣人理万物之化者，济之以道：其然与；不然乎？

    Explanation

    139

    When it is human, one does not know it will become a tiger; when it becomes a tiger, one does not know it was once human. Thus, during the Western Jin dynasty, in the reign of Emperor Sima Zhong, a man from Chenliu named Ruanyi was bitten by a snake. Unable to bear the pain, he sniffed his wound repeatedly, and later two snakes formed in his nose. In the reign of Emperor Sima Ying, a guest from Liyang named Jiyuan ate a turtle, which later turned into a tumor. A doctor treated him with medicine, and several liters of turtle offspring were expelled, each as large as a small coin, with heads, feet, and shells intact, though the internal organs were dead. The nose is not a place for reproduction, and enjoyment of the Dao is not a tool for bringing down things. From this perspective, the birth and death of all things, and their transformations, cannot be understood without a divine insight, even if one seeks within oneself, how can one know the origin of such transformations? Yet, rotten grass becomes fireflies due to decay, and wheat becomes butterflies due to moisture. Therefore, all transformations of things have their causes. The farmer stops the transformation of wheat by soaking it in ash; the sage manages the transformations of all things by guiding them with the Dao. Is this true, or is it not?

    140

    季桓子穿井，获如土缶，其中有羊焉，使问之仲尼，曰：“吾穿井其获狗，何耶？”仲尼曰：“以丘所闻，羊也。丘闻之：木石之怪，夔，‘魍魉。’水中之怪，龙，‘罔象。’土中之怪曰‘贲羊。’”夏鼎志曰：“‘罔象’如三岁儿，赤目，黑色，大耳，长臂，赤爪。索缚，则可得食。”王子曰：“木精为‘游光，’金精为‘清明’”也。

    Explanation

    140

    Duke Ji Huan was digging a well and found an object resembling a clay jar. Inside it, there was a sheep. He sent someone to ask Confucius, saying, "When I dug the well, I found a dog. Why is that?" Confucius replied, "According to what I have heard, it is a sheep. I have heard that among the strange creatures of wood and stone are the kui and wailing; among those of water are the dragon and wangxiang; and among those of the earth is the benyang." The Xia Ding Zhi states, "The wangxiang looks like a three-year-old child, with red eyes, black skin, large ears, long arms, and red claws. If you bind it, you can eat it." The Prince said, "The spirit of wood is called youguang, and the spirit of metal is called qingming."

    141

    晋惠帝元康中，吴郡娄县怀瑶家忽闻地中有犬声隐隐。视声发处，上有小窍，大如螾穴。瑶以杖刺之，入数尺，觉有物。乃掘视之，得犬子，雌雄各一，目犹未开，形大于常犬。哺之，而食。左右咸往观焉。长老或云：“此名‘犀犬，’得之者，令家富昌，宜当养之。”以目未开，还置窍中，覆以磨砻，宿昔发视，左右无孔，遂失所在。瑶家积年无他祸幅。至太兴中，吴郡太守张懋，闻斋内床下犬声。求而不得。既而地坼，有二犬子，取而养之，皆死。其后懋为吴兴兵沈充所杀。尸子曰：“地中有犬，名曰‘地狼；’有人，名曰‘无伤。’夏鼎志曰：“掘地而得狗，名曰‘贾；’掘地而得豚，名曰‘邪；’掘地而得人；名曰‘聚：’‘聚’无伤也。”此物之自然，无谓鬼神而怪之。然则‘贾’与‘地狼’名异，其实一物也。淮南毕万曰：“千岁羊肝，化为‘地宰；’蟾蜍得‘(上艹下瓜)，’卒时为‘鹑。’”此皆因气化以相感而成也。

    Explanation

    141

    During the Yuan Kang period of Emperor Huai of Jin, a man named Huai Yao from Lou County in Wu Prefecture suddenly heard faint barking coming from underground. Upon examining the source of the sound, he found a small hole, about the size of a worm's burrow. Using a stick, he probed the hole and, after inserting it several feet, felt something inside. He then dug further and discovered two puppies, one male and one female, whose eyes were not yet open and whose bodies were larger than those of ordinary dogs. He fed them, and they were soon taken to see by everyone around. An elder remarked, "These are called 'rhinoceros dogs,' and whoever finds them will bring prosperity and wealth to their household. They should be kept." Since the puppies' eyes were not yet open, he returned them to the hole, covered it with a stone mill, and left them there. After a night or two, when he checked again, the hole was gone, and the puppies had disappeared. For many years, Huai Yao's family experienced no other misfortune. Later, during the Tai Xing period, the governor of Wu Prefecture, Zhang Mao, heard barking coming from under his bed in his study. He searched but could not find the source. Suddenly, the ground split open, and two puppies emerged. He took them and kept them, but both died soon after. Eventually, Zhang Mao was killed by Wu Xing's military leader, Shen Chong. Shi Zi said, "A dog found underground is called 'earth wolf'; a person found underground is called 'unharmed.'" The Xia Ding Zhi states, "A dog found by digging is called 'Jia'; a pig found by digging is called 'Yi'; a person found by digging is called 'Ju'; 'Ju' means 'unharmed.'" These are natural occurrences and should not be attributed to ghosts or gods and seen as strange. Thus, 'Jia' and 'earth wolf' have different names but refer to the same thing. Huainan Bi Wan said, "A thousand-year-old sheep's liver transforms into an 'earth ruler'; a toad that gets 'upper grass lower melon' suddenly becomes a pheasant." All these phenomena are due to the transformation of qi and mutual influence.

    142

    吴诸葛恪为丹阳太守，尝出猎，两山之间，有物如小儿，伸手欲引人。恪令伸之，乃引去故地。去故地，即死。既而参佐问其故，以为神明。恪曰：“此事在白泽图内；曰：‘两山之间，其精如小儿，见人，则伸手欲引人，名曰“傒囊，”引去故地，则死。’无谓神明而异之。诸君偶未见耳。”
    　　王莽建国四年，池阳有小人景，长一尺余，或乘车，或步行，操持万物，大小各自相称，三日乃止。莽甚恶之。自后盗贼日甚，莽竟被杀。管子曰：“涸泽数百岁，谷之不徙，水之不绝者，生‘庆忌。’‘庆忌’者，其状若人，其长四寸，衣黄衣，冠黄冠，戴黄盖，乘小马，好疾驰，以其名呼之，可使千里外一日反报。”然池阳之景者，或“庆忌”也乎。又曰：“涸小水精，生‘蚳。’”‘蚳’者，一头而两身，其状若蛇，长八尺，以其名呼之，可使取鱼鳖。

    Explanation

    142

    Wu's Zhuge Ke served as the Governor of Danyang. Once, while out hunting, he encountered a creature between two mountains that resembled a child, stretching out a hand to pull someone. Zhuge Ke ordered it to stretch its hand, and it pulled away from its original place. Upon leaving its original place, it died. Later, his advisors asked about the reason for this, thinking it was a divine being. Zhuge Ke replied, "This matter is recorded in the Bai Ze Diagram; it says: 'Between two mountains, its essence is like a child, and when it sees people, it stretches out a hand to pull them, called "Xinang," and if it is pulled away from its original place, it dies.' Do not consider it divine and be surprised by it. You gentlemen have just not seen it before."

    During the fourth year of Wang Mang's reign in the Xin Dynasty, in Chi Yang, there appeared small figures about a foot and a half long, some riding in carriages, others walking, carrying all kinds of objects, large and small, in proportion to their size, and this continued for three days. Wang Mang greatly disliked it. Afterward, bandits became more rampant, and Wang Mang was eventually killed. The Guanzi states: "A dried-up river for several hundred years, the valley does not move, but the water does not stop, giving birth to 'Qing Ji.' 'Qing Ji' is a creature that looks like a person, four inches tall, wearing yellow clothes, a yellow crown, a yellow canopy, riding a small horse, and enjoys running fast. If you call its name, it can return a report from a thousand miles away in one day." Perhaps the figures in Chi Yang are 'Qing Ji'? It also states: "A dried-up small water spirit gives birth to 'Chi.'" 'Chi' is a creature with one head and two bodies, looking like a snake, eight feet long, and if you call its name, it can fetch fish and turtles.

    143

    晋，扶风杨道和，夏于田中，值雨，至桑树下，霹雳下击之，道和以锄格折其股，遂落地，不得去。唇如丹，目如镜，毛角长三寸，余状似六畜，头似狝猴。
    　　秦时，南方有“落头民，”其头能飞。其种人部有祭祀，号曰“虫落，”故因取名焉，吴时，将军朱桓，得一婢，每夜卧后，头辄飞去。或从狗窦，或从天窗中出入，以耳为翼，将晓，复还。数数如此，傍人怪之，夜中照视，唯有身无头，其体微冷，气息裁属。乃蒙之以被。至晓，头还，碍被不得安，两三度，堕地。噫咤甚愁，体气甚急，状若将死。乃去被，头复起，傅颈。有顷，和平。桓以为大怪，畏不敢畜，乃放遣之。既而详之，乃知天性也。时南征大将，亦往往得之。又尝有覆以铜盘者，头不得进：遂死。

    Explanation

    143

    During the Jin Dynasty, Yang Daohe from Fufeng was in the fields during the summer when he encountered rain. He took shelter under a mulberry tree, and a thunderbolt struck from above. Daohe used a hoe to block and break its leg, causing it to fall to the ground and be unable to leave. The creature had lips red like cinnabar, eyes bright like mirrors, hairs and horns three inches long, an overall appearance resembling livestock, and a head resembling a macaque.

    During the Qin Dynasty, there were mythical people in the south called "落头民," whose heads could fly. Their kind had a ritual called "虫落," which is why they were named as such. During the Wu Dynasty, General Zhu Huan obtained a servant. Every night after she lay down, her head would fly away. It would fly through dog holes or skylights, using its ears as wings, and return in the morning. Those around her found this strange. One night, they illuminated her to see that she had only a body with no head, and her body was slightly cold with just a breath of life remaining. They covered her with a blanket. In the morning, her head returned, obstructed by the blanket and unable to settle, falling to the ground several times. She was very distressed, her body was very tense, and she seemed on the verge of death. They then removed the blanket, and her head returned to her neck. After a while, she calmed down. Zhu Huan thought this was a great marvel and was afraid to keep her, so he released her. Later, he realized that this was her natural nature. At that time, generals on southern campaigns also often encountered such cases. There was once a case where a copper plate was used, and the head could not enter, leading to death.

    144

    江，汉之域，有“貙人，”其先，廪君之苗裔也，能化为虎。长沙所属蛮县东高居民，曾作槛捕虎，槛发，明日众人共往格之，见一亭长，赤帻，大冠，在槛中坐。因问“君何以入此中？”亨长大怒曰：“昨忽被县召，夜避雨，遂误入此中。急出我。”曰：“君见召，不当有文书耶？”即出怀中召文书。于是即出之。寻视，乃化为虎，上山走。或云：“貙，虎化为人，如着紫葛衣，其足无踵，虎，有五指者，皆是貙。”

    Explanation

    144

    The regions along the Yangtze and Han rivers are home to the "貙人," whose ancestors are descendants of Lord Lin, and who can transform into tigers. In a county under the jurisdiction of Changsha, the residents of Donggao set a trap to catch a tiger. The trap was triggered, and the next day, a group of people went to confront it. They saw a local official, wearing a red headgear and a large hat, sitting in the trap. They asked him, "How did you enter here?" The official, named Hengzhang, became very angry and said, "I was suddenly summoned by the county last night, and while avoiding the rain, I accidentally entered here. Let me out quickly!" They replied, "Shouldn't you have received a summons?" He then took out a document from his chest, which was the summons. Upon inspection, he transformed back into a tiger and ran up the mountain. It is said that the "貙" is a creature that can transform into a human, often wearing a purple cotton robe and having feet without heels, and tigers with five fingers are all "貙."

    145

    蜀中西南高山之上，有物，与猴相类，长七尺，能作人行，善走逐人，名曰“猳国，”一名“马化，”或曰“玃猿。”伺道行妇女有美者，辄盗取，将去，人不得知。若有行人经过其旁，皆以长绳相引，犹故不免。此物能别男女气臭，故取女，男不取也。若取得人女，则为家室。其无子者，终身不得还。十年之后，形皆类之。意亦迷惑，不复思归。若有子者，辄抱送还其家，产子，皆如人形。有不养者，其母辄死；故惧怕之，无敢不养。及长，与人不异。皆以杨为姓。故今蜀中西南多诸杨，率皆是“●国”“马化”之子孙也。

    Explanation

    145

    In the high mountains of the southwest of Shu, there is a creature similar to monkeys, seven feet tall, capable of walking like a human and good at chasing people. It is called "Jiaoguo," also known as "Mahuo," or "Jueyuan." It waits for beautiful women traveling on the road and steals them, taking them away without anyone knowing. If there are passersby nearby, they all use long ropes to pull each other, but they still cannot escape. This creature can distinguish between the scent of men and women, so it takes women but not men. If it takes a human woman, it makes her its wife. Those who do not have children cannot return for life. After ten years, their appearance becomes similar to the creature. They also become confused and no longer think of returning. If they have children, they are carried back to their families. The children they produce are all human-like. If they do not raise the children, the mother will die; therefore, they are afraid and dare not neglect the children. When they grow up, they are no different from humans. All are surnamed Yang. Therefore, there are many people surnamed Yang in the southwest of Shu today, most of whom are descendants of the "Jiaoguo" and "Mahuo."

    146

    临川间诸山有妖物，来常因大风雨，有声如啸，能射人，其所着者，有顷，便肿，大毒。有雌雄：雄急，而雌缓；急者不过半日间，缓者经宿。其旁人常有以救之，救之少迟，则死。俗名曰“刀劳鬼。”故外书云：“鬼神者，其祸福发扬之验于世者也。”老子曰：“昔之得一者：天得一以清，地得一以宁，神得一以灵，谷得一以盈，侯王得一以为天下贞。”然则天地鬼神，与我并生者也；气分则性异，域别则形殊，莫能相兼也。生者主阳，死者主阴，性之所托，各安其生，太阴之中，怪物存焉。

    Explanation

    146

    In the mountains around Linchuan, there is a supernatural entity that often appears during violent storms. It makes a howling sound and can shoot at people. Those struck by it will swell and become severely poisoned within a short time. The entity has both male and female forms: the male acts quickly, while the female acts slowly. The male form causes effects within half a day, while the female form takes a whole night. There are methods to save those affected, but if the rescue is delayed, the victim will die. This entity is commonly known as the "Dao Laogui." As an external source states, "Ghosts and spirits are the manifestations of fortune and misfortune in the world." Laozi says, "In the past, those who attained unity: heaven attained clarity, earth attained peace, spirits attained divinity, valleys attained fullness, and rulers attained the stability of the state." Thus, heaven, earth, ghosts, and spirits coexist with us; different essences lead to different natures, and different realms result in different forms, and none can be combined. Living beings are associated with yang, while the dead are associated with yin. Each entity finds its place and lives according to its nature. In the realm of yin, strange and monstrous entities exist.

    147

    越地深山中有鸟，大如鸠，青色，名曰“冶鸟，”穿大树，作巢，如五六升器，户口径数寸：周饰以土垭，赤白相分，状如射侯。伐木者见此树，即避之去；或夜冥不见鸟，鸟亦知人不见，便鸣唤曰：“咄咄上去！”明日便宜急上；“咄咄下去！”明日便宜急下；若不使去，但言笑而不已者，人可止伐也。若有秽恶及其所止者，则有虎通夕来守，人不去，便伤害人。此鸟，白日见其形，是鸟也；夜听其鸣，亦鸟也；时有观乐者，便作人形，长三尺，至涧中取石蟹；就人炙之，人不可犯也。越人谓此鸟是“越祝”之祖也。

    Explanation

    147

    In the deep mountains of Yue, there is a bird as large as a jay, with a greenish-blue color, named "冶鸟." It digs into large trees to build its nest, which is about the size of a container holding five or six sheng, with an entrance several inches in diameter. The nest is decorated with earth and clay, alternating between red and white, resembling a target. Woodcutters who see such a tree will immediately avoid and leave it. Sometimes, at night when the woodcutter cannot see the bird, the bird also knows that the person cannot see it and will call out, "Dude, go up!" The woodcutter should climb the tree quickly the next day. "Dude, go down!" The woodcutter should climb down quickly the next day. If the bird does not want the woodcutter to leave, it will laugh persistently until the woodcutter stops. If the nest is defiled, tigers will guard it all night long, and if the woodcutter does not leave, the tigers will harm them. This bird appears as a bird during the day and makes bird-like sounds at night. Sometimes, it transforms into a human-like form, about three feet tall, to fetch stone crabs from a stream. It roasts the crabs and warns humans not to interfere. The people of Yue consider this bird to be the ancestor of the "越祝" (Yue shamans).

    148

    南海之外，有“鲛人，”水居，如鱼，不废织绩。其眼，泣，则能出珠。
    　　庐江耽，枞阳二县境，上有大青小青黑居山野之中，时闻哭声多者至数十人，男女大小，如始丧者。邻人惊骇，至彼奔赴，常不见人。然于哭地，必有死丧。率声若多，则为大家；声若小，则为小家。
    　　庐江大山之间，有“山都，”似人，裸身，见人便走。有男，女，可长四五丈，能●相唤，常在幽昧之中，似魑魅鬼物。
    　　汉光武中平中，(编者按：中平当为中元，因光武无中平年号。或光武为灵帝之误。)有物处于江水，其名曰“蜮，”一曰“短狐。”能含沙射人。所中者，则身体筋急，头痛，发热。剧者至死。江人以术方抑之，则得沙石于肉中。诗所谓“为鬼，为蜮，”则不可测也。今俗谓之“溪毒。”先儒以为男女同川而浴，淫女，为主乱气所生也。

    Explanation

    148

    Beyond the South Sea, there are "鲛人" (mermaids), who live in water, resembling fish yet do not cease from weaving. When their eyes weep, they can produce pearls.

    In the regions of Lujiang and Zongyang, there are sometimes heard cries, often as many as dozens of people, men, women, young and old, as if they had just lost someone. Neighbors are startled and rush to the scene, but often do not see anyone. However, at the place where they cried, there is always a death. Generally, if the sound was loud, it was for a large family; if it was soft, it was for a small family.

    In the vast mountains of Lujiang, there are "山都" (mountain people), who resemble humans, are naked, and run away when they see people. They can grow up to four or five zhang tall, can call to each other, and often reside in dark and obscure places, resembling ghosts and spirits.

    During the reign of Emperor Guangwu in the Zhongping era (Editor's note: Zhongping should be Zhongyuan, as Emperor Guangwu did not have a Zhongping era. Or perhaps it is a mistake and refers to Emperor Ling.), there was a creature in the river, known as "yù" or "short fox." It can shoot people with sand. Those who are hit experience muscle stiffness, headache, fever, and severe cases can lead to death. People from the river use techniques to suppress it, and sand and stones are found in the flesh. As the poem says, "they are ghosts or yù," they are unpredictable. Nowadays it is called "river poison." Ancient scholars believed that it was caused by men and women bathing in the same river, with promiscuous women being the source of disorder.

    149

    汉，永昌郡不违县，有禁水；水有毒气，唯十一月，十三月差可渡涉，自正月至十月不可渡；渡辄病杀人，其气中有恶物，不见其形，其似有声。如有所投击内中木，则折；中人，则害。士俗号为“鬼弹。”故郡有罪人，徙之禁防，不过十日，皆死。
    　　余外妇姊夫蒋士，有佣客，得疾，下血；医以中蛊，乃密以蘘荷根布席下，不使知，乃狂言曰：“食我虫者，乃张小小也。”乃呼“小小亡”云，今世攻蛊，多用蘘荷根，往往验。蘘荷，或谓嘉草。
    　　鄱阳赵寿，有犬，蛊，时陈岑诣寿，忽有大黄犬六七群，出吠岑，后余相伯归与寿妇食，吐血，几死。乃屑桔梗以饮之而愈。蛊有怪物，若鬼，其妖形变化杂类殊种：或为狗豕，或为虫蛇。其人不自知其形状，行之于百姓，所中皆死。

    Explanation

    149

    During the Han dynasty, in the county of Buiwu of Yongchang Prefecture, there was a river known as the Forbidden Water. This river emitted toxic gases, making it only safe to cross in the 11th and 13th lunar months. From the 1st to the 10th months, it was dangerous to cross, as doing so would cause illness and death. The air around the river contained something evil, which could not be seen but seemed to make a sound. If anything were thrown into the middle of the water, the wood would break; if it hit a person, it would harm them. Locals called this phenomenon "Ghost Bullet." Therefore, criminals from the prefecture were exiled to the forbidden area, and within ten days, they all died.

    My sister-in-law's husband, Jiang Shi, had a hired guest who fell ill and bled. The doctor diagnosed it as a case of poisoning by a venomous creature. He secretly placed the roots of the náng hé (a type of herb) under the mat, without the patient knowing. The patient then spoke wildly, saying, "The one who ate my worm is Zhang Xiaoxiao." He also cried out, "Xiaoxiao has died." In modern times, treating poisonings often involves using náng hé roots, and it is often effective. Náng hé is also called "good grass."

    In Poyang, Zhao Shou had a dog that was also affected by poisoning. When Chen Cen visited Zhao Shou, suddenly six or seven groups of large yellow dogs appeared and barked at Chen Cen. Later, my uncle returned home with Zhao Shou's wife and they ate together, and she vomited blood and nearly died. He then ground up qi ji (a type of herb) and gave it to her to drink, and she recovered. Poisonous creatures are described as monsters like ghosts, with strange forms that change into various kinds of creatures. Sometimes they appear as dogs or pigs, sometimes as insects or snakes. The person affected does not know their own form. They act among the people, and those who are affected all die.

    150

    荥阳郡有一家，姓廖，累世为蛊，以此致富。后取新妇，不以此语之。遇家人咸出，唯此妇守舍，忽见屋中有大缸，妇试发之，见有大蛇，妇乃作汤灌杀之。及家人归，妇具白其事，举家惊惋。未几，其家疾疫，死亡略尽。
    搜神记卷十三
    　　泰山之东，有澧泉，其形如井，本体是石也。欲取饮者，皆洗心志，跪而挹之，则泉出如飞，多少足用，若或污漫，则泉止焉。盖神明之尝志者也。
    　　二华之山，本一山也，当河，河水过之，而曲行；河神巨灵，以手擘开其上，以足蹈离其下，中分为两。以利河流。今观手迹于华岳上，指掌之形具在；脚迹在首阳山下，至今犹存。故张衡作西京赋所称“巨灵赑屃，高掌远跖，以流河曲，”是也。

    Explanation

    150

    In Xingyang Prefecture, there was a family surnamed Liao, who had practiced the art of "蛊" for generations, thereby becoming wealthy. After they took a new wife, they did not tell her about their practice. One day, when the family members went out, leaving only the new wife at home, she suddenly saw a large jar in the house. Curious, she opened it and found a large snake inside. She then poured water over it and killed it. When the family returned, the new wife reported the incident in detail, and the entire family was shocked and grieved. Soon after, the family suffered from illness and pestilence, and nearly all of them died.

    Search for the Gods Volume Thirteen
    In the east of Mount Tai, there is a spring called Li Spring, which looks like a well and is actually made of stone. Those who wish to drink from it must cleanse their hearts and minds, kneel down, and scoop the water. The spring then flows out as if flying, providing enough water for their needs. If the water is polluted, the spring will stop flowing. This is said to be a test of one's sincerity by the divine.

    The two peaks of Mount Hua were originally one mountain, situated in the path of the Yellow River. The river flowed around it in a curved path. The river god, Great Spirit, used his hands to split the mountain apart and his feet to separate it further, dividing it into two. This action was done to facilitate the flow of the river. Today, one can still see the handprints on Mount Hua, with the shapes of fingers and palms clearly visible. The footprints are found at the base of Mount Shouyang and are still present. This is what Zhang Heng referred to in his Western Capital Fu when he wrote, "The Great Spirit, with his powerful hands and long feet, flowed through the bends of the Yellow River."

    151

    汉武徙南岳之祭于庐江，灊县，霍山之上，无水，庙有四镬，可受四十斛，至祭时，水辄自满，用之，足了，事毕，即空，尘土树叶，莫之污也。积五十岁，岁作四祭，后但作三祭，一镬自败。
    　　樊东之口，有樊山，若天旱，以火烧山，即至大雨。今往有验。
    　　空乘之地，今名为孔宝，在鲁南，山之穴外，有双石，如桓楹起立，高数丈。鲁人弦歌祭祀，穴中无水，每当祭时，洒扫以告，辄有清泉自石间出，足以周事。既已，泉亦止。其验至今存焉。
    　　湘穴中有黑土，岁大旱，人则共壅水以塞此穴；穴淹，则大雨立至。
    　　秦惠王二十七年，使张仪筑成都城，屡颓。忽有大龟浮于江，至东子城东南隅而毙。仪以问巫。巫曰：“依龟筑之。”便就，故名龟化城。

    Explanation

    151

    During the reign of Emperor Wu of Han, the sacrifices to the Southern Mountain (Nanyue) were relocated to the area of Lujiang, in Qian County and on Mount Huoshan. There was no water there, but the temple had four ritual vessels, each capable of holding forty dou. When the sacrifices were performed, the vessels would always fill with water on their own, and the water was sufficient for the rites. Once the sacrifices were completed, the vessels would become empty, and neither dust nor leaves could defile them. This phenomenon lasted for fifty years, during which four sacrifices were held each year. Later, only three sacrifices were held, and one of the vessels broke on its own.

    At the mouth of Fan East, there is Fan Mountain. If there was a drought, people would burn the mountain, and immediate heavy rain would follow. This practice is still in use today and has been verified.

    In a place now called Kongbao, located in the south of Lu, there is a cave outside a mountain. Outside the cave, there are two stones, standing like pillars, several zhang tall. The people of Lu would sing and play music during their sacrifices. There was no water in the cave, but whenever the sacrifices were performed, after cleaning and announcing, there would always be a clear spring emerging from between the stones, sufficient for the rites. Once the sacrifices were completed, the spring would stop flowing. This phenomenon still exists to this day.

    In the cave of Xiang, there is black soil. During a severe drought, people would block the cave with water, and once the cave was blocked, heavy rain would immediately arrive.

    In the 27th year of King Hui of Qin's reign, he ordered Zhang Yi to build the city of Chengdu. The city repeatedly collapsed until suddenly, a large turtle floated down the river and died at the southeast corner of the eastern city. Zhang Yi asked the diviners about this, and they said, "Build the city according to the turtle." The city was completed, and thus it was named the Turtle Transformation City.

    152

    由拳县，秦时长水县也。始皇时童谣曰：“城门有血，城当陷没为湖。”有妪闻之，朝朝往窥。门将欲縳之。妪言其故。后门将以犬血涂门，妪见血，便走去。忽有大水，欲没县。主簿令干入白令，令曰：“何忽作鱼？”干曰：“明府亦作鱼。”遂沦为湖。
    　　秦时，筑城于武周塞内，以备胡，城将成，而崩者数焉。有马驰走，周旋反复，父老异之，因依马迹以筑城，城乃不崩。遂名马邑。其故城今在朔州。
    　　汉武帝凿昆明池，极深，悉是灰墨，无复土。举朝不解。以问东方朔。朔曰：“臣愚不足以知之。”曰：“试问西域人。”帝以朔不知，难以移问。至后汉明帝时，西域道人入来洛阳，时有忆方朔言者，乃试以武帝时灰墨问之。道人云：“经云：‘天地大劫将尽，则劫烧。’此劫烧之余也。”乃知朔言有旨。

    Explanation

    152

    Yōuquán County, during the Qin dynasty, was formerly known as Chángshuǐ County. During the reign of the First Emperor, a children's rhyme circulated: "If there is blood at the city gate, the city will sink and become a lake." An old woman heard this and went to peek at the city gate every day. The city gate guard wanted to tie her up. The old woman explained the reason. Later, the guard smeared dog blood on the city gate. When the old woman saw the blood, she ran away. Suddenly, a great flood came, threatening to engulf the entire county. The county clerk sent a messenger to inform the magistrate. The magistrate asked, "Why did you suddenly become a fish?" The messenger replied, "The magistrate also became a fish." The county was thus submerged and became a lake.

    During the Qin dynasty, a city was built within the Wúzhōu pass to defend against the Hu (northern nomads). The city was repeatedly destroyed before it could be completed. A horse ran around and turned repeatedly, which the elders found strange. They then built the city following the horse's path, and the city did not collapse. It was then named Mǎyì. The ruins of the old city are now located in Shuozhou.

    During the reign of Emperor Wu of Han, he dug the Kunming Pool, which was very deep, filled with ash and soot, with no soil. The entire court could not understand why. They asked Dongfang Shuo, who replied, "I am too foolish to know." They suggested asking a person from the Western Regions.
