The emperor thought Dongfang Shuo did not know and found it hard to ask someone else. During the reign of Emperor Ming of the Eastern Han, a Buddhist monk from the Western Regions came to Luoyang. Someone remembered what Dongfang Shuo had said and tried asking about the ash and soot from Emperor Wu's time. The monk said, "The scriptures say, 'When the great calamity of the world is about to end, there will be a conflagration.' This is the aftermath of the conflagration." Thus, it was understood that Dongfang Shuo's words were meaningful.

    153

    临汜县有廖氏，世老寿。后移居，子孙辄残折。他人居其故宅，复累世寿。乃知是宅所为。不知何故。疑井水赤。乃掘井左右，得古人埋丹砂数十斛；丹汁入井，是以饮水而得寿。
    　　江东名“余腹”者：昔吴王阖闾江行，食脍，有余，因弃中流，悉化为鱼；今鱼中有名“吴王脍余”者，长数寸，大者如箸，犹有脍形。
    　　蟛(虫越)，蟹也。尝通梦于人，自称“长卿。”今临海人多以“长卿”呼之。
    　　南方有虫，名“●(虫禺)，”一名“●蠋，”又名“青蚨，”形似蝉而稍大，味辛美，可食。生子必依草叶，大如蚕子，取其子，母即飞来，不以远近，虽潜取其子，母必知处。以母血涂钱八十一文，以子血涂钱八十一文：每市物。或先用母钱，或先用子钱，皆复飞归。轮转无已。故淮南子术以之还钱，名曰“青蚨。”

    Explanation

    153

    In Lin Si County, there was a family named Liao, who were long-lived throughout generations. After they moved, their descendants suffered misfortune. Others who lived in their old house also lived long lives for generations. It was then known that the house was responsible for this. It is not known why. It was suspected that the well water was red. They then dug around the well and found dozens of hu of ancient people burying cinnabar. The cinnabar juice seeped into the well, so drinking from it granted longevity.

    In Jiangdong, it is called "Yu Fu." In the past, when King Helu of Wu was traveling on the river, he ate raw fish slices and had some leftovers, which he discarded into the middle of the river, and they all turned into fish. Now, there are fish in the river called "King Helu's leftover raw fish slices," which are a few inches long, the larger ones like chopsticks, still resembling raw fish slices.

    Peng (a type of crab). It once communicated dreams to people, calling itself "Changqing." Now, people near the sea often call it "Changqing."

    In the south, there is a bug named "Yuyu," also known as "Yuzhu," and another name is "Qingfu." It resembles a cicada but is slightly larger, with a spicy and delicious taste, and can be eaten. When it gives birth, it must rely on grass leaves, and the offspring are as large as silkworm eggs. If you take its offspring, the mother will fly over, regardless of distance. Even if you secretly take its offspring, the mother will definitely know where they are. Use the mother's blood to coat eighty-one coins, and use the offspring's blood to coat eighty-one coins. Every time you buy something, either use the mother's coins or the offspring's coins, and they will all return to fly back. They will keep rotating endlessly. Therefore, the technique in the Huainanzi uses this to return money, and it is called "Qingfu."

    154

    土蜂，名曰“蜾●，”今世谓“●●，”“细腰”之类。其为物雄而无雌，不交，不产；常取桑虫或阜螽子育之，则皆化成己子。亦或谓之“螟蛉。”诗曰：“螟蛉有子，果羸负之，”是也。
    　　木蠹，生虫，羽化为蝶。
    　　猬多刺，故不使超踰杨柳。
    　　昆仑之(山虚)，地首也，是惟帝之下都，故其外绝以弱水之深，又环以炎火之山。山上有鸟兽草木，皆生育滋长于炎火之中；故有“火澣布，”非此山草木之皮枲，则其鸟兽之毛也。汉世西域旧献此布，中闲久绝。至魏初时，人疑其无有。文帝以为火性酷裂，无含生之气，着之典论，明其不然之事，绝智者之听。及明帝立，诏三公曰：“先帝昔着典论，不朽之格言，其刊石于庙门之外及太学，与“石经”并以永示来世。”至是，西域使人献“火浣布”袈裟，于是刊灭此论，而天下笑之。

    Explanation

    154

    Earth Wasps, Known as "Gua Mo," are also called "Mo Mo" in modern times, and are classified as "slender-waisted" insects. They are all male and do not mate or reproduce; they often take silkworms or locust eggs to raise, which transform into their own offspring. They are also sometimes referred to as "mengling." The Book of Songs says, "The mengling has children, and they are carried by the wasp," which is true.

    Woodworms, which live in wood, transform into butterflies.

    Hedgehogs have many spines, which prevent them from jumping over willows.

    Mount Kunlun, known as the "empty mountain," is the head of the earth and the lower capital of the emperor. Beyond it lies the deep waters of the Weak Water, and it is surrounded by the fiery mountains. On the mountain, birds, animals, and plants all grow in the midst of fire; hence there is "fire-washed cloth," which is either made from the bark of the mountain's plants or the fur of its animals. During the Han dynasty, the Western Regions used to offer this cloth, but it had been absent for a long time. By the early Wei dynasty, people doubted its existence. Emperor Wen of Wei believed that fire is harsh and destructive, without life-generating properties, and wrote about this in his Classic Treatise to show that it was impossible, thus silencing the wise. When Emperor Ming ascended the throne, he ordered the Three Excellencies to inscribe the Classic Treatise on stone outside the temple and at the Imperial Academy, alongside the "Stone Classics," to be shown to future generations. Eventually, envoys from the Western Regions presented "fire-washed cloth" robes, leading to the destruction of the Classic Treatise, and people laughed at the emperor's earlier skepticism.

    155

    夫金之性一也，以五月丙午日中铸，“为阳燧，”以十一月壬子夜半铸，为“阴燧。”(言丙午日铸为“阳燧，”可取火；壬子夜铸为“阴燧，”可取水也。)
    　　汉灵帝时，陈留蔡邕，以数上书陈奏，忤上旨意，又内宠恶之，虑不免，乃亡命江海，远迹吴会。至吴，吴人有烧桐以爨者，邕闻火烈声，曰：“此良材也。”因请之，削以为琴，果有美音。而其尾焦，因名“焦尾琴。”
    　　蔡邕尝至柯亭，以竹为椽，邕仰盼之，曰：“良竹事。”取以为笛，发声辽亮。一云：“邕告吴人曰：‘吾昔尝经会稽高迁亭，见屋东间第十六竹椽可为笛，取用，果有异声。’”

    Explanation

    155

    The nature of metal is uniform. It was cast at noon on the day of Bingwu (丙午) in the fifth month to create a yang mirror, which could start a fire; and at midnight on the day of Renzi (壬子) in the eleventh month to create a yin mirror, which could collect water. (This means that casting on Bingwu day creates a yang mirror capable of starting a fire, and casting at midnight on Renzi day creates a yin mirror capable of collecting water.)

    During the reign of Emperor Ling of Han, Cai Yong from Chenliu repeatedly submitted memorials that offended the emperor's wishes and was further disliked by the emperor's favorites. Fearing he could not escape punishment, he fled to the rivers and seas, distancing himself to Wu and Kuaiji. When he arrived in Wu, there was a Wu person who was burning a paulownia log for cooking. Cai Yong heard the sound of the burning log and said, "This is fine material." He asked for it, had it carved into a zither, and indeed it produced beautiful music. But the tail was charred, so it was named the "Jiaowei Zither."

    Cai Yong once went to Keting, where he used bamboo for the rafters. He looked up and said, "This is fine bamboo." He took it to make a flute, which produced a clear and resonant sound. Another account says: "Cai Yong told the Wu people, 'I once passed by the Gaoqianting Pavilion in Kuaiji and saw that the sixteenth rafter in the eastern room could be used to make a flute. When I used it, it indeed produced a unique sound.'"

    156

    搜神记卷十四
    　　昔高阳氏，有同产而为夫妇，帝放之于崆峒之野。相抱而死。神鸟以不死草覆之，七年，男女同体而生。二头，四手足，是为蒙双氏。
    　　高辛氏，有老妇人，居于王宫，得耳疾，历时，医为挑治，出顶虫，大如茧。妇人去，后置以瓠篱，覆之以盘，俄尔顶虫乃化为犬。其文五色。因名盘瓠，遂畜之。时戎吴强盛，数侵边境，遣将征讨，不能擒胜。乃募天下有能得戎吴将军首者，赠金千斤，封邑万户，又赐以少女。后盘瓠衔得一头，将造王阙。王诊视之，即是戎吴。为之奈何？群臣皆曰：“盘瓠是畜，不可官秩，又不可妻。虽有功，无施也。”少女闻之，启王曰：“大王既以我许天下矣。盘瓠衔首而来，为国除害，此天命使然，岂狗之智力哉。王者重言，伯者重信，不可以女子微躯，而负明约于天下，国之祸也。”王惧而从之。令少女从盘瓠，盘瓠将女上南山，草木茂盛，无人行迹。

    Explanation

    156

    In ancient times, the GaoYang clan had siblings who became husband and wife. The emperor exiled them to the wilds of the KongTong mountains. They embraced each other and died. A divine bird covered them with the herb of immortality. After seven years, they were born as a hermaphrodite, with two heads, four hands, and four feet. This became the MengShuang clan.

    In the era of the GaoXin clan, there was a woman in the royal palace who suffered from an ear ailment for a long time. A physician treated her by picking out a parasite, which was as large as a silkworm cocoon. After the treatment, the parasite was placed in a gourd container and covered with a plate. Soon, the parasite transformed into a dog with fur of five colors. It was named PanHu and kept as a pet.

    At that time, the RongWu were powerful and strong, repeatedly invading the borders. The king sent generals to attack but could not capture or defeat them. So, a bounty was offered to anyone who could bring back the head of a RongWu general. The reward was a thousand catties of gold and a fief of ten thousand households, and also a young maiden as a reward.

    Later, PanHu carried back the head of one and brought it to the king's palace. The king examined it and found it to be indeed a RongWu general. He asked what should be done. All the ministers said, "PanHu is an animal, it cannot be given an official rank, nor can it be married. Even though it has done good, it cannot be rewarded."

    The young maiden heard this and approached the king, saying, "Your Majesty has already promised me to the world. PanHu brought back the head, eliminating the enemy for the country. This is the will of heaven, not the intelligence of a dog. A king values his words, a hegemon values his trust. One cannot break a clear promise to the world because of a woman's small body. It would be a disaster for the country."

    The king feared and agreed. He ordered the young maiden to follow PanHu, who took her to the Southern Mountain. The grass and trees were lush, with no signs of human activity.

    157

    于是女解去衣裳，为仆竖之结，着独力之衣，随盘瓠升山，入谷，止于石室之中。王悲思之，遣往视觅，天辄风雨，岭震，云晦，往者莫至。盖经三年，产六男，六女。盘瓠死，后自相配偶，因为夫妇。织绩木皮，染以草实。好五色衣服，裁制皆有尾形，后母归，以语王，王遣使迎诸男女，天不复两。衣服褊裢，言语侏(人离)，饮食蹲踞，好山恶都。王顺其意，赐以名山，广泽，号曰蛮夷。蛮夷者，外痴内黠，安土重旧，以其受异气于天命，故待以不常之律。田作，贾贩，无关繻，符传，租税之赋。有邑，君长皆赐印绶。冠用獭皮，取其游食于水。今即梁汉、巴蜀、武陵、长沙、庐江郡夷是也。用糁，杂鱼肉，叩槽而号，以祭盘瓠，其俗至今。故世称“赤髀，横裙，盘瓠子孙。”

    Explanation

    157

    Thereupon, the woman undressed and tied herself up like a servant, wearing a self-reliant garment. She followed the dog, Pangu, up the mountain, into the valley, and stopped in a cave. The king mourned for her and sent people to look for her, but the heavens were overcast with rain and wind, the mountains trembled, and the clouds darkened, preventing anyone from reaching her. After about three years, she gave birth to six sons and six daughters. When Pangu died, they paired off and became couples. They wove clothes from tree bark and dyed them with plant seeds. They liked colorful clothes, all cut and made with tail shapes. The mother returned and told the king, who sent envoys to bring back all the men and women, and the heavens no longer separated them. Their clothes were tight-fitting, their speech short and simple, they ate and sat in a squatting position, and they liked mountains and disliked cities. The king followed their wishes and gave them famous mountains, vast lakes, and called them the barbarians. These barbarians seemed simple on the outside but were clever inside, loved their land and valued tradition, because they received a different breath from heaven, they were treated with special laws. They farmed and traded without customs barriers, official documents, or taxes. They had settlements, and chiefs were given seals and ribbons. They wore hats made of otter fur because they lived by fishing in the water. These are the people of Lianghan, Bashu, Wuling, Changsha, and Lujiang. They used millet mixed with fish and meat, beat the trough and called out to worship Pangu, and this custom continues to this day. Therefore, the world calls them "Red legs, wide skirts, descendants of Pangu."

    158

    槁离国王侍婢有娠，王欲杀之。婢曰：“有气如鸡子，从天来下，故我有娠。”后生子，捐之猪圈中，猪以喙嘘之；徙至马枥中马复以气嘘之。故得不死。王疑以为天子也，乃令其母收畜之，名曰东明。常令牧马。东明善射，王恐其夺己国也，欲杀之。东明走，南至施掩水，以弓击水。鱼鳖浮为桥，东明得渡。鱼鳖解散，追兵不得渡。因都王夫余。
    　　古徐国宫人娠而生卵，以为不祥，弃之水滨。有犬，名鹄苍，衔卵以归。遂生儿，为徐嗣君。后鹄苍临死，生角而九尾，实黄龙也。葬之徐里中。见有狗垄在焉。
    　　斗伯比父早亡，随母归在舅姑之家，后长大，乃奸妘子之女，生子文。其妘子妻耻女不嫁而生子。乃弃于山中。妘子游猎，见虎乳一小儿，归与妻言，妻曰：“此是我女与伯比私通生此小儿。我耻之，送于山中。”妘子乃迎归养之，配其女与伯比。楚人因呼子文为“谷乌菟。”仕至楚相也。

    Explanation

    158

    The King of Gao Li had a palace servant who became pregnant. The king wanted to kill her. She said, "A ball of air like an egg came down from heaven, so I became pregnant." Later, she gave birth to a son, whom she abandoned in the pigsty. The pigs breathed on him with their snouts; later, when he was moved to the horse stable, the horses also breathed on him. Thus, he survived. The king suspected that he was a heavenly child and ordered his mother to raise him, naming him Dongming. He often ordered him to herd horses. Dongming was skilled in archery, and the king feared he might seize his kingdom, so he wanted to kill him. Dongming fled south to the Shiyin River, striking the water with his bow. Fish and turtles floated to form a bridge, allowing Dongming to cross. When the fish and turtles dispersed, the pursuing soldiers could not cross. He then established his capital in Fuyu.

    In ancient Guxu, a palace woman gave birth to an egg, which was considered an omen, and she abandoned it by the water. There was a dog named Huaguang, which carried the egg back. Later, it gave birth to a son who became the heir of Guxu. After Huaguang was on the verge of death, it grew horns and had nine tails, and was actually a yellow dragon. It was buried in the village of Guxu, and there is a dog mound there.

    Dou Bibo's father died early, and he followed his mother back to his father-in-law's house. When he grew up, he had an affair with the daughter of Yunzi and gave birth to a son named Ziwén. Yunzi's wife felt ashamed that the daughter did not marry and gave birth to a child, so she abandoned him in the mountains. Yunzi went hunting and saw a tiger nursing a little boy. He brought the boy back to raise him and married his daughter to Bibo. The people of Chu then called Ziwén "Guwutu," and he served as the chancellor of Chu.

    159

    齐惠公之妾萧同叔子见御，有身，以其贱，不敢言也，取薪而生顷公于野，又不敢举也。有狸乳而鹯覆之。人见而收，因名曰无野是为顷公。
    　　袁(金刃)者，羌豪也，秦时，拘执为奴隶，后得亡去，秦人追之急迫，藏于穴中，秦人焚之，有景相如虎来为蔽，故得不死。诸羌神之，推以为君。其后种落炽盛。
    　　后汉定襄太守窦奉妻生子武，幷生一蛇。奉送蛇于野中，及武长大，有海内俊名。母死，将葬未窆，宾客聚集，有大蛇从林草中出，径来棺下，委地俯仰，以头击棺，血涕并流，状若哀恸，有顷而去。时人知为窦氏之祥。
    　　晋怀帝永嘉中，有韩媪者，于野中见巨卵。持归育之，得婴儿。字曰撅儿。方四岁，刘渊筑平阳城，不就，募能城者。撅儿应募。因变为蛇，令媪遗灰志其后，谓媪曰：“凭灰筑城，城可立就。”竟如所言。渊怪之，遂投入山穴间，露尾数寸，使者斩之，忽有泉出穴中，汇为池，因名金龙池。

    Explanation

    159

    During the reign of Duke Qǐng of Qi, his concubine Xiao Tongshuzi was impregnated, but because she was lowly, she did not dare to speak of it. She gathered firewood and gave birth to Duke Qǐng in the wilderness, and she did not dare to raise him. A weasel nursed him, and a falcon covered him, and people saw and took him, thus they named him Wuyě, who became Duke Qǐng.

    Yuan (Jinren), a leader of the Qiang people, was captured and made a slave during the Qin period, but later escaped. The Qin people pursued him urgently, and he hid in a cave, which the Qin people burned. A tiger like a shadow came to shield him, thus he did not die. The Qiang people revered him and elevated him to a position of leadership. His descendants later became numerous and powerful.

    During the Later Han period, Dou Feng, the governor of Dingxiang, had a wife who gave birth to a son named Wu and also gave birth to a snake. Dou Feng sent the snake into the wild, and when Wu grew up, he gained a reputation as a talented person. When his mother died, before the burial, guests gathered, and a large snake came out from the forest and grass, came directly to the coffin, lay down and looked around, hit the coffin with its head, and blood and tears flowed, as if mourning, and after a while, it left. People at the time knew it was a sign of good fortune for the Dou family.

    During the Yongjia period of Emperor Huai of Jin, there was an elderly woman named Han who saw a large egg in the wild. She took it home and raised it, and got an infant, whom she named Ju'er. At the age of four, Liu Yuan, a Xiongnu leader, attempted to build the city of Píngyáng but did not succeed. He offered rewards to those who could build it. Ju'er responded to the call and transformed into a snake. He ordered the old woman to leave ashes as a marker and told her, "With the help of the ashes, the city can be built quickly." As he said, the city was built. Liu Yuan was surprised and threw the snake into a mountain cave, with part of its tail exposed. The messenger cut it, and suddenly a spring emerged from the cave and formed a pool, which was named the Golden Dragon Pool.

    160

    元帝永昌中，暨阳人任谷，因耕，息于树下，忽有一人着羽衣就淫之。既而不知所在。谷遂有妊。积月，将产，羽衣人复来，以刀穿其阴下，出一蛇子，便去。谷遂成宦者，诣阙自陈，留于宫中。
    　　旧说：太古之时，有大人远征，家无余人，唯有一女。牡马一匹，女亲养之。穷居幽处，思念其父，乃戏马曰：“尔能为我迎得父还，吾将嫁汝。”马既承此言，乃绝缰而去。径至父所。父见马，惊喜，因取而乘之。马望所自来，悲鸣不已。父曰：“此马无事如此，我家得无有故乎！”亟乘以归。为畜生有非常之情，故厚加刍养。马不肯食。每见女出入，辄喜怒奋击。如此非一。父怪之，密以问女，女具以告父：“必为是故。”父曰：“勿言。恐辱家门。且莫出入。”于是伏弩射杀之。暴皮于庭。

    Explanation

    160

    During the Yongchang period of Emperor Yuan, a man named Ren Gu from Jiyang was plowing when he rested under a tree. Suddenly, a person wearing a feathered robe approached him and had a supernatural encounter with him. Afterward, the person disappeared. Ren Gu then became pregnant. After several months, he was about to give birth, and the person in the feathered robe returned, using a knife to cut open his lower body and remove a snake-like child, then left. Ren Gu then became a eunuch, went to the palace to report, and was kept in the palace.

    According to an old story: In ancient times, there was a man who went on a long journey, leaving no one else in the house except for his daughter. He had a male horse, which the daughter raised herself. Living in a remote and secluded place, she missed her father and playfully said to the horse, "If you can bring my father back, I will marry you." The horse, hearing these words, broke its tether and left, going directly to the father's place. The father saw the horse, was surprised and delighted, and took it to ride. The horse looked back to where it came from and kept crying sadly. The father said, "This horse has no reason to behave this way; is there something wrong at home?" He quickly rode back home. Because the animal had unusual feelings, he fed it very well. However, the horse refused to eat. Every time it saw the girl coming and going, it would become angry and attack. This happened more than once. The father was puzzled and secretly asked the daughter, who told him everything. "It must be because of this," she said. The father replied, "Do not say anything. It might disgrace our family. Do not go out." He then set up a crossbow and shot the horse dead, flaying its skin and displaying it in the courtyard.

    161

    父行，女以邻女于皮所戏，以足蹙之曰：“汝是畜生，而欲取人为妇耶！招此屠剥，如何自苦！”言未及竟，马皮蹶然而起，卷女以行。邻女忙怕，不敢救之。走告其父。父还求索，已出失之。后经数日，得于大树枝间，女及马皮，尽化为蚕，而绩于树上。其(上尔下虫)纶理厚大，异于常蚕。邻妇取而养之。其收数倍。因名其树曰桑。桑者，丧也。由斯百姓竞种之，今世所养是也。言桑蚕者，是古蚕之余类也。案：天官：“辰，为马星。”蚕书曰：“月当大火，则浴其种。”是蚕与马同气也。周礼：“教人职掌，票原蚕者。”注云：“物莫能两大，禁原蚕者，为其伤马也。”汉礼皇后亲采桑祀蚕神，曰：“菀窳妇人，寓氏公主。”公主者，女之尊称也。菀窳妇人，先蚕者也。故今世或谓蚕为女儿者，是古之遗言也。

    Explanation

    161

    A Father Went Out, and His Daughter Played with a Neighbor's Daughter Using a Piece of Leather

    One day, the father went out, and his daughter played with a neighbor's daughter using a piece of leather. She stomped on it with her foot and said, "You are an animal, and you want to take someone as a wife! You will be slaughtered and skinned, how will you suffer yourself!" Before she finished speaking, the horse's skin suddenly stood up and rolled up the girl, carrying her away. The neighbor's daughter was frightened and helpless, unable to save her. She ran to tell the girl's father. The father returned to search for her, but she had already left and was lost. After several days, they found her on a tree branch. The girl and the horse's skin had both turned into silkworms, spinning silk on the tree. The silk fibers were thick and large, different from ordinary silkworms. A neighbor's wife took them and raised them. The yield was several times greater. Therefore, they named the tree mulberry. Mulberry means mourning. From this, people began to compete to plant mulberry trees, and this is what is cultivated today. The term "mulberry silkworm" refers to descendants of ancient silkworms. According to the Tian Guan (Astronomical Official), "the star of the horse is in the position of the Big Dipper." The Silkworm Book says, "When the month is in the position of the Big Dipper, then one should bathe the seeds." This indicates that silkworms and horses share a common essence. The Zhou Li (Rites of Zhou) states, "Those who raise silkworms are responsible for their cultivation." It is noted, "Nothing can be two great things at once; those who raise silkworms are forbidden because it harms horses." During the Han Dynasty, the empress personally picked mulberry leaves to worship the silk goddess, calling her "Wanyu Woman, Yushi Princess." Princess is a respectful title for women. Wanyu Woman is the first silkworm goddess. Therefore, in modern times, people sometimes refer to silkworms as "daughters," which is an ancient saying.

    162

    羿请无死之药于西王母，嫦娥窃之以奔月，将往，枚筮之于有黄。有黄占之曰：“吉。翩翩归妹，独将西行。逢天晦芒，毋恐毋惊。后且大昌。”嫦娥遂托身于月，是为“蟾蠩”。
    　　舌埵山帝之女死，化为怪草，其叶郁茂，其华黄色，其实如兔丝。故服怪草者，恒媚于人焉。
    　　荥阳县南百余里，有兰岩山，峭拔千丈，常有双鹤，素羽皦然，日夕偶影翔集。相传云：“昔有夫妇隐此山，数百年，化为双鹤，不绝往来。”忽一旦，一鹤为人所害，其一鹤岁常哀鸣。至今响动岩谷，莫知其年岁也。
    　　豫章新喻县男子，见田中有六七女，皆衣毛衣，不知是鸟。匍匐往得其一女所解毛衣，取藏之，即往就诸鸟。诸鸟各飞去，一鸟独不得去。男子取以为妇。生三女。其母后使女问父，知衣在积稻下，得之，衣而飞去，后复以迎三女，女亦得飞去。

    162

    Yi requested the elixir of immortality from the Queen Mother of the West, and Chang'e stole it and fled to the moon. Before she left, she consulted the diviner You Huang. You Huang divined and said: "It is auspicious. The graceful maiden will fly west alone. She will encounter a dim and hazy sky, but she should not be afraid or alarmed. She will later flourish greatly." Chang'e then resided on the moon, becoming known as the toad (Chánér).

    The daughter of the emperor of Shetu Mountain died and transformed into a strange grass. Its leaves were lush, its flowers yellow, and its fruit resembled silk from rabbits. Therefore, those who consumed this strange grass always became charming to others.

    South of Xingyang County, more than a hundred miles away, there is a mountain called Lan Rock Mountain. The mountain is steep and rises a thousand feet, often hosting a pair of white cranes with bright feathers. Day and night, they fly together and gather in pairs. It is said that in the past, a couple lived in this mountain for several hundred years, transforming into two cranes, never ceasing to come and go. One day, one of the cranes was harmed by a person, and the other crane mourns year after year. To this day, the sound echoes through the mountains and valleys, and no one knows how many years have passed.

    A man from Xinyu County, Yu Province, saw six or seven girls in the fields, all wearing feathered clothing, not knowing they were birds. He crawled forward and obtained one girl's feathered garment, taking it and hiding it. He then went to join the other birds, and they all flew away, leaving one bird behind. The man took the bird as his wife and they had three daughters. Later, the mother sent one of the daughters to ask the father, who revealed that the feathered garment was under a pile of rice. The daughter retrieved it and flew away. Later, she returned to bring back the three daughters, who also flew away.

    163

    汉灵帝时，江夏黄氏之母浴盘水中，久而不起，变为鼋矣。婢惊走告。比家人来，鼋转入深渊。其后时时出见。初，浴，簪一银钗，犹在其首。于是黄氏累世不敢食鼋肉。
    　　魏黄初中，清河宋士宗母，夏天于浴室里浴，遣家中大小悉出，独在室中。良久，家人不解其意，于壁穿中窥之。不见人体，见盆水中有一大鳖。遂开户，大小悉入，了不与人相承。尝先着银钗，犹在头上。相与守之。啼泣无可奈何。意欲求去，永不可留。视之积日，转懈。自捉出户外。其去甚驶，逐之不及，遂便入水。后数日，忽还，巡行宅舍如平生，了无所言而去。时人谓士宗应行丧治服；士宗以母形虽变，而生理尚存，竟不治丧。此与江夏黄母相似。

    Explanation

    163

    During the reign of Emperor Ling of Han, the mother of the Huang family from Jiangxia bathed in a basin of water and, after a long time, did not rise, transforming into a large freshwater turtle. The servant girl, frightened, ran to report the incident. By the time the family arrived, the turtle had turned into a deep pool. Afterward, it appeared frequently. Initially, while bathing, she wore a silver hairpin, which remained on its head. As a result, the Huang family refrained from eating turtle meat for generations.

    In the early years of the Huang period in the Wei dynasty, Song Shizong's mother from Qinghe bathed in the summer in a bathroom, sending all family members out, and remained alone in the room. After a long time, the family did not understand her intentions and peered through a hole in the wall. They saw no human body but a large turtle in the basin of water. They then opened the door, and all entered, completely not continuing as usual. She previously wore a silver hairpin, which was still on her head. They guarded her together, crying helplessly. She intended to leave but could never be kept. They watched for many days, becoming increasingly lax. She herself caught herself outside the door. Her departure was very swift, and they could not catch up, so she entered the water. After several days, she suddenly returned, walking around the house as usual, saying nothing before leaving. People thought Song Shizong should perform the funeral rites; however, he believed that although his mother's form had changed, her life force still existed, and thus he did not perform the funeral rites. This is similar to the case of the mother of the Huang family from Jiangxia.

    吴孙皓宝鼎元年六月，晦，丹阳宣骞母，年八十矣。亦因洗浴化为鼋，其状如黄氏。骞兄弟四人，闭户卫之，掘堂上作大坎，泻水其中。鼋入坎游戏。一二日间，恒延颈外望，伺户小开，便轮转自跃入于深渊。遂不复还。
    　　汉献帝建安中，东郡民家有怪；无故，瓮器自发訇訇作声，若有人击。盘案在前，忽然便失，鸡生子，辄失去。如是数岁，人甚恶之。乃多作美食，覆盖，着一室中，阴藏户间窥伺之。果复重来，发声如前。闻，便闭户，周旋室中，了无所见。乃闇以杖挝之。良久，于室隅间有所中，便闻呻吟之声，曰：“●！●！”宜死。开户视之，得一老翁，可百余岁，言语了不相当，貌状颇类于兽。遂行推问，乃于数里外得其家，云：“失来十余年。”得之哀喜。后岁余，复失之。闻陈留界复有怪如此。时人咸以为此翁。

    Explanation

    164

    In the first year of Emperor Sun Hao's reign during the Wu kingdom, in June, on the last day of the lunar month, the mother of Xuan Qian from Danyang, who was eighty years old, transformed into a turtle while bathing. The turtle looked like a yellow one. Xuan Qian and his three brothers closed the door and guarded the area, digging a large pit in the courtyard and pouring water into it. The turtle entered the pit and played. For a day or two, it constantly extended its neck to look outside, waiting for the door to open slightly, and then spun and leaped into the deep water. It never returned.

    During the Jian'an period of Emperor Xian of Han, a household in Dongjun experienced strange phenomena; without reason, jars and pots made loud noises, as if someone was striking them. Plates and tables in front suddenly disappeared, and chickens laid eggs, but the chicks immediately disappeared. This continued for several years, greatly displeasing the people. They prepared many delicious foods, covered them, and placed them in a room, hiding behind the door to watch. Indeed, the entity returned again, making sounds as before. Hearing this, they closed the door and moved around the room, seeing nothing. They struck it with a stick in the dark. After a long time, they hit something in the corner of the room, hearing groaning sounds, saying, "●! ●!" It should die. Opening the door to see, they found an old man, about a hundred years old, whose words did not make sense, and whose appearance somewhat resembled an animal. They proceeded to investigate and found his home several miles away, where he said, "I have been missing for over ten years." Finding him, they felt a mix of sadness and joy. After a year or so, he disappeared again. They heard that similar strange occurrences happened in Chenliu. People at the time believed it was this old man.

    搜神记卷十五
    　　秦始皇时，有王道平，长安人也，少时与同村人唐叔偕女，小名父喻，容色俱美，誓为夫妇。寻王道平被差征伐，落堕南国，九年不归，父母见女长成。即聘与刘祥为妻，女与道平，言誓甚重，不肯改事。父母逼迫，不免出嫁刘祥。经三年，忽忽不乐，常思道平，忿怨之深，悒悒而死。死经三年，平还家，乃诘邻人：“此女安在？”邻人云：“此女意在于君，被父母凌逼，嫁与刘祥，今已死矣。”平问：‘墓在何处？”邻人引往墓所，平悲号哽咽，三呼女名，绕墓悲苦，不能自止。

    Search for the Supernatural, Volume Fifteen

    During the reign of Qin Shi Huang, there was a man named Wang Dao Ping from Chang'an. In his youth, he fell in love with a girl from his village, the daughter of Tang Shuxie, whose pet name was Fu Yu. She was both beautiful in appearance and character, and they swore to be husband and wife. Soon after, Wang Dao Ping was ordered to go to war and was lost in the southern lands, not returning for nine years. When his parents saw their daughter had grown up, they immediately betrothed her to Liu Xiang. The girl, however, had taken a strong oath with Wang Dao Ping and refused to change her mind. Despite their parents' pressure, she could not avoid being married to Liu Xiang. Three years later, she was miserable and unhappy, constantly thinking of Wang Dao Ping. Her deep resentment and sorrow led her to die in a gloomy state. Three years after her death, Wang Dao Ping returned home and questioned his neighbors, "Where is this girl?" The neighbors replied, "This girl had feelings for you, but she was forced by her parents to marry Liu Xiang, and she has already passed away." Wang Dao Ping asked, "Where is her tomb?" The neighbors led him to the tomb. He cried out in grief, calling her name three times, circling the tomb in sorrow, unable to stop his tears.

    166

    平乃祝曰：“我与汝立誓天地，保其终身，岂料官有牵缠，致令乖隔，使汝父母与刘祥，既不契于初心，生死永诀。然汝有灵圣，使我见汝生平之面。若无神灵，从兹而别。”言讫，又复哀泣逡巡。其女魂自墓出，问平：“何处而来？良久契阔。与君誓为夫妇，以结终身，父母强逼，乃出聘刘祥，已经三年，日夕忆君，结恨致死，乖隔幽途。然念君宿念不忘，再求相慰，妾身未损，可以再生，还为夫妇。且速开冢，破棺，出我，即活。”平审言，乃启墓门，扪看。其女果活。乃结束随平还家。其夫刘祥闻之，惊怪，申诉于州县。检律断之，无条，乃录状奏王。王断归道平为妻。寿一百三十岁。实谓精诚贯于天地，而获感应如此。

    Explanation

    166

    Dao Ping then prayed, saying, "I and you swore an oath to heaven and earth, to keep our promise for life. Who would have thought that official matters would entangle us, leading to such separation, causing your parents and Liu Xiang to no longer be in harmony with our original intentions, and to part in life and death. Yet, if you have a spiritual presence, let me see your face as it was in life. If there is no divine intervention, then let us part forever." After he finished speaking, he wept and hesitated. The spirit of the woman emerged from the tomb and asked Dao Ping, "Where have you come from? We have been separated for so long. We swore to be husband and wife, to bind our lives together, but our parents forced me to marry Liu Xiang. It has been three years, and I thought of you day and night, until my hatred led to my death, and we were separated in the netherworld. Yet, I still remember our old feelings and wish to comfort each other again. My body is not damaged, and I can be reborn, to return as husband and wife. Quickly open the tomb, break the coffin, and release me, and I will live." Dao Ping carefully listened to her words and opened the tomb door, touching and examining. Indeed, the woman came back to life. She dressed herself up and followed him back home. Her husband, Liu Xiang, upon hearing of this, was surprised and shocked, and appealed to the local officials. The officials checked the law to decide, but found no relevant law, so they recorded the case and reported it to the king. The king decided to give the woman back to Dao Ping as his wife. She lived to be one hundred and thirty years old. Indeed, sincere and pure-hearted, permeating heaven and earth, she received such a response.

    167

    晋武帝世，河间郡有男女私悦，许相配适；寻而男从军，积年不归，女家更欲适之，女不愿行，父母逼之，不得已而去，寻病死。其男戍还，问女所在，其家具说之；乃至冢，欲哭之叙哀，而不胜其情，遂发冢，开棺，女即苏活，因负还家，将养数日，平复如初。后夫闻，乃往求之；其人不还，曰：“卿妇已死，天下岂闻死人可复活耶？此天赐我，非卿妇也。”于是相讼，郡县不能决，以谳廷尉，秘书郎王导奏以；“精诚之至，感于天地，故死而更生，此非常事，不得以常礼断之。请还开冢者。”朝廷从其议。

    Explanation

    167

    During the reign of Emperor Wu of Jin, in the county of Hejian, there was a man and a woman who had privately agreed to marry. Soon after, the man went to war and did not return for many years. The woman's family then wanted to marry her off to someone else, but she did not wish to go. Her parents forced her, and she went against her will. Soon after, she fell ill and died.

    When the man returned from his military service, he asked about the woman's whereabouts. Her family told him, and he went to her grave to mourn and express his grief. Overwhelmed by his emotions, he opened the coffin, and the woman immediately revived. He carried her home, nursed her for several days, and she recovered completely as before.

    The second husband, upon hearing about this, went to ask for her. The man refused to give her back, saying, "Your wife is already dead; how can anyone in the world hear of a dead person coming back to life? This is a gift from heaven to me; she is not your wife anymore." They then sued each other, and the local officials could not decide. The case was sent to the Grand Judge, and the Secretary of the Secretariat, Wang Dao, presented a report stating, "The utmost sincerity moved heaven and earth, therefore, she died and came back to life. This is not an ordinary matter; it cannot be judged by ordinary rules. Request that the man who opened the grave be allowed to keep her." The imperial court followed his suggestion.

    168

    汉献帝建安中，南阳贾偶，字文合，得病而亡。时有吏，将诣太山司命，阅簿，谓吏曰：“当召某郡文合，何以召此人？可速遣之。”时日暮，遂至郭外树下宿，见一年少女独行，文合问曰：“子类衣冠，何乃徒步？姓字为谁？”女曰：“某，三河人，父见为弋阳令，昨被召来，今却得还，遇日暮，惧获瓜田李下之讥，望君之容，必是贤者，是以停留，依凭左右。”文合曰：“悦子之心，愿交欢于今夕。”女曰：“闻之诸姑：女子以贞专为德，洁白为称。”文合反复与言，终无动志。天明，各去。文合卒巳再宿，停丧将殓，视其面，有色，扪心下，稍温，少顷，却苏。后文合欲验其实，遂至弋阳，修刺谒令，因问曰：“君女宁卒而却苏耶？”具说女子姿质，服色，言语，相反覆本末。令入问女，所言皆同。乃大惊叹。竟以此女配文合焉。

    Explanation

    168

    During the Jian'an period of Emperor Xian of Han, there was a man from Nanyang named Jia Ou, courtesy name Wenhe, who died of an illness. At that time, there was an official who escorted him to the realm of Mount Tai, where the deity in charge of life and death reviewed the records. The deity said to the official, "This person is supposed to be summoned from a certain prefecture named Wenhe. Why is this person being summoned? Can you quickly send him away?" It was dusk, so they stopped under a tree outside the city to rest. There, Jia Ou saw a young woman walking alone and asked her, "You seem to be a gentleman or scholar. Why are you walking on foot? What is your name?" The woman replied, "I am from the Sanhe region, and my father is currently the magistrate of Yiyang. I was summoned yesterday but returned today. It is now dusk, and I fear being accused of impropriety. I see that you are a gentleman, so I hope you are wise. That is why I stopped, relying on your protection." Jia Ou said, "I am pleased with your heart, and I wish to enjoy each other's company tonight." The woman responded, "I have heard from my aunts that a woman's virtue lies in her chastity and purity." Jia Ou engaged in repeated conversation with her, but she remained steadfast in her resolve. At dawn, they parted ways. Jia Ou had already stayed for two nights, and the funeral preparations were underway. When they looked at his face, it showed color, and when he touched his chest, it was slightly warm. A short while later, he revived. Later, Jia Ou wanted to verify the truth, so he went to Yiyang, prepared a letter, and visited the magistrate. He asked, "Did your daughter die and then revive?" He described the girl's appearance, clothing, words, and the entire story in detail. The magistrate asked the girl, and her answers matched. The magistrate was greatly surprised. In the end, he arranged for this girl to marry Jia Ou.

    169

    汉建安四年二月，武陵充县妇人李娥，年六十岁，病卒，埋于城外，已十四日。娥比舍有蔡仲，闻娥富，谓殡当有金宝，乃盗发冢求金，以斧剖棺。斧数下，娥于棺中言曰：“蔡仲！汝护我头。”仲惊，遽便出走，会为县吏所见，遂收治。依法，当弃市。娥儿闻母活，来迎出，将娥回去。武陵太守闻娥死复生，召见，问事状。娥对曰：“闻谬为司命所召，到时，得遣出，过西门外，适见外兄刘伯文，惊相劳问，涕泣悲哀。

    Explanation

    169

    During the second month of the fourth year of the Jian'an era (199 AD), a woman named Li E from Chong County in Wuling, who was sixty years old, fell ill and died. She was buried outside the city walls, and fourteen days had passed. Li E's neighbor, Cai Zhong, heard that she was wealthy and believed that her burial must contain valuable treasures. He decided to rob her grave, using an axe to open the coffin. As he struck the coffin several times, Li E spoke from within, saying, "Cai Zhong! Protect my head!" Cai Zhong was startled and fled immediately. He was soon spotted by local officials, who arrested him and brought him to trial. According to the law, he was sentenced to be executed in public.

    Li E's son, upon hearing that his mother had come back to life, came to retrieve her and took her home. The governor of Wuling, upon learning of Li E's miraculous resurrection, summoned her to ask about the details of what had happened. Li E replied, "I heard that I was mistakenly summoned by the God of Life and Death. When I arrived, I was allowed to leave. As I passed by the west gate, I unexpectedly met my distant relative Liu Bo Wen. We were both surprised and greeted each other, and we cried and grieved deeply."

    170

    娥语曰：‘伯文！我一日误为所召，今得遣归，既不知道，不能独行，为我得一伴否？又我见召在此，已十余日，形体又为家人所葬埋，归，当那得自出？’伯文曰：‘当为问之。’即遣门卒与尸曹相问：‘司命一日误召武陵女子李娥，今得遣还，娥在此积日，尸丧，又当殡殓，当作何等得出；又女弱，独行，岂当有伴耶？是吾外妹，幸为便安之。”答曰：‘今武陵西界，有男子李黑，亦得遣还，便可为伴。兼敕黑过娥比舍蔡仲，发出娥也。’于是娥遂得出。

    Explanation

    170

    E said, "Bo Wen! One day I was mistakenly summoned, and now I have been sent back. I do not know the way and cannot travel alone. Can you find me a companion? Also, I have been summoned here for over ten days, and my body has been buried by my family. When I return, how will I be able to come out on my own?" Bo Wen said, "I will ask about it." He immediately sent a door guard to consult with the official in charge of the dead: "The deity in charge of life and death mistakenly summoned a woman from Wuling named Li E, and now she has been sent back. Li E has been here for many days, and her body has been buried. How can she come out? Also, she is a weak woman and cannot travel alone. Should she have a companion? She is my cousin, so please arrange it so that she is comfortable." The official replied, "There is a man named Li Hei in the western part of Wuling who has also been sent back. He can be her companion. Also, order Hei to pass by Pian's house and get Li E out of the grave." Thus, Li E was able to come out.

    171

    与伯文别，伯文曰：‘书一封，以与儿佗。’娥遂与黑俱归。事状如此。”太守闻之，慨然叹曰：“天下事真不可知也。”乃表，以为：“蔡仲虽发冢为鬼神所使；虽欲无发，势不得已，宜加宽宥。”诏书报可。太守欲验语虚实，即遣马吏于西界，推问李黑，得之，与黑语协。乃致伯文书与佗，佗识其纸，乃是父亡时送箱中文书也。表文字犹在也，而书不可晓。乃请费长房读之，曰：“告佗：我当从府君出案行部，当以八月八日日中时，武陵城南沟水畔顿。汝是时必往。

    Explanation

    171

    Upon parting with Bo Wen, Bo Wen said, "I have a letter for you to give to Er Tuo." E then returned home with Hei. The situation unfolded as such. The prefect, upon hearing of it, sighed and remarked, "The affairs of the world truly cannot be predicted." He then proposed that, "Although Cai Zhong had to open the tomb due to the influence of spirits; even if he did not wish to, the circumstances left him no choice, and thus he should be pardoned and shown leniency." The imperial edict approved this suggestion. The prefect wished to verify the truth of the words and immediately dispatched a horse officer to the western boundary to interrogate Li Hei. Upon finding him, Li Hei's statements were consistent. The prefect then gave Bo Wen's letter to Er Tuo, who recognized the paper as the one sent by his father at the time of his death. The text of the memorial was still there, but the letter itself was not understandable. He then asked Fei Changfang to read it, who said, "It says to Er Tuo: 'I will accompany the prefect on an inspection tour, at noon on the 8th day of the 8th month, at the water's edge of the southern ditch of Wuling City. You must come at that time.'"

    172

    ”到期，悉将大小于城南待之。须臾果至，但闻人马隐隐之声，诣沟水，便闻有呼声曰：“佗来！汝得我所寄李娥书不耶？”曰：“即得之，故来至此。”伯文以次呼家中大小，久之，悲伤断绝，曰：“死生异路，不能数得汝消息，吾亡后，儿孙乃尔许大！”良久，谓佗曰：“来春大病，与此一丸药，以涂门户，则辟来年妖疠矣。”言讫，忽去，竟不得见其形。至来春，武陵果大病，白日皆见鬼，唯伯文之家，鬼不敢向。费长房视药丸，曰：“此‘方相’脑也。”

    Explanation

    172

    When the time came, all people of all ages were gathered in the south of the city. Soon, they heard the faint sounds of people and horses approaching. They reached the ditch and heard a voice calling out, "He has come! Have you received the letter I sent to Li E?" One responded, "I have received it, so I came here." Baiwen then called out to each family member in turn, and after a long while, he was overcome with grief, saying, "Death and life are different paths; I cannot often hear about you. After I die, your children and grandchildren will be this big!" After a long pause, he told the visitor, "By the following spring, there will be a great illness. Give this pill to you, and apply it to the door and window, and it will ward off evil and illness next year." After finishing speaking, the visitor suddenly left, and they never saw his form. By the following spring, Wuling indeed fell seriously ill and saw ghosts during the day, but only at Baiwen's house did ghosts not dare to approach. Fei Changfang examined the pill and said, "This is the brain of the Fangxiang."

    173

    汉，陈留考城，史姁，字威明，年少时，尝病，临死，谓母曰：“我死，当复生。埋我，以竹杖柱于瘗上，若杖折，掘出我。”及死，埋之柱，如其言。七日，往视，杖果折。即掘出之，已活。走至井上，浴，平复如故。后与邻船至下邳卖锄，不时售，云：“欲归。”人不信之，曰：“何有千里暂得归耶？”答曰：“一宿便还。”即书，取报以为验。实一宿便还，果得报。考城令江夏●贾和姊病，在邻里，欲急知消息，请往省之。路遥三千，再宿还报。
    　　会稽贺瑀、字彦琚，曾得疾，不知人，惟心下温，死三日，复苏。云：“吏人将上天，见官府，入曲房，房中有层架，其上层有印，中层有剑，使瑀惟意所取；而短不及上层，取剑以出门，吏问：‘何得？’云：‘得剑，’曰：‘恨不得印，可策百神，剑惟得使社公耳。’”疾愈，果有鬼来，称社公。

    Explanation

    173

    During the Han Dynasty, in Kaocun of Chenliu, there was a woman named Shi Xu, whose courtesy name was Weiming. When she was young, she once fell ill. On the verge of death, she told her mother, "If I die, I will come back to life. Bury me, and place a bamboo staff vertically on the grave. If the staff breaks, dig me up." After her death, she was buried as instructed. Seven days later, when they went to check, the staff had indeed broken. They dug her up, and she had revived. She walked to a well, bathed, and returned to her normal state. Later, she traveled with neighbors by boat to sell shovels in Xiangpi. The shovels did not sell immediately, and she said, "I want to return home." People did not believe her, saying, "How could one return home over a thousand miles in a short time?" She replied, "I will return in one night." She wrote a letter, and it was delivered as proof. Indeed, she returned in one night, and the letter was received. The magistrate of Kaocun, Jia He from Jiangxia, had a sister who was ill in the neighborhood. He wanted to quickly know her condition and asked Shi Xu to check on her. The journey was three thousand miles, but she returned in two nights to report.

    In Kuaiji, there was a man named He Yu, whose courtesy name was Yanju. He once fell ill and lost consciousness, but his chest remained warm. He died for three days and then revived. He said, "Officials took me to heaven, where I saw government offices and entered a small room. There was a multi-tiered shelf in the room, with a seal on the upper layer and a sword on the middle layer. They told me to take whatever I desired. However, I was too short to reach the upper layer, so I took the sword and left. The officials asked, 'What did you take?' I said, 'I took the sword,' and they replied, 'We could not give you the seal, which can command all spirits, but the sword can only command the village god.'" After his illness healed, a ghost came and claimed to be the village god.

    174

    戴洋，字国流，吴兴长城人，年十二，病死。五日而苏。说：“死时，天使其酒藏吏授符箓，给吏从幡麾，将上蓬莱、昆仑、积石、太室、庐、衡等山，既而遣归、”妙解占候。知吴将亡，托病不仕，还乡里，行至濑乡，经老子祠，皆是洋昔死时所见使处，但不复见昔物耳。因问守藏应凤曰：“去二十余年，尝有人乘马东行，经老君祠而不下马，未达桥，坠马死者否？”凤言有之。所问之事，多与洋同。
    　　吴，临海松阳人，柳荣，从吴相张悌至扬州，荣病，死船中，二日，军士已上岸。无有埋之者，忽然大叫，言：“人缚军师！人缚军师！”声甚激扬。遂活。人问之。荣曰：“上天北斗门下卒，见人缚张悌，意中大愕，不觉大叫言。何以缚军师？”门下人怒荣，叱逐使去。荣便怖惧，口余声发扬耳。其日，悌即死战。荣至晋元帝时犹存。

    174

    Dai Yang, courtesy name Guoliu, was from Changcheng, Wu County. At the age of twelve, he died from illness but revived five days later. He said, "When I died, Heaven sent its wine store official to give me a talisman, accompanied by officials with flags and banners, and I was about to ascend to Mount Penglai, Kunlun, Jishu, Taishan, Lu, and Heng. Afterward, I was sent back." He had a remarkable ability to interpret omens. Knowing that Wu would fall, he pretended to be ill and did not take office. He returned to his hometown and traveled to Lai Village, passing by the Laozi Temple. These places were the same as those he had seen in his previous life, but he no longer saw the things he had seen before. He then asked the keeper of records, Ying Feng, saying, "About twenty years ago, was there once a person riding a horse eastward who did not dismount when passing by the Laozi Temple? Did he not reach the bridge and fall off the horse, dying?" Ying Feng confirmed that there was such a person. The things he asked about were mostly the same as what Dai Yang had experienced.

    Wu, from Songyang, Linhai, and Liu Rong, accompanied Wu's chancellor Zhang Ti to Yangzhou. Liu Rong fell ill and died on the ship. Two days later, the soldiers had already gone ashore, and no one buried him. Suddenly, he let out a loud cry, shouting, "Someone is binding the military advisor! Someone is binding the military advisor!" The sound was very forceful. He then revived. People asked him about it. Liu Rong said, "I was a low-ranking official under the North Star, and I saw someone binding Zhang Ti. I was greatly shocked and unconsciously shouted. Why is the military advisor being bound?" The officials under the North Star were angry with Liu Rong, scolded him, and drove him away. Liu Rong was terrified, and the sound of his voice still echoed. On that day, Zhang Ti died in battle. Liu Rong still lived during the reign of Emperor Yuan of Jin.

    175

    吴国富阳人马势妇，姓蒋，村人应病死者，蒋辄恍惚熟眠经日，见病人死，然后省觉。觉，则具说。家中人不信之。语人云：“某中病我欲杀之，怒强，魂难杀，未即死。我入其家内，架上有白米(食卞)，几种鲑，我暂过灶下，戏，婢无故犯我，我打其脊，使婢当时闷绝，久之乃苏。”其兄病，在乌衣人令杀之，向其请乞，终不下手。醒，乃语兄云，“当活。”
    　　晋咸宁二年十二月，琅琊颜畿，字世都，得病，就医，张瑳自治，死于张家。棺敛已久。家人迎丧，旐每绕树木而不可解。人咸为之感伤。引丧者忽颠仆，称畿言曰：“我寿命未应死，但服药太多，伤我五脏耳。今当复活，慎无葬也。”其父拊而祝之，曰：“若尔有命，当复更生，岂非骨肉所愿；今但欲还家，不尔葬也。”旐乃解。及还家，其妇梦之曰：“吾当复生，可急开棺。”妇便说之。其夕，母及家人又梦之。

    Explanation

    175

    The wife of Ma Shi, a wealthy woman from Fuyang in the Wu Kingdom, surnamed Jiang, would often fall into a deep trance or sleep for days, during which she would see the death of someone and then awaken. Upon waking, she would fully recount what she had seen. Her family did not believe her, and she told others, saying, "Someone was ill, and I wanted to kill him. Because he was angry and strong, his soul was hard to kill, so he did not die immediately. I entered his house, where there were several types of fish on the shelf. I briefly passed by the stove, playing, when the maid wrongfully offended me. I struck her back, causing her to faint immediately. She remained unconscious for a long time before regaining consciousness." Her brother was also ill, and someone from Wuyi ordered her to kill him. She pleaded with them, but she ultimately did not carry out the order. When she woke up, she told her brother, "You will live."

    In December of the second year of the Xianning era during the Jin Dynasty, Yan Ji, a man from Langya, fell ill and sought treatment from Zhang Cuo. He died in Zhang's home. The body had already been prepared and placed in a coffin for some time. When the family came to mourn him, the funeral banner would get entangled in trees and could not be untangled. People were deeply moved by this. The mourners suddenly fell down, and the spirit of Yan Ji spoke through them, saying, "My life has not yet come to an end. I only died because I took too many medicines, which harmed my internal organs. I will be reborn now, so do not bury me." Yan Ji's father patted him and prayed, saying, "If you have a destiny, you will be reborn. Isn't this what family members wish? Now we just want to bring you home, not bury you." The banner then untangled. When they returned home, Yan Ji's wife dreamed of him and said, "I will be reborn, so open the coffin quickly." She told her family about the dream. That night, both Yan Ji's mother and the rest of the family also dreamed of him.

    176

    即欲开棺，而父不听；其弟含，时尚少，乃慨然曰：“非常之事，自古有之；今灵异至此，开棺之痛，孰与不开相负？”父母从之。乃共发棺，果有生验，以手刮棺，指爪尽伤，然气息甚微，存亡不分矣，于是急以绵饮沥口，能咽，遂与出之。将护累月，饮食稍多，能开目视瞻，屈伸手足，不与人相当，不能言语，饮食所须，托之以梦。如此者十余年。家人疲于供护，不复得操事；含乃弃绝人事，躬亲侍养，以知名州党。后更衰劣，卒复还死焉。

    Explanation

    176

    Upon hearing that they wanted to open the coffin, the father refused to allow it. His younger brother, Han, who was still young, then spoke resolutely, saying, "Extraordinary events have occurred throughout history; today, we have such a miraculous occurrence. Is the pain of opening the coffin worse than not opening it and bearing the guilt?" The parents agreed with him. They then jointly opened the coffin, and indeed, there was a sign of life. He scratched the coffin with his hand, injuring his fingers and nails, but his breathing was very faint, and it was unclear whether he was alive or dead. They quickly poured a small amount of liquid into his mouth with a cotton thread, and he was able to swallow. Thus, they brought him out. They took care of him for several months, and he ate and drank a little more. He was able to open his eyes and look around, bending and straightening his limbs, but he did not interact with people and could not speak. His needs for food and drink were communicated through dreams. Like this, it lasted for over ten years. The family was exhausted from caring for him and could no longer manage household affairs. Han then abandoned worldly affairs and personally took care of him, becoming well-known in the local area. Later, he became weaker and weaker, and finally, he died again.

    177

    羊祜，年五岁时，令乳母取所弄金镮，乳母曰：“汝先无此物。”祜即诣邻人李氏东垣桑树中，探得之。主人惊曰：“此吾亡儿所失物也，云何持去？”乳母具言之。李氏悲惋。时人异之。
    　　汉末，关中大乱，有发前汉宫人冢者，宫人犹活，既出，平复如旧。魏郭后爱念之，录置宫内，常在左右，问汉时宫中事，说之了了，皆有次绪。郭后崩，哭泣过哀，遂死。
    　　魏时太原发冢，破棺，棺中有一生妇人，将出，与语，生人也。送之京师，问其本事，不知也。视其冢上树木，可三十岁，不知此妇人三十岁，常生于地中耶？将一朝欻生，偶与发冢者会也？
    　　晋世，杜锡，字世嘏，家葬而婢误不得出。后十余年，开冢祔葬，而婢尚生。云：“其始如瞑目。有顷，渐觉。”问之，自谓。“当一再宿耳。”初婢埋时，年十五六，及开冢后，姿质如故。更生十五六年，嫁之，有子。

    Explanation

    177

    Translation:

    Yang Hu, at the age of five, ordered his wet nurse to fetch the gold ring he had been playing with. The wet nurse said, "You did not have this object before." Yang Hu then went to the eastern wall of the mulberry tree in the courtyard of his neighbor Li and found it there. The owner was astonished and said, "This was an object lost by my deceased son; how did you take it away?" The wet nurse explained the matter in detail. Li's family was deeply moved. At the time, people were amazed by this.

    At the end of the Han dynasty, when the region of Guanzhong was in great turmoil, someone opened a tomb of a Han imperial concubine and found her still alive. After she was brought out, she returned to normal as if nothing had happened. The Wei empress Guo cherished her and recorded her in the palace, always keeping her close by. She would ask about matters in the Han palace, and she spoke about them clearly, with everything in order. When the empress Guo passed away, the concubine cried so bitterly that she died from grief.

    During the Wei dynasty, in Taiyuan, a tomb was opened, and the coffin was broken open. Inside was a living woman. When she was brought out, she was spoken to and confirmed to be alive. She was sent to the capital, where they asked her about her past, but she did not know. When they looked at the trees on the tomb, they were about thirty years old, so it was unclear whether this woman had been alive for thirty years underground or if she had suddenly come to life and coincidentally met the tomb robbers.

    In the Jin dynasty, Du Xi, whose courtesy name was Shigao, had a servant buried with him by mistake. After more than ten years, when the tomb was opened for a secondary burial, the servant was still alive. She said, "At first, I was as if asleep. After a while, I gradually regained consciousness." When asked, she said, "I thought I would stay there for a night or two." When the servant was first buried, she was around fifteen or sixteen years old, and after the tomb was opened, her appearance remained unchanged. She lived for another fifteen or sixteen years, was married, and had children.

    178

    汉桓帝冯贵人，病亡；灵帝时有盗贼发冢，七十余年，颜色如故，但肉小冷；群贼共奸通之，至斗争相杀，然后事觉。后窦太后家被诛，欲以冯贵人配食下邳陈公达；议以贵人虽是先帝所幸，尸体秽污，不宜配至尊，乃以窦太后配食。
    　　吴孙休时，戍将于广陵掘诸冢，取版，以治城，所坏甚多。复发一大冢，内有重阁，户扇皆枢转可开闭，四周为徼道，通车，其高可以乘马，又铸铜人数十，长五尺，皆大冠，朱衣，执剑，侍列。灵坐皆刻铜人。背后石壁，言：殿中将军，或言：侍郎，常侍。似公侯之冢。破其棺，棺中有人，发已班白，衣冠鲜明，面体如生人。棺中云母，厚尺许，以白玉璧三十枚借尸。兵人辇共举出死人，以倚冢壁；有一玉，长尺许，形似冬瓜，从死人怀中透出，堕地；两耳及孔鼻中。皆有黄金，如枣许大。

    Explanation

    178

    Emperor Huan's noblewoman, Empress Feng, died of illness. During Emperor Ling's reign, bandits desecrated her tomb, which had been undisturbed for over seventy years. Her body remained well-preserved, with only a slight chill in the flesh. The bandits engaged in immoral acts with her, leading to internal conflict and mutual killings before their crimes were discovered. Later, when the family of Empress Dowager Dou was executed, there was a plan to have Empress Feng's remains accompany those of Chen Gongda of Xiapi in the afterlife. However, it was argued that although Empress Feng had been favored by the previous emperor, her body had been defiled by the bandits and was thus inappropriate to accompany the highest-ranking individuals in the afterlife. Instead, Empress Dowager Dou's remains were chosen for this honor.

    During the reign of Sun Quan's son, Sun Shao, military officers in Guangling dug up various tombs, taking materials to build the city, causing significant damage. They later discovered a large tomb with a multi-story structure inside, featuring doors and windows that could rotate and open/close. The tomb had surrounding pathways suitable for vehicles and was high enough to ride horses. Inside, dozens of bronze figures, each about five feet tall, wore large hats, red clothing, held swords, and stood in rows. The spirit seats were carved with bronze figures, and the back of the stone walls bore inscriptions reading "General of the Palace," "Attendant," or "Attendant-in-Attendance." The tomb seemed to belong to a high-ranking noble. When the coffin was broken open, a person with white hair was found inside, dressed in bright and clean clothes, with a face and body that looked like a living person. Inside the coffin was a layer of mica, about a foot thick, and thirty pieces of white jade discs were placed around the body. Soldiers used a cart to lift out the dead body and leaned it against the tomb wall. A jade piece, about a foot long and shaped like a winter melon, slipped out of the dead person's chest and fell to the ground. Gold pieces, about the size of dates, were found in the ears and nostrils.

    179

    汉广川王好发冢。发栾书冢，其棺柩盟器，悉毁烂无余；唯有一白狐，见人惊走；左右逐之，不得，戟伤其左足。是夕，王梦一丈夫，须眉尽白，来谓王曰：“何故伤吾左足？”乃以杖叩王左足。王觉，肿痛，即生疮，至死不差。
    搜神记卷十六
    　　昔颛顼氏有三子，死而为疫鬼：一居江水，为疟鬼；一居若水，为魍魉鬼；一居人宫室，善惊人小儿，为小鬼。于是正岁，命方相氏帅肆傩以驱疫鬼。
    　　挽歌者，丧家之乐，执绋者相和之声也。挽歌辞有薤露，蒿里二章。汉田横门人作。横自杀，门人伤之，悲歌，言：人如薤上露，易稀灭；亦谓人死，精魂归于蒿里。故有二章。

    Explanation

    179

    The King of Guangchuan had a fondness for opening tombs. When he opened the tomb of Luan Shu, all the coffins, caskets, and ritual vessels were completely ruined and rotten, leaving nothing behind. There was only one white fox that started and ran away when it saw people. The attendants chased it but failed to catch it, and they injured its left foot with a halberd. That night, the king dreamed of a man with all-white beard and eyebrows who came to him and said, "Why did you injure my left foot?" Then he tapped the king's left foot with a stick. When the king woke up, his foot was swollen and painful, and he immediately developed sores, which did not heal until his death.

    In the sixteenth volume of Soushenji (Records of Searching for the Supernatural):
    Formerly, Emperor Zhuanxu had three sons who died and became plague spirits: one resided in the Yangtze River and became a malaria spirit; one resided in the River Luo and became a ghost of the dark; one resided in human palaces and was good at startling children, becoming a little ghost. Therefore, on the first day of the year, officials were ordered to lead the ritual of exorcism to drive away plague spirits.

    Funeral songs are the music played at funerals, and they are the harmonized sounds of those who hold the funeral ropes. There are two chapters in the funeral songs: "Allium Leaves and Dew" and "Hemp Fields," written by the disciples of Tianheng of the Han dynasty. When Tianheng killed himself, his disciples mourned him and sang mournfully, saying: "People are like dew on Allium leaves, easily evaporate and disappear; also, people die, their spirits return to the hemp fields." Therefore, there are two chapters.

    180

    阮瞻，字千里，素执无鬼论。物莫能难。每自谓，此理足以辨正幽明。忽有客通名诣瞻，寒温毕，聊谈名理。客甚有才辨，瞻与之言，良久，及鬼神之事，反复甚苦。客遂屈，乃作色曰：“鬼神，古今圣贤所共传，君何得独言无？即仆便是鬼。”于是变为异形，须臾消灭。瞻默然，意色太恶。岁余，病卒。
    　　吴兴施续为寻阳督，能言论，有门生亦有理意，常秉无鬼论。忽有一黑衣白袷客来，与共语，遂及鬼神。移日，客辞屈。乃曰：“君辞巧，理不足。仆即是鬼。何以云无；问：“鬼何以来？”答曰：“受使来取君。期尽明日食时。”门生请乞，酸苦，鬼问：“有人似君者否？”门生云：“施续帐下都督，与仆相似。”便与俱往，与都督对坐；鬼手中出一铁凿，可尺余，安着都督头，便举椎打之。都督云：“头觉微痛。”向来转剧，食顷，便亡。

    Explanation

    180

    阮瞻，字千里，素执无鬼论。物莫能难。每自谓，此理足以辨正幽明。忽有客通名诣瞻，寒温毕，聊谈名理。客甚有才辨，瞻与之言，良久，及鬼神之事，反复甚苦。客遂屈，乃作色曰：“鬼神，古今圣贤所共传，君何得独言无？即仆便是鬼。”于是变为异形，须臾消灭。瞻默然，意色太恶。岁余，病卒。

    吴兴施续为寻阳督，能言论，有门生亦有理意，常秉无鬼论。忽有一黑衣白袷客来，与共语，遂及鬼神。移日，客辞屈。乃曰：“君辞巧，理不足。仆即是鬼。何以云无；问：“鬼何以来？”答曰：“受使来取君。期尽明日食时。”门生请乞，酸苦，鬼问：“有人似君者否？”门生云：“施续帐下都督，与仆相似。”便与俱往，与都督对坐；鬼手中出一铁凿，可尺余，安着都督头，便举椎打之。都督云：“头觉微痛。”向来转剧，食顷，便亡。

    Translation:
    阮瞻, courtesy name Qianli, had always held the view that there were no ghosts. No one could refute it. He often said that this reasoning was sufficient to distinguish between the visible and the invisible. Suddenly, a guest came to visit him, they exchanged greetings, and began discussing the principles of names and principles. The guest was very skilled in debate, and after a long conversation, they discussed the matter of ghosts and spirits, which was intensely debated. The guest eventually conceded and changed his expression, saying, "Ghosts and spirits are commonly believed by ancient and modern sages; how can you alone say there are none? Then I am a ghost." He then transformed into an unusual form and disappeared in an instant. 阮瞻 remained silent, his expression becoming very displeased. After a year, he died of illness.

    施续 from Wu County served as the supervisor of Xunyang, skilled in debate and discussion, and had a student who also held the view that there were no ghosts. Suddenly, a guest wearing a black robe and white undergarment came to visit him, and they began talking, eventually discussing the matter of ghosts and spirits. After a day, the guest conceded. He said, "Your words are clever, but your reasoning is insufficient. I am a ghost. How can you say there are none? You asked, 'Why did the ghost come?' The guest replied, 'I was sent to take you. I will finish by tomorrow at mealtime.' The student pleaded, feeling bitter, and the ghost asked, 'Is there anyone who resembles you?' The student said, 'There is a deputy under Supervisor Shixu, who resembles me.' The ghost then went with them, sat opposite the deputy, and took out an iron chisel about a foot long, placed it on the deputy's head, and struck it with a mallet. The deputy said, 'My head feels slightly painful.' It gradually became more severe, and after an hour, he died.

    181

    蒋济，字子通，楚国平阿人也，仕魏，为领军将军。其妇梦见亡儿，涕泣曰：“死生异路，我生时为卿相子孙，今在地下，为泰山伍伯，憔悴困苦，不可复言。今太庙西讴士孙阿见召为泰山令，愿母为白侯，属阿，令转我得乐处。”言讫，母忽然惊寤。明日以白济。济曰：“梦为虚耳，不足怪也。”日暮，复梦曰：“我来迎新君，止在庙下未发之顷，暂得来归。新君，明日日中当发。临发多事，不复得归。永辞于此。侯气强难感悟，故自诉于母，愿重启侯：何惜不一试验之？”遂道阿之形状言甚备悉。

    Explanation

    181

    Jiang Ji, styled Zi Tong, was from Ping'a in the state of Chu. He served in the state of Wei and held the position of General-in-Chief. His wife had a dream in which she saw her deceased son, who wept and said, "Life and death are separate paths. When I was alive, I was the descendant of a high-ranking official, but now in the underworld, I serve as a minor official known as a Wubai of Taishan, enduring suffering and hardship beyond words. Now, Sun A, a song performer from the west of the Imperial Ancestral Temple, has been appointed as the new Governor of Taishan. I beg you, Mother, to inform Lord Jiang and entrust Sun A, so that I may be transferred to a place of happiness." After he finished speaking, his mother suddenly awoke in alarm. The next day, she told Jiang Ji about the dream. Jiang Ji said, "This was just a dream, nothing to be surprised about." That evening, she dreamed again, and the child said, "I have come to escort the new ruler, and I am now waiting below the temple, having not yet departed. I have come back briefly to visit you. The new ruler will depart at noon tomorrow. At the time of departure, there are many matters to attend to, and I will not be able to return. This is our final farewell. Lord Jiang's spirit is strong and difficult to move, so I have come to plead with you, Mother. I beg you, Lord Jiang, to at least give this one thing a try?" He then described Sun A's appearance in great detail.

    182

    天明，母重启济：“虽云梦不足怪，此何太适。适，亦何惜不一验之？”济乃遗人诣太庙下，推问孙阿，果得之，形状证验，悉如儿言。济涕泣曰：“几负吾儿。”于是乃见孙阿，具语其事。阿不惧当死，而喜得为泰山令，惟恐济言不信也，曰：“若如节下言，阿之愿也。不知贤子欲得何职？”济曰：“随地下乐者与之。”阿曰：“辄当奉教。”乃厚赏之。言讫，遣还。济欲速知其验，从领军门至庙下，十步安一人，以传消息。辰时，传阿心痛；已时，传阿剧；日中，传阿亡。济曰：“虽哀吾儿之不幸，且喜亡者有知。”后月余，儿复来，语母曰：“已得转为录事矣，”
    　　汉，不其县，有孤竹城，古孤竹君之国也，灵帝光和元年，辽西人见辽水中有浮棺，欲斫破之；棺中人语曰：“我是伯夷之弟，孤竹君也。海水坏我棺椁，是以漂流。汝斫我何为？”人惧，不敢斫。因为立庙祠祀。吏民有欲发视者，皆无病而死。

    Explanation

    182

    At dawn, the mother urged Ji again: "Though it is not strange to dream, why is this so comfortable? Why not just test it once?" Ji then sent someone to the Imperial Ancestral Temple to investigate Sun A. They indeed found him, and his appearance matched the son's description exactly. Ji wept and said, "I almost let my son down." Thus, he met Sun A and told him everything. Sun A did not fear death but was happy to become the magistrate of Mount Tai, only worried that Ji might not believe him. He said, "If it is as you say, it is what I wish for. I do not know what position your honorable son wants." Ji replied, "Grant him any position he desires in the underworld." Sun A said, "I will follow your instructions." Ji then rewarded him generously. After finishing the conversation, he was sent back. Ji wanted to quickly know the outcome, so he placed a messenger every ten steps from the commander's gate to the temple to relay messages. At the hour of Chen, they reported that Sun A had a heartache; at the hour of Yi, they reported that Sun A was in severe pain; at noon, they reported that Sun A had died. Ji said, "Although I grieve for my son's misfortune, I am also glad that the deceased has consciousness." A month later, the son returned and told his mother, "I have already been promoted to the position of recorder."

    In the Han dynasty, there was a city called Guzhu in Buxi County, which was the ancient capital of the state of Guzhu. In the first year of the Guanghe era during Emperor Ling's reign, a man from Liaoxi saw a floating coffin in the Liao River and wanted to chop it open. The person in the coffin said, "I am the younger brother of Bo Yi, the ruler of Guzhu. The sea has damaged my coffin, so it has drifted here. Why would you chop me?" The man was frightened and did not dare to chop it. Therefore, they built a temple to worship him. Officials and commoners who wanted to open and inspect the coffin all died without apparent illness.

    183

    温序，字公次，太原祈人也，任护军校尉，行部至陇西，为隗嚣将所劫，欲生降之。序大怒，以节挝杀人，贼趋，欲杀序。荀宇止之曰：“义士欲死节。”赐剑，令自裁。序受剑，衔须着口中，叹曰：“则令须污土。”遂伏剑死。更始怜之，送葬到洛阳城旁，为筑冢。长子寿，为印平侯，梦序告之曰“久客思乡。”寿即弃官，上书乞骸骨，归葬。帝许之。
    　　汉，南阳文颖，字叔长，建安中为甘陵府丞，过界止宿，夜三鼓时，梦见一人跪前曰：“昔我先人，葬我于此，水来湍墓，棺木溺，渍水处半，然无以自温。闻君在此，故来相依，欲屈明日暂住须臾，幸为相迁高燥处。”鬼披衣示颖，而皆沾湿。颖心怆然，即寤。语诸左右。曰：“梦为虚耳亦何足怪。

    Explanation

    183

    Wen Xu, courtesy name Gongci, was from Taiyuan in the state of Qi. He served as a military officer and traveled to Longxi, where he was captured by a general of Wei Xiu, who wanted to force him to surrender alive. Wen Xu was furious and struck the captors with his staff, killing some of them. The captors rushed to kill Wen Xu, but Xun Yu intervened and said, "A righteous man wishes to die for his principles." He was given a sword and ordered to commit suicide. Wen Xu accepted the sword, held his mustache in his mouth, and sighed, "Then let my mustache soil the earth." He then fell on the sword and died. Emperor Gengshi pitied him and sent his body to be buried near Luoyang, where a tomb was built for him. His eldest son, Wen Shou, who was the Marquis of Yinping, dreamed that Wen Xu told him, "I have been a long-term guest and miss my hometown." Wen Shou immediately resigned his position, wrote a petition to the emperor asking to be allowed to return and bury his father, and the emperor granted his request.

    In another account, Han Wen Ying, courtesy name Shuchang, was from Nanyang and served as a county magistrate in Ganling during the Jian'an period. One night, he stayed overnight outside the city boundary and, at the third watch of the night, dreamed of a person kneeling before him and saying, "My ancestors buried me here, but the water has washed away half of the tomb, and the coffin has sunk. There is no way for me to stay warm. I heard that you are here, so I have come to rely on you. I would like to ask you to move me to a higher, drier place for a short while tomorrow." The ghost showed Wen Ying his wet clothes. Wen Ying was deeply moved and woke up. He told his attendants, "The dream was unreal; what's there to be surprised about?"

    184

    ”颖乃还眠向寐处，梦见谓颖曰：“我以穷苦告君，奈何不相愍悼乎？”颖梦中问曰：“子为谁？”对曰：“吾本赵人，今属汪芒氏之神。”颖曰：“子棺今何所在？”对曰：“近在君帐北十数步水侧枯杨树下，即是吾也。天将明，不复得见，君必念之。”颖答曰：“喏！”忽然便寤。天明，可发，颖曰：“虽曰梦不足怪，此何太适。”左右曰：“亦何惜须臾，不验之耶？”颖即起，率十数人将导顺水上，果得一枯杨，曰：“是矣。”掘其下，未几，果得棺。棺甚朽坏，没半水中。颖谓左右曰：‘向闻于人，谓之虚矣；世俗所传，不可无验。”为移其棺，葬之而去。

    Explanation

    184

    Ying returned to sleep in the place where he was about to sleep. In his dream, he heard someone say to him, "I told you of my poverty and suffering, why don't you pity me?" Ying, still in his dream, asked, "Who are you?" The voice replied, "I was originally from Zhao, but now I belong to the god of the Wamang people." Ying asked, "Where is your coffin now?" The voice answered, "It is near your tent, northward by a dozen steps, beside a dead willow tree by the water, that is me. It will soon be dawn, and I won't be able to see you again, so you must remember me." Ying responded, "Yes!" Suddenly, he woke up. At dawn, as they were about to set out, Ying said, "Even though it's a dream, it's not unusual, but why is it so strange?" Those around him said, "Why not spend a little time to verify it?" Ying immediately got up, led a dozen people upstream, and indeed found a dead willow tree. He said, "That's it." They dug underneath, and in a short while, they indeed found the coffin. The coffin was very rotten and half-submerged in water. Ying told those around him, "What I heard from others, they said it was false; what is passed down by the common people cannot be without verification." They moved the coffin, buried it, and left.

    185

    汉，九江何敞，为交州刺史，行部到苍梧郡高安县，暮宿鹄奔亭，夜犹未半，有一女从楼下出，呼曰：“妾姓苏，名娥，字始珠，本居广信县修里人。早失父母，又无兄弟，嫁与同县施氏，薄命夫死，有杂缯帛百二十疋，及婢一人，名致富，妾孤穷羸弱，不能自振；欲之傍县卖缯，从同县男子王伯赁牛车一乘，直钱万二千，载妾幷缯，令致富执辔，乃以前年四月十日到此亭外。于时日已向暮，行人断绝，不敢复进，因即留止，致富暴得腹痛。

    Explanation

    185

    During the Han Dynasty, He Chang of Jiujiang served as the governor of Jiaozhou. On his inspection tour, he arrived at Gao'an County in the苍梧郡 region and spent the night at the鹄奔亭 inn. It was still early in the night when a woman emerged from downstairs and called out: "I am Su E, also known as Shi Zhu, originally from Xiu Village in Guangxin County. I lost my parents at a young age and had no brothers. I married a man named Shi from the same county, but he died young. I have a hundred and twenty bolts of assorted silk fabrics and a maid named Zengfu. Being poor, weak, and destitute, I could not support myself. I wished to sell the fabrics in a neighboring county, so I rented a cart from a man named Wang Bo from the same county. The cart cost 12,000 coins, and I loaded myself and the fabrics onto it, having Zengfu hold the reins. We arrived at this inn on April 10th of the previous year. By then, it was already late in the day, and there were no more travelers. We dared not go further, so we stayed there. Suddenly, Zengfu suffered from severe abdominal pain.

    186

    妾之亭长舍乞浆，取火，亭长龚寿，操戈持戟，来至车旁，问妾曰：‘夫人从何所来车上所载何物？丈夫安在？何故独行？’妾应曰：‘何劳问之？’寿因持妾臂曰：‘少年爱有色，冀可乐也。’妾惧怖不从，寿即持刀刺胁下一创，立死。又刺致富，亦死。寿掘楼下，合埋妾在下，婢在上，取财物去。杀牛，烧车，车缸及牛骨，贮亭东空井中。妾既冤死，痛感皇天，无所告诉，故来自归于明使君。敞曰：“今欲发出汝尸，以何为验？”女曰：“妾上下着白衣，青丝履，犹未朽也，愿访乡里，以骸骨归死夫。”掘之，果然。敞乃驰还，遣吏捕捉，拷问，具服。下广信县验问，与娥语合。寿父母兄弟，悉捕系狱。敞表寿，常律，杀人不至族诛，然寿为恶首，隐密数年，王法自所不免。令鬼神诉者，千载无一，请皆斩之，以明鬼神，以助阴诛。上报听之。

    Explanation

    186

    A woman visited the residence of a local official to request water and fire. The official, named Gong Shou, wielding a spear and a halberd, approached the carriage and asked her, "Madam, where do you come from? What is in your carriage? Where is your husband? Why are you traveling alone?" The woman replied, "Why bother asking?" Shou then grabbed her arm and said, "Young men love beauty and hope to be pleased." The woman was terrified and refused, but Shou immediately drew a knife and stabbed her in the side, causing her to die instantly. He then stabbed another person, also causing them to die. Shou dug a pit beneath the carriage, buried the woman and her servant together, with the woman below and the servant above, and took their belongings. He then slaughtered a cow, burned the carriage, and stored the carriage parts and cow bones in a well in the east of the pavilion. The woman had died unjustly, and her pain moved the heavens. Having nowhere to appeal, she came to seek justice from the wise official. The official asked, "If we want to exhume your body, what will be the proof?" The woman replied, "I wore white clothes and had silk shoes, which are still intact. I wish to visit my hometown and return my bones to my deceased husband." The officials exhumed the bodies, and indeed, the descriptions matched. The official then returned quickly, sent officials to capture the perpetrators, interrogated them, and they confessed. The officials in Guangxin County verified the statements, and they matched those of the woman. The parents and brothers of the perpetrator were all captured and imprisoned. The official petitioned for the perpetrator, stating that according to the law, killing does not warrant collective punishment. However, the perpetrator was the leader of the crime, kept hidden for years, and thus could not escape the law. Let the ghosts and spirits who have appealed, who are rare in a thousand years, all be executed to demonstrate the power of the spirits and to assist in the divine punishment. The emperor approved the request.

    187

    濡须口有大船，船覆在水中，水小时便出见，长老云：“是曹公船。”尝有渔人，夜宿其旁，以船系之；但闻竽笛弦歌之音，又香气，非常。渔人始得眠，梦人驱遣，云：“勿近官妓。”相传云：“曹公载妓，船覆于此，至今在焉。”

    Explanation

    187

    There is a large ship at the mouth of the Ru River. When the ship overturned in the water, it became visible when the water level was low. The elders say, "This is Cao Cao's ship." Once, a fisherman spent the night beside it, tying his boat to it. He only heard the sounds of flutes, pipes, and singing, along with a pleasant fragrance, which was unusual. The fisherman finally fell asleep and dreamt of someone driving him away, saying, "Do not approach the official courtesans." It is said that Cao Cao carried courtesans on the ship, which sank here, and it remains here to this day.

    188

    夏侯恺，字万仁，因病死、宗人儿苟奴，素见鬼，见恺数归，欲取马，幷病其妻，着平上帻，单衣，入坐生时西壁大床，就人觅茶饮。
    　　诸仲务，一女，显姨，嫁为米元宗妻，产亡于家。俗闻，产亡者，以墨点面。其母不忍，仲务密自点之，无人见者。元宗为始新县丞，梦其妻来，上床，分明见新白，面上有黑点。
    　　晋世，新蔡王昭平，犊车在厅事上，夜，无故自入斋室中，触壁而出。后又数闻呼噪攻击之声，四面而来。昭乃聚众设弓弩战斗之备，指声弓弩俱发，而鬼应声接矢数枚，皆倒入土中。
    　　吴，赤乌三年，句章民杨度，至余姚，夜行，有一少年，持琵琶，求寄载。度受之。鼓琵琶数十曲，曲毕，乃吐舌，擘目，以怖度而去。复行二十里许，又见一老父，自云：“姓王，名戒。”因复载之。谓曰：“鬼工鼓琵琶，甚哀。”戒曰：“我亦能鼓。”即是向鬼。复擘眼，吐舌，度怖几死。

    188

    Xiahou Kai, courtesy name Wan Ren, died of illness. A clan member named Gou Nu, who often saw ghosts, saw Kai appear multiple times, wanting to take a horse and harm his wife. He wore a simple head covering and a plain robe, entered the bed in the west wall of the house where he used to live, and approached people to ask for tea.

    Zhong Wu had a daughter named Xian Ai, who married Mi Yuanzong. She died during childbirth at home. According to custom, those who die in childbirth are marked with ink on their faces. Her mother did not want to do it, so Zhong Wu secretly marked her own face, and no one saw her. Yuanzong, as the county magistrate of Shixin, dreamed of his wife coming, climbing onto the bed, and clearly seeing her face, which had black marks.

    During the Jin Dynasty, Xincai Wang Zhaoping had a small cart in the main hall. At night, it entered the study room without reason and exited after hitting the wall. Later, he frequently heard shouting and attacking sounds coming from all directions. Zhaoping gathered people to set up bows and arrows for defense, pointing and shooting at the sounds. The ghosts caught the arrows, and they fell into the ground.

    In the Wu Kingdom, during the third year of the Xichu era, a man from Juchang named Yang Du traveled to Yuyao. One night, he met a young man holding a pipa, asking for a ride. Du accepted the request. The young man played the pipa for many songs. After the songs ended, he stuck out his tongue and opened his eyes wide, scaring Du and leaving. Du continued for about twenty miles and saw an old man who said his name was Wang Jie. Du let him ride again. The old man said, "The ghost plays the pipa very mournfully." Wang Jie replied, "I can play too," and was the same ghost. He opened his eyes and stuck out his tongue again, terrifying Du almost to death.

    琅琊秦巨伯，年六十，尝夜行，饮酒，道经蓬山庙，忽见其两孙迎之；扶持百余步，便捉伯颈着地，骂：“老奴！汝某日捶我，我今当杀汝。”伯思，惟某时信捶此孙。伯乃佯死，乃置伯去。伯归家，欲治两孙，两孙惊惋，叩头言：“为子孙宁可有此？恐是鬼魅，乞更试之。”伯意悟，数日，乃诈醉，行此庙间，复见两孙来扶持伯。伯乃急持，鬼动作不得；达家，乃是两人也。伯着火炙之，腹背俱焦坼，出着庭中，夜皆亡去。伯恨不得杀之，后月余，又佯酒醉，夜行，怀刃以去，家不知也，极夜不还，其孙恐又为此鬼所困，乃俱往迎伯，伯竟刺杀之。
    　　汉，武建元年，东莱人，姓池，家常作酒，一日，见三奇客，共持面饭至，索其酒饮。饮竟而去。顷之，有人来，云：“见三鬼酣醉于林中。”
    　　吴先主杀武卫兵钱小小，形见大街，顾借赁人吴永，使永送书与街南庙，借木马二匹，以酒噀之，皆成好马，鞍勒俱全。

    189

    Lángyá Qín Jùbó, aged sixty, once traveled at night, drinking wine. On his way, he passed by Pénghuān Temple. Suddenly, he saw his two grandsons welcoming him. They supported him for more than a hundred steps, then grabbed Jùbó's neck and pressed him to the ground, scolding, "Old slave! You beat me on a certain day, and now I will kill you." Jùbó thought, only on a certain time did he believe he beat this grandson. Jùbó then pretended to be dead, and they left him. Jùbó returned home, intending to punish his two grandsons. The grandsons were surprised and grieved, knocking their heads and saying, "For descendants, how could there be such a thing? Fearing it might be a ghost or demon, begging to try again." Jùbó understood, and after several days, he pretended to be drunk and walked past the temple. He saw his two grandsons coming to support him again. Jùbó then quickly held them, and the ghosts could not move. When he arrived home, it turned out to be two people. Jùbó lit a fire and roasted them, their backs and bellies were both burned and cracked. He took them out and placed them in the courtyard, and at night they all fled. Jùbó could not bear not to kill them. After a month or so, he again pretended to be drunk and left with a knife, the family did not know. He did not return until very late at night. His grandsons feared they would be trapped again by this ghost, so they went together to meet Jùbó, and Jùbó finally stabbed and killed them.

    During the reign of Emperor Wu of Han, a man from Dōnglái named Chí, whose family frequently made wine, saw three strange guests one day. They brought cooked rice and asked for their wine to drink. They drank and then left. After a while, someone came and said, "Saw three ghosts drunk in the forest."

    Wú Xiānzhǔ killed the Wǔwèi soldier Qián Xiǎoxiǎo, and his spirit appeared on the main street. He looked for a hired man named Wú Yǒng, asking Yǒng to deliver a message to the temple on the south side of the street, borrowing two wooden horses, and sprinkled wine on them, turning them into good horses with saddles and bridles complete.

    南阳宋定伯，年少时，夜行，逢鬼，问之。鬼言：“我是鬼。”鬼问：“汝复谁？”定伯诳之，言：“我亦鬼。”鬼问：“欲至何所？”答曰：“欲至宛市。”鬼言：“我亦欲至宛市。”遂行。数里，鬼言：“步行太迟，可共递相担，何如？”定伯曰：“大善。”鬼便先担定伯数里。鬼言：“卿太重，将非鬼也。”定伯言：“我新鬼，故身重耳。”定伯因复担鬼，鬼略无重。如是再三，定伯复言：“我新鬼，不知有何所畏忌？”鬼答言：“惟不喜人唾。”于是共行。道遇水，定伯令鬼先渡，听之，了然无声音。定伯自渡，漕漼作声。鬼复言：“何以有声？”定伯曰：“新死，不习渡水故耳。勿怪吾也。”行欲至宛市，定伯便担鬼，着肩上，急执之。鬼大呼，声咋咋然，索下，不复听之。径至宛市中下着地，化为一羊，便卖之，恐其变化，唾之，得钱千五百，乃去。当时石崇有言：“定伯卖鬼，得钱千五。”

    Explanation

    190

    Nanyang's Song Dingbo, when young, was walking at night and encountered a ghost. He asked the ghost, "Who are you?" The ghost replied, "I am a ghost." The ghost then asked, "And who are you?" Dingbo deceived the ghost, saying, "I am also a ghost." The ghost asked, "Where do you wish to go?" Dingbo replied, "I wish to go to the market in Wan." The ghost said, "I also wish to go to the market in Wan." They then proceeded together. After walking a few miles, the ghost said, "Walking is too slow; we can take turns carrying each other, what do you think?" Dingbo said, "That's a great idea." The ghost then carried Dingbo for several miles. The ghost said, "You are too heavy; are you not a ghost?" Dingbo replied, "I am a new ghost, so my body is heavier." Dingbo then carried the ghost, and the ghost seemed to have no weight at all. They repeated this exchange several times. Dingbo again said, "I am a new ghost, and I don't know what I should be afraid of." The ghost replied, "I just don't like human spittle." They continued on their way. When they came across water, Dingbo told the ghost to cross first and listened carefully, but heard no sound. When Dingbo crossed the water, it made a splashing noise. The ghost asked, "Why is there a sound?" Dingbo said, "I am newly dead and not used to crossing water, so don't be surprised by me." As they were nearing the market in Wan, Dingbo suddenly picked up the ghost and placed it on his shoulder, quickly seizing it. The ghost let out a loud cry, sounding like "Zaza," and begged to be put down, but Dingbo did not listen. He carried the ghost directly to the market in Wan and put it down on the ground, where it transformed into a sheep. Dingbo then sold the sheep, fearing it might change again, and spat on it. He received one thousand five hundred coins and left. At that time, Shi Chong said, "Dingbo sold a ghost and received one thousand five hundred coins."
