    吴王夫差，小女，名曰紫玉，年十八，才貌俱美。童子韩重，年十九，有道术，女悦之，私交信问，许为之妻。重学于齐，鲁之间，临去，属其父母使求婚。王怒、不与。女玉结气死，葬阊门之外。三年，重归，诘其父母；父母曰：“王大怒，玉结气死，已葬矣。”重哭泣哀恸，具牲币往吊于墓前。玉魂从墓出，见重流涕，谓曰：“昔尔行之后，令二亲从王相求，度必克从大愿；不图别后遭命，奈何！”玉乃左顾，宛颈而歌曰：“南山有乌，北山张罗；乌既高飞，罗将奈何！意欲从君，谗言孔多。悲结生疾，没命黄垆。命之不造，冤如之何！羽族之长，名为凤凰；一日失雄，三年感伤；虽有众鸟，不为匹双。故见鄙姿，逢君辉光。身远心近，何当暂忘。”歌毕，歔欷流涕，要重还冢。

    Explanation

    191

    King Fuchai of Wu had a daughter named Ziyu, who was eighteen years old and both talented and beautiful. A young man named Han Zhong, aged nineteen, possessed Daoist techniques, and Princess Ziyu was fond of him. They secretly exchanged letters and agreed to marry. Han Zhong studied in the states of Qi and Lu. Before he left, he instructed his parents to propose marriage to the princess. King Fuchai became furious and refused the proposal. Princess Ziyu died of a broken heart and was buried outside the Chuan Gate. Three years later, Han Zhong returned and questioned his parents. They replied, "The king was very angry, and Princess Ziyu died of grief. She has already been buried." Han Zhong cried bitterly and prepared sacrificial offerings to mourn at her grave. The spirit of Princess Ziyu emerged from the tomb, saw Han Zhong, and wept, saying, "After you left, I asked my parents to seek your hand from the king, hoping we would fulfill our wish. I did not expect that after our separation, I would meet such a fate. What can I do?" Princess Ziyu then turned her head to the left and sang, "There is a bird in the south mountain, and a net in the north mountain. The bird has already flown high, what can the net do? I wish to follow you, but there are many slanderous words. Grief has caused me to fall ill, and I have died in the yellow earth. My fate was not kind, and I am full of grievances. The leader of the birds is called the phoenix. Losing the male one day, I grieve for three years. Even though there are many birds, they cannot form a pair. Thus, I see my humble self, and I meet your radiance. We are physically far apart, but close in heart. When will we temporarily forget this sorrow?" After finishing her song, she sighed and wept, inviting Han Zhong back to the tomb.

    重曰：“死生异路，惧有尤愆，不敢承命。”玉曰：“死生异路，吾亦知之；然今一别，永无后期。子将畏我为鬼而祸子乎？欲诚所奉，宁不相信。”重感其言，送之还冢。玉与之饮燕，留三日三夜，尽夫妇之礼。临出，取径寸明珠以送重曰：“既毁其名，又绝其愿，复何言哉！时节自爱。若至吾家，致敬大王。”重既出，遂诣王自说其事。王大怒曰：“吾女既死，而重造讹言，以玷秽亡灵，此不过发冢取物，托以鬼神。”趣收重。重走脱，至玉墓所，诉之。玉曰：“无忧。今归白王。”王妆梳，忽见玉，惊愕悲喜，问曰：“尔缘何生？”玉跪而言曰：“昔诸生韩重来求玉，大王不许，玉名毁，义绝，自致身亡。重从远还，闻玉已死，故赍牲币，诣冢吊唁。感其笃，终辄与相见，因以珠遗之，不为发冢。愿勿推治。”夫人闻之，出而抱之。玉如烟然。

    192

    Zhong replied, "Life and death are different paths, and I fear I have committed a grave fault, so I dare not accept your command." Jade said, "Life and death are different paths, and I also know this; however, this parting will be forever, with no more meetings in the future. Are you afraid that I will become a ghost and bring disaster upon you? If you truly wish to honor me, why wouldn't you trust me?" Moved by her words, Zhong sent her back to her tomb. Jade entertained him with wine and music, and they spent three days and nights together, observing the rites of a married couple. As he was leaving, she gave him a pearl as large as a thumb and said, "Having destroyed my reputation and cut off my wishes, what more can I say? Take care of yourself in due time. If you come to my home, pay respects to the great king." After Zhong left, he went to the king to tell him about the matter. The king was furious and said, "My daughter is already dead, yet Zhong has spread false rumors to defile her spirit. This is nothing more than grave robbing, pretending to be guided by ghosts." He ordered Zhong to be arrested. Zhong fled, and when he reached Jade's tomb, he told her what had happened. Jade said, "Do not worry. I will return and explain to the king." The king, after dressing and combing his hair, suddenly saw Jade and was shocked, filled with both sorrow and joy. He asked, "Why have you come back to life?" Jade knelt and said, "In the past, the scholar Han Zhong came to seek me, but the great king did not allow it. My reputation was ruined, and our bond was severed, leading to my own death. Now that Zhong has returned from afar and heard that I am dead, he brought offerings to my tomb to mourn me. Moved by his sincerity, I met him and gave him the pearl, not for grave robbing. I hope you will not pursue this matter." The lady heard this and came out to embrace her. Jade then disappeared like smoke.

    陇西辛道度者，游学至雍州城四五里，比见一大宅，有青衣女子在门。度诣门下求飧。女子入告秦女，女命召入。度趋入阁中，秦女于西榻而坐。度称姓名，叙起居，既毕，命东榻而坐。即治饮馔。食讫，女谓度曰：“我秦闵王女，出聘曹国，不幸无夫而亡。亡来已二十三年，独居此宅，今日君来，愿为夫妇，经三宿。”三日后，女即自言曰：“君是生人，我鬼也，共君宿契，此会可三宵，不可久居，当有祸矣。然兹信宿，未悉绸缪，既已分飞，将何表信于郎？”即命取床后盒子开之，取金枕一枚，与度为信。

    193

    Xin Dao Du from Longxi, while traveling for study to within four or five miles of Yongzhou city, saw a large house nearby, with a maid in green clothes at the door. Dao Du went to the door to ask for food. The maid went inside to inform Qin's daughter, who ordered her to be called in. Dao Du hurried into the inner chamber, where Qin's daughter was sitting on the western couch. Dao Du introduced his name and discussed daily routines, after which she ordered him to sit on the eastern couch. She immediately prepared food and drink. After eating, Qin's daughter said to Dao Du, "I am the daughter of King Qin Min of Qin, who was betrothed to the state of Cao but unfortunately died without a husband. I have been dead for twenty-three years and have lived alone in this house. Today you have come, and I wish to be your wife for three nights."

    Three days later, Qin's daughter said to herself, "You are a living person, and I am a ghost. Our meeting is for three nights only, and I cannot stay long, as it will bring disaster. But since we have spent these two nights together, and now we must part, what shall I give you as a token of our bond?" She then ordered a box from behind the bed to be opened, took out a golden pillow, and gave it to Dao Du as a token.

    194

    乃分袂泣别，即遣青衣送出门外。未逾数步，不见舍宇，惟有一冢。度当时荒忙出走，视其金枕在怀，乃无异变。寻至秦国，以枕于市货之，恰遇秦妃东游，亲见度卖金枕，疑而索看。诘度何处得来？度具以告。妃闻，悲泣不能自胜，然向疑耳，乃遣人发冢启柩视之，原葬悉在，唯不见枕。解体看之，交情宛若。秦妃始信之。叹曰：“我女大圣，死经二十三年，犹能与生人交往。此是我真女婿也。”遂封度为驸马都尉，赐金帛车马，令还本国。因此以来，后人名女婿为“驸马；”今之国婿！亦为“驸马”矣。

    Explanation

    194

    They parted with tears, and immediately sent a servant in blue robes to see him out. No sooner had he taken a few steps than the house was no longer visible, and before him lay only a mound. At that time, Du had fled in a hurried panic, and upon checking, the golden pillow was still in his possession, with no strange change. He then made his way to the State of Qin, where he sold the golden pillow in the marketplace. Just then, the Princess of Qin was traveling eastward, and she personally saw Du selling the golden pillow. Suspicious, she asked to see it. She questioned Du about where he had obtained it, and he told her the whole story. Upon hearing this, the princess wept bitterly, unable to control her emotions. Although she had previously suspected, she now sent people to open the grave and examine the coffin. Everything in the original burial was still there, except the golden pillow was missing. Upon inspecting the body, they found the affection between the couple still intact. Only then did the princess believe him. She sighed and said, "My daughter was a great saint, having died twenty-three years ago, yet she could still interact with the living. This is my true son-in-law." She then conferred upon Du the title of Prince’s Guard, granted him gold, silk, carriages, and horses, and ordered him to return to his homeland. From this time onward, later generations began to call a son-in-law "驸马," and today's national son-in-law is also called "驸马."

    195

    汉，谈生者，年四十，无妇，常感激读诗经，夜半，有女子，年可十五六，姿颜服饰，天下无双，来就生为夫妇之言，曰：“我与人不同，勿以火照我也，三年之后，方可照耳。”与为夫妇，生一儿，已二岁，不能忍，夜，伺其寝后，盗照视之。其腰已上生肉，如人，腰已下，但有枯骨。妇觉，遂言曰：“君负我。我垂生矣，何不能忍一岁，而竟相照也？”生辞谢涕泣，不可复止。云：“与君虽大义永离；然顾念我儿若贫不能自偕活者，暂随我去，方遗君物。”生随之去，入华堂，室宇器物不凡。以一珠袍与之，曰：“可以自给。”裂取生衣裾留之而去。后生持袍诣市，睢阳王家买之，得钱千万。王识之曰：“是我女袍，那得在市？此必发冢。”乃取拷之。生具以实对。王犹不信，乃视女冢，冢完如故，发视之，棺盖下果得衣裾，呼其儿视，正类王女王乃信之，即召谈生，复赐遗之，以为女婿。表其儿为郎中。

    Explanation

    195

    During the Han dynasty, there was a man named Tan who was forty years old and without a wife. He often moved by emotion while reading the Book of Songs. One night, a woman appeared, about fifteen or sixteen years old, with an appearance and attire unparalleled in the world. She came to Tan and proposed marriage, saying, "I am different from others; do not use fire to see me. After three years, you may see me." They lived together as husband and wife, and she gave birth to a son who was already two years old. Unable to bear it, one night, after she had fallen asleep, he secretly lit a fire to see her. Above her waist, she had flesh like a human, but below her waist, there were only dry bones. The woman awoke and said, "You have wronged me. I was almost complete, why could you not wait one more year before seeing me?" Tan begged for forgiveness and wept uncontrollably. She said, "Although we must part forever, I will take my son with me if he cannot live on his own. I will leave you something." Tan followed her, and they entered a magnificent hall, where the rooms and objects were extraordinary. She gave him a pearl robe, saying, "It will provide for you." She tore a piece of Tan's clothing and left it behind. Later, Tan took the robe to the market, where it was bought by the family of the Duke of Suixiang, and he received a million coins. The duke recognized it and said, "This is my daughter's robe. How could it be in the market? This must be a grave robbery." He then had him interrogated. Tan told him everything. The duke still did not believe him, so he inspected the tomb of his daughter, which was intact. When he opened the coffin, he found a piece of her clothing. He called his son to look, and it was indeed his daughter. The duke then believed him. He immediately summoned Tan, gave him gifts, and made him his son-in-law. He made his son an official.

    196

    卢充者，范阳人，家西三十里，有崔少府墓，充年二十，先冬至一日，出宅西猎戏，见一獐，举弓而射，中之，獐倒，复起。充因逐之，不觉远，忽见道北一里许，高门瓦屋，四周有如府舍，不复见獐。门中一铃下唱客前。充曰：“此何府也？”答曰：“少府府也，”充曰：“我衣恶，那得见少府？”即有一人提一幞新衣，曰：“府君以此遗郎。”充便着讫，进见少府。展姓名。酒炙数行。谓充曰：“尊府君不以仆门鄙陋，近得书，为君索小女婚，故相迎耳。”便以书示充。充，父亡时虽小，然已识父手迹，即欷歔无复辞免。

    Explanation

    196

    Lu Chong, a man from Fan Yang, lived thirty li west of his home, where there was the tomb of Cui the County Magistrate. When Lu Chong was twenty years old, one day before the Winter Solstice, he went out to the west of his house to hunt and play. He saw a deer and raised his bow to shoot it, hitting the deer. The deer fell but then got up again. Lu Chong chased after it and, without realizing how far he had gone, suddenly saw, about one li north of the road, a tall gate and tiled house, surrounded by what looked like official residences. He no longer saw the deer. A bell in the gate announced guests to come forward. Lu Chong asked, "What kind of office is this?" The response was, "This is the office of the County Magistrate." Lu Chong said, "My clothes are shabby; how can I meet the County Magistrate?" Immediately, a person brought a bundle of new clothes and said, "The County Magistrate has sent these for you." Lu Chong put on the clothes and went inside to see the County Magistrate. He introduced himself. They drank and ate several rounds. The County Magistrate said to Lu Chong, "Your esteemed father did not consider my humble and lowly family, and recently received a letter asking for your hand in marriage for my daughter, so I have come to welcome you." He then showed Lu Chong the letter. Lu Chong, though young when his father died, still recognized his father's handwriting and sighed, unable to refuse any longer.

    便敕内：“卢郎已来，可令女郎妆严。”且语充云：“君可就东廊，及至黄昏。”内白：“女郎妆严已毕。”充既至东廊，女已下车，立席头，却共拜。时为三日，给食三日毕，崔谓充曰：“君可归矣。女有娠相，若生男，当以相还，无相疑。生女，当留自养。”敕外严车送客。充便辞出。崔送至中门，执手涕零。出门，见一犊车，驾青衣，又见本所着衣及弓箭，故在门外。寻传教将一人提幞衣与充，相问曰：“姻援始尔，别甚怅恨。今复致衣一袭，被褥自副。”充上车，去如电逝，须臾至家。家人相见，悲喜推问，知崔是亡人，而入其墓。追以懊惋。

    197

    Immediately, the inner chamber was ordered: "The Lu scholar has arrived; can the young lady be asked to dress up?" And Chong was told: "You may go to the east corridor until dusk." The inner chamber reported: "The young lady has finished dressing up." Chong then went to the east corridor, where the young lady had already gotten off the carriage, stood at the head of the seat, and they bowed to each other. For three days, food was provided, and after three days, Cui said to Chong: "You may return now. The young lady has signs of pregnancy; if she gives birth to a boy, I will return him, so do not doubt. If she gives birth to a girl, she will be kept and raised by me." The outer chamber was ordered to prepare the carriage to send the guest. Chong then took his leave. Cui saw him off to the middle gate, holding hands and shedding tears. Upon leaving, he saw a small carriage driven by a servant in green, and also saw his original clothes and bow and arrow, still outside. Soon after, a messenger brought a person who held a bundle of clothes for Chong, and they said: "Our marriage alliance has just begun, and parting is very regrettable. Now I am sending another set of clothes and bedding for you." Chong got on the carriage, and left like lightning, arriving home in a short while. The family met, and they were both sad and happy, asking questions. They realized that Cui was a deceased person and entered her tomb, feeling regret and sorrow.

    别后四年，三月三日，充临水戏，忽见水旁有二犊车，乍沈乍浮，既而近岸，同坐皆见，而充往开车后户，见崔氏女与三岁男共载。充见之，忻然欲捉其手，女举手指后车曰：“府君见人。”即见少府。充往问讯，女抱儿还。充又与金鋺，幷赠诗曰：“煌煌灵芝质，光丽何猗猗！华艳当时显，嘉异表神奇。含英未及秀，中夏罹霜萎。荣耀长幽灭，世路永无施。不悟阴阳运，哲人忽来仪。会浅离别速，皆由灵与只。何以赠余亲，金鋺可颐儿。恩爱从此别，断肠伤肝脾。”充取儿，鋺及诗，忽然不见二车处。充将儿还，四坐谓是鬼魅，佥遥唾之。形如故。问儿：“谁是汝父？”儿径就充怀。

    Explanation

    198

    After four years of separation, on the third day of the third month, Chong was playing by the water when he suddenly saw two ox-drawn carts by the water, which were suddenly sinking and floating. Then they approached the shore, and all those present saw them. Chong went to open the back door of the cart and saw the Cui family woman and a three-year-old boy together. Chong saw her and was glad to take her hand, but the woman raised her finger and pointed to the rear cart, saying, "The official sees people." Then Chong saw the Lesser Official. Chong went to greet them, and the woman took the child back. Chong then gave her a gold bowl and also gave her a poem, saying: "Shining like a divine mushroom, how splendid and graceful! Beautiful and prominent at the time, wonderful and extraordinary, showing supernatural qualities. Holding beauty but not yet blooming, in midsummer suffering from frost and withering. Glory long fades into obscurity, the world's path forever has no place for it. Not understanding the workings of yin and yang, wise person suddenly appears. Brief encounter and quick separation, all due to spirits and deities. What to give as a gift to my dear ones, a gold bowl can nourish the child. Love and affection part from here, heartbroken and grieving." Chong took the child, the bowl, and the poem, and suddenly the two carts disappeared. Chong took the child back, and all present thought it was a ghost or demon, spitting at it from a distance. The child remained in the same form. Chong asked the child, "Who is your father?" The child immediately went into Chong's arms.

    众初怪恶，传省其诗，慨然叹死生之玄通也。充后乘车入市，卖鋺，高举其价，不欲速售，冀有识。欻有一老婢识此，还白大家曰：“市中见一人，乘车，卖崔氏女郎棺中鋺。”大家，即崔氏亲姨母也，遣儿视之，果如其婢言。上车，叙姓名，语充曰：“昔我姨嫁少府，生女，未出而亡。家亲痛之，赠一金鋺，着棺中。可说得鋺本末。”充以事对。此儿亦为之悲咽。赉还白母，母即令诣充家，迎儿视之。诸亲悉集。儿有崔氏之状，又复似充貌。儿、鋺俱验。姨母曰：‘我外甥三月末间产。父曰春，暖温也。愿休强也。”即字温休。温休者，盖幽婚也，其兆先彰矣。儿遂成令器。历郡守二千石，子孙冠盖相承。至今其后植，字子干，有名天下。

    Explanation

    199

    Initially, the crowd was surprised and repulsed, passing around and reading the poem, moved to sigh at the profound understanding of life and death. Chong then rode his carriage into the market, selling a coffin, setting a high price, not wanting to sell quickly, hoping someone would recognize it. Suddenly, an old servant recognized this, went back to inform the mistress, saying, "In the market, I saw a person riding in a carriage, selling a coffin from Lady Cui's daughter." The mistress, who is Lady Cui's aunt, sent her son to see it, and it was exactly as the servant had said. He got on the carriage, exchanged names, and told Chong, "My aunt married a minor official, had a daughter who died before marriage. The family mourned deeply, giving a golden coffin, placed in the coffin. Can you tell me the story of the coffin?" Chong recounted the story. This child also wept. He returned with the news to his mother, and the mother then ordered him to visit Chong's house, to welcome the child and see her. All the relatives gathered. The child resembled Lady Cui, and also resembled Chong's appearance. Both the child and the coffin were verified. The aunt said, "My nephew was born in late March. His father named him Chun, meaning warmth. Hoping he would be strong." So he was named Wenxiu. Wenxiu, it seems, was a secret marriage, and the signs were already evident. The child grew up to be a fine person, serving as a county magistrate and holding a high rank. His descendants continued in high office. One of his descendants, named Zigan, was famous throughout the world.

    后汉时，汝南汝阳西门亭，有鬼魅，宾客止宿，辄有死亡。其厉，厌者皆亡发，失精。寻问其故，云：“先时颇已有怪物。其后，郡侍奉掾宜禄郑奇来，去亭六七里，有一端正妇人乞寄载，奇初难之，然后上车，入亭，趋至楼下。亭卒白：“楼不可上。”奇云：“吾不恐也。”时亦昏冥，遂上楼，与妇人栖宿。未明，发去。亭卒上楼扫除，见一死妇，大惊，走白亭长。亭长击鼓，会诸庐吏，共集诊之。乃亭西北八里吴氏妇，新亡，夜临殡，火灭，及火至，失之。其家即持去。奇发，行数里，腹痛，到南顿利阳亭，加剧，物故。楼遂无敢复上。

    Explanation

    200

    During the Later Han period, in the western gatehouse of Ruyang, Ru'an, there were ghosts and spirits that haunted the place. Whenever guests stayed overnight, they would invariably die. Those who were afflicted by the haunting would lose their hair and suffer from a loss of vital energy. Upon investigating the cause, it was said: "Previously, there were already strange phenomena. Later, when the prefectural official, Zheng Qi of Yilu, arrived, about six or seven miles away from the gatehouse, a beautiful woman appeared and asked to be carried along. Qi initially hesitated but then got on the carriage, entered the gatehouse, and hurried downstairs. The inn attendant reported: 'The upper floor cannot be entered.' Qi replied: 'I am not afraid.' It was already evening, so he went upstairs and spent the night with the woman. Before dawn, he left. The inn attendant went upstairs to clean and saw a dead woman, greatly shocked, he ran to inform the head of the inn. The head of the inn beat the drum, gathered all the staff, and together examined the body. It turned out to be a woman from the Wu family, who had recently died, during the night of her funeral, the fire went out, and when it was relit, she was gone. Her family took her away. Qi left, walked several miles, suffered from abdominal pain, and arrived at the South Dun Liyang Inn, where the pain worsened, and he died. The upper floor of the gatehouse was no longer dared to be entered.

    颍川钟繇，字符常，尝数月不朝会，意性异常。或问其故。云：“常有好妇来，美丽非凡。”问者曰：“必是鬼物，可杀之。”妇人后往，不即前，止户外。繇问；“何以？”曰：“公有相杀意。”繇曰：“无此。”勤勤呼之，乃入。繇意恨，有不忍之，然犹●之。伤髀。妇人即出，以新绵拭血，竟路。明日，使人寻迹之，至一大冢，木中有好妇人，形体如生人，着白练衫，丹绣裲裆，伤左髀，以裲裆中绵拭血。

    201

    Yingchuan Zhong You, courtesy name Yuan Chang, once went several months without attending court meetings, and his mood and nature were abnormal. Someone asked him why. He said, "There is a beautiful woman who comes to visit me, and she is extraordinary." The questioner said, "It must be a ghostly being; it can be killed." The woman came again, but she did not immediately enter. She stopped at the door. Zhong You asked, "Why?" She said, "You have an intention to kill me." Zhong You said, "No, I do not." He repeatedly called for her, and she finally entered. Zhong You felt regret and was unwilling to harm her, but he still injured her. She was injured in the thigh. The woman then left and used the silk lining in her armor to wipe the blood. The next day, Zhong You sent someone to follow the trail, and they arrived at a large tomb. Inside the tomb, there was a beautiful woman, her body like a living person, wearing a white silk robe and a red embroidered armor. She was injured in the left thigh and used the silk lining in her armor to wipe the blood.

    搜神记卷十七
    　　陈国张汉直到南阳从京兆尹延叔坚学左氏传。行后，数月，鬼物持其妹，为之扬言曰：“我病死。丧在陌上，常苦饥寒。操二三量“不借，”挂屋后楮上。传子方送我五百钱，在北墉下，皆亡取之。又买李幼一头牛，本券在书箧中。”往索取之，悉如其言。妇尚不知有此妹，新从巩(革改耳)家来，非其所及。家人哀伤，益以为审。父母诸弟衰绖到来迎丧，去舍数里，遇汉直与诸生十余人相追。汉直顾见家人，怪其如此。家见汉直，谓其鬼也。怅惘良久。汉直乃前为父拜说其本末。且悲且喜。凡所闻见，若此非一。得知妖物之为。

    Explanation

    202

    Records of the Supernatural, Volume Seventeen

    In the state of Chen, there was a man named Zhang Hanzhi who traveled to Nanyang to study the Zuo Zhuan under the high-ranking official Yan Shujian. After he left, several months later, a spirit took his sister and spoke on her behalf, saying, "I died of illness. My body lies on the road, often suffering from hunger and cold. I have two or three items labeled 'not borrow,' hung on the paper behind the house. The man named Chuan Zifang sent me five hundred coins, which are buried under the north wall. All these things are true. Also, I bought a cow from Li You, and the original contract is in my book chest."

    When Zhang Hanzhi went to verify these claims, everything was exactly as the spirit had said. His wife did not know about this sister, as she had recently come from the village of Gou. The family was deeply saddened and became even more convinced of the spirit's authenticity. The parents and brothers, dressed in mourning attire, went to meet the supposed funeral procession. They traveled several miles and met Zhang Hanzhi and over ten students following behind. Zhang Hanzhi was surprised to see his family and wondered why they were there. The family saw Zhang Hanzhi and thought he was a ghost. They were filled with grief and confusion for a long time. Zhang Hanzhi then approached his father and explained the entire story. He said, "What I have heard and seen, such events are not isolated. We now know it was the work of an evil spirit."

    汉，陈留外黄范丹，字史云，少为尉，从佐使檄谒督邮，丹有志节，自恚为厮役小吏，乃于陈留大泽中，杀所乘马，捐弃官帻，诈逢劫者，有神下其家曰：“我史云也。为劫人所杀。疾取我衣于陈留大泽中。”家取得一帻。丹遂之南郡，转入三辅，从英贤游学十三年，乃归。家人不复识焉。陈留人高其志行，及没，号曰贞节先生。

    Explanation

    203

    Fan Dan of Waihuang, Chenliu, Han dynasty, courtesy name Shi Yun, served as an officer when young, following as an assistant to deliver official documents to the supervisor. Fan Dan had high moral standards and was self-blamed for being a low-ranking clerk. He then, in the great marsh of Chenliu, killed the horse he was riding, discarded his official hat, and pretended to encounter robbers. A spirit descended to his family and said, "I am Shi Yun. I was killed by robbers. Quickly take my clothes from the great marsh of Chenliu." His family obtained one hat. Fan Dan then went to Nanjun and turned to the three regions surrounding the capital, studying and traveling with outstanding scholars for thirteen years, then returned. His family no longer recognized him. People of Chenliu admired his virtue and conduct, and when he died, he was posthumously honored as Mr. of Chastity and Integrity.

    204

    吴人费季，久客于楚，时道多劫，妻常忧之。季与同辈旅宿庐山下，各相问出家几时。季曰：“吾去家已数年矣。临来，与妻别，就求金钗以行。欲观其志当与吾否耳。得钗，乃以着户楣上。临发，失与道，此钗故当在户上也。”尔夕，其妻梦季曰：“吾行遇盗，死，已二年。若不信吾言，吾行时，取汝钗，遂不以行，留在户楣上，可往取之。”妻觉，揣钗，得之家遂发丧。后一年余，季乃归还。
    　　余姚虞定国，有好仪容，同县苏氏女，亦有美色，定国常见悦之。后见定国来，主人留宿，中夜，告苏公曰：“贤女令色，意甚钦之。此夕能令暂出否？”主人以其乡里贵人，便令女出从之。往来渐数，语苏公云：“无以相报。若有官事，某为君任之。”主人喜，自尔后有役召事，往造定国。定国大惊曰：“都未尝面命。何由便尔？此必有异。”具说之。定国曰：“仆宁肯请人之父而淫人之女。若复见来，便当斫之。”后果得怪。

    Explanation

    204

    A Man from Wu named Fei Ji, who had been a long-term guest in Chu, often worried about his wife because the roads were frequently plagued by bandits. One day, Fei Ji and his companions stayed overnight at the foot of Mount Lu, where they asked each other how long they had been away from home. Fei Ji said, "I have been away from home for several years now. Before I left, I bid farewell to my wife and asked her to give me a gold hairpin for the journey. I wanted to see if her heart was as resolute as mine. After obtaining the hairpin, I placed it on the door lintel. Just before I left, I forgot to tell her about it. The hairpin should still be on the door lintel." That night, his wife dreamed that Fei Ji said, "I encountered bandits on my journey and died two years ago. If you do not believe me, remember that when I left, I took your hairpin but did not take it with me; it was left on the door lintel. You can go and retrieve it." The wife woke up, felt for the hairpin, found it, and the family then held a funeral. About a year later, Fei Ji returned.

    In Yuyao, there was a man named Yu Dingguo, who was known for his good appearance. In the same county, there was a woman from the Su family who was also very beautiful, and Yu Dingguo often admired her. One day, when Yu Dingguo came to visit, the owner of the house invited him to stay for the night. In the middle of the night, the owner told Su Gong, "Your beautiful daughter is very charming, and I have a strong desire for her. Could she come out for a moment tonight?" The owner, considering Yu Dingguo a respected figure in the community, allowed the daughter to meet him. As their meetings became more frequent, Yu Dingguo told Su Gong, "There is nothing I can do to repay you. If you have any official matters, I will take care of them for you." The owner was pleased and, from then on, whenever there were official duties or summons, he would send someone to Yu Dingguo. Yu Dingguo was greatly surprised and said, "I have never spoken to you face-to-face. How could you do this? There must be something unusual." He asked for a detailed explanation. Yu Dingguo replied, "I would never ask for the father of someone and then defile their daughter. If you come again, I will chop you down." Indeed, something strange happened afterward.

    205

    吴孙皓世，淮南内史朱诞，字永长，为建安太守。诞给使妻有鬼病，其夫疑之为奸；后出行，密穿壁隙窥之，正见妻在机中织，遥瞻桑树上，向之言笑。给使仰视树上，有一年少人，可十四五，衣青衿袖，青幧头。给使以为信人也，张弩射之，化为鸣蝉，其大如箕，翔然飞去。妻亦应声惊曰：“噫！人射汝。”给使怪其故。后久时，给使见二小儿在陌上共语曰：“何以不复见汝？”其一，即树上小儿也。答曰：“前不幸为人所射，病疮积时。”彼儿曰：“今何如？”曰：“赖朱府君梁上膏以傅之，得愈。”给使白诞曰：“人盗君膏药，颇知之否？”诞曰：“吾膏久致梁上，人安得盗之？”给使曰：“不然。府君视之。”诞殊不信，试为视之，封题如故。诞曰：“小人故妄言，膏自如故。”给使曰：“试开之。”则膏去半。为掊刮，见有趾迹。诞因大惊。乃详问之。具道本末。

    Explanation

    205

    During the reign of Sun Hao of Wu, Zhu Dan, the governor of Huainan, also known as Zhu Yongchang, served as the governor of Jian'an. Zhu Dan's attendant's wife was afflicted with a ghostly illness, and her husband suspected her of infidelity. After leaving on a trip, he secretly dug a hole in the wall to spy on her. He saw his wife weaving at the loom, while she gazed at a mulberry tree and spoke to someone on it. Looking up at the tree, he saw a young boy, about fourteen or fifteen years old, dressed in a blue collar and sleeves, and wearing a blue cap. Believing the boy to be real, the attendant drew his bow and shot at him. The boy transformed into a chirping cicada, as large as a winnowing basket, and flew away gracefully. The wife also exclaimed in surprise, saying, "Ah! Someone shot you." The attendant was puzzled by this. After some time, the attendant saw two children talking on the road, one of whom asked, "Why haven't you been seen again?" The other child, who was the boy from the tree, replied, "I was unfortunately shot by someone earlier and have been suffering from a wound for a long time." The other child asked, "How are you now?" The boy replied, "Thanks to the medicinal ointment on the beam provided by Governor Zhu, I have recovered." The attendant reported to Zhu Dan, saying, "Someone stole your medicinal ointment. Do you know about it?" Zhu Dan replied, "My ointment has been on the beam for a long time. How could someone steal it?" The attendant said, "That's not true. Please check it yourself, Governor." Zhu Dan did not believe him but decided to look. The seal was still intact. Zhu Dan said, "The servant is lying. The ointment is still the same." The attendant said, "Please open it and see." Upon opening it, they found that half of the ointment was gone. Upon scraping the container, they saw footprints. Zhu Dan was greatly shocked. He then asked the attendant in detail, and the attendant fully explained the beginning and end of the incident.

    206

    吴时，嘉兴倪彦思居县西埏里，忽见鬼魅入其家，与人语，饮食如人，惟不见形彦思奴婢有窃骂大家者。云：“今当以语。”彦思治之，无敢詈之者。彦思有小妻，魅从求之，彦思乃迎道士逐之。酒殽既设，魅乃取厕中草粪，布着其上。道士便盛击鼓，召请诸神。魅乃取伏虎于神座上吹作角声音。有顷。道士忽觉背上冷，惊起解衣，乃伏虎也。于是道士罢去。彦思夜于被中窃与妪语，共患此魅。魅即屋梁上谓彦思曰：“汝与妇道吾，吾今当截汝屋梁。”即隆隆有声。彦思惧梁断，取火照视，魅即灭火。截梁声愈急。彦思惧屋坏，大小悉遣出，更取火视，梁如故。魅大笑，问彦思：“复道吾否？”郡中典农闻之曰：“此神正当是狸物耳。”魅即往谓典农曰：“汝取官若干百斛谷，藏着某处，为吏污秽，而敢论吾！今当白于官，将人取汝所盗谷。”典农大怖而谢之。自后无敢道者。三年后，去，不知所在。

    Explanation

    206

    During the Wu period, Ni Yansi of Jiaxing lived in Xishan Village to the west of the county. Suddenly, a ghostly apparition entered his home, speaking with people and eating and drinking like a human, but could not be seen. Some of his servants and maids secretly cursed their master, and the ghost said, "I will now tell him." Ni Yansi punished them, and no one dared to curse him again. Ni Yansi had a concubine, and the ghost sought to take her. Ni Yansi then invited a Taoist priest to drive it away. When the wine and food were set out, the ghost took a tiger and placed it on the altar, blowing a horn-like sound. After a while, the Taoist priest suddenly felt cold on his back, jumped up, and removed his clothes, only to find a tiger there. The Taoist priest then left. At night, Ni Yansi secretly spoke with his wife under the covers, and they both suffered from this ghost. The ghost, perched on the roof beam, told Ni Yansi, "You and your wife talk about me, and I will now cut your roof beam." There was a loud noise. Ni Yansi feared the beam would break and lit a fire to look, but the ghost extinguished the fire. The sound of cutting the beam became more urgent. Ni Yansi feared the house would collapse and sent everyone out, then relit the fire to check, and the beam remained unchanged. The ghost laughed and asked Ni Yansi, "Are you still talking about me?" The local agricultural official heard about this and said, "This spirit is just a fox." The ghost then went to the official and said, "You took several hundred bushels of grain from the government and hid it somewhere, tainted by officials, and dared to speak about me! I will now report you to the authorities and have your stolen grain taken." The official was greatly frightened and apologized. After this, no one dared to speak about the ghost. Three years later, the ghost left, and no one knew where it went.

    207

    魏，黄初中，顿邱界，有人骑马夜行，见道中有一物，大如兔，两眼如镜，跳跃马前，令不得前。人遂惊惧，堕马。魅便就地捉之。惊怖，暴死。良久得苏。苏，已失魅，不知所在。乃更上马前行。数里，逢一人，相问讯已，因说向者事变如此，今相得为伴，甚欢。人曰：“我独行，得君为伴，快不可言。君马行疾，且前，我在后相随也。”遂共行。语曰：“向者物何如，乃令君怖惧耶？”对曰：“其身如兔，两眼如镜，形甚可恶。”伴曰：“试顾视我耶？”人顾视之，犹复是也。魅便跳上马。人遂坠地，怖死。家人怪马独归，即行推索，乃于道边得之。宿昔乃苏，说状如是。

    Explanation

    207

    During the Huangchu era of the Wei dynasty, in the vicinity of Duntu, there was a man who was riding at night. He saw something on the road ahead that was as large as a rabbit, with eyes like mirrors, and it leaped in front of his horse, preventing him from proceeding. The man became terrified and fell off his horse. The spirit then seized him on the ground. Filled with fear, he died suddenly. After a long time, he regained consciousness. Upon waking, he had lost the spirit and did not know where it had gone. He then remounted his horse and continued his journey. After traveling several miles, he met another person. They exchanged greetings, and the man told him about the strange encounter. He was very pleased to have found a companion. The man said, "I was traveling alone, and now I have you as a companion, which is wonderful. Your horse moves quickly, so please go ahead, and I will follow behind." They continued their journey together. The companion asked, "What was that creature like, which made you so frightened?" The man replied, "It had a body like a rabbit, with eyes like mirrors, and its appearance was very ugly." The companion said, "Try looking at me." The man looked at him, and it was still the same. The spirit then leaped onto the horse. The man fell to the ground and died from fear. His family was surprised to find the horse returning alone and immediately went to search for him. They found him by the roadside. After a night, he woke up and recounted the events as described.

    208

    袁绍，字本初，在冀州，有神出河东，号度朔君，百姓共为立庙。庙有主簿大福。陈留蔡庸为清河太守，过谒庙，有子，名道，亡已三十年，度朔君为庸设酒曰：“贵子昔来，欲相见。”须臾子来。度朔君自云：“父祖昔作兖州，”有一士，姓苏，母病，往祷。主簿云：“君逢天士留待。”闻西北有鼓声，而君至。须臾，一客来，着皂角单衣，头上五色毛，长数寸。去后，复一人，着白布单衣，高冠，冠似鱼头，谓君曰：“昔临庐山，共食白李，忆之未久，已三千岁。日月易得，使人怅然。”去后，君谓士曰：“先来，南海君也。”士是书生，君明通五经，善礼记，与士论礼，士不如也。士乞救母病。

    Explanation

    208

    Yuan Shao, courtesy name Benchu, was in Jizhou when a deity emerged from Hedong, known as Lord Duosuo. The common people collectively built a temple for him. The temple had an official named Dafu, who brought great fortune. Chenliu's Cai Yong, serving as the governor of Qinghe, visited the temple. Cai Yong had a son named Dao, who had been dead for thirty years. Lord Duosuo set up wine for Cai Yong and said, "Your esteemed son came in the past and wants to meet you." Soon after, the son appeared. Lord Duosuo introduced himself, saying, "My ancestors were once in Yanzhou," and mentioned a scholar named Su whose mother was ill and had come to pray. The official said, "The lord will stay and wait for a celestial scholar." They heard drum sounds from the northwest, and the lord arrived. Soon, a guest appeared, wearing a dark-colored single robe, with five-colored hair on his head, several inches long. After he left, another person came, wearing a white cloth single robe, with a tall hat resembling a fish head, and said to the lord, "We once visited Mount Lushan together and ate white plums. Remembering it not long ago, it has already been three thousand years. Time passes easily, making people feel melancholic." After he left, the lord told the scholar, "The first one to arrive was the Lord of the South Sea." The scholar was a student of books, and the lord was well-versed in the Five Classics, skilled in the Liji. They discussed rites, but the scholar could not match the lord. The scholar asked for help to save his mother's illness.

    209

    君曰：“卿所居东，有故桥，人坏之，此桥所行，卿母犯之，能复桥，便差。”曹公讨袁谭，使人从庙换千疋绢，君不与。曹公遣张合毁庙。未至百里，君遣兵数万，方道而来。合未达二里，云雾绕合军，不知庙处。君语主簿：“曹公气盛，宜避之。”后苏井邻家有神下，识君声，云：“昔移入湖，阔绝三年，乃遣人与曹公相闻，欲修故庙，地衰，不中居，欲寄住。”公曰：“甚善。”治城北楼以居之。数日，曹公猎得物，大如麑，大足，色白如雪，毛软滑可爱。公以摩面，莫能名也。夜闻楼上哭云：“小儿出行不还。”公拊掌曰：“此子言真衰也。”晨将数百犬，绕楼下，犬得气，冲突内外。见有物，大如驴，自投楼下。犬杀之。庙神乃绝。

    209

    The ruler said, "In the east where you reside, there is an old bridge that has been destroyed by people. The path this bridge spans was transgressed by your mother. If you can restore the bridge, then the matter will be resolved." General Cao attacked Yuan Tan and sent someone from the temple to exchange a thousand bolts of silk, but you did not give it. General Cao then sent Zhang He to destroy the temple. Before reaching one hundred li, you sent tens of thousands of troops, coming straight along the path. Zhang He had not reached two li when clouds and mist surrounded his army, and they did not know the location of the temple. You told the chief clerk, "General Cao's momentum is strong; it is advisable to avoid it." Later, a god descended at Su Jing's neighbor's house and recognized your voice, saying, "In the past, we moved into the lake and were absent for three years. Then we sent someone to inform General Cao, wanting to repair the old temple. The land is barren and not suitable for living, so we wanted to temporarily reside." General Cao said, "Very good." He built a tower in the north of the city to house the god. Several days later, General Cao hunted and obtained an object as large as a young deer, with large feet, white as snow, and soft, smooth fur that was lovable. He used it to rub his face, but no one could name it. That night, he heard crying on the tower, saying, "The little boy went out and did not return." General Cao clapped his hands and said, "This child's words are truly pitiful." In the morning, he led hundreds of dogs, surrounding the base of the tower. The dogs sensed the energy and charged inside and outside. They saw an object as large as a donkey, which jumped down from the base of the tower. The dogs killed it, and the temple god then ceased.

    210

    临川陈臣家大富，永初元年，臣在斋中坐，其宅内有一町筋竹，白日忽见一人，长丈余，面如“方相，”从竹中出。径语陈臣：“我在家多年，汝不知；今辞汝去，当令汝知之。”去一月许日，家大失火，奴婢顿死。一年中，便大贫。

    Explanation

    210

    In the first year of the Yongchu era, Chen Chen, a wealthy man from Linchuan, was sitting in his study when he saw a person emerge from a plot of bamboo in his courtyard. The person was over ten feet tall and had a face like "Fang Xiang," a fearsome mythical creature. The figure directly spoke to Chen Chen, saying, "I have been in your house for many years, but you did not know. Now I am leaving, and you will know." About a month later, the house caught fire, and the slaves died suddenly. Within a year, Chen Chen became very poor.

    211

    东莱有一家姓陈，家百余口，朝炊釜，不沸。举甑看之，忽有一白头公，从釜中出。便诣师卜。卜云：“此大怪，应灭门。便归，大作械，械成，使置门壁下，坚闭门，在内，有马骑麾盖来扣门者，慎勿应。”乃归，合手伐得百余械，置门屋下。果有人至，呼。不应。主帅大怒，令缘门入，从人窥门内，见大小械百余，出门还说如此。帅大惶惋，语左右云：“教速来，不速来，遂无一人当去，何以解罪也？从此北行可八十里，有一百三口，取以当之。”后十日，此家死亡都尽。此家亦姓陈云。
    　　晋惠帝永康元年，京师得异鸟，莫能名。赵王伦使人持出，周旋城邑市，以问人。即日，宫西有一小儿见之，遂自言曰：“服留鸟。”持者还白伦。伦使更求，又见之。乃将入宫。密笼鸟，幷闭小儿于户中。明日往视：悉不复见。

    Explanation

    211

    In the region of Donglai, there was a family named Chen, with over a hundred members. One morning, as they heated water in a pot, it did not boil. Lifting the steamer to look at it, they suddenly saw an elderly man emerge from the pot. They went to a fortune-teller to seek advice. The fortune-teller said, "This is a great omen, and your family will be wiped out. Return home and make many weapons. Once made, place them under the door and seal it tightly. Inside, if anyone with a horse and a banner comes to knock on the door, do not answer." They returned home and made over a hundred weapons, placing them under the door. Indeed, someone came and called out, but they did not respond. The leader became furious and ordered his men to enter through the door. His men peered inside and saw over a hundred weapons, then reported back to him. The leader was greatly distressed and told his subordinates, "If you do not act quickly, no one will be left, and how can we atone for this? Travel eighty li north and find a family of 130 people to sacrifice to appease the spirits." Ten days later, the entire family was wiped out. This family also happened to be named Chen.

    During the reign of Emperor Huai of Jin in the year Yongkang, an unusual bird was found in the capital city, but no one could identify it. Sima Lun, the regent, had the bird shown around the city to seek identification. That same day, a child in the western part of the palace saw the bird and said, "It is a 'fúliú niǎo' (服留鸟)." The person who brought the bird returned to inform Sima Lun. Sima Lun then had the bird brought back and placed in a secret cage, along with the child, inside a closed room. The next day, when they went to check, the bird and the child were nowhere to be found.

    212

    南康郡南东望山，有三人入山，见山顶有果树，众果毕植，行列整齐如人行，甘子正熟。三人共食，致饱，乃怀二枚，欲出示人。闻空中语云：“催放双甘，乃听汝去。”
    　　秦瞻，居曲阿彭皇野，忽有物如蛇，突入其脑中。蛇来，先闻臭气，便于鼻中入，盘其头中。觉哄哄。仅闻其脑闲食声咂咂。数日而出。去，寻复来。取手巾缚鼻口，亦被入。积年无他病，唯患头重。
    搜神记卷十八
    　　魏，景初中，咸阳县吏家有怪。每夜无故闻拍手相呼。伺，无所见。其母，夜作，倦，就枕寝息；有顷，复闻灶下有呼声曰：“文约何以不来？”头下枕应曰：“我见枕，不能往。汝可来就我饮。”至明，乃(食卞)臿也。即聚烧之。其怪遂绝。

    Explanation

    212

    In the south of Nankang County, there is a mountain to the east that can be seen from afar. Three people entered the mountain and saw a grove of fruit trees on the summit, with all kinds of fruits planted in neat rows, resembling human formations, and sweet fruits ripening. The three people ate together until they were full, then each took two fruits to show others. They heard a voice from the sky saying, "Release two fruits, and then you may leave."

    Qin Zhan, who lived in Qu'a Penghuang Field, suddenly experienced something snake-like entering his brain. The snake came, first smelling a foul odor, then entering through the nose, coiling in the head. He felt a loud noise and heard the sound of eating inside the head. After several days, the snake left. It went away, but soon returned. Qin Zhan tied a handkerchief over his nose and mouth, but the snake still entered. For many years, he had no other illnesses, only suffering from a heavy head.

    During the Jingzhong period of the Wei Dynasty, a strange occurrence happened in the household of an official in Xianyang County. Every night, they heard clapping and calling without reason. They tried to observe it, but saw nothing. The mother, tired from working at night, fell asleep. Soon after, she heard someone calling from under the stove, asking, "Why hasn't Wenyue come?" Her head responded, "I see the pillow, I can't go. You can come to drink with me." The next morning, it turned out to be a (食卞)臿 (a type of pest), which was then burned, and the strange phenomenon ceased.

    213

    魏郡张奋者，家本巨富，忽衰老，财散，遂卖宅与程应。应入居，举家病疾，转卖邻人阿文。文先独持大刀，暮入北堂中梁上，至三更竟，忽有一人长丈余，高冠，黄衣，升堂，呼曰：“细腰！”细腰应诺。曰：“舍中何以有生人气也？”答曰：“无之。”便去。须臾，有一高冠，青衣者。次之，又有高冠，白衣者。问答并如前。及将曙，文乃下堂中，如向法呼之，问曰：“黄衣者为谁？”曰：“金也。在堂西壁下。”“青衣者为谁？”曰：“钱也。在堂前井边五步。”“白衣者为谁？”曰：“银也。在墙东北角柱下。”“汝复为谁？”曰：“我，杵也。今在灶下。”及晓，文按次掘之：得金银五百斤，钱千万贯。仍取杵焚之。由此大富。宅遂清宁。

    Explanation

    213

    In the Wei Commandery, there was a man named Zhang Fen, whose family was originally very wealthy. Suddenly, the family became old, and their wealth dissipated. Thus, they sold their house to Cheng Ying. Cheng Ying moved in, but the whole family fell ill. As a result, they sold the house to a neighbor named A Wen. A Wen first held a large knife alone and entered the beams of the north hall at dusk, staying until the third watch of the night. Suddenly, there was a person over ten feet tall, wearing a tall hat and yellow clothing, who ascended the hall and called out, "Fine waist!" Fine waist responded affirmatively. The tall figure asked, "How can there be living human breath in the house?" A Wen replied, "There isn't." The figure then left. A short while later, another figure appeared, wearing a tall hat and blue clothing. Soon after, yet another figure appeared, wearing a tall hat and white clothing. The questions and answers were the same as before. As dawn approached, A Wen descended to the hall and called out to them as he had before, asking, "Who is the one in yellow clothing?" The figure replied, "It is gold. It is under the west wall of the hall." A Wen then asked, "Who is the one in blue clothing?" The figure replied, "It is money. It is five steps from the well in front of the hall." A Wen then asked, "Who is the one in white clothing?" The figure replied, "It is silver. It is under the northeast corner pillar of the wall." A Wen then asked, "Who are you?" The figure replied, "I am a pestle. I am now under the stove." By morning, A Wen dug in sequence and found five hundred catties of gold and silver, and ten thousand strings of cash. He then took the pestle and burned it. Thus, he became very wealthy. The house then became peaceful.

    214

    秦时，武都故道，有怒特祠，祠上生梓树，秦文公二十七年，使人伐之，辄有大风雨，树创随合，经日不断。文公乃益发卒，持斧者至四十人，犹不断。士疲，还息；其一人伤足，不能行，卧树下，闻鬼语树神曰：“劳乎？攻战！”其一人曰：“何足为劳。”又曰：“秦公将必不休，如之何？”答曰：“秦公其如予何。”又曰：“秦若使三百人，被发，以朱丝绕树，赭衣，灰坌伐汝，汝得不困耶？”神寂无言。明日，病人语所闻。公于是令人皆衣赭，随斫创，坌以灰，树断。中有一青牛出，走入丰水中。其后，青牛出丰水中，使骑击之，不胜；有骑堕地，复上，髻解，被发，牛畏之，乃入水，不敢出。故秦自是置“旄头骑。”

    Explanation

    214

    During the Qin dynasty, on the ancient road of Wudu, there was a temple dedicated to a fierce bull deity. On the temple grounds, a paulownia tree grew. In the twenty-seventh year of Duke Wen of Qin's reign, people were sent to cut down the tree, but there were always strong winds and heavy rain. The wounds on the tree would heal immediately, and it could not be cut down for days. Duke Wen then sent more soldiers, forty with axes, but still, the tree could not be cut down. The soldiers were tired and rested. One person was injured and could not walk, so he lay under the tree and heard the ghosts speaking to the tree spirit: "Tired? Fighting!" One person said, "What is there to be tired about?" Another asked, "Duke Qin will not stop. What can be done?" The tree spirit replied, "What can Duke Qin do to me?" Then, the ghost said, "If Duke Qin sends three hundred people, with their hair loose, tying red silk around the tree, wearing ochre clothes, and covering it with ash to cut it down, will you not be in trouble?" The spirit remained silent. The next day, the injured person told what he had heard. Duke Wen then ordered everyone to wear ochre clothes, cut at the wounds, and cover them with ash. The tree was cut down. A green ox emerged from the center of the tree and ran into the Feng River. Later, the green ox emerged from the Feng River, and the riders tried to attack it but failed. One rider fell off, got back on, his hair loose, and the ox feared him, so it went back into the water and did not come out. Therefore, Qin established the 'Máo Tóu Jì' (a type of cavalry unit).

    215

    庐江龙舒县陆亭流水边，有一大树，高数十丈，常有黄鸟数千枚巢其上，时久旱，长老共相谓曰：“彼树常有黄气，或有神灵，可以祈雨。”因以酒脯往亭中。有寡妇李宪者，夜起，室中忽见一妇人，着绣衣，自称曰：“我，树神黄祖也。能兴云雨，以汝性洁，佐汝为生。朝来父老皆欲祈雨，吾已求之于帝，明日日中，大雨。”至期，果雨。遂为立祠。宪曰：“诸卿在此，吾居近水，当致少鲤鱼。”言讫，有鲤鱼数十头，飞集堂下，坐者莫不惊悚。如此岁余，神曰：“将有大兵，今辞汝去。”留一玉环曰：“持此可以避难。”后刘表、袁术相攻，龙舒之民皆徙去，唯宪里不被兵。

    Explanation

    215

    In the Longshu County of Lujiang, near a watercourse by the Lu Pavilion, there was a large tree that stood several dozen zhang tall. It was home to thousands of yellow birds, and it was often said that the tree emitted a yellow aura, indicating the presence of a divine spirit. The elders of the village, believing that the tree had supernatural powers, decided to pray for rain. They brought wine and sacrificial offerings to the pavilion.

    One night, a widow named Ruan Xian saw a woman dressed in embroidered clothing appear in her room. The woman introduced herself as Huang Zu, the spirit of the tree, and said, "I can summon clouds and rain. Because of your pure nature, I will assist you in your livelihood. The elders of the village are going to pray for rain, and I have already asked the heavens. There will be heavy rain tomorrow at noon." As promised, it rained the following day, and the villagers built a shrine in gratitude.

    Huang Zu then said to Ruan Xian, "All of you here, I live near the water. I will bring some carp." After these words, dozens of carp flew to the courtyard, and those present were astonished. This continued for over a year, until Huang Zu said, "There will be a great war soon, and I must leave you now." She left behind a jade ring and said, "Hold onto this to protect yourself from harm."

    Later, Liu Biao and Yuan Shu engaged in a conflict, and the people of Longshu fled. However, only Ruan Xian's village remained unscathed by the war.

    216

    魏，桂阳太守江夏张辽，字叔高，去鄢陵，家居，买田，田中有大树，十余围，枝叶扶疏，盖地数亩，不生谷。遣客伐之。斧数下，有赤汁六七斗出，客惊怖，归白叔高。叔高大怒曰：“树老汁赤，如何得怪？”因自严行复斫之。血大流洒。叔高使先斫其枝，上有一空处，见白头公，可长四五尺，突出，往赴叔高。高以刀逆格之，如此，凡杀四五头，并死。左右皆惊怖伏地。叔高神虑怡然如旧。徐熟视，非人，非兽。遂伐其木。此所谓木石之怪夔魍魉者乎？是岁应司空辟侍御史兖州刺史以二千石之尊，过乡里，荐祝祖考，白日绣衣荣羡，竟无他怪。

    Explanation

    216

    During the state of Wei, Jiangxia Zhang Liao, the governor of Guiyang, known by his courtesy name Shugao, left for Yanling, lived at home, and bought land. There was a large tree in the field, more than ten cun in circumference, with branches and leaves spread out, covering several acres, but no grain grew. He sent a guest to cut it down. After several strikes with the axe, red juice, six or seven dou, came out. The guest was terrified and returned to tell Shugao. Shugao became very angry and said, "The tree is old and the juice is red; how could it be strange?" Then he personally went and cut it down again. Blood flowed and splattered. Shugao ordered to first cut its branches. There was a hollow on top, and he saw a white-haired old man, about four or five chi long, pop out and rush towards Shugao. Shugao countered with his knife, like this, killing four or five heads, all of which died. Those around him were all terrified and fell to the ground. Shugao's spirit remained calm and unchanged. He looked carefully and saw that it was neither human nor animal. Then he cut down the tree. Is this what is called the wood and stone monster, the kui and wangling? That year, he was appointed as a censor, governor of Yan state, and held the rank of two thousand stones. Passing through his hometown, he offered sacrifices to his ancestors, dressed in embroidered clothes in broad daylight, admired by all, there were no other strange occurrences.

    217

    吴先主时，陆敬叔为建安太守，使人伐大樟树，下数斧，忽有血出，树断，有物，人面，狗身，从树中出。敬叔曰：“此名‘彭侯。’”乃烹食之。其味如狗。白泽图曰：“木之精名‘彭侯，’状如黑狗，无尾，可烹食之。”
    　　吴时。有梓树，巨围，叶广丈余，垂柯数亩；吴王伐树作船，使童男女三十人牵挽之，船自飞下水，男女皆溺死。至今潭中时有唱唤督进之音也。
    　　董仲舒下帷讲诵，有客来诣，舒知其非常客。又云：“欲雨。”舒戏之曰：“巢居知风，穴居知雨。卿非狐狸，则是鼷鼠。”客遂化为老狸。

    Explanation

    217

    During the reign of Wu's first ruler, Lu Jingshu served as the Governor of Jian'an. He ordered the cutting down of a large camphor tree, and after several blows, suddenly blood flowed out. The tree split open, and a creature emerged with a human face and a dog's body. Lu Jingshu said, "This is called 'Peng Hou.'" He then cooked and ate it, and its taste was like that of a dog. The Baize Tu (Book of White Tiger) states, "The spirit of a tree is called 'Peng Hou,' it looks like a black dog without a tail, and can be cooked and eaten."

    During the Wu period, there was a paulownia tree with a huge circumference and leaves over ten feet wide, with branches spreading over several acres. Wu Wang cut down the tree to make a boat and had thirty young men and women pull it. The boat magically flew into the water, and the young men and women all drowned. Even now, the sound of singing and urging can be heard in the pond.

    Dong Zhongshu was studying with a curtain drawn when a visitor came to see him. He knew the visitor was not an ordinary person. The visitor also mentioned that it was about to rain. Dong Zhongshu teased him, saying, "Those who live in nests know the wind, and those who live in burrows know the rain. You are either a fox or a mouse." The visitor then transformed into an old fox.

    218

    张华，字茂先，晋惠帝时为司空，于时燕昭王墓前，有一斑狐，积年，能为变幻，乃变作一书生，欲诣张公。过问墓前华表曰：“以我才貌，可得见张司空否？”华表曰：“子之妙解，无为不可。但张公智度，恐难笼络。出必遇辱，殆不得返。非但丧子千岁之质，亦当深误老表。”狐不从，乃持刺谒华。华见其总角风流，洁白如玉，举动容止，顾盼生姿，雅重之。于是论及文章，辨校声实，华未尝闻。比复商略三史，探颐百家，谈老、庄之奥区，披风、雅之绝旨，包十圣，贯三才，箴八儒，擿五礼，华无不应声屈滞。乃叹曰：“天下岂有此少年！若非鬼魅则是狐狸。”乃扫榻延留，留人防护。此生乃曰：“明公当尊贤容众，嘉善而矜不能，奈何憎人学问？墨子兼爱，其若是耶？”言卒，便求退。华已使人防门，不得出。既而又谓华曰：“公门置甲兵栏骑，当是致疑于仆也。

    Explanation

    218

    Zhang Hua, courtesy name Maoxian, served as Chancellor during the reign of Emperor Huai of Jin. At that time, there was a spotted fox near the tomb of Yan Zhao Wang, which had lived there for many years and possessed the ability to transform. It changed into a scholar and wished to visit Zhang Hua. Passing by the stone tablet at the tomb, it asked, "With my talents and appearance, can I meet Chancellor Zhang?" The stone tablet replied, "Your profound understanding is such that nothing is impossible. However, Chancellor Zhang's wisdom and strategy may be difficult to outsmart. If you leave, you will likely suffer humiliation and may not return. Not only will you lose your long-lived nature, but you will also deeply mislead the old stone tablet." The fox did not heed the warning and instead held a visiting card to meet Zhang Hua. Zhang Hua saw the fox with a refined and elegant appearance, as pure as jade, with graceful movements and a charming presence, and held him in high regard. They then discussed literature, distinguishing and comparing appearances and realities, which Zhang Hua had never encountered before. They further explored the Three Histories, delved into the depths of all schools of thought, discussed the profound aspects of Laozi and Zhuangzi, uncovered the ultimate meanings of the Feng (Odes) and Ya (Elegance) sections of the Shijing (Book of Poetry), encompassed the wisdom of ten sages, connected the three talents, advised eight Confucian scholars, and analyzed the five rites. Zhang Hua was unable to respond without hesitation. He exclaimed, "How can there be such a young man in the world! If he is not a ghost or a spirit, then he must be a fox." Zhang Hua then swept the mat to invite the fox to stay and arranged for guards to protect him. The fox said, "Your Excellency should respect the wise and accommodate the many, commend the good and pity the incapable. Why do you hate learning? Mozi's philosophy of universal love, is that not the case?" After finishing his words, the fox requested to leave. Zhang Hua had already arranged for guards to watch the gate, so the fox could not go out. The fox then said to Zhang Hua, "Your gate is guarded by armed soldiers and cavalry, which must be to doubt and mistrust me."

    219

    将恐天下之人卷舌而不言，智谋之士望门而不进。深为明公惜之。”华不应，而使人防御甚严。时丰城令雷焕，字孔章，博物士也，来访华；华以书生白之。孔章曰：“若疑之，何不呼猎犬试之？”乃命犬以试，竟无惮色。狐曰：“我天生才智，反以为妖，以犬试我，遮莫千试，万虑，其能为患乎？”华闻，益怒曰：“此必真妖也。闻魑魅忌狗，所别者数百年物耳，千年老精，不能复别；惟得千年枯木照之，则形立见。”孔章曰：“千年神木，何由可得？”华曰：“世传燕昭王墓前华表木已经千年。”乃遣人伐华表，使人欲至木所，母空中有一青衣小儿来，问使曰：“君何来也？”使曰：“张司空有一少年来谒，多才，巧辞，疑是妖魅；使我取华表照之。”青衣曰：“老狐不智，不听我言，今日祸已及我，其可逃乎！”乃发声而泣，倏然不见。使乃伐其木，血深；便将木归，燃之以照书生，乃一斑狐。华曰：“此二物不值我，千年不可复得。”乃烹之。

    Explanation

    219

    Zhang Huan, the Vice Minister, had a guest who was a young man, exceptionally talented and eloquent. Zhang suspected he might be an evil spirit and ordered his guards to watch the young man closely. At the time, Feicheng County Magistrate Lei Huan, whose courtesy name was Kongzhang, was a learned scholar. He visited Zhang and told him about the guest. Kongzhang said, "If you doubt him, why not try a hunting dog on him?" Zhang then ordered the dog to test the young man, but the young man showed no fear. The fox said, "I was born with natural talent and intelligence, but it is mistakenly regarded as evil. You are using a dog to test me. Even if you try me a thousand times, with a myriad of considerations, how could I possibly cause harm?" Zhang heard this and became even angrier, saying, "This must indeed be a true evil spirit. I have heard that spirits and monsters fear dogs. They can only distinguish those that are several hundred years old. A thousand-year-old spirit cannot be distinguished. Only a thousand-year-old dry wood can reveal its form." Kongzhang asked, "How can one obtain a thousand-year-old tree?" Zhang replied, "It is said that the tablet in front of Yan Zhao Wang's tomb has already existed for a thousand years." He then sent someone to cut down the tablet. As the messenger was about to reach the tree, a little green-clad child appeared in the air and asked the messenger, "Where are you going?" The messenger said, "Zhang Huan has a young man who came to pay respects. He is very talented and eloquent, but Zhang suspects he is an evil spirit. He sent me to get the tablet to test him." The green-clad child said, "The old fox is not wise enough to listen to my advice. Now the disaster has already befallen me, and there is no way to escape!" He then cried out and suddenly disappeared. The messenger then cut down the tree, which was stained with blood. The messenger brought the tree back and burned it to illuminate the young man, revealing him to be a spotted fox. Zhang said, "These two beings would not have been caught if they had not encountered me. They are rare and valuable, and will not be found again in a thousand years." He then cooked and consumed them.

    220

    晋时，吴兴一人有二男，田中作，时尝见父来骂詈赶打之。童以告母。母问其父。父大惊，知是鬼魅。便令儿斫之。鬼便寂不复往。父忧，恐儿为鬼所困，便自往看。儿谓是鬼，便杀而埋之。鬼便遂归，作其父形，且语其家，二儿已杀妖矣。儿暮归，共相庆贸，积年不觉。后有一法师过其家，语二儿云：“君尊侯有大邪气。”儿以白父，父大怒。儿出以语师，令速去。师遂作声入，父即成大老狸，入床下，遂擒杀之。向所杀者，乃真父也。改殡治服。一儿遂自杀，一儿忿懊，亦死。
    　　句容县麋村民黄审，于田中耕，有一妇人过其田，自塍上度，从东适下而复还。审初谓是人。日日如此，意甚怪之。审因问曰：“妇数从何来也？”妇人少住，但笑而不言，便去。审愈疑之。预以长镰伺其还，未敢斫妇，但斫所随婢。妇化为狸，走去。视婢。乃狸尾耳。审追之，不及。后人有见此狸出坑头，掘之，无复尾焉。

    Explanation

    220

    During the Jin Dynasty, in Wu County, there was a man who had two sons. They were working in the fields when they often saw their father come to scold and beat them. The children reported this to their mother. The mother asked the father about it. The father was greatly surprised and realized it was a ghost or demon. He then ordered his sons to cut it down. The ghost became silent and stopped coming. The father, worried that his sons would be trapped by the ghost, went to check himself. The sons thought it was a ghost and killed and buried it. The ghost then returned, taking the form of the father, and told their family that the two sons had already killed the demon. The sons returned home in the evening, celebrating together, and did not realize the truth for many years. Later, a monk passed by their house and told the two sons, "Your honorable lord has a great evil aura." The sons reported this to their father, who became very angry. The sons told the monk and ordered him to leave quickly. The monk made a sound and entered, and the father turned into a large old fox, going under the bed, where he was captured and killed. The one they killed earlier was actually their real father. They changed the burial and mourning attire. One son committed suicide, and the other, filled with anger and regret, also died.

    In Milu Village, Jurong County, there was a villager named Huang Shen who was farming in the fields. One day, a woman passed through his field, crossing the ridge from east to west and back again. Huang Shen initially thought she was a person. Every day, she would do the same, and he found it very strange. He asked her, "Where do you come from so often?" The woman stopped briefly, just smiled, and then left. Huang Shen became even more suspicious. He prepared a long sickle to wait for her return, but he did not dare to attack the woman; instead, he attacked the servant girl following her. The woman transformed into a fox and ran away. When he looked at the servant girl, she had only a fox's tail. Huang Shen tried to chase her but could not catch her. Later, someone saw the fox come out of a pit and dug it up, finding no tail left.

    221

    博陵刘伯祖为河东太守，所止承尘上有神，能语，常呼伯祖与语，及京师诏书诰下消息，辄预告伯祖。伯祖问其所食啖。欲得羊肝。乃买羊肝于前，切之脔，随刀不见。尽两羊肝。忽有一老狸，眇眇在案前，持刀者欲举刀斫之，伯祖呵止，自着承尘上。须臾大笑曰：“向者啖羊肝，醉，忽失形与府君相见。大惭愧。”后伯祖当为司隶，神复先语伯祖曰：“某月某日，诏书当到。”至期，如言。及入司隶府，神随遂在承尘上，辄言省内事。伯祖大恐怖。谓神曰：“今职在刺举，若左右贵人闻神在此，因以相害。”神答曰：“诚如府君所虑。当相舍去。”遂即无声。

    Explanation

    221

    Liu Bozhu of Boling served as the governor of Hedong. While staying there, a spirit on the ceiling could speak and often called out to Liu Bozhu to talk. Whenever news of imperial edicts or messages from the capital came, the spirit would foretell Liu Bozhu. Liu Bozhu asked what it ate, and it replied that it wanted sheep liver. He then bought sheep liver and cut it into pieces, which disappeared as he cut them. All the sheep liver was consumed. Suddenly, an old cat appeared, mewing in front of the table. The person holding the knife wanted to chop it, but Liu Bozhu stopped him, and the cat climbed onto the ceiling. After a moment, it laughed and said, "Just now, I ate the sheep liver, got drunk, and accidentally revealed my true form to you. I am very embarrassed." Later, when Liu Bozhu was to become the Governor of Sili, the spirit again told him, "On a certain day in a certain month, the imperial edict will arrive." On the appointed day, it came as predicted. When he entered the Sili office, the spirit followed and often spoke about matters inside the office. Liu Bozhu was greatly terrified and told the spirit, "Now that I am in charge of investigating and reporting, if the powerful people hear that the spirit is here, they might harm me." The spirit replied, "Indeed, as you have feared. I will leave you." And then it was silent.

    222

    后汉建安中，沛国郡陈羡为西海都尉，其部曲王灵孝无故逃去。羡欲杀之。居无何，孝复逃走。羡久不见，囚其妇，妇以实对。羡曰：“是必魅将去，当求之。”因将步骑数十，领猎犬，周旋于城外求索。果见孝于空冢中。闻人犬声，怪遂避去。羡使人扶孝以归，其形颇象狐矣。略不复与人相应，但啼呼“阿紫。”阿紫，狐字也。后十余日，乃稍稍了悟。云：“狐始来时，于屋曲角鸡栖间，作好妇形，自称阿紫，招我。如此非一。忽然便随去，即为妻，暮辄与共还其家。遇狗不觉云。乐无比也。”道士云：“此山魅也。”名山记曰：“狐者，先古之淫妇也，其名曰阿紫化而为狐。”故其怪多自称阿紫。

    Explanation

    222

    During the Jian'an period of the Later Han dynasty, Chen Xian of Pei State served as the commander of the Western Sea. One of his subordinates, Wang Lingxiao, fled without cause. Xian wanted to kill him. Not long after, Lingxiao fled again. Since Xian had not seen him for a long time, he imprisoned Lingxiao's wife, who truthfully confessed. Xian said, "This must be a spirit that has taken him away; I shall search for him." He then led a group of several dozen foot soldiers and cavalry, accompanied by hunting dogs, and roamed around outside the city searching. Indeed, he found Lingxiao inside an empty tomb. Upon hearing the sounds of people and dogs, the spirit fled. Xian had his men carry Lingxiao back, but his form was somewhat like that of a fox. He barely responded to people anymore, but only cried out, "Azi." Azi is the name of the fox. After more than ten days, he gradually regained clarity. He said, "The fox first came to me when it appeared in the corner of the house where the chickens roosted, taking on the form of a beautiful woman and calling herself Azi, calling me. This happened more than once. Suddenly, I followed her away, and immediately became her husband, returning home with her each evening. I did not realize it was a dog. The joy was indescribable." A Daoist said, "This is a mountain spirit." The Classic of Mountains states, "The fox is the former prostitute of ancient times, whose name was Azi, who was transformed into a fox." Hence, this spirit often calls itself Azi.

    223

    南阳西郊有一亭，人不可止，止则有祸，邑人宋大贤以正道自处，尝宿亭楼，夜坐鼓琴，不设兵仗，至夜半时，忽有鬼来登梯，与大贤语，●目，磋齿，形貌可恶。大贤鼓琴如故。鬼乃去。于市中取死人头来，还语大贤曰：“宁可少睡耶？”因以死人头投大贤前。大贤曰：“甚佳！我暮卧无枕，正欲得此。”鬼复去。良久乃还，曰：“宁可共手搏耶？”大贤曰：“善！”语未竟，鬼在前，大贤便逆捉其腰。鬼但急言死。大贤遂杀之。明日视之，乃老狐也。自是亭舍更无妖怪。

    Explanation

    223

    In the western suburbs of Nanyang, there was a pavilion where no one could linger, for doing so would bring misfortune. Cao Da Xian, a virtuous man who conducted himself according to the righteous way, once stayed in the pavilion's tower. At midnight, a ghost climbed the ladder and spoke with Cao Da Xian, glaring at him with its eyes and grinding its teeth, its appearance grotesque. Yet Cao Da Xian continued to play the qin as before. The ghost then left. It went to the market to fetch a severed human head and returned, speaking to Cao Da Xian: "Would you like to rest a bit?" It then threw the severed head in front of Cao Da Xian. Cao Da Xian replied, "Very good! I have no pillow for my evening sleep, and this is just what I need." The ghost left again. After a long time, it returned, saying, "Would you like to engage in hand-to-hand combat?" Cao Da Xian replied, "Yes!" As the ghost approached, Cao Da Xian seized its waist from behind. The ghost merely cried out in fear. Cao Da Xian then killed it. The next day, it was discovered that the ghost was an old fox. From then on, the pavilion was free of ghosts.

    224

    北部督邮西平到伯夷，年三十许，大有才决，长沙太守到若章孙也，日晡时，到亭，敕前导人且止。录事掾曰：“今尚早，可至前亭。”曰：“欲作文书。”便留，吏卒惶怖，言当解去。传云：“督邮欲于楼上观望，亟扫除。”须臾，便上。未暝，楼镫阶下，复有火敕云：“我思道，不可见火，灭去。”吏知必有变，当用赴照，但藏置壶中。日既暝，整服坐，诵六甲、孝经、易本讫，卧。有顷，更转东首，以拏巾结两足帻冠之，密拔剑解带。夜时，有正黑者四五尺，稍高，走至柱屋，因覆伯夷伯夷持被掩之，足跣脱，几失，再三以剑带击魅脚，呼下火照上。视之，老狐，正赤，略无衣毛。持下烧杀。明旦，发楼屋，得所髡人髻百余。因此遂绝。
    　　吴中有一书生，皓首，称胡博士，教授诸生。忽复不见。九月初九日，士人相与登山游观，闻讲书声；命仆寻之，见空冢中群狐罗列，见人即走，老狐独不去，乃是皓首书生。

    224

    A Postal Inspector from Xiping named Dao Bei, about thirty years old, was very talented and decisive. He was the grandson of the former Governor of Changsha, Dao Ruozhang. At the time of day when the sun is setting, he arrived at a post station and ordered the leading person to stop. The clerk said, "It's still early, we can reach the next post station." Dao Bei replied, "I want to write documents." He decided to stay, causing the officials and soldiers to be terrified and say they should leave. The message said, "The postal inspector wants to observe from the upper floor, quickly clean up." A short while later, he went up. Before it got dark, there were lights under the staircase, and there was another fire command. "I think about the Dao, cannot see fire, extinguish it." The officials knew something would happen, should use it for illumination, but put it in a pot. When it got dark, he got dressed and sat down, recited the Six Jia, the Classic of Filial Piety, and the I Ching, and then lay down. After a while, he turned to face east, used a handkerchief to tie his feet and head, secretly drew his sword and untied his belt. At night, there was a dark figure about four to five feet tall, gradually grew taller, ran to the pillar of the house, and then covered the inspector. Dao Bei held the blanket to cover it, but his feet slipped off, almost losing it. He hit the demon's feet with his sword and belt several times, called for the light below to illuminate above. He looked at it and saw an old fox, bright red, with almost no fur. He took it down and burned it. The next morning, he searched the upper floor and found more than a hundred hair buns from shaved people. From then on, it stopped.

    In Wu, there was a scholar, white-haired, called Hu Doctor, who taught the students. Suddenly, he disappeared again. On the ninth day of the ninth month, scholars went up the mountain together to enjoy the scenery and heard the sound of teaching. They ordered the servant to look for it and saw a group of foxes arranged in an empty tomb. The foxes ran away when they saw people, but the old fox did not leave. It was the white-haired scholar.

    225

    陈郡谢鲲，谢病去职，避地于豫章，尝行经空亭中，夜宿。此亭，旧每杀人，夜四更，有一黄衣人呼鲲字云：“幼舆！可开户。”鲲澹然无惧色，令申臂于窗中。于是授腕。鲲即极力而牵之。其臂遂脱。乃还去。明日看，乃鹿臂也。寻血取获。尔后此亭无复妖怪。
    　　晋有一士人姓王，家在吴郡，还至曲阿，日暮，引船上，当大埭，见埭上有一女子，年十七八，便呼之，留宿。至晓，解金铃系其臂，使人随至家，都无女人。因逼猪栏中，见母猪臂有金铃。
    　　汉，齐人梁文，好道，其家有神祠，建室三四间，座上施皁帐，常在其中，积十数年，后因祀事，帐中忽有人语，自呼高山君，大能饮食，治病有验。文奉事甚肃。积数年，得进其帐中，神醉，文乃乞得奉见颜色。谓文曰：“授手来！”文纳手，得持其颐，髯须甚长；文渐绕手，卒然引之，而闻作羊声。座中惊起，助文引之，乃袁公路家羊也，失之七八年，不知所在。杀之，乃绝。

    Explanation

    225

    Tchen Jun's Xie Kun, after resigning from office due to illness, sought refuge in Yuzhang. Once, he passed through an abandoned pavilion and stayed there for the night. This pavilion was notorious for killing people. At the fourth watch of the night, a man in yellow clothing called out to Xie Kun by name, saying, "Young Yu! Open the door!" Xie Kun remained calm and fearless, extending his arm through the window. The man then took his hand. Xie Kun exerted all his strength to pull, and the man's arm was torn off. The man then departed. The next day, they found a deer's arm. Following the trail of blood, they caught the deer. After this, the pavilion was no longer haunted.

    During the Jin dynasty, there was a scholar named Wang, whose family lived in Wu Commandery. On his way back to Qu'e, he arrived late in the evening and docked his boat at a large embankment. He saw a young woman, around seventeen or eighteen years old, on the embankment and called out to her, inviting her to stay for the night. At dawn, he removed a golden bell from her arm and sent someone to follow her home, but there was no woman there. They then searched the pig pen and found a sow with a golden bell on its arm.

    In the Han dynasty, there was a man from Qi named Liang Wen, who was fond of Daoism. His family had a shrine to a deity, and they built three or four rooms for it. There was a black curtain on the seat, and the deity would often appear there. After several years, during a ritual, someone suddenly spoke from the curtain, introducing himself as Lord of the High Mountain. He was said to be able to eat and drink, and his cures were effective. Liang Wen served him with great reverence. After several years, he was allowed to enter the curtain, and the deity became drunk. Liang Wen then asked to see the deity's face. The deity said, "Give me your hand!" Liang Wen reached out, and the deity took his chin, with a long beard and mustache. Liang Wen gradually wrapped his hand around the deity's neck and suddenly pulled, hearing a sheep's bleat. The people in the room were startled and helped Liang Wen pull. It turned out to be a sheep from Yuan Shu's household, which had been missing for seven or eight years. They killed the sheep, and the supernatural occurrences ceased.

    226

    北平田琰，居母丧，恒处庐向。一暮夜，忽入妇室，密怪之曰：“君在毁灭之地，幸可不甘。”琰不听而合。后琰暂入，不与妇语。妇怪无言，幷以前事责之。琰知鬼魅。临暮，竟未眠，衰服挂庐。须臾，见一白狗，撄庐衔衰服，因变为人，着而入。琰随后逐之，见犬将升妇床，便打杀之、妇羞愧而死。
    　　司空南阳来季德，停丧在殡，忽然见形坐祭床上，颜色服饰声气，熟是也，孙儿妇女，以次教戒，事有条贯。鞭朴奴婢，皆得其过。饮食既绝，辞诀而去。家人大小，哀割断绝。如是数年。家益厌苦。其后饮酒过多，醉而形露，但得老狗。便共打杀。因推问之，则里中沽酒家狗也。
    　　山阳王瑚。字孟琏，为东海兰陵尉，夜半时。辄有黑帻白单衣吏，诣县，叩阁。迎之，则忽然不见。如是数年。后伺之，见一老狗，白躯犹故，至阁，便为人。以白孟琏，杀之，乃绝。

    Explanation

    226

    In the city of Beiping, there was a man named Tian Yan who was observing the mourning for his mother. He always lived in a thatched hut facing east. One night, a ghost suddenly entered his wife's room and whispered in surprise, saying, "You are in a place of destruction, fortunately you cannot bear it." Tian Yan did not listen and closed the door. Later, when Tian Yan briefly entered the room, he did not speak to his wife. His wife was puzzled by his silence and blamed him for the earlier incident. Tian Yan then realized it was a ghost. That evening, he stayed awake all night, hanging his mourning attire in the hut. Soon after, he saw a white dog climb the thatched hut and bite the mourning attire, then transform into a person and enter the room. Tian Yan followed and saw the dog about to climb onto his wife's bed. He struck it down and killed it. His wife, ashamed and humiliated, died.

    In another incident, the Grand Works Minister from Nanyang, Lai Jide, had a funeral in progress when he suddenly saw the deceased sitting on the sacrificial bed. The appearance, clothing, and voice were all familiar. He then proceeded to teach and admonish his grandchildren and daughters-in-law in turn, with everything being done in an orderly manner. He even punished the servants and slaves according to their faults. After the food and drink were finished, he bid farewell and left. The entire family, young and old, felt a deep sense of sorrow and grief. This continued for several years, and the household grew increasingly weary and troubled. Later, after drinking too much wine and becoming drunk, the ghost's true form was revealed, and they found it was just an old dog. They all beat and killed it. Upon investigation, it turned out to be a dog from the village wine shop.

    In the city of Shanyang, there was a man named Wang Hu, whose courtesy name was Menglian. He served as the magistrate of Lanling in the state of Donghai. Every midnight, a black-capped, white-garbed official would come to the county office and knock on the door. When they went to greet him, he would suddenly disappear. This happened for several years. Later, they waited for him and saw an old dog with a white body, which transformed into a person upon reaching the gate. They informed Menglian, who then killed it, and the apparitions ceased.

    227

    桂阳太守李叔坚，为从事，家有犬，人行。家人言：“当杀之。”叔坚曰：“犬马喻君子。犬见人行，效之，何伤！”顷之，狗戴叔坚冠走。家大惊。叔坚云：“误触冠缨挂之耳。”狗又于灶前畜火。家益怔营。叔坚复云：“儿婢皆在田中，狗助畜火，幸可不烦邻里。此有何恶。”数日，狗自暴死。卒无纤芥之异。
    　　吴郡无锡有上湖大陂，陂吏丁初天，每大雨，辄循堤防。春盛雨，初出行塘，日暮回顾，有一妇人，上下青衣，戴青伞，追后呼：“初掾待我。”初时怅然，意欲留俟之。复疑本不见此，今忽有妇人，冒阴雨行，恐必鬼物。初便疾走。顾视妇人，追之亦急。初因急行，走之转远；顾视妇人，乃自投陂中，泛然作声，衣盖飞散。视之，是大苍獭，衣伞皆荷叶也。此獭化为人形，数媚年少者也。

    Explanation

    227

    In the prefecture of Guiyang, there was a magistrate named Li Shujian who served as an assistant official. He had a dog at home that would mimic human behavior. The family suggested, "We should kill it." Li Shujian replied, "Dogs and horses are metaphors for virtuous men. The dog sees people walking and imitates them; what harm is there in that?" Soon after, the dog was seen wearing Li Shujian's hat and running away. The family was greatly alarmed. Li Shujian said, "It must have accidentally caught the hat on its head." The dog also helped to keep the fire going in the kitchen. The family became even more anxious. Li Shujian reassured them, "All the children and servants are out working in the fields. The dog is helping to keep the fire going, which is fortunate as it means we don't need to bother the neighbors. There is nothing wrong with this." After a few days, the dog died suddenly. There were no further unusual occurrences.

    In the prefecture of Wu, in Wuxi, there was a large pond known as Shanghu Dipei. The official responsible for the pond, Ding Chutian, would patrol the embankment during heavy rains. One spring, when the rains were particularly heavy, Ding Chutian was walking along the pond when he looked back and saw a woman dressed in green clothes and carrying a green umbrella. She called out to him, "Wait for me, Official Ding!" Initially, Ding Chutian felt a mix of emotions and considered staying to see the woman. However, he then became suspicious, thinking that he had never seen her before and that she might be a ghost appearing in the rain. He quickly ran away. As he looked back, he saw the woman following him, but he ran faster. As he ran, he got further away from her. When he looked back again, he saw the woman jump into the pond, making a splash and scattering her clothes and umbrella. Upon closer inspection, he realized that the woman was actually a large water otter, with the clothes and umbrella being made of lotus leaves. It turned out that this otter had transformed into a human form to seduce young men.

    魏齐王芳正始中，中山王周南，为襄邑长，忽有鼠从穴出，在厅事上语曰：“王周南！尔以某月某日当死。周南急往，不应。鼠还穴。后至期，复出，更冠帻皁衣而语曰：“周南！尔日中当死。”亦不应。鼠复入穴。须臾，复出，出，复入，转行，数语如前。日适中。鼠复曰：“周南！尔不应死，我复何道！”言讫，颠蹶而死。即失衣冠所在。就视之，与常鼠无异。
    　　安阳城南有一亭，夜不可宿；宿，辄杀人。书生明术数，乃过宿之，亭民曰：“此不可宿。前后宿此，未有活者。”书生曰：“无苦也。吾自能谐。”遂住廨舍。乃端坐，诵书。良久乃休。夜半后，有一人，着皁单衣，来，往户外，呼亭主。亭主应诺。“见亭中有人耶？”答曰：“向者有一书生在此读书。适休，似未寝。”乃喑嗟而去，须臾，复有一人，冠赤帻者，呼亭主。问答如前。复喑嗟而去。既去，寂然。

    Explanation

    228

    During the Zhengshi era of King Wang of Wei, Prince Zhou Nan of Zhongshan, who served as the magistrate of Xiangyi, suddenly saw a mouse emerge from its hole in the main hall and speak to him: "Prince Zhou Nan! You will die on a certain day and month." Prince Zhou Nan hurried to the spot but did not respond. The mouse returned to its hole. Later, on the designated day, the mouse emerged again, this time wearing a headgear and black robe, and said: "Prince Zhou Nan! You will die at noon." Prince Zhou Nan still did not respond. The mouse went back into its hole. Shortly after, it emerged again, moving around and repeating the same words as before. Just as the sun reached its zenith, the mouse said: "Prince Zhou Nan! You should not die, what else can I say!" After speaking, the mouse fell and died. The clothes and headgear it had worn were immediately lost. Upon inspection, the mouse was no different from ordinary mice.

    In the south of Anyang, there was a pavilion that was said to be dangerous to stay in at night; anyone who stayed there would be killed. A scholar skilled in divination and numerology decided to spend the night there. The villagers warned him: "This place is not safe. No one has survived after staying here." The scholar replied: "There is no need to worry. I can manage." He then stayed in the pavilion and sat upright, reciting books. After a long time, he rested. After midnight, a man dressed in a black robe appeared, went outside, and called the pavilion's caretaker. The caretaker responded: "Do you see anyone in the pavilion?" The man answered: "Earlier, there was a scholar reading here. He just rested and seems not yet asleep." The man then sighed and left. Shortly after, another man appeared, wearing a red headgear, and called the caretaker. The exchange was the same as before. The man sighed again and left. After they left, everything was silent.

    229

    书生知无来者，即起，诣向者呼处，效呼亭主。亭主亦应诺。复云：“亭中有人耶？”亭主答如前。乃问曰：“向黑衣来者谁？”曰：“北舍母猪也。”又曰：“冠赤帻来者谁？”曰：“西舍老雄鸡父也。”曰：“汝复谁耶？”曰：“我是老蝎也。”于是书生密便诵书。至明不敢寐。天明，亭民来视，惊曰：“君何得独活？”书生曰：“促索剑来，吾与卿取魅：”乃握剑至昨夜应处，果得老蝎，大如琵琶，毒长数尺。西舍，得老雄鸡父；北舍，得老母猪，凡杀三物，亭毒遂静，永无灾横。

    229

    The scholar knew that no one else was coming, so he immediately rose and went to the place where he had heard the call, imitating the call of the innkeeper. The innkeeper responded affirmatively. The scholar then asked, "Is there someone in the inn?" The innkeeper answered as before. The scholar asked, "Who is the one coming in black clothing?" The innkeeper replied, "The old sow from the north house." The scholar asked again, "Who is the one coming with a red headband?" The innkeeper replied, "The old rooster father from the west house." The scholar asked, "And who are you?" The innkeeper replied, "I am the old scorpion." The scholar then quietly began reciting books and did not dare to sleep until dawn. When morning came, the innkeeper came to see and was surprised, saying, "How did you manage to survive alone?" The scholar said, "Quickly fetch the sword, I will help you catch the demon." He held the sword and went to the place where it had responded the previous night. Sure enough, he found the old scorpion, which was as large as a lute and had a poison several feet long. From the west house, he caught the old rooster father; from the north house, he caught the old sow. In total, he killed three creatures. The inn was then quiet, and there were no more disasters or calamities.

    230

    吴时，庐陵郡都亭重屋中，常有鬼魅，宿者辄死。自后使官，莫敢入亭止宿。时丹阳人汤应者，大有胆武，使至庐陵，便止亭宿。吏启不可。应不听。迸从者还外，惟持一大刀，独处亭中。至三更。竟忽闻有叩阁者。应遥问是谁？答云：“部郡相闻。”应使进。致词而去。顷间，复有叩阁者如前，曰：“府君相闻。”应复使进。身着皂衣。去后，应谓是人，了无疑也。旋又有叩阁者，云：“部郡府君相诣。”应乃疑曰：“此夜非时，又部郡府君不应同行。”知是鬼魅。因持刀迎之。见二人皆盛衣服，俱进，坐毕，府君者便与应谈。谈未竟，而部郡忽起至应背后，应乃回顾，以刀逆击，中之。府君下坐走出。应急追至亭后墙下，及之，斫伤数下，应乃还卧。达曙，将人往寻，见有血迹，皆得之云。称府君者，是一老狶也；部郡者，是一老狸也。自是遂绝。

    Explanation

    230

    During the Wu period, there was a two-story building at the town gate of庐陵郡 that was often haunted by ghosts. Anyone who stayed there died immediately. After that, no official dared to enter the building to stay overnight. At that time, there was a man from DanYang named Tang Ying, who was very brave and strong. When he was sent to庐陵, he decided to stay in the building for the night. The official advised against it, but Tang Ying refused to listen. He dismissed his attendants and went inside, carrying only a large knife, and stayed alone in the building. It was the third watch of the night when suddenly he heard someone knocking on the door. Tang Ying asked from afar who it was. The answer came, "This is from the prefecture." Tang Ying allowed them to enter and they delivered their message and left. Soon after, there was another knock on the door, and the voice said, "This is from the prefecture's official." Tang Ying allowed them to enter again. The person was dressed in black. After they left, Tang Ying thought it was a human and had no doubts. Soon after, there was another knock on the door, and the voice said, "This is the prefecture's official coming to visit." Tang Ying then became suspicious, saying, "It is not the proper time for this visit, and the prefecture's official should not be traveling together." He realized they were ghosts. He then held his knife and went to meet them. He saw two people, both well-dressed, and they both entered and sat down. The one called "prefecture's official" began talking to Tang Ying. Before the conversation was over, the prefecture's official suddenly got up and approached Tang Ying from behind. Tang Ying turned around and struck him with his knife, hitting him. The prefecture's official got up and ran out. Tang Ying quickly chased him to the back wall of the building and caught up with him, striking him several times. He then returned to his room and lay down. At dawn, he took people to search for the prefecture's official and found bloodstains. They confirmed that the one called "prefecture's official" was an old pig, and the prefecture's official was an old fox. From then on, the haunting stopped.
