    搜神记卷十九
    　　东越闽中，有庸岭，高数十里，其西北隙中，有大蛇，长七八丈大十余围，土俗常惧。东治都尉及属城长吏，多有死者。祭以牛羊，故不得福，或与人梦，或下谕巫祝，欲得啖童女年十二三者。都尉令长并共患之，然气厉不息，共请求人家生婢子，兼有罪家女养之，至八月朝，祭送蛇穴口，蛇出吞啮之。累年如此，已用九女。尔时预复募索，未得其女。将乐县李诞家有六女。无男，其小女名寄，应募欲行。父母不听。寄曰：“父母无相，惟生六女，无有一男。虽有如无。

    Explanation

    231

    Search for Gods, Volume 19

    In the region of Dongyue (Eastern Yue) in Fujian (Minzhong), there is a mountain called Yongling, which is tens of miles high. In the gap in the northwest of this mountain, there is a large snake, about seventy to eighty feet long and over ten encirclements in girth. The local people are always afraid of it. The Eastern Commandant and officials of the subordinate cities have often died. They sacrifice oxen and sheep, but they do not receive blessings; sometimes the snake appears in people's dreams, or gives instructions to the shamans, wanting to eat young girls aged twelve or thirteen. The Commandant and officials all suffer from this, but the spirit is fierce and relentless. They jointly request that families provide young maidservants, and also provide daughters from families with crimes, and raise them until the eighth day of the eighth month, when they are sacrificed at the snake's den. The snake comes out and swallows them. For many years this has been the case, and already nine girls have been used. At that time, they again sought volunteers, but no suitable girl was found. In Jiangle County, Li Dan's family has six daughters. They have no sons, and their youngest daughter is named Ji. She volunteered to go, but her parents did not allow it. Ji said, "Our parents have no good fortune, and we have only six daughters, no sons. Even though we have them, it is as if we do not."

    232

    女无缇萦济父母之功，既不能供养，徒费衣食，生无所益，不如早死；卖寄之身，可得少钱，以供父母，岂不善耶！”父母慈怜，终不听去。寄自潜行，不可禁止。寄乃告请好剑及咋蛇犬，至八月朝，便诣庙中坐，怀剑，将犬，先将数石米餈，用蜜(麦少)灌之，以置穴口，蛇便出。头大如囷，目如二尺镜，闻瓷香气，先啖食之。寄便放犬，犬就啮咋，寄从后研得数创，疮痛急，蛇因踊出，至庭而死。寄入视穴，得其九女髑髅，悉举出，咤言曰：“汝曹怯弱，为蛇所食，甚可哀愍。”于是寄女缓步而归。越王闻之，聘寄女为后，指其父为将乐令，母及姊皆有赏赐。自是东治无复妖邪之物。其歌谣至今存焉。

    232

    The girl had no virtue like that of Tiying to save her parents, nor could she provide for them, only wasting food and clothing, living brought no benefit, it would be better to die early. To sell one's own body, one can earn a little money, to provide for one's parents, isn't that good? Her parents showed kindness and pity, never allowing her to leave. Ji secretly left, could not be stopped. Ji carried a sword and led a dog, first taking several stone of sweet rice cakes, using honey to moisten them, placing them at the entrance of the hole. The snake came out, its head was as big as a granary, its eyes were like two-foot mirrors, smelling the fragrance of the cakes, first eating the cakes. Ji then released the dog, the dog bit and gnawed, Ji struck from behind, causing several wounds, the wounds were painful, the snake jumped out, dying in the courtyard. Ji entered the hole, finding the skulls of nine girls, all lifting them out, exclaiming, "You are all weak and timid, eaten by the snake, very pitiful." She slowly returned home. King Yu heard of it, marrying Ji's daughter as his queen, appointing her father as the governor of Jiangle, her mother and sister also received rewards. From then on, there were no more evil spirits in Dongzhi, its songs and ballads still exist today.

    233

    晋武帝咸宁中，魏舒为司徒，府中有二大蛇，长十许丈，居厅事平橑上，止之数年，而人不知，但怪府中数失小儿，及鸡犬之属。后有一蛇夜出，经柱侧伤于刃，病不能登于是觉之。发徒数百，攻击移时，然然杀之。视所居，骨骼盈宇之间。于是毁府舍更立之。
    　　汉武帝时张宽为扬州刺史。先是，有二老翁争山地，诣州，讼疆界，连年不决，宽视事，复来。宽窥二翁，形状非人，令卒持杖戟将入问“汝等何精？”翁走。宽呵格之，化为二蛇。
    　　荥阳人张福船行，还野水边，夜有一女子，容色甚美，自乘小船来投福，云：“日暮，畏虎，不敢夜行。”福曰：“汝何姓？作此轻行。无笠，雨驶，可入船就避雨。”因共相调，遂入就福船寝。以所乘小舟，系福船边，三更许，雨晴，月照，福视妇人，乃是一大鼍枕臂而卧福惊起，欲执之，遽走入水。向小舟是一枯槎段，长丈余。

    Explanation

    233

    During the Xianning period of Emperor Wu of Jin, Wei Shu served as Simu, and in his government office, there were two large snakes, about ten zhang long, living on the flat beams of the hall. They stayed there for several years, but the people did not know about them, only noticing because children and poultry were frequently missing. Later, one of the snakes came out at night, was injured by a sword on the side of a pillar, became ill and unable to climb, and thus was discovered. Hundreds of men were mobilized, attacking for a while, and finally killed it. Upon inspection, the bones of the snakes filled the courtyard. Therefore, the government office was destroyed and rebuilt.

    During the reign of Emperor Wu of Han, Zhang Kuan served as the governor of Yangzhou. Before that, two old men had been arguing over land boundaries for many years and came to the state to sue each other. When Zhang Kuan took office, they came again. Zhang Kuan observed the two old men and noticed they had an unusual appearance. He ordered soldiers to bring them in with spears and asked, "What are you?" The old men fled. Zhang Kuan shouted at them and they transformed into two snakes.

    Zhang Fu from Xingyang was traveling by boat and returned to a wild riverbank. At night, a beautiful woman came to Zhang Fu in a small boat and said, "It's getting dark, I'm afraid of tigers, and I dare not travel at night." Zhang Fu said, "What is your surname? Why are you traveling so lightly? You have no hat, and the rain is heavy; you can come aboard my boat to take shelter." They chatted and then entered Zhang Fu's boat to sleep. She tied her small boat to Zhang Fu's boat. Around the third watch, the rain stopped, and the moon came out. Zhang Fu looked at the woman and saw she was actually a large toad sleeping with her arm under her head. Zhang Fu woke up in shock and tried to catch her, but she quickly jumped into the water. The small boat she had tied to Zhang Fu's boat was actually a piece of dead wood, about ten feet long.

    234

    丹阳道士谢非往石城买台釜，还，日暮，不及至家；山中庙舍于溪水上，入中，宿，大声语曰“吾是天帝使者，停此宿，犹畏人劫夺其釜，意苦搔搔不安。”二更中，有来至庙门者，呼曰：“何铜：”铜应喏。曰：“庙中有人气，是谁？”铜云“有人。言是天帝使者。”少顷便还。须臾又有来者，呼铜问之，如前。铜答如故。复叹息而去。非惊扰不得眠。遂起，呼铜问之：“先来者谁？”答言：“是水边穴中白鼍。”“汝是何等物？”答言：“是庙北岩嵌中龟也。”非皆阴识之。天明，便告居人言：“此庙中无神，但是龟鼍之辈，徒费酒食祀之。急具锸来，共往伐之。”诸人亦颇疑之，于是并会伐掘，皆杀之。遂坏庙，绝祀。自后安静。

    Explanation

    234

    A Taoist priest named Xie Fei from Danyang went to Shicheng to buy a large pot. On his return, it was late in the evening, and he did not make it home in time. He stayed overnight in a temple house in the mountains by the stream. He spoke loudly and said, "I am a messenger of the Heavenly Emperor. I am staying here for the night, but I am still afraid that someone might steal my pot. I am very uneasy and restless." Around the second watch of the night, someone came to the temple gate and called out, "Who is there?" The person named Tong replied. The caller asked, "There is a human presence in the temple, who is it?" Tong said, "There is someone. He says he is a messenger of the Heavenly Emperor." After a short while, the caller returned. Shortly after, another person came. He called out to Tong and asked him, just as before. Tong answered as before. The person sighed and left. Xie Fei was disturbed and could not sleep. He got up and called out to Tong to ask him, "Who was the first person?" Tong replied, "It was a white alligator from a hole by the water." Xie Fei asked, "What kind of creature are you?" Tong replied, "I am a turtle in the crevice of the rock north of the temple." Xie Fei secretly recognized them. At dawn, he told the local people, "There is no god in this temple, it is just a place for turtles and alligators, and it is a waste to offer wine and food to them. Quickly bring shovels and come with me to dig them up." The others also somewhat doubted him. They all gathered and dug them up, killing them all. They then destroyed the temple and stopped the worship. Afterwards, it became quiet.

    孔子厄于陈，弦歌于馆，中夜，有一人长九尺余，着皁衣，高冠，大咤，声动左右。子贡进问“何人耶？”便提子贡而挟之。子路引出与战于庭，有顷，未胜，孔子察之，见其甲车间时时开如掌，孔子曰：“何不探其甲车，引而奋登？”子路引之，没手仆于地。乃是大鳀鱼也。长九尺余。孔子曰：“此物也，何为来哉？吾闻物老。则群精依之。因衰而至此。其来也，岂以吾遇厄，绝粮，从者病乎！夫六畜之物，及龟蛇鱼鳖草木之属，久者神皆凭依，能为妖怪，故谓之‘五酉。’‘五酉’者，五行之方，皆有其物，酉者，老也，物老则为怪，杀之则已，夫何患焉。或者天之未丧斯文，以是系予之命乎！不然，何为至于斯也。”弦歌不辍。子路烹之，其味滋。病者兴，明日，遂行。

    Explanation

    235

    During his time of distress in Chen, Confucius was singing and playing music in the hall. In the middle of the night, a man appeared, over nine feet tall, wearing black clothing and a high hat, and let out a loud shout that caused a commotion. Zigong approached to ask, "Who are you?" The man grabbed Zigong and carried him away. Zilu led him out to fight in the courtyard, but after a while, they did not succeed. Confucius observed and saw that the man's armor opened like a palm. Confucius said, "Why don't you investigate the man's armor and pull to attack?" Zilu pulled and attacked, and the man fell to the ground. It turned out to be a large hagfish, over nine feet long. Confucius said, "What is this creature doing here? I have heard that when things grow old, spirits gather upon them. Due to decline, it has arrived here. Is it because of our current hardship, lack of food, and the illness of those who follow us? All things, whether animals, turtles, snakes, fish, turtles, and plants, if they have lived long, have spirits that depend on them, and can become monsters. This is why they are called 'Five Things That Grow Old.' 'Five Things That Grow Old' refers to the five elements, each with its corresponding thing. The element of earth is old, and when things grow old, they become monsters; kill them to stop them. What harm is there? Perhaps heaven has not yet abandoned this culture, to bind my fate. If not, why did it come to this?" Confucius continued to sing and play music without pause. Zilu cooked the hagfish, and its taste was delicious. The sick ones recovered, and the next day, they continued on their way.

    豫章有一家，婢在灶下，忽有人长数寸，来灶间壁，婢误以履践之，杀一人；须臾，遂有数百人，着衰麻服，持棺迎丧，凶仪皆备，出东门，入园中覆船下。就视之，皆是鼠妇。婢作汤灌杀，遂绝。

    236

    In the region of Yuzhang, there was a household where a female servant was working near the kitchen hearth. Suddenly, a being several inches tall appeared by the hearth wall. The servant accidentally stepped on it, killing the small creature. Soon after, hundreds of beings appeared, dressed in mourning attire, carrying coffins to meet the funeral procession, with all funeral rites prepared. They emerged from the eastern gate and gathered under an overturned boat in the garden. Upon closer inspection, they were all found to be mouse beetles. The servant made a hot water bath to drown them, and thus the strange events ceased.

    237

    狄希，中山人也，能造千日酒饮之，千日醉；时有州人，姓刘，名玄石，好饮酒，往求之。希曰：“我酒发来未定，不敢饮君。”石曰：“纵未熟，且与一杯，得否？”希闻此语，不免饮之。复索，曰：“美哉！可更与之。”希曰：“且归。别日当来。只此一杯，可眠千日也。”石别，似有怍色。至家，醉死。家人不之疑，哭而葬之。经三年，希曰：“玄石必应酒醒，宜往问之。”既往石家，语曰：“石在家否？”家人皆怪之曰：“玄石亡来，服以阕矣。”希惊曰：“酒之美矣，而致醉眠千日，今合醒矣。”乃命其家人凿冢，破棺，看之。冢上汗气彻天。遂命发冢，方见开目，张口，引声而言曰：“快者醉我也！”因问希曰：“尔作何物也？令我一杯大醉，今日方醒，日高几许？”墓上人皆笑之。被石酒气冲入鼻中，亦各醉卧三月。

    Explanation

    237

    Dizi, a man from Zhongshan, was able to brew a legendary thousand-day wine. Whoever drank it would sleep for a thousand days. At that time, there was a man from the same state, surnamed Liu, named Xuan Shi, who loved drinking. He went to Dizi to request some of the wine. Dizi said, "My wine hasn't fully fermented yet, so I dare not offer it to you." Xuan Shi replied, "Even if it's not fully matured, can you give me just one cup? Would that be possible?" Upon hearing this, Dizi could not refuse and gave him a cup. Xuan Shi asked for more, saying, "How wonderful! Can you give me more?" Dizi said, "Go back for now. You can come again another day. Just this one cup, you can sleep for a thousand days." After leaving, Xuan Shi seemed somewhat embarrassed. When he got home, he fell into a drunken sleep and died. His family did not suspect anything and buried him after mourning. Three years later, Dizi said, "Xuan Shi must have woken up from the wine. I should go ask him." So he went to Xuan Shi's house and asked, "Is Xuan Shi at home?" The family all looked surprised and said, "Xuan Shi has been dead for a long time, and the mourning period has ended." Dizi was astonished and said, "How wonderful is this wine! It caused him to sleep for a thousand days. Now he should be awake." He then ordered his family to dig up the grave and break open the coffin to look inside. The grave emitted a strong odor that reached the sky. They opened the grave and saw Xuan Shi with his eyes open, mouth wide, and speaking loudly, "What a wonderful drink to get me drunk!" He then asked Dizi, "What did you make? You got me so drunk with just one cup. I just woke up today. How high is the sun?" The people at the grave all laughed. The wine's vapor entered their noses, and they also fell into a drunken sleep for three months.

    陈仲举微时，常宿黄申家，申妇方产，有扣申门者，家人咸不知，久久方闻屋里有人言：“宾堂下有人，不可进。”扣门者相告曰：“今当从后门往。”其人便往。有顷，还，留者问之：“是何等？名为何？当与几岁？”往者曰：“男也。名为奴。当与十五岁。”“后应以何死？”答曰：“应以兵死。”仲举告其家曰：“吾能相此儿当以兵死。”父母惊之，寸刃不使得执也。至年十五，有置凿于梁上者，其末出，奴以为木也，自下钩之，凿从梁落，陷脑而死，后仲举为豫章太守，故遣吏往饷之申家，幷问奴所在；其家以此具告。仲举闻之，叹曰：“此谓命也。”

    Explanation

    238

    When Chen Zhongju was of humble status, he often stayed at Huang Shen's house. Huang Shen's wife was giving birth, and there was someone knocking at Huang Shen's door. The household was unaware of the situation, and after a long while, they heard someone inside the house say, "There is someone in the guest hall. Do not enter." The knocker replied, "I will go through the back door." That person went through the back door. After a while, he returned, and the one who stayed asked him, "What kind of person is he? What is his name? How old will he be?" The returnee answered, "He is a boy. His name is Nu. He will be fifteen years old." "How will he die later?" the one who stayed asked. The returnee replied, "He will die by weapons." Chen Zhongju said to Huang Shen's family, "I can predict that this child will die by weapons." His parents were alarmed and did not allow him to hold any sharp objects. When he was fifteen, there was a chisel placed on the beam, with the end sticking out. Nu thought it was wood and hooked it from below. The chisel fell from the beam, striking his head and causing his death. After Chen Zhongju became the Governor of Yuzhang, he sent an official to visit Huang Shen's family and asked about Nu's whereabouts. His family told him everything. Chen Zhongju heard this and sighed, "This is fate."

    搜神记卷二十
    　　晋魏郡亢阳，农夫祷于龙洞，得雨，将祭谢之。孙登见曰：“此病龙，雨，安能苏禾稼乎？如弗信，请嗅之。”水果腥秽。龙时背生大疽，闻登言，变为一翁，求治，曰：“疾痊，当有报。”不数日，果大雨。见大石中裂开一井，其水湛然，龙盖穿此井以报也。
    　　苏易者，庐陵妇人，善看产，夜忽为虎所取，行六七里，至大圹，厝易置地，蹲而守，见有牝虎当产，不得解，匍匐欲死，辄仰视。易怪之，乃为探出之，有三子。生毕，牝虎负易还，再三送野肉于门内。

    Explanation

    239

    Translation

    The Twenty-Second Volume of Search for the Supernatural
    During the reign of the state of Jin in the region of Hui, there was a severe drought. A farmer prayed at a dragon cave and received rain. He intended to offer thanks. Sun Deng, upon seeing this, said, "This is a sick dragon. How could the rain it brought revive the crops? If you do not believe me, please smell it." The fruit indeed had a foul, fishy odor. At that time, the dragon had a large boil on its back. Upon hearing Sun Deng's words, it transformed into an old man and sought treatment, saying, "When my disease is cured, I will repay you." Not long after, it rained heavily. A large stone split open, revealing a well with clear water. It seems the dragon had dug this well as a repayment.

    Su Yi, a woman from the region of Luoyang, was skilled in midwifery. One night, she was suddenly taken by a tiger, who carried her for six or seven miles to a large pit. The tiger placed her on the ground and crouched down, guarding her. She saw a female tiger in labor, unable to deliver, and crawling as if she were about to die, looking up. Su Yi was surprised and helped to remove the obstruction, and there were three cubs. After they were born, the female tiger carried Su Yi back and repeatedly brought wild meat to her doorstep as a token of gratitude.

    240

    哙参，养母至孝，曾有玄雀，为弋人所射，穷而归参，参收养，疗治其疮，愈而放之。后雀夜到门外，参执烛视之，见雀雌雄双至，各衔明珠以报参焉。
    　　汉时，弘农杨宝，年九岁时。至华阴山北，见一黄雀，为鸱枭所搏，坠于树下，为蝼蚁所困。宝见，愍之，取归置巾箱中，食以黄花，百余日，毛羽成，朝去，暮还。一夕，三更，宝读书未卧，有黄衣童子，向宝再拜曰：“我西王母使者，使蓬莱，不慎，为鸱枭所搏。君仁爱，见拯，实感盛德。”乃以白环四枚与宝曰：“令君子孙洁白，位登三事，当如此环。”
    　　隋县溠水侧，有断蛇邱。隋侯出行，见大蛇被伤，中断，疑其灵异，使人以药封之，蛇乃能走，因号其处断蛇邱。岁余，蛇衔明珠以报之。珠盈径寸，纯白，而夜有光，明如月之照，可以烛室。故谓之“隋侯珠，”亦曰“灵蛇珠，”又曰“明月珠。”邱南有隋季良大夫池。

    Explanation

    240

    Kuā Cān, filial to his mother to the utmost, once encountered a black bird that was shot by a hunter and was in a pitiful state, returning to Cān for refuge. Cān took it in, treated its wounds, and after it healed, released it. Later, the bird arrived at Cān's door at night. Cān held a candle to see it and found that both male and female birds had come, each carrying a pearl to repay Cān.

    During the Han dynasty, Yang Bao of Hongnong was nine years old when he reached the north side of Mount Huayin and saw a yellow bird that was attacked by a hawk and fell to the ground, where it was trapped by ants. Yang Bao felt pity for it, took it home, and placed it in his cloth box, feeding it yellow flowers. After more than a hundred days, the bird's feathers grew back, and it would leave in the morning and return in the evening. One night, at the third watch, while Yang Bao was reading and had not yet gone to bed, a yellow-robed boy knelt twice before him and said, "I am a messenger of the Queen Mother of the West, sent to Penglai, but I was careless and was attacked by a hawk. Your kindness saved me; I am truly grateful for your great virtue." He then gave Yang Bao four white rings and said, "Your descendants will be pure and white, and their positions will be as high as the three offices, just as these rings are."

    In Suí County, on the side of the Zhà River, there is a place called Broken Snake Hill. When the ruler of Suí went out, he saw a large snake that was wounded and cut in half. He suspected it was a divine creature and sent someone to bandage it with medicine. The snake was able to walk again, and the place was called Broken Snake Hill. After a year, the snake carried a pearl to repay him. The pearl was a full inch in diameter, pure white, and shone brightly at night like the moon, illuminating the room. Therefore, it is called the Suí Hóu Pearl, also known as the Divine Snake Pearl, and the Moonlight Pearl. South of the hill is the Suí Jìliáng Grandee's Pool.

    孔愉，字敬康，会稽山阴人，元帝时以讨华轶功，封侯，愉少时尝经行余不亭，见笼龟于路者，愉买之，放于饮不溪中。龟中流左顾者数过。及后，以功封余不亭侯，铸印，而龟钮左顾，三铸，如初，印工以闻，愉乃悟其为龟之报，遂取佩焉。累迁尚书左仆射，赠车骑将军。
    　　古巢，一日江水暴涨，寻复故道，港有巨鱼，重万斤，三日乃死，合郡皆食之。一老姥独不食。忽有老叟曰：“此吾子也。不幸罹此祸，汝独不食，吾厚报汝。若东门石龟目赤，城当陷。”姥日往视。有稚子讶之，姥以实告。稚子欺之，以朱傅龟目；姥见，急出城。有青衣童子曰：“吾龙之子。”乃引姥登山，而城陷为湖。

    241

    Kong Yu, courtesy name Jingkang, was from Shanyin, Kuaiji. During the reign of Emperor Yuan, he was enfeoffed as a marquis due to his meritorious service in subduing Hua Yi. When young, Kong Yu once passed by Yu Bu Pavilion and saw a turtle in a cage on the road. He bought it and released it into the Yin Bu Creek. The turtle looked left several times in the middle of the stream. Later, due to his achievements, he was enfeoffed as Marquis of Yu Bu Pavilion. When the seal was cast, the turtle on the seal turned left, and this happened three times, just as before. The seal maker reported it, and Kong Yu then realized it was a sign from the turtle. He took the seal and wore it. He was repeatedly promoted to the position of Left Censor and posthumously granted the title of General of the Cavalry.

    In Guchao, one day the river suddenly rose and soon returned to its original course. There was a large fish in the harbor, weighing ten thousand pounds, and it died after three days. The entire county ate it, except for one old woman who alone did not eat it. Suddenly an old man said, "This is my son. Unfortunately, it suffered this calamity. You alone did not eat it, I will reward you greatly. If the stone turtle at the east gate turns red in the eyes, the city will be captured." The old woman went to look every day. A young boy was surprised by this and the old woman told him the truth. The young boy painted the turtle's eyes with red. When the old woman saw it, she quickly left the city. There was a young boy dressed in green who said, "I am the son of a dragon." He then led the old woman up the mountain, and the city was captured and became a lake.

    吴富阳县董昭之，尝乘船过钱塘江，中央，见有一蚁，着一短芦，走一头，回复向一头，甚惶遽。昭之曰：“此畏死也。”欲取着船。船中人骂：“此是毒螫物，不可长，我当蹋杀之，”昭意甚怜此蚁，因以绳系芦，着船，船至岸，蚁得出。其夜梦一人，乌衣，从百许人来，谢云：“仆是蚁中之王。不慎，堕江，惭君济活。若有急难，当见告语。”历十余年，时所在劫盗，昭之被横录为劫主，系狱余杭。昭之忽思蚁王梦，缓急当告，今何处告之。结念之际，同被禁者问之。昭之具以实告。其人曰：“但取两三蚁。着掌中，语之。”昭之如其言。夜，果梦乌衣人云：“可急投余杭山中，天下既乱，赦令不久也”于是便觉。蚁啮械已尽。因得出狱，过江，投余杭山。旋遇赦，得免。

    Explanation

    242

    During the reign of the Wu dynasty, in the Fuyang county, there was a man named Dong Zhaozhi. Once, while traveling by boat across the Qiantang River, he saw an ant clinging to a short piece of reed, moving back and forth in great distress. Dong said, "This ant is afraid of dying." He wanted to take the reed onto the boat. However, the other passengers cursed, saying, "This is a poisonous stinging creature; it cannot be allowed to grow. I will trample it to death." Dong felt deep pity for the ant and tied the reed with a rope, placing it on the boat. When the boat reached the shore, the ant was able to escape. That night, he dreamed of a person dressed in black, accompanied by about a hundred others, who apologized and said, "I am the king of the ants. Unintentionally, I fell into the river. I am grateful to you for saving me. If you have any urgent difficulties, please inform me." After more than ten years, during a time when bandits were rampant everywhere, Dong was wrongly recorded as the leader of the bandits and imprisoned in Yuhang. Suddenly remembering the dream of the ant king, he thought, "In times of urgency, one should inform." But where could he inform them now? At the moment of deep thought, a fellow prisoner asked him about it. Dong told him everything. The other prisoner said, "Just take two or three ants, place them in your hand, and speak to them." Dong followed his advice. That night, he indeed dreamed of the person in black clothes saying, "You can quickly go to the mountains of Yuhang. Since the world is in chaos, the amnesty will not be long." He woke up immediately. The ants had gnawed through his shackles. He was able to escape from prison, crossed the river, and went to the mountains of Yuhang. Soon after, he encountered amnesty and was freed.

    243

    孙权时李信纯，襄阳纪南人也，家养一狗，字曰黑龙，爱之尤甚，行坐相随，饮馔之间，皆分与食。忽一日，于城外饮酒，大醉。归家不及，卧于草中。遇太守郑瑕出猎，见田草深，遣人纵火爇之。信纯卧处，恰当顺风，犬见火来，乃以口拽纯衣，纯亦不动。卧处比有一溪，相去三五十步，犬即奔往入水，湿身走来卧处，周回以身洒之，获免主人大难。犬运水困乏，致毙于侧。俄尔信纯醒来，见犬已死，遍身毛湿，甚讶其事。睹火踪迹，因尔恸哭。闻于太守。太守悯之曰：“犬之报恩，甚于人，人不知恩，岂如犬乎！”即命具棺椁衣衾葬之，今纪南有义犬葬，高十余丈。

    Explanation

    243

    During the reign of Sun Quan, there was a man named Li Xin Chun from Jina, Xiangyang. He kept a dog at home, which he named Heilong, and loved it dearly, always keeping it close by his side, even sharing his meals with it. One day, while drinking outside the city, he became very drunk. Unable to return home in time, he lay down in the grass. Coincidentally, Prefect Zheng Xia was out hunting and saw the deep grass in the fields, ordering his men to set it on fire. Li Xin Chun's resting place was just in the path of the wind, and as the fire approached, Heilong saw the danger and pulled on Chun's clothes with its mouth, but Chun did not move. Nearby there was a stream, about thirty to fifty steps away, and Heilong rushed to it, got wet, and ran back to where Chun was lying, sprinkling water around to extinguish the fire and save its master from great danger. Exhausted from carrying water, the dog died by his side. Soon after, Li Xin Chun woke up, saw the dog dead, with its fur all wet, and was greatly surprised by the event. Seeing the traces of the fire, he cried bitterly. The incident was heard by the Prefect. Moved by the event, the Prefect said, "A dog's gratitude is greater than that of a person; if people do not know gratitude, how can they compare to a dog!" He immediately ordered a coffin, shroud, and burial clothes to be prepared for the dog. Now in Jina, there is a tomb for the loyal dog, which is over ten zhang high.

    244

    太兴中，吴民华隆，养一快犬，号的尾，常将自随。隆后至江边伐荻，为大蛇盘绕，犬奋咋蛇，蛇死。隆僵仆无知，犬彷徨涕泣，走还舟，复反草中。徒伴怪之，随往，见隆闷绝。将归家。犬为不食。比隆复苏，始食。隆愈爱惜，同于亲戚。
    　　庐陵太守太原庞企，字子及，自言其远祖，不知几何世也，坐事系狱，而非其罪，不堪拷掠，自诬服之，及狱将上，有蝼咕虫行其左右，乃谓之曰：“使尔有神，能活我死，不当善乎。”因投饭与之。蝼咕食饭尽，去，顷复来，形体稍大。意每异之，乃复与食。如此去来，至数十日间，其大如豚。及竟报，当行刑，蝼咕夜掘壁根为大孔，乃破械，从之出。去久，时遇赦，得活。于是庞氏世世常以四节祠祀之于都衢处。后世稍怠，不能复特为馔，乃投祭祀之余以祀之，至今犹然。

    Explanation

    244

    During the TaiXing period, a man from Wu named Hua Long kept a swift dog named De Wei, who always accompanied him. Later, Hua Long went to the riverbank to cut reeds and was suddenly surrounded by a large snake. The dog fought fiercely and bit the snake, killing it. Hua Long fainted and became unconscious. The dog wandered aimlessly, crying, and ran back to the boat, then returned to the reeds. His companions found this strange and followed him, discovering that Hua Long had fainted. They decided to take him home. The dog refused to eat. When Hua Long revived, the dog finally started eating. Hua Long grew even more fond of the dog, treating it like a relative.

    In the Eastern Jin Dynasty, Pang Qi, the governor of庐陵 from Taiyuan, was known by his courtesy name Zi Ji. He claimed that his distant ancestor, whose name he did not know, was imprisoned for a crime he did not commit. Unable to withstand torture, the ancestor falsely confessed. As the case was about to be reported, a蝼咕虫appeared around him. The ancestor told it, "If you have any power, you can save me from death. Wouldn't that be good?" He threw some food to it. The蝼咕虫ate all the food, disappeared, and returned a short while later, having grown larger. The ancestor was surprised and fed it again. This went on for several days, and the蝼咕虫grew as big as a pig. When the execution was imminent, the蝼咕虫dug a large hole in the wall at night and broke the chains, allowing the ancestor to escape. After a long time, the ancestor was pardoned and saved. From then on, the Pang family continued to worship the蝼咕虫every season in the main streets. Over time, they became less diligent and could no longer prepare special food for it, so they used leftover food from their sacrifices to honor it. This practice continues to this day.

    245

    临川东兴有人入山，得猿子，便将归，猿母自后逐至家。此人缚猿子于庭中树上以示之。其母便抟颊向人欲乞哀，状直谓口不能言耳。此人既不能放，竟击杀之。猿母悲唤，自掷而死。此人破肠视之，寸寸断裂。未半年，其家疫死，灭门。
    　　冯乘虞荡夜猎，见一大麈，射之。麈便云：“虞荡！汝射杀我耶？”明晨，得一麈而入，实时荡死。
    　　吴郡海盐县北乡亭里，有士人陈甲，本下邳人，晋元帝时寓居华亭，猎于东野大薮，欻见大蛇，长六七丈，形如百斛船，玄黄五色，卧冈下。陈即射杀之，不敢说。三年，与乡人共猎，至故见蛇处，语同行曰：“昔在此杀大蛇。”其夜梦见一人，乌衣，黑帻，来至其家，问曰：“我昔昏醉，汝无状杀我。我昔醉，不识汝面，故三年不相知；今日来就死。”其人即惊觉。明日，腹痛而卒。

    Explanation

    245

    A man from Dongxing in Linchuan entered a mountain and caught a baby monkey, taking it home. The monkey's mother followed him to his house. The man tied the baby monkey to a tree in his courtyard to show her. The mother monkey touched her cheeks to the man, seemingly pleading for mercy, as if she could not speak. Unable to release the monkey, the man eventually killed it. The mother monkey cried out in sorrow and threw herself to her death. The man cut open the monkey's intestines and found them cut into small pieces. Within half a year, the man's entire family died from an epidemic, and the family line was extinguished.

    One night, Yu Dang from Fengcheng went hunting and saw a large deer. He shot it, and the deer said, "Yu Dang! Did you shoot and kill me?" The next morning, he found a deer that had entered his home and died immediately.

    In the northern village of Haixian in Wu Prefecture, there was a scholar named Chen Jia, originally from Xiapi. During the reign of Emperor Yuan of Jin, he lived in Huating. While hunting in a vast wilderness to the east, he suddenly saw a large snake, about six or seven zhang long, shaped like a hundred shi boat, with a mix of black and yellow colors, lying on a hill. Chen shot and killed the snake, but he did not dare to speak of it. Three years later, while hunting with his fellow villagers, they reached the place where he had seen the snake before. He told them, "I killed a large snake here in the past." That night, he dreamed of a man dressed in black and wearing a black hat who came to his home and asked, "I was drunk and you killed me without mercy. I was drunk and did not recognize your face, so I did not know you for three years; today I come to seek my death." The man woke up in shock. The next day, he died from abdominal pain.

    246

    邛都县下有一老姥，家贫，孤独，每食，辄有小蛇，头上戴角，在床间，姥怜而饴之。食后稍长大，遂长丈余。令有骏马，蛇遂吸杀之，令因大忿恨，责姥出蛇。姥云：“在床下。”令即掘地，愈深愈大，而无所见。令又迁怒，杀姥。蛇乃感人以灵言，瞋令“何杀我母？当为母报雠。”此后每夜辄闻若雷若风，四十许日，百姓相见，咸惊语：“汝头那忽戴鱼？”是夜，方四十里，与城一时俱陷为湖，土人谓之为陷湖，唯姥宅无恙，讫今犹存。渔人采捕，必依止宿，每有风浪，辄居宅侧，恬静无他。风静水清，犹见城郭楼橹畟然。今水浅时，彼土人没水，取得旧木，坚贞光黑如漆。今好事人以为枕，相赠。
    　　建业有妇人背生一瘤，大如数斗囊，中有物，如茧栗，甚众，行即有声。恒乞于市。自言：“村妇也，常与姊姒辈分养蚕，己独频年损耗，因窃其姒一囊茧焚之，顷之，背患此疮，渐成此瘤。以衣覆之，即气闭闷；常露之，乃可，而重如负囊。”

    Explanation

    246

    In the county of Qingdu, there lived a poor old woman who was alone and lived in poverty. Every time she ate, a small snake with a horn on its head appeared in her room. Moved by pity, she fed it. After being fed, the snake gradually grew larger and eventually reached a length of over ten feet. The magistrate had a fine horse, which the snake then killed by sucking its blood. The magistrate became extremely angry and demanded that the old woman produce the snake. She replied, "It is under the bed." The magistrate immediately began digging the ground, but the deeper he dug, the larger the snake became, and he found nothing. The magistrate's anger shifted to the old woman, and he killed her. The snake then spoke in a supernatural voice, saying to the magistrate, "Why did you kill my mother? I will avenge her." After that, every night, people heard sounds like thunder and wind. For about forty days, when people met, they would all exclaim in surprise, "Why do you suddenly have a fish on your head?" That night, a forty-li area, along with the city, suddenly sank into a lake. The locals called it the "Sink Lake," but the old woman's house remained unharmed and still stands to this day. Fishermen who come to fish and catch must stay near her house, and whenever there are storms, they take refuge beside it, remaining calm and undisturbed. When the wind is calm and the water is clear, the submerged city and its towers can still be seen. Nowadays, when the water is shallow, the local people dive into the water to retrieve old wood, which is as hard and black as lacquer. People who are fond of such things use it to make pillows and give them as gifts.

    In Jianye, there was a woman who had a tumor on her back, as large as a basket. Inside the tumor were many small objects, like cocoons and chestnuts, which made a sound when she walked. She often begged in the market. She said, "I am a village woman. I used to share the rearing of silkworms with my sisters-in-law, but I alone suffered losses year after year. I secretly stole a bag of cocoons from one of my sisters-in-law and burned them. Soon after, I developed this wound on my back, which gradually turned into this tumor. If I cover it with clothing, I feel suffocated; only by exposing it can I breathe, but it is as heavy as carrying a bag."
